# Toras Menachem Vol 03

Toras Menachem

## – 3 – 5711 – Part Two

## With the help of Hashem. Reshimos, Tuesday, 11 Nissan, 5711

#### 3

Unedited

[Before traveling to the Ohel, the Rebbe requested that the following be conveyed in his name:]

All those who wish to dedicate themselves ("*ibergeben zich*") and to obey ("*folgen*") everything that will be told to them, without asking questions—should sign their name and their mother’s name on a *petek*.

Those who sign have nothing to fear ("*zei hobn zich nit vos tzu shrekn*"), because they will not be asked to do things that are in the category of "ascending to the heavens"[1](#_ftn1). However, on the other hand, they must know that this is a serious matter, not a game ("*es iz an ernste zach, nit kein gelechter*"), and they will need to fulfill their promise.

[When the *petek* with all the names was handed to the Rebbe, he said once more:]

As stated, this is a serious matter, even though they will not be asked to "ascend to the heavens."

## 4

It is well known that the exodus of our forefathers from Egypt marked their departure from the status of Bnei Noach to receive the Torah and to receive the presence of the Shechinah[1](#_ftn2)—whether it was the beginning of the exodus or the complete exodus[2](#_ftn3), which is why our Sages learned the laws of conversion from there. It is understood that this also indicates their spiritual state: the evil within the souls of Yisrael was still in its full strength within the left chamber [of the heart]... their goal and desire, however, was for their neshamah elokis to emerge from the exile of the sitra achra, which is the impurity of Egypt, and to achieve dveikus with Him, may He be blessed[3](#_ftn4).

And so it is every single day, that a person is obligated to see himself as if he went out of Egypt today—as brought in the maamar in the Kuntres—and especially during the days of Pesach.

Since the themes of every chag and moed are aroused each year at their respective times, as is known[4](#_ftn5),

Every single person—and especially those who have not yet reached the level of the Beinoni, which is the standard for every person and to which every person should aspire—must strive to extract and elevate their neshamah elokis from the *exile* of the body and the nefesh habehamis. On the contrary, they must elevate the neshamah elokis above the body and the nefesh habehamis, higher and higher, and achieve dveikus with Him, may He be blessed, through the Torah and mitzvos that they study and fulfill.

And all the days of Pesach (and certainly the first night of Pesach) are uniquely elevated[5](#_ftn6) above the rest of the year and even above the other Yomim Tovim. For then, Yisrael are nourished by the eating of matzah, which contains a semblance of the essence of the greatness of Abba[6](#_ftn7)—the *essence* of Elokus. This means that his physical body becomes connected to the vitality of his soul, so that he may live even a physical life through the consumption of food that contains the essence of Elokus. Therefore, besides the effect it has on the neshamah elokis, it also acts upon the nefesh habehamis—which is the yetzer hara—so that it will

#### 5

not incite as much, and so that it will begin to be refined and allow the neshamah elokis to believe with perfect faith even in that which it does not grasp through the intellect.

***

In the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his sicha in the Kuntres: *These hours are so precious!*

**Menachem Schneerson**

*11 Nissan, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## B’s”d. 13th of Nissan, 5711

#### 6

**A.** [The Rebbe instructed R’ Shlomo Zalman Levitan to lead the davening, and after Maariv, instructed him to farbreng with the crowd.

R’ Shlomo Zalman related in the name of his father—who was present at the time of the histalkus of the Tzemach Tzedek—that the Rebbe Maharil was not in Lubavitch at the time of the histalkus. Upon arriving in Lubavitch, he said: A Rebbe such as this—has never been before. One line from his maamarim in Chassidus can be used to construct an entire maamar! The Rebbe Maharash added: Not only one line, but even one word!

And the Rebbe said:]

The maamarim of Chassidus of the Tzemach Tzedek are *hon rav* (great wealth).

I have not yet studied them all with the necessary depth, only at a first glance; however, from the portion that I have studied with the necessary depth, I can say that every single word is *hon rav*.

**B.** I saw in a Chassidus notebook regarding what is explained in Tanya that "the Avos are the Merkavah", which adds there that even *during sleep* they were in a state of Merkavah.

—The Rebbe once said to his granddaughter, Rabbanit Sheindel [the youngest daughter of the Rebbe Rayatz, with whom the household members loved to play and tease, and who was accustomed to eating at the table of her grandfather, the Rebbe], that she should do everything for the honor of Shabbos: eat for the honor of Shabbos, go for a walk for the honor of Shabbos, and the like. She replied that she could do everything for the honor of Shabbos, except for sleeping—to sleep for the honor of Shabbos—because she did not understand how it is possible to sleep for the honor of Shabbos: when one is sleeping, one is simply sleeping, and how can one then do something for the honor of Shabbos?!...

**C.** [R’ Shlomo Zalman said that the Rebbe Rashab used to lead the davening on the yahrtzeit of the Tzemach Tzedek, but not on the yahrtzeits of the Rebbes before him. Similarly, the Rebbe Rayatz used to lead the davening on the yahrtzeit of the Rebbe Maharash, but not on the yahrtzeits of the Rebbes before him. He asked the Rebbe for the reason for this, and the Rebbe replied:]

The reason for leading the davening on the yahrtzeit of one’s *grandfather* (and not before that) is due to the mitzvah of honoring one’s father. This includes observing the yahrtzeit of the father, by leading the davening on the yahrtzeit of one’s father’s father, just as one’s father would lead the davening on that day.

**D.** [Someone asked the Rebbe if it is permissible to give small grandchildren machine-made matzos (*mashinove matzos*) on Pesach, and the Rebbe replied:]

Regarding *gebrochts* or other stringencies, one can be lenient, but not regarding machine-made matzos. For the essence of matzah is *emunah* (*michla d’mehemnusa*), and one must work on this from a young age.

—Regarding the matter of *emunah* that is achieved through eating matzah, it is brought in Chassidus that this is in accordance with the teaching of our Sages, "An infant does not know how to call 'Abba' until he tastes the taste of grain." And it is obvious that this does not refer to machine-made matzos!...

## With the help of Heaven. 14 Nissan, Erev Chag HaPesach, 5711

#### 8

Unedited

[Following the burning of the chametz, the Rebbe said:]

A kosher and joyous Pesach. – We are already finished with "chametz."

## With the Help of Heaven. Sicha of the Night of the Second Day of Pesach, 5711

#### 9

*Unedited*

**A.** [After conducting the Seder at the home of the Rebbe, the Rebbe Rayatz, before entering his room, the Rebbe said:]

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, said that the *nigun* "A-li Atah Ve'odcha" is a *segulah* for the revelation of Eliyahu, and therefore, we shall now sing this *nigun* with joy and dancing.

[They sang "A-li Atah Ve'odcha," and the Rebbe gestured for them to dance.

Afterward, the Rebbe went out to accompany his mother, the Rebbetzin, to her home. When he returned, he gestured with his holy hand to dance with greater vitality, and he himself joined the circle and danced for a while with great joy.

And afterward—while standing in the *Gan Eden HaTachton*—he said:]

**B.** Among the novel aspects of the night of Pesach that falls on *Motzaei Shabbos* [as in this year, when Pesach falls on Shabbos, and the night of the second day of the festival is *Motzaei Shabbos*] is the change in the text of the *Asher Ga'alnu* blessing—that we say "and we shall eat there of the *pesachim* and of the *zevachim*," and not as is said in most years (when the night of Pesach falls on other days of the week), "and we shall eat there of the *zevachim* and of the *pesachim*."

The difference between the two versions depends on the timing of *Erev Pesach* (the time for offering the *Korban Pesach*): On an *Erev Pesach* that falls on a weekday, we also offer the *Korban Chagigah*, and on the night of Pesach, we eat the *Korban Chagigah* before the *Korban Pesach* so that the *Pesach* is eaten when one is already satiated [20]. Therefore, we say "and we shall eat there of the *zevachim* (the *Chagigah*, and afterward) and of the *pesachim*." This is not the case on an *Erev Pesach* that falls on Shabbos [21], when we offer only the *Korban Pesach* and not the *Korban Chagigah*, as the *Chagigah* does not override Shabbos [22], and it comes only the following day. Therefore, on *Motzaei Shabbos*, we say "and we shall eat there of the *pesachim* (and afterward) and of the *zevachim* (the *Chagigah* that will come the following day)" [23].

#### 10

It follows that regarding the matter of eating the *Pesach* while satiated, there is a difference between Shabbos and a weekday—that on an *Erev Pesach* that falls on Shabbos, it is not as critical that the *Pesach* be eaten while satiated as it is on an *Erev Pesach* that falls on a weekday.

**C.** To understand this, we must first preface an explanation of the concept of eating the *Pesach* while satiated:

One of the reasons [24] that the *Pesach* is eaten specifically while satiated (unlike the Shabbos meal, for which one should strive to enter Shabbos *with an appetite* and eat the Shabbos meal *with relish* [25]) is to demonstrate that the eating of the *Pesach* is *for the sake of the mitzvah*, and not for the sake of bodily pleasure. It is to such an extent that *one does not consider the body at all*; even though the body is full and does not desire to eat anymore, nevertheless, one eats the *Pesach* with the same vitality as one eats when one has an appetite. Moreover, the eating of the *Pesach* is done with the greatest vitality and joy, as the Gemara [26] states: "A *kezayis* of *Pesach* and the *Hallel* bursts the roofs."

**D.** An explanation of this matter (the negation of consideration for the body) in the *avodah* of man:

Although the primary *avodah* concerns the body specifically [27], and a person knows in his soul that from the perspective of the body and the *nefesh habahamit* he is in a state and situation that is not as it should be [as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the *maamar* [28] that "even if he contemplates with Divine contemplation... it does not effect a shift to depart from his habit... to depart from the straits of the body and its desires," and furthermore, it is possible that he has not even begun his *avodah* with the body], nevertheless, he should not consider the body, but rather perform his *avodah* with vitality and joy.

In the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in *Tanya* [29]—that "even though the body stands in its filth and abomination... nevertheless, his soul should be dearer to him, to rejoice in its joy more than in the despised body, so as not to mix and confuse the joy of the soul with the sadness of the body" [as is explained elsewhere [30] that although "weeping is lodged in my heart from one side," nevertheless, "joy is lodged in my heart from the other side"]. That is to say, instead of being sad with the sadness of the body, it is better to rejoice in the soul—"the soul that You have placed within me is pure," and especially in the spark of the Creator that is clothed within the soul [31].

#### 11

And as he continues to explain in *Tanya* [29] that "this level is the level of *Yetziat Mitzrayim* (the essence of the festival of Pesach) of which it is said [32] that the people *fled*... because the evil in the souls of Israel was still in its strength in the left chamber... only their goal and desire was for their Divine soul to *depart* from the exile of the *Sitra Achra*, which is the impurity of Egypt, etc." (for while they were there, they were sunken in the forty-nine gates of impurity [33]).

That is to say: The calculations regarding the state and situation of the body have their time throughout the entire year. This is not the case on Pesach, "the time of our freedom," and in the words of our Sages [34], "freedom from the Angel of Death," "he is the *Yetzer Hara*" [35]—there is no place for calculations regarding the state and situation of the body, as is also emphasized in the eating of the *Pesach* while satiated, without considering the body.

**E.** It can be said that the interpretation of the *Pesach* being eaten while satiated is (not only regarding the satiety of the body, but) also regarding the satiety of the soul:

The eating of the *Pesach* is also when the soul is in a state and situation of "satiety," because the satiety of the soul is from the perspective of the level of *revelations*, whereas the essence of Pesach is the revelation of the *Atzmut* (the Essence). In the words of the Haggadah: "The King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, revealed Himself to them," "the Holy One, Blessed be He, *in His glory and His Essence*," which refers to the *Malchut* of *Ein Sof* (in His glory) and the *Atzmut* of *Ein Sof* (in His Essence) that is before the *Tzimtzum* (as explained by the Rebbe [Rashab] [36]). Therefore, even after the satiety of the soul from the perspective of the level of revelations, there exists the matter of the eating of the *Pesach*—the revelation of the *Atzmut*.

And based on this, we can explain the words of the Gemara [26], "A *kezayis* of *Pesach* and the *Hallel* bursts the roofs":

Through the eating of a *kezayis* of *Pesach* ("a *kezayis* of *Pesach*"), and in this time through the eating of a *kezayis* of *Matzah* (and likewise a *kezayis* of *Maror*)—one "takes," as it were, the *Essence and Being of Ein Sof, Blessed be He*, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, explains in the *maamar* [28] that "now, through the Torah and *mitzvot* that were given to us, even in the *Matzah* before midnight, there shines for us also a revelation from the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He" (a revelation of the *Atzmut*).

And from the perspective of the revelation of the *Atzmut* (which is through the "a *kezayis* of *Pesach*"), "the roofs burst" [37]—that even the *house*, the distant *makif* (encompassing light) that is not made according to the measure of man [38] [unlike a garment, a close *makif*, which is made according to the measure of man, and certainly not

#### 12

like food, which is internal [39]], which refers to the *makif* of *Yechidah* [40], cannot absorb and contain ("*einhalten*") this lofty revelation, to such an extent that the roofs burst because of the intensity of the revelation!

And from the perspective of the revelation of the *Atzmut*, the joy also comes about—the "*Hallel*"—in a manner that is above measurement and limitation (like the simple interpretation of "the *Hallel* bursts the roofs," "at the sound of the clamor of the multitude from the *Hallel*, it is as if the roofs are bursting" [37]).

**F.** And it should be added to the interpretation that the *Pesach* is eaten while satiated regarding the body and the soul together—that even when one is in a low state and situation where there is a need for a command and instruction not to consider the body (the satiety of the body), one can and must reach the most lofty state and situation where one does not consider the satiety of the soul.

The reason for this is because the essence of Pesach is *leaping* [41], not through a gradual process at all. Therefore, without looking at his state and situation, he can and must come to the most lofty level in *avodah*, even to the point of *mesiras nefesh*, as in the fulfillment of the command to take the lamb—the god of Egypt—for the *Korban Pesach*, slaughtering it and placing its blood on the lintel and on the two doorposts, without being affected by the danger involved [42].

Seemingly, one could make a calculation and argue: Is it possible that they demand of him an *avodah* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (the chain of progression)? If he is not relevant to the *avodah* of *Hishtalshelus*—then to an *avodah* above *Hishtalshelus*, all the more so?! The answer to this is that this is the advice of the *Yetzer Hara*, for this calculation is relevant for the entire year, but not for Pesach!

On Pesach [43], we open the door [44]. And since the Holy One, Blessed be He, commands the Children of Israel to open the door, certainly He Himself does so as well [according to the exposition of our Sages [45] on the verse [46], "He tells His words to Yaakov, His statutes and His judgments to Yisrael," "What He does, He tells Yisrael to do"]—that on Pesach, the Holy One, Blessed be He, opens [47] all the doors and all the gates [48] for every single one of the Children of Israel. And everyone, without considering his deeds

#### 13

during the previous year, can then reach the most lofty levels, by way of skipping and leaping, not through a gradual process at all.

**G.** And more deeply:

It was explained above (Section 5) that the revelation of Pesach is the revelation of the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*. From the perspective of the revelation of the *Atzmut*, one does not consider anything—neither the satiety of the body nor the satiety of the soul—because His Essence, may He be blessed, is above and beyond, to no end, and below and below, to no limit [49].

In simple terms: When a Jew knows that on Pesach he can connect with the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*, which is not limited by anything, above and beyond, to no end, and below and below, to no limit—then all matters and all calculations are nullified for him, and there is nothing physical or spiritual that can confuse him, because his entire desire is to connect with the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*!

And similar to what is said [50], "Whom have I in heaven, and with You I desire nothing on earth," and as the Tzemach Tzedek said regarding our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, who would say in these words: "*Ich vill zeh gornit, ich vill nit dein Gan Eden, ich vill nit dein Olam Haba, ich vill mer nit az dich alein*" (I do not want anything, I do not want Your Gan Eden, I do not want Your Olam Haba, I want only You Yourself)—that there is in this also an *instruction for all* [51] [for the intent of the story is not to glorify the greatness of the level of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe], that nothing, physical or spiritual, should confuse him, because he does not want anything, not this world and not the World to Come, not the lower *Gan Eden* and not the upper *Gan Eden*, but only the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*!

—"Worldly Jews" will be alarmed to hear such things, and will argue: A Jew who fulfills Torah and *mitzvot*, puts on *tefillin*, wears *tzitzit*, etc., and also innovates novel ideas in Torah—what more can they demand of him?!... But Chassidim, who have merited to be connected to the Rebbe, and through him to all our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*, up to our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, to Moshe Rabbeinu, and to the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*—nothing matters to them, except for the connection with the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*!...

**H.** The truth is that even when he is in a state and situation of "Whom have I in heaven, and with You I desire nothing on earth," the Holy One, Blessed be He, desires the good of a Jew, in this world and in the World to Come,

#### 14

in the lower *Gan Eden* and in the upper *Gan Eden*, and He bestows upon him all good, upper *Gan Eden* and lower *Gan Eden*, the World to Come and this world, children, life, and abundant sustenance, below ten *tefachim*,

— [The Rebbe turned to those present, and to many of them he gave personal blessings for what they needed, and afterward continued:] —

However, the Jew, for his part, must not *make his mesiras nefesh conditional* upon the Holy One, Blessed be He, giving him everything he needs. That is to say, he is prepared not to desire anything other than Him, may He be blessed, "Whom have I in heaven, and with You I desire nothing on earth," *on the condition* that for this, the Holy One, Blessed be He, will give him upper *Gan Eden* and lower *Gan Eden*, the World to Come and this world...

He, for his part, must *devote himself completely* ("*avekgeben zich ingantzen*"), without any condition, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, for His part, will bestow upon him *automatically* everything he needs.

**I.** Now, although from the perspective of the revelation of the *Atzmut* on Pesach, one should not consider the state and situation of the body, as is emphasized in *Yetziat Mitzrayim* of which it is said, "because the people fled," because the evil remained in its strength, etc. (as above, Section 4), nevertheless, the ultimate intent is that the *avodah* should be with the body specifically, through the refining and purification of the body, "taking along" ("*mit-nemen*") the body as well. The perfection of this will be in the time to come, "when Hashem will remove [52] the spirit of impurity from the earth." Therefore, the future redemption will not be in the manner of "the people fled," but as it is said [53], "For you shall not go out in haste, nor shall you go in flight" (as explained in *Tanya* [29]).

It can be said that something similar to this is the case on an *Erev Pesach* that falls on Shabbos—that then it is not critical that the *Pesach* be eaten while satiated, but the eating of the *Pesach* can be when one has an appetite:

The eating of Shabbos is different from the eating of weekdays—that even the hunger that comes from the body is in a more lofty manner, for it is not for the sake of bodily pleasure alone, but it is a matter of *mitzvah*, *Oneg Shabbos* [54].

— The Rebbe, my father-in-law, writes in one of his letters [55] that the reason for the body's hunger for physical food is the soul's hunger for the Divine spark clothed within the physical food. And as a result of the soul's hunger for the Divine spark, the body's hunger for physical food is created, so that through the eating of the food, the soul may refine the Divine spark clothed within it —

And based on this, we can explain the reason why on an *Erev Pesach* that falls on Shabbos, the eating of the *Pesach* can be with an appetite (and it is not critical that the *Pesach* be eaten while satiated)—that then

#### 15

one can also include the body in the eating of the *Pesach* ("*m'nempt-mit oich dem guf*"), which is elevated to a more lofty state and situation, similar and analogous to the perfection of the refining and purification of the body in the future redemption.

**J.** The conclusion from all that has been said above is that this night—the night of Pesach that falls on *Motzaei Shabbos*, on which we say "and we shall eat there of the *pesachim* and of the *zevachim*," because it is not critical that the *Pesach* be eaten while satiated, in which is hinted something similar and analogous to the perfection of the refining of the body in the future to come (as explained above at length)—is most capable of illuminating the revelations of the time to come.

(And the Rebbe concluded:) May the Holy One, Blessed be He, grant that speedily in our days and in our time, the Rebbe will lead us toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

The last day of Pesach is drawing near, which is, in the words of the Rebbe [56], the day of Moshiach ("*Moshiach's tog*"), on which we read the *Haftorah*, "And a shoot shall spring forth from the stem of Yishai, etc." [57].

And may it be His will that in the very near days this prophecy will be fulfilled, and the Rebbe—who is "from the stem of Yishai," from the kingdom of the House of David [58]—will redeem us from the spiritual exile and from the physical exile, and lead us to the true and complete redemption.

[The Rebbe returned to his room, and the entire congregation continued to dance with great joy.]

***

**K.** [After some time, the Rebbe entered the *Beis Medrash* with a Pesach Haggadah, sat in his place, and said:]

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related [59] that his father, the Rebbe [Rashab], used to begin the second Seder at the ninth hour and finish it several hours after midnight.

And since "a person is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher,"

— This statement is brought in several places [60], and its source is in the Mishnah in Tractate

#### 16

Eduyot [61]: "Hillel says: A full *hin* of drawn water invalidates the *mikveh*, but a person is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher." And one of the interpretations of this [62] is that because "a person is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher," Hillel was precise in his language to say "*a full* *hin*" (even though it is sufficient to say "*a hin* of water, etc."), because in this language ("*a full* *hin*") he heard from his teachers, Shemayah and Avtalyon, who "were converts [63], and there remained in their speech the stammering of the language of the idolaters, and they would say *in* instead of *hin*." Therefore, they had to add "*a full* *hin* of water, etc.," and they could not say "*a hin* of water, etc.," so that it would not sound like "*in* (there is no) water drawn invalidates the *mikveh*"—the opposite of the *halachah*.

And if these things are said regarding the language of his teacher which is from the perspective of a *deficiency* (the matter of conversion), that even then "a person is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher," regarding the language of his teacher which is from the perspective of *excellence and perfection*, all the more so that "a person is obligated to speak in the language of his teacher"—

All the students, who are connected and belong to the Rebbe, must conduct themselves according to the order of the Rebbe's conduct.

Even those who have some connection at least to the Rebbe, that is to say, those who merited that the Rebbe brought them in to him for *Yechidut*, and merited to hear from the Rebbe a few words ("*etleche verter*"), whether in spiritual matters or in physical matters,

— And in truth, it makes no difference if the things they heard from the Rebbe are in spiritual matters or in physical matters. For the *listeners* there is a difference—that *physicality* matters to them *more* than spirituality, for although according to intellect it is understood that spirituality should matter more than physicality, nevertheless, we see tangibly that physicality matters more than spirituality. And not only that, but there is a need for the exertion of the soul and the exertion of the flesh to effect that spirituality should matter to him, and if only it would matter not only in the intellect in the head but also in the emotions in the heart. But for the *Rebbe*—physicality and spirituality are exactly the same. And in every matter (spiritual or physical) that the Rebbe would answer in *Yechidut*, the words were (not from the lips outward, Heaven forbid, but) *from the inwardness of his soul*. Thus, through hearing the words of the Rebbe (in any matter whatsoever), they connected with the inwardness of the Rebbe's soul —

#### 17

the relationship of each one of them to the Rebbe becomes such that the Rebbe is "*his* teacher," and consequently, the obligation "to speak in the language of his teacher" applies to him (and especially "the language of his teacher" which is from the perspective of excellence and perfection, as above), to conduct himself according to the order of the Rebbe's conduct.

And in our case, regarding the conducting of the second Seder—that one must begin at the ninth hour and finish several hours after midnight.

**L.** At the first Seder, the Rebbe [Rashab] would be precise to eat the *Afikoman* before midnight, but at the second Seder, he would not be precise about this, and he would eat the *Afikoman* after midnight [59]. And so did the Rebbe, my father-in-law, conduct himself. And since the Rebbe, my father-in-law, and the Rebbe [Rashab] conducted themselves in this way, it is understood that so did our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*, before them.

— According to the *Nigleh* (revealed Torah), in the *Shulchan Aruch* [64], we do not find a reason to differentiate in the time of eating the *Afikoman* between the first Seder and the second Seder. But it is understood and also simple that since our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*, conducted themselves in this way, certainly they had a reason for this, according to the inwardness of the matters.

And besides the inward reasons for this, there is also the simple reason—that at the second Seder, they would customarily extend the explanation of the Haggadah [59], and consequently, the eating of the *Afikoman* would be delayed until after midnight.

**M.** The explanations of our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*, on the Haggadah—were only on the first half of the Haggadah, whereas on the second half of the Haggadah, from *Hallel* until the end of the Haggadah, they would not say explanations.

The explanations on the first half of the Haggadah were said on specific passages, sometimes on these passages, and sometimes on other passages.

And it is understood that this is not because in that year they had something to say ("*zei hoben gehat vos tzu zogen*") only on these passages, and in another year they had something to say only on other passages,

— There were years in which they also customarily repeated things they had already said in previous years —

but rather, *for reasons known to them*, they had to explain in these years these passages and in other years other passages.

\*

#### 18

**N.** "*The son asks*":

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, said [65] that the fact that the "*son* asks," specifically a *young* son (a child)—arouses above the matter of "Yisrael is a youth and I love him" [66].

And the matter of this [67]:

We see tangibly that the love for a young son is greater—an essential love, above reason and knowledge, for the love for an older son can be because of his virtues and talents and the like, whereas the love for a young son is not because of his virtues and talents, but rather, an essential love that is above reason and knowledge.

And analogous to this in the *Nimshal* (the concept being explained), regarding the Holy One, Blessed be He, and the Children of Israel—that there is a special virtue in a young son [68],

[not only young in the simple sense, according to the number of years recorded in the "passport" (an official document in which the number of years is noted), but, as the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law [69], that it is possible that in the number of his years he is old, but since he did not utilize his years for matters of Torah and *mitzvot* (but for other matters), he remained young. And consequently, it is possible to have a Jew with a white beard who remained a young child],

in whom specifically is revealed the matter of "Yisrael is a youth and I love him," that the love is not because of his virtues and talents, but an essential love.

And from this essential love comes the revelation of the *Atzmut*—"The King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, revealed Himself to them in His glory and His Essence," which revelation that was in Egypt after midnight, shines for us now in the *Matzah* before midnight (as above, Section 5).

**O.** "*The son asks 'Mah' (What)*":

In addition to the simple interpretation that "asks" (*sho'el*) is from the language of a question and difficulty, there is also the interpretation that "asks" (*sho'el*) is from the language of a *request*, similar to what is said [70], "And a woman shall ask (*vesha'alah*) of her neighbor," which means (not from the language of a question and difficulty, but) from the language of a request [71].

#### 19

And based on this, we can interpret "The son *asks 'Mah'* (What)"—that he asks and requests and arouses the revelation and the *hemshech* (drawing down) of the Name *Mah* [72].

And in this itself—not only the level of "What is his name," but also the level of "What is His name" [73].

**P.** And following this comes the question and the answer—"*What is different this night from all other nights*... *We were slaves to Pharaoh in Egypt, and Hashem our G-d took us out from there, etc.*":

Since throughout the entire year there are calculations, etc., and a person knows in his soul his state and situation ("*vau er halt*")—the question is asked: "What is different this night from all other nights," that on this night, the night of Pesach, there are no calculations, and for every single one of the Children of Israel, without looking at his state and situation, the revelation of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, in His glory and His Essence, comes about?!

And the answer to this—"We were slaves to Pharaoh in Egypt, and Hashem our G-d took us out from there, etc."—is that this is not a new thing, but it has already been for all time:

While they were in Egypt, the Children of Israel were sunken in the forty-nine gates of impurity [74], and to such an extent that the possibility of taking them out from there could not be except by the Holy One, Blessed be He, in His glory and His Essence, in the words of the Haggadah: "And Hashem took us out from Egypt, not by an angel and not by a seraph and not by a messenger, but the Holy One, Blessed be He, in His glory and His Essence." And the reason for this—as explained in the writings of the AriZal [75], "because the impurity of Egypt was so strong that if an angel had descended, he would, Heaven forbid, have been sunken into the *kelipah*," that is to say, that an angel or a seraph, not only would they not have succeeded in taking the Children of Israel out of Egypt, but on the contrary, they themselves would have been sunken there!

And despite their being in such a low state—"The King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, revealed Himself to them (in His glory and His Essence, as mentioned, *Malchut* of *Ein Sof* and the Essence and Being of *Ein Sof, Blessed be He*) and redeemed them," "from slavery to freedom... from darkness to a great light and from servitude to redemption."

And likewise "this night": without looking at his state and situation—for every single one of the Children of Israel, the revelation of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, comes about to take him out from slavery to freedom and from servitude to redemption.

#### 20

**Q.** "*And even if we are all wise, we are all understanding, we are all knowledgeable in the Torah, it is a mitzvah upon us to tell of the exodus from Egypt.* And proof of the matter—"*It happened that Rabbi Eliezer and Rabbi Yehoshua... were reclining... and were telling of the exodus from Egypt all that night*":

The author of the Haggadah is precise: "And even... we are all *knowledgeable* in the Torah" (and not only "learning the Torah")—that even one who has already fulfilled the *mitzvah* of knowledge of Torah [as is known [76] that in the study of Torah there are two *mitzvot*: (a) learning Torah, (b) knowledge of Torah], who knows the entire Torah,

— as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains in the *Laws of Torah Study* [77] that "there is no end or limit to the depth of the reasons for the *halachot* and the *pilpul* in their reasons and their expositions, etc.," but "the *halachot* revealed to us and to our children have an end and a limit," and consequently, it is possible to fulfill the *mitzvah* of learning and knowing the entire Torah, "to learn once in order the entire Talmud Bavli and Yerushalmi and Mechilta and Sifra and Sifrei and Toseftot and all the Midrashim, etc."—

And consequently, he also knows all the details of the matters of the exodus from Egypt—nevertheless, it is a *mitzvah* upon him to tell of the exodus from Egypt.

And seemingly: A Jew who knows the entire Torah—it would be better for him to utilize the time to innovate novel ideas in Torah, to resolve difficulties and refute answers, and instead of this, they command him to recline with all the Children of Israel equally and tell of the exodus from Egypt?!...

He, the true "innovator in Torah" ("*der emeser mechadesh b'Torah*"), who every morning recites the blessing of the Torah with a special delight ("*mit gor an ander geshmak*"), thinking to himself that the words of our Sages [78] regarding "what a veteran student is destined to innovate" (that "it was said to Moshe at Sinai") are certainly directed *to him*, and "to whom [79] would the King desire to do honor more than to him"... And nevertheless, they command him to recline together with everyone and tell of the exodus from Egypt—even though among all those reclining there is not even one who is capable of appreciating his "Torah innovations"!... At the very least, they should have seated him in a gathering where there are those who can appreciate the greatness of the level of his innovations, and before them he could say his innovations!

And nevertheless, they tell him to recline with everyone equally, and to tell of the exodus from Egypt simply: to say "We were slaves to Pharaoh in Egypt," and to say—without

#### 21

being ashamed...—"In the beginning our ancestors were idolaters" (for since this is the reality, one must say it), and the main thing, "and now the Place has brought us near to His service"—"*and now*" specifically [although seemingly it would be more appropriate to say "*and afterward* He brought us near, etc.," since it is speaking about the time of Avraham Avinu [80]]—for, when he contemplates his state and situation, he will realize *that in the moment before*, he himself was in the level of an "idolater" in a subtle way, so that he can say "*and now* the Place has brought us near to His service."

And the explanation of this:

The study of Torah must be *with absolute nullification*, as our Sages said [81], "Just as there it was with awe and fear and trembling and quaking, so too here it must be with awe and fear and trembling and quaking." And our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains [82]—"that seemingly this comparison is not understood, 'Just as there... so too here, etc.,' for at the Standing at Mount Sinai and all the people see the sounds and face-to-face Hashem spoke, whereas in the study of Torah of every person when he learns by himself"—that "also the study of Torah in every person and at every time is the word of Hashem that was said to Moshe at Sinai," and as our Sages said [83], "Whoever reads and learns, the Holy One, Blessed be He, reads and learns opposite him," and as is emphasized also in the text of the blessing of the Torah: "Giver of the Torah" in the present tense [84], "and through this, awe and fear will fall upon him as if he received it today from Mount Sinai."

And as long as he has not effected upon himself that the study of Torah should be with absolute nullification, "with awe and fear and trembling and quaking"—he is in the level of an "idolater" in a subtle way.

And regarding our matter:

When he contemplates properly the matter of "Giver of the Torah" in the present tense, that the Giving of the Torah is on this

## With the help of Hashem. 2nd Day of Pesach, 5711

#### 27

– After Mincha –

Unedited

[Several of Anash approached the Rebbe and requested that he say a Maamar, and he said:]

The essence of the festival of Pesach is a drawing down of light from Above to below[1](#_ftn122). However, on the second day of Pesach, the avodah of Sefiras HaOmer begins[2](#_ftn123), the essence of which is an elevation from below to Above[1](#_ftn122). Consequently, the avodah must be performed through one’s own strength (“one must do it oneself”).

## B’s”d. R”D Tuesday, 18 Nissan*, 2nd Day of Chol HaMoed Pesach, 5711

#### 28

– Following Mincha prayers –

Unedited

The Rebbe instructed that a farbrengen be held, and said that in honor of the farbrengen, he would provide a transcript of a sicha by the Rebbe Rayatz (which had not yet been published).

Someone began collecting money for wine, and the Rebbe said that they should not take money from the bochurim, because from them one must demand ruchniyus and not gashmiyus; and if one demands gashmiyus from them, it is liable to cause a deficiency in their demand for ruchniyus[1](#_ftn124).

The Rebbe provided the money for the wine and gave a transcript of a sicha by the Rebbe Rayatz[2](#_ftn125) to be studied at the farbrengen.

The next morning, after davening, when they returned the aforementioned transcript, the Rebbe said that if they were to hold a farbrengen again today, he would provide another transcript of a sicha by the Rebbe Rayatz (and later he provided money for wine and a transcript of a sicha[3](#_ftn126)).

Toward Mincha time, the Rebbe entered the beis medrash in the middle of the farbrengen and said—with a smile—that it is possible to delay the Mincha prayer, or the farbrengen...

## B’s”D. Sicha of Shevi’i Shel Pesach, 5711

#### 29

– After Mincha –

(Unedited)

Shevi’i[1](#_ftn127) Shel Pesach is the day of Moshe Rabbeinu, as emphasized in the day’s Torah reading: “Then *Moshe* sang”[2](#_ftn128) [and furthermore, the song of Bnei Yisrael is also included in the song of Moshe, which is why it says “*Moshe* and the children of Israel *sang*” in the singular form[3](#_ftn129), because of the inclusion of Bnei Yisrael within the level of Moshe]. And Acharon Shel Pesach is the day of Moshiach, as emphasized in the day’s Haftorah (following the introduction, “This very day he will halt at Nov, etc.”[4](#_ftn130)) regarding the matter of Moshiach: “And there shall come forth a shoot out of the stock of Yishai, etc.”[5](#_ftn131).

Moshe and Moshiach are connected to one another; and furthermore, “The first redeemer (Moshe) *is* the final redeemer” (Moshiach)[6](#_ftn132). And even though Moshe is from the tribe of Levi, and Moshiach is from the tribe of Yehudah[7](#_ftn133), this distinction is only on the exterior; but in their interiority, they are connected to one another, as stated: “The first redeemer is the final redeemer.”

And in any case—both of them (Moshe and Moshiach) are “sheine Yidden”...

And as we stand in the moments between the day of Moshe Rabbeinu and the day of Moshiach, we must strive to utilize this time as is fitting.

## Acharon Shel Pesach, 5711

#### 30

(Unedited transcript)

**"And He shall wave His hand over the river with the strength of His spirit, and He shall strike it into seven streams"**[1](#_ftn134) — this verse refers to Mashiach, as it is written immediately prior: "And there shall come forth a shoot out of the stock of Yishai, and a twig shall grow forth out of his roots. And the spirit of Hashem shall rest upon him, the spirit of wisdom and understanding, the spirit of counsel and might, the spirit of knowledge and the fear of Hashem. And he shall be animated by the fear of Hashem; he shall not judge after the sight of his eyes, neither shall he decide after the hearing of his ears. But with righteousness shall he judge the poor," etc.

We must understand the meaning of "he shall be animated by the fear of Hashem" (*ve-haricho b'yiras Hashem*), regarding which our Sages said[3](#_ftn136) that he "smells and judges" (*morach v'dain*). On the face of it, this is difficult to understand: the matter of judgment is the clarification of a thing—what does this have to do with the sense of smell? Furthermore, we must understand why this is the primary excellence of Mashiach, such that when they needed to test Mashiach, they checked whether he "smells and judges." This implies that all the excellences of "the spirit of wisdom and understanding, counsel and might, knowledge and the fear of Hashem" are not yet sufficient; rather, the primary excellence is "he shall be animated by the fear of Hashem," that he "smells and judges." For this reason, regarding all the other excellences of Mashiach—"the spirit of wisdom and understanding, counsel and might, knowledge and the fear of Hashem"—only the positive is stated. But regarding "he shall be animated by the fear of Hashem," the negative is also stated: "he shall not judge after the sight of his eyes, neither shall he decide after the hearing of his ears." This proves that the primary excellence of Mashiach lies in this matter.

b) **The explanation of this matter**[4](#_ftn137): Our Sages said[5](#_ftn138), "What is something that the soul derives pleasure from, but the body does not? You must say, this is scent." This is the difference between eating and drinking versus scent: eating and drinking are things that the body derives pleasure from, whereas scent is something that the soul derives pleasure from. Therefore, they differ in the manner of their operation in binding the soul to the body. The soul, in its essential being, is distant from the body, and its binding to the body is only through the "power that performs wonders,"[6](#_ftn139) which connects spirituality and physicality. Therefore, there can sometimes be weakness or concealment in this binding. The function of eating and drinking is to strengthen the binding of the soul to the body. As is known, the interpretation[7](#_ftn140) of the verse[8](#_ftn141)

#### 31

"That man does not live by bread alone, but by everything that proceeds out of the mouth of Hashem does man live," is that the intent is the "proceeding out of the mouth of Hashem" that is within the bread—namely, the Divine spark within the bread—which gives life to the person. Since in its root it is in the category of *Ohr Pnimi* (internal light), it has the power to strengthen the binding of the soul to the body in the category of internal vitality. However, when the soul departs from the body, such as in a faint, Heaven forbid, then eating and drinking are of no avail; only scent is effective, for it has the power to draw forth the essence of the soul, since the root of scent is from the category of *Ohr Makif* (surrounding light). This is also the reason why scent does not cause any deficiency in the essence of the thing; therefore, "sound, sight, and scent" do not involve the prohibition of *me'ilah* (misappropriation of consecrated property),[9](#_ftn142) because they are merely a category of *Ohr Makif*. Because it is *Ohr Makif*, it has the power to reach and draw from the essence of the soul. Therefore, the law is that if someone is buried under a collapsed building, they must check him up to his nose.[10](#_ftn143) *Rabbeinu Bachya* provides the reason for this:[11](#_ftn144) just as the drawing of the soul into the body is through the nose, as it is written,[11](#_ftn144) "And He breathed into his nostrils the soul of life," so too its departure is through the nose. Therefore, even if they checked all the limbs, and even the heart, and found no vitality in them, this is not sufficient; one must check up to the nose. For when there is vitality in the nose—which is the essential vitality—then it is possible to draw it forth into revelation through various actions.

This is also why the nose is the "gate of the *mochin*" (intellects),[12](#_ftn145) by which is meant the interiority of the *mochin*. For it is taught that the nose is specifically the gate of the *mochin*, whereas the gate of the heart is the mouth, which is the matter of speech. The revelation of the *midos* (emotional attributes) is through speech, and the body and essence of speech have their root in the "breath of the heart." Seemingly, speech is also the gate of the *mochin*, for the revelation of intellect is through speech. However, the revelation that comes through speech is the category of the *exteriority* of the *mochin*—which is intellect—because the influence of intellect is only an external influence. Therefore, the influence of intellect is only for one who is a "possessor of intellect" by his own nature; but for one who is not a possessor of intellect, the influence of intellect will not help him, because the influence of intellect does not innovate anything, being merely an external influence. When we say the nose is the gate of the *mochin*, the intent is the *interiority* of the *mochin*.

**Now**[13](#_ftn146), in the nose itself there are two levels, as it is stated in *Idra Rabba*:[14](#_ftn147) the nose has two nostrils, the right nostril and the left nostril. "From one nostril (the right) comes life,"

#### 32

"and from one nostril (the left) comes the life of life." It is explained that in the right nostril, the category of *Makif* of *Ohr Yashar* (direct light) is drawn, which reaches the level of "life," the category of the exteriority of *Atik*. In the left nostril, the category of *Makif* of *Ohr Chozer* (returning light) is drawn, which reaches the level of "life of life," the category of the interiority of *Atik*. Its meaning in the *avodah* of man: the *Makif* of *Ohr Yashar* is to draw the revelation of *Elokus* into physicality, and this reaches the level of "life." The *Makif* of *Ohr Chozer* is to make the physical world a vessel for *Elokus*, and this reaches the level of "life of life."

An analogy for this in the physical: in a regular faint, a simple scent is effective. But in an extremely severe faint, a simple scent is not effective; rather, one needs a scent from something that has sharpness and pungency—a sharp thing—which has the power to restore the soul even from an extremely severe faint, because it reaches deeper into the soul. So it is also in *avodah*: when the *avodah* is in the path of *Ohr Yashar*, where there are not so many concealments and hides, one reaches the level of "life," the *Makif* of vitality, the category of *re'uta d'liba* (the desire of the heart). Although it is above intellect and emotion, it is connected with intellect and emotion, as the intellect is a vessel for the *re'uta d'liba*. It is specifically when the *avodah* is in the path of *Ohr Chozer*—when there are concealments and hides, etc.—that one reaches the level of "life of life," the category of the interiority of *Atik*.

**Now**, the drawing forth from the category of the interiority of *Atik* also acts upon the matter of intellect, so that it occurs in an entirely different manner; this is the matter of the "interiority of *Abba* [within] the interiority of *Atik*."[15](#_ftn148) The matter is as follows:[16](#_ftn149) the drawing forth of intellect comes from the power of the *maskil* (the one who intellectualizes). However, this drawing is not necessarily guaranteed, as we see that sometimes intellect is not drawn forth from the power of the *maskil*. The advice for this is the matter of *ratzon* (will), as our Sages said,[17](#_ftn150) "A person should always study in a place where his heart desires," for the will draws the power of the *maskil* to come into revelation. Yet sometimes, due to various reasons—side reasons or internal reasons (such as *timtum ha-moach*, the clogging of the mind)—even the will does not help to bring about the drawing of intellect. The advice for this is engaging in Torah with *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), where one forces oneself and surrenders oneself with one's entire essence to the study, and through this, a revelation of intellect occurs. However, the root of this revelation is above the power of the *maskil*; it is the category of "the air above the membrane that covers the brain,"[18](#_ftn151) the category of the "brain of *Atik*," for "the *Da'as* of *Atik* shines light into this air,"[19](#_ftn152) which pierces the membrane and draws from the category of *Chochmah Stima'ah* (the Hidden Wisdom), through which the revelation of intellect occurs in a manner that is

#### 33

exalted to the highest degree. This is the matter of the "interiority of *Abba* [within] the interiority of *Atik*," for from the interiority of *Atik*, the existence of intellect must necessarily be drawn forth. This intellect that is drawn forth by the interiority of *Atik* is above all limitation. That is, the intellect drawn from the power of the *maskil* through the will is limited according to the will. And the intellect drawn from the exteriority of *taanug* (delight)—which is connected with will—is limited according to the measure of perfection in the intellect that exists in the exteriority of *taanug*. But when the study is by way of *kabbalas ol*, which draws from the interiority of *taanug*, then the intellect is above all limitation; although it is drawn into the existence of revealed intellect, it contains no limitation.

c) **Based on this, we can understand** that the primary excellence of Mashiach is in the matter of scent—that he "smells and judges"—which is due to the excellence of the matter of scent that reaches the *etzem* (essence), the category of the interiority of *Atik*. And it is in such a way that from there, it is drawn also into *Chochmah* and revealed intellect. This is the matter of "smelling and judging": that although it is a matter of judgment, nevertheless, "he shall not judge after the sight of his eyes, neither shall he decide after the hearing of his ears." That is, he will not judge according to understanding and comprehension, nor according to intellectualization, and not even according to the "sight" of *Chochmah*; rather, he "smells and judges," where the judgment is according to the matter of scent that reaches the *etzem*, and from there it is drawn also into *Chochmah* and down to revealed intellect.

**This is also the content** of the words of the Rebbe Rayatz in his *sicha*[20](#_ftn153) explaining what is said regarding Mashiach, "He shall be animated by the fear of Hashem; he shall not judge after the sight of his eyes, neither shall he decide after the hearing of his ears." The judgment of Mashiach will be such that he will know the reasons that brought the other person to the state in which he is found. As the saying goes,[21](#_ftn154) "Do not judge your fellow until you reach his place." A person himself recognizes and knows the reasons that brought him to his state, and so it must be also in the judgment of others: one must know the reasons that brought him to this state. That is, in his essence he is good, and the fact that he is in an undesirable state is only due to side reasons. By way of introduction: some think that a *sicha* is merely a discourse of *drush* (homiletics). But in truth, the *sichos* of *talmidei chachamim* require study, as our Sages expounded[22](#_ftn155) from the verse,[23](#_ftn156) "And its leaf shall not wither." How much more so, *kal v'chomer*, the *sicha* of a Rebbe, the *Nasi* and leader of the generation (for which the aforementioned exposition of our Sages is not even needed), whose *sicha* is founded upon the depths of Kabbalah. This is according to what we explained above regarding the excellence of the matter of scent that reaches the *etzem*. In such a manner will be the judgment of Mashiach: he will see the essence of the person, that in his essence he is good, etc. This is also understood according to

#### 34

what is explained elsewhere[24](#_ftn157) regarding what Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai said,[25](#_ftn158) "I do not know by which path they are leading me," even though he did not leave out any small or large matter, etc.[26](#_ftn159) This is because the revealed powers do not indicate the essence; it is possible that his revealed powers are as they should be, and yet the essence is in the depths of the *kelipos*. Proof of this is from Yochanan the High Priest, who served in the High Priesthood for eighty years and in the end became a *Tzadoki* (Sadducee).[27](#_ftn160) The fact that he served in the High Priesthood for eighty years proves that he was a *tzaddik*, for a High Priest who was not as he should be and entered the Holy of Holies on Yom Kippur would not survive the year.[28](#_ftn161) And yet, since his essence was in the depths of the *kelipos*, over time this was drawn also into the revealed powers, until in the end he became a *Tzadoki*. From this it is proven that the revealed powers do not indicate the essence. Therefore, out of his humility, Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai was afraid regarding his own essence, etc. From this it is understood also to the contrary: that Mashiach will not judge according to the external state, etc., but rather according to the essence, which is the matter of "smelling and judging."

d) **This is also what is meant by** "And He shall wave His hand over the river with the strength of His spirit, and He shall strike it into seven streams." The matter is as follows: it is known[29](#_ftn162) that just as the splitting of the Red Sea was a preparation for the Giving of the Torah, so too the splitting of the river in the future is a preparation for the revelation of the interiority of the Torah by Mashiach. As the Rebbe Rayatz explains in the *maamar* in the *Kuntres Chag HaPesach*,[30](#_ftn163) the matter of the splitting of the Red Sea was not for the sake of walking through the desert—for on the same side they went down into the sea, on that same side they came up from the sea[31](#_ftn164)—rather, the splitting of the Red Sea is a preparation for the Giving of the Torah. Regarding the Giving of the Torah, it is stated in the *Midrash*:[32](#_ftn165) "A parable of a king who decreed and said: 'The people of Rome shall not go down to Syria, and the people of Syria shall not go up to Rome,' etc." At the Giving of the Torah, He annulled the decree and said that the upper ones shall descend to the lower ones, and the lower ones shall ascend to the upper ones. This is the innovation in the fulfillment of *mitzvos* after the Giving of the Torah. Although even before the Giving of the Torah there was the matter of fulfilling *mitzvos* by the Patriarchs through physical things—such as the hospitality of Abraham our Patriarch, the digging of the wells by Isaac, and the work of the rods by Jacob, which was done with physical things—nevertheless, the effect of the *mitzvah* did not remain in the physical thing,

#### 35

and the effect of the *mitzvah* was only above.[33](#_ftn166) The innovation of the Giving of the Torah is that through the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, a change is made in the physical thing. Furthermore, the drawing of holiness into the physical thing occurs already when it is prepared to perform the *mitzvah* with it, even before the *mitzvah* is performed with it (as explained in *Shaarei Orah* by the Mitteler Rebbe in the *maamar* beginning "They shall bring royal apparel").[34](#_ftn167) The preparation for this is through the matter of the splitting of the Red Sea, where a splitting was made in the sea—the category of *Malchus* of *Atzilus*—[35](#_ftn168) through which a connection was made between *Atzilus* and *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*. In this itself there are two opinions [and in truth there is no dispute between the two opinions, but both are true, as there are two matters],[36](#_ftn169) the opinion of the *AriZal*[37](#_ftn170) that the splitting of the Red Sea is the matter of drawing *Atzilus* into *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, and the opinion of the *Zohar*[38](#_ftn171) that the splitting of the Red Sea is the matter of elevating *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* to *Atzilus*. It can be said that this is analogous to the difference between the two types of *avodah*: whether "all is *Elokus*" or "everything is *Elokus*,"[39](#_ftn172) as is known that this is the difference between the Maggid and the Alter Rebbe.[40](#_ftn173) And higher still, the matter of the splitting of the Red Sea is not only the splitting in *Malchus* of *Atzilus*, which is the intermediary connecting *Atzilus* to *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, but also the splitting in *Keter*, which is the intermediary between *Atzilus* and the worlds above *Atzilus* (this is the matter of the two categories in *Keter*, *Atik* and *Arich*, the lower aspect of the higher and the higher aspect of the lower). And higher yet, the matter of the splitting of the Red Sea is the splitting in the category of *Malchus* of *Ein Sof*, which is the intermediary between the light before the *Tzimtzum* and the *Seder Hishtalshelus* (order of progression) after the *Tzimtzum*. The matter of the splitting is that there should be the connection of before the *Tzimtzum* and after the *Tzimtzum*.

**Now**, just as in the Exodus from Egypt there needed to be the matter of the splitting of the Red Sea as a preparation for the revealed Giving of the Torah, so too in the future redemption, of which it is said,[43](#_ftn176) "As in the days of your coming out of the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders," before the revelation of the interiority of the Torah by Mashiach,

#### 36

there must be the matter of the splitting of the river. Here too there are two methods:[44](#_ftn177) whether the matter of the splitting of the river is in such a way that the river becomes dry land—which is the matter of drawing *Elokus* downwards—or that the river remains but is split, which is the matter of elevating the lower. Among the differences between the splitting of the Red Sea and the splitting of the river: the splitting of the Red Sea in the Exodus from Egypt was through a staff,[45](#_ftn178) whereas the splitting of the river in the future will be by "hand,"[46](#_ftn179) as it is written, "And He shall wave His hand over the river," etc. For, at the beginning of the *avodah* of making the physical a vessel for *Elokus*, the splitting had to be specifically by a staff, as is also understood from the statement of our Sages[47](#_ftn180) on the verse,[48](#_ftn181) "Take your staff": "Just as it is the way of a dog to be struck with a staff, so too," etc. Not so in the future to come, when there will be the conclusion and completion of the *avodah*; then there will be no need for the matter of the splitting of the river to be by a staff, but rather, "And He shall wave His hand over the river," and through this will be the elevation of the physical to become a vessel for *Elokus*, even to the point where it will be possible to see the essence of *Elokus*. In such a manner will also be the Torah study by Mashiach, who will teach Torah to the entire people;[49](#_ftn182) seemingly, how will he be able to teach all of Israel? But the matter is[50](#_ftn183) that the study that Mashiach will teach all of Israel will be in a manner of seeing the essence, which in this time we have no conception of, for all our comprehension is only in the existence of the thing but not in the essence. With the coming of Mashiach, the matter of seeing the essence will be innovated.

e) **With this, we can also understand**[51](#_ftn184) what our Sages said, "Mashiach comes to bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*."[52](#_ftn185) Seemingly, what is the matter of *teshuvah* in *tzaddikim*? But the matter is, as is known,[53](#_ftn186) that the matter of *teshuvah* is not specifically for sin and transgression, but rather the matter of *teshuvah* is that there should be a departure from one's previous standing and state, through not being satisfied with one's previous state. This matter applies also to *tzaddikim*, for whom the matter of sin and transgression does not apply, for they too can depart from their previous state, similar to the statement of our Sages,[54](#_ftn187) "If he was accustomed to study one chapter, he should study two chapters," etc. From this it is understood also regarding the matter of Mashiach: since through him there will be the matter of seeing the essence, and there will be "smelling

#### 37

and judging," which is the matter of the revelation of the *Etzem* (Essence) and *Mahus* (Being) of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, then regarding the *Etzem*, "Even in His angels He puts no trust."[55](#_ftn188) Therefore, there will then be the matter of *teshuvah* in *tzaddikim*, that there will be for them a departure from their previous standing and state due to the revelation of the *Etzem*, that "even in His angels He puts no trust." This is also what is written,[56](#_ftn189) "And the man Moses was very humble, more than any man who was upon the face of the earth." It is explained[57](#_ftn190) that Moses saw the generation of the "heels of Mashiach," who would not be connected to understanding and comprehension, and there would then be concealments and hides, and there would be double and redoubled darkness, and yet they would fulfill *mitzvos* with *mesiras nefesh* (self-sacrifice). That is, not only would the concealments not interfere with their *avodah*, but furthermore, from the concealments and hides themselves, they would have exertion and added strength. This matter brought about *bitul* (self-nullification) in Moses. It can be said by way of possibility in the interpretation of these words, that Moses felt the exaltation of Mashiach, which is the matter of the revelation of the *Etzem* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, through which "he comes to bring the *tzaddikim* to *teshuvah*," and this matter also brought about in Moses the movement of *teshuvah*, etc.[58](#_ftn191)

f) **This is also what is written,[59](#_ftn192)** "I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me; let Your anger turn away and comfort me." The intent is that there should be gratitude for the very fact that "You were angry with me." The matter is as we explained above regarding the excellence of the *avodah* of *Ohr Chozer*, that specifically through the concealments and hides one reaches higher, etc. Therefore, "I will thank You, Hashem," for this, that "You were angry with me," because in the end, it is specifically through the *avodah* of *Ohr Chozer* that the revelation of Mashiach will come. And this (the one who) "was wounded because of our transgressions and crushed because of our iniquities,"[60](#_ftn193) "he bore our sicknesses and carried our pains,"[61](#_ftn194) will lead us toward the complete and true redemption,[62](#_ftn195) and the excellence of the *avodah* of *Ohr Chozer* will be revealed,[58](#_ftn191) "let Your anger turn away and comfort me."

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Acharon Shel Pesach, 5711

#### 38

[The Rebbe washed his hands for the meal.]

**1.** The Rebbe, my father-in-law, says in one of his sichos[1](#_ftn196): The seventh day of Pesach is connected with Moshe Rabbeinu, and therefore we read on it "Then Moshe sang" [Az Yashir Moshe][2](#_ftn197).

— And it should be added that this verse emphasizes the *stature* of Moshe as he is in his *entire essence* ("as he stands with his entire essence"): This verse speaks of the song of "Moshe and the Children of Israel," and yet it says "*yashir*" [he sang] in the singular (even though, seemingly, it would be more appropriate to say "*yashiru*" [they sang] in the plural[3](#_ftn198)), to indicate the inclusion of all the Children of Israel within the level of Moshe. This is the stature of Moshe as the *Nasi of Israel*, for the stature of the Nasi of Israel lies in his being together with his flock, at which time they stand in their entire essence. And since the seventh day of Pesach is the day of Moshe Rabbeinu as he is in his entire essence, it includes all the Children of Israel: "Then Moshe and the Children of Israel sang," "yashir" in the singular.

And Acharon Shel Pesach is connected with Moshiach, and therefore we read in the Haftorah, "And a shoot shall spring from the stem of Yishai, etc."[4](#_ftn199).

Moshe and Moshiach belong to one another, to the point that "the first redeemer (Moshe) *is* the final redeemer (Moshiach)"[5](#_ftn200). And as has been explained previously[6](#_ftn201), the difference regarding the tribes [that Moshe is from the tribe of Levi, and Moshiach ("a shoot from the stem of Yishai") is from the tribe of Yehudah] is only in the externality, but in the internality, "the first redeemer is the final redeemer." And each of them has a special quality.

— In one of the booklets[7](#_ftn202) there is a story that the Tzemach Tzedek once said a maamar from which it was implied that the stature of Moshe Rabbeinu is greater than the stature of Moshiach. His mind was troubled and he dozed off, and the Alter Rebbe came to him (in his dream) and told him that there is a quality in Moshe and a quality in Moshiach: Moshe was a "practical doctor" (a physician with practical experience), and therefore *practical mitzvos* were given through him, whereas Moshiach is not a "practical doctor," rather, it is through him that the *internality of the Torah* will be revealed.

***

**2.** Maamar beginning "And he waved his hand over the river, etc."

***

**3.** The special quality of the festival of Pesach in relation to other Yomim Tovim is that the physical body is nourished by the eating of matzah, which is a mitzvah.

And even though eating on Shabbos and Yom Tov is also a mitzvah—for on Shabbos there is the obligation to "delight in it with the delight of eating and drinking"[8](#_ftn203), and on Yom Tov there is the obligation of "simcha... with food and drink"[8](#_ftn203), "there is no simcha except with meat, etc., there is no simcha except with wine"[9](#_ftn204) ["at the time the Beis Hamikdash existed they would eat the meat of peace-offerings for simcha, and now... one does not fulfill the obligation of simcha except with wine"[10](#_ftn205)]—nevertheless, there is a difference between eating on Shabbos and Yom Tov and eating matzah on Pesach. On Shabbos and Yom Tov, the food and drink themselves are not the mitzvah; rather, a mitzvah is fulfilled through them, but the mitzvah does not pertain to the body of the food, which is merely a *cause* for the fulfillment of the mitzvah. This is not the case on Pesach, where the *matzah itself* is a mitzvah.

*Similar* to what was mentioned above (in the maamar[11](#_ftn206)) regarding the difference between the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Patriarchs and the fulfillment of mitzvos after the Giving of the Torah: Even though the fulfillment of mitzvos by the Patriarchs was also with physical objects, nevertheless, they were "scents"[12](#_ftn207), since the fulfillment of the mitzvah did not act upon the body of the physical object. This is not the case after the Giving of the Torah, where the mitzvah acts upon the physicality itself, such that the body of the physical object in which the mitzvah is performed is refined and purified until it becomes an object of holiness.

**4.** And the explanation of the matter[13](#_ftn208):

Matzah is called "michla d'meheimenusa"[14](#_ftn209) (food of faith), for "through the eating of matzah, faith is strengthened in the hearts of the souls of Israel"[15](#_ftn210).

#### 40

And the analogy for this is from the Sages[16](#_ftn211): "An infant does not know how to call 'Abba,' etc., until he tastes the taste of grain." The parallel in the spiritual realm is that through the eating of matzah (the taste of grain), the knowledge to call out to their Father in Heaven is created in every Jew, so that faith in Him, may He be blessed, is established in their hearts.

From this, one can understand the greatness of the elevation of eating matzah—like the infant who tastes the taste of grain. Even though at the time of tasting the grain he does not yet call "Abba" (for through tasting the grain, the *knowledge* to call "Abba" is created, while the actual calling of "Abba" comes afterwards), and furthermore, even his "calling 'Abba,' etc., after tasting the taste of grain is not a true knowledge and comprehension of who his father is—that he is his progenitor... and that it is natural for a father's mercy to be upon the son to provide for him and sustain him and supply all his needs, for the infant does not recognize any of this, he only calls him 'Abba'—nevertheless, 'in this calling that he calls 'Abba,' there is, in a hidden way, the entire true essence'"[17](#_ftn212) ("the entire essence"), and this calling (which contains the entire essence) comes from the *tasting of the grain*, the parallel to which in the spiritual realm is the *eating of the matzah*.

In the language of Kabbalah and Chassidus[18](#_ftn213)—matzah is the *katnus* [smallness] of Abba, but it also contains the *gadlus* [greatness] of Abba, the essence and being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He.

**5.** From this, one can also understand regarding the effect on the physical body that is nourished by the eating of matzah:

In the eating of Shabbos and Yom Tov, which becomes blood and flesh like his own flesh—even though the portion of blood and flesh that is made from this eating is more elevated than the other parts of the body, since it is only a partial part, it does not have the power to act upon the entirety of the body and the animal soul so that they do not conceal and hide; this is not the case with the eating of matzah—the effect is not on a partial part or matter, but on the matter of *faith* ("food of faith"), and regarding the matter of faith, concealment, hiding, and confusion from the body and the animal soul do not apply.

Faith[19](#_ftn214) is a matter of truth (as the saying goes[20](#_ftn215), "He is truth and she is faith"), which is called the central bolt that bolts from one end to the other[21](#_ftn216), which penetrates completely ("it takes through and through"), and consequently, it is impossible for there to be anything that conceals faith.

\*

#### 41

**6.** Regarding the details of the splitting of the Sea (on the seventh day of Pesach), we find that in the introduction to the splitting of the sea (which was "toward morning"[22](#_ftn217), and before that, throughout the entire night), it is written[23](#_ftn218), "And there was the cloud and the darkness, and it illuminated the night."

And it is explained in Chassidus[24](#_ftn219) that the meaning of the verse is that *the cloud and the darkness* themselves *illuminated* the night[25](#_ftn220)—meaning, not only was the darkness nullified, but more than that, the reality[26](#_ftn221) of the darkness itself became an illuminating light ("the darkness itself shone").

And through this, the matter of the splitting of the sea was accomplished—the splitting of the concealment, and not only the concealment of Malchus of Atzilus (which will be drawn down and illuminate also in Biah, the connection of Atzilus with Biah), but also the concealment that is higher than that and higher than that ("higher and higher"), up to the splitting of the concealment of the first Tzimtzum, where the aspect of the Ohr Ein Sof that was before the Tzimtzum was revealed, the essence and being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He.

And the point of the matter is that through the concealment ("the cloud and the darkness") one arrives at a higher revelation, and this is the intent of the concealment—that through it one will arrive at a higher revelation. And it begins from the concealment of the first Tzimtzum, which is by way of withdrawal—for it is impossible to say that the intent of the Tzimtzum is only for the sake of the drawing down of the Kav, but rather the intent is that after the Tzimtzum, all the light that shone before the Tzimtzum will be drawn down, and more than that, that a higher light will be drawn down and illuminate, which could not have illuminated before the Tzimtzum, but only after and through the Tzimtzum specifically[27](#_ftn222).

**7.** And just as the revelations of the splitting of the sea were accomplished through the introduction of the illumination of the darkness, so too is it regarding the revelations of the future to come—for which it is said[28](#_ftn223), "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders"—that the preparation for them is accomplished through the illumination of the darkness:

It is known[29](#_ftn224) that the revelations of the future to come are accomplished through our deeds and our avodah throughout the entire duration of the exile, for the entirety of the avodah during the time of exile is in a state and situation

#### 42

of *concealment and hiding* specifically, and nevertheless, not only are we not affected by the concealments and hidings, but on the contrary, we utilize the reality[30](#_ftn225) of the concealment and hiding itself, through which even more is added to the strength of the avodah, etc.

And for example—regarding the entirety of the avodah with the concealment and hiding of the body specifically:

It was explained above[31](#_ftn226) the difference between the exodus from Egypt and the future to come—that at the exodus from Egypt (when there was only the *beginning* of the avodah), it is said[32](#_ftn227), "for the people fled," "because the evil in the souls of Israel was still in its strength, etc."[33](#_ftn228), meaning, that the body was not yet refined but remained in its filth and loathsomeness, to the point that they needed to "flee" from the state and situation of the body. This is not the case in the future to come, for it is written[34](#_ftn229), "And you shall not go in haste," because this will be after the perfection of the avodah with the body specifically, to effect the refinement and purification of the body until the body itself will shine ("the body itself will shine").

And specifically through the avodah with the body will the elevation of seeing the essence of Divinity in a tangible vision with physical eyes be renewed in the future to come:

At this time, we do not know and we cannot conceive in our minds the concept of seeing the essence of Divinity. Seeing the essence pertains to us only regarding physical things, and in physicality itself, only in the reality of the essence, and not in the truth of its essence (the essence of the essence), which is the soul within it, regarding which only knowledge and understanding apply, and even the vision of the eye of the intellect, but not a tangible vision. And the innovation of the future to come, in the coming of Moshiach, is that in the essence of Divinity there will be a tangible vision with physical eyes, and the innovation in this is twofold: (a) seeing the essence of Divinity, (b) in a tangible vision with physical eyes.

And this innovation (tangible vision with physical eyes in the essence of Divinity) is from the side of the *body* specifically, for, from the side of the soul, the matter of understanding and comprehension, feeling, and even the vision of the eye of the intellect applies, but *tangible vision with physical eyes* applies only from the side of the *body*, except that through the avodah in the refinement and purification of the body, one effects that in the future to come there will be a tangible vision with physical eyes *in the essence of Divinity*.

**8.** From this, one can also understand regarding the matter of passing [histalkus]:

The matter of passing is the greatest concealment and hiding—greater than the concealment

#### 43

and hiding (that is from the side of the body, and especially) that is during the time of exile—as the Sages say[35](#_ftn230), "The passing of the righteous is as difficult before the Holy One, blessed be He, *more*... than the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash."

However, it is specifically through this that one arrives at a greater elevation—as is hinted at in the language of the Zohar[36](#_ftn231), "*is-talkei* [is elevated/withdrawn] the glory of the Holy One, blessed be He, in all the worlds," which refers to the drawing down and revelation of a most elevated light that is in a manner of *exaltation*, which is why it is called by a term of withdrawal [suluk][37](#_ftn232).
