— The truth is that as much as the stature of the light grows, one is not satisfied with the aspect of revelations alone. It is not for this that the Children of Israel suffered ("not for this were Jews torn apart"...) throughout the entire duration of the exile, and it is not for this that there was the matter of passing, which is "more difficult... than the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash." Rather, the desire of the Children of Israel, Jews in general and Chassidim in particular, is that there be a revelation of *His essence, may He be blessed* ("the essence itself")!...

And this will be speedily in our days—when the Rebbe will lead us toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

\*

**9.** [The Rebbe stood to his full height and said:]

When the Rebbe, my father-in-law, wrote the Sefer Torah for the welcoming of Moshiach, he said[39](#_ftn234) that initially it occurred to him to write the Sefer Torah himself, and afterwards he decided to grant the merit of writing the Sefer Torah to all of Israel. The Rebbe wanted and granted the merit to all of Israel, both those who wanted and participated in the writing of the Sefer Torah at the time, and those who will want and participate afterwards, and even those who even afterwards will not want this in a revealed desire, since this is their true desire[40](#_ftn235).

Writing a Sefer Torah is (not so that it should lie in a corner[41](#_ftn236), but) so that they should study it and fulfill it, to learn and to teach, to disseminate Torah in public. And since this is so, all those who participate in the writing of the Sefer Torah must involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah in public.

And more specifically:

Those who received instructions from the Rebbe regarding the dissemination of Torah—certainly

#### 44

must involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah, and it is not a good thing that there are among them those who have become weak in the dissemination of Torah.

And even those who did not receive instructions from the Rebbe regarding the dissemination of Torah, but rather an opportunity to involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah has presented itself to them—must know that in truth, this itself is an instruction from the Rebbe, for all matters are by Divine Providence, and among Chassidim all matters are connected with the Rebbe, who even after the passing will not abandon his flock[42](#_ftn237). Thus, the fact that an opportunity to involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah has presented itself to them constitutes *an instruction from the Rebbe* that they must involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah.

And since this is the instruction of the Rebbe—*the Rebbe himself goes*, and in his entire essence ("the entire Rebbe") *with each one* ("the entire Rebbe goes with this, and the entire Rebbe goes with this"), for the essence, when you grasp a part of it, you grasp the whole of it[43](#_ftn238).

And therefore, it is a holy obligation and a holy merit for each one to involve himself in the dissemination of Torah, not to seclude himself within his four cubits, but to involve himself in the dissemination of Torah, and to know the magnitude of the responsibility that was placed upon him by the Rebbe, who, as mentioned, goes with him in his entire essence.

And through the fulfillment of the instructions of the Rebbe to involve oneself in the dissemination of Torah—we will merit that the Rebbe will lead us to the true and complete Redemption.

— The precision of the language "true and complete Redemption" is not in relation to a specific matter[44](#_ftn239) that some fools consider as the "beginning of the Redemption"[45](#_ftn240), but rather, in relation to the "beginning of the Redemption" that is in the revelation of the general Torah of Chassidus by the Baal Shem Tov and the revelation of the Torah of Chassidus Chabad by the Alter Rebbe and our Rebbes, the Nesi'im who followed, which is the "beginning of the Redemption" from which we come to the true and complete Redemption.

**10.** [The Rebbe gave wine with his holy hand to those involved in the dissemination of Torah, and blessed them with success in the dissemination of Torah, and to several of them he also gave personal blessings.

At this event, some of the householders who support the Yeshiva requested wine, and the Rebbe replied:]

#### 45

I do not want to mix physicality with spirituality, for when the supporters of the Yeshiva involve themselves in spirituality, then there will be a lack in physicality[46](#_ftn241).

**11.** (Afterwards he said:)

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, wanted and demanded that the elder Rabbis of Anash dedicate themselves to guiding the youth. I do not know if they are doing so, but in any case, they must do so.

And therefore, I will give them wine for involving themselves in the work that the Rebbe placed upon them, and may it be His will that they succeed in their work.

[The Rebbe gave wine to the elder Rabbis of Anash, and blessed them with personal blessings].

**12.** [Afterwards, the Rebbe gave wine to the householders who support the Yeshiva, "supporters of the Torah," and blessed each one personally.

To one he said:]

A Chassid—the Rebbe says[47](#_ftn242)—is like a goat, which fulfills its role of giving milk, and does not know any worry for its sustenance, since its owner worries about providing it with all its needs. And so too must a Chassid fulfill the role that the Rebbe demands of him, and consequently, the Rebbe will worry about all his affairs.

[To one he said:]

Simcha breaks through barriers[48](#_ftn243).

Simcha—the Rebbe, my father-in-law, says in the sicha[49](#_ftn244)—is from the good of the other ("from the other's good"), for, by himself, there is nothing to be happy about... rather, the simcha is from the other, because the other is good ("the other is indeed good").

And this simcha breaks through barriers. In truth, there is no reality of a barrier, and it only seems that there is a barrier, but this itself (that it seems there is a barrier) is the barrier. And the breaking of the barrier is through the simcha.

[To one he said:]

There must be an exiting from one's self ("one must go out of oneself").

#### 46

— On Purim there is a suggestion, according to the revealed Torah[50](#_ftn245), to sleep... but on Acharon Shel Pesach this suggestion does not exist!

**13.** [The Rebbe said that he would give wine to the students of the Yeshiva, and before that he said:]

Unformed material—can be worked ("worked out") in the most elevated manner, to such an extent that from the side of the power of the actor that is in the acted-upon, one can effect in the material an elevation that is incomparable, even though from its own side it has no value for this.

And just as with a Rav and a student, that although they are not comparable to one another, to the extent that "until forty years a person does not stand on the mind of his Rav"[51](#_ftn246), nevertheless, from the side of the power of the Rav, the power of the actor in the acted-upon, an incomparable elevation is created in the student, to the point that over time the senses of the student become like the senses of the Rav[52](#_ftn247).

And all this is *with a Rav and a student*—that although the elevation of the student through the Rav is an incomparable elevation, it is ultimately *in order and gradation*, since the entirety of the influence from the Rav to the student is in order and gradation, contraction and expansion, etc.; whereas with a *Rebbe and a Chassid*—the elevation that the Rebbe elevates the Chassid is *without limit*.

And behold, although this elevation is from the side of the *power of the actor*, from whose side specifically the action can be in the material to elevate it to a level that from its own side it is not connected to at all, nevertheless, a certain condition is required also from the side of the material—*that it should not have a form of its own* ("he should not have any own form"), and then, its elevation can be from the side of the power of the actor without measure.

(And the Rebbe concluded:)

There are those who have already acquired their own form ("they have already gotten a form themselves"), and consequently, it is impossible (and perhaps unnecessary...) to change them from their form; but the bochurim, the students of the Yeshiva, are *unformed material*, and consequently, their elevation from the side of the power of the actor of the Rebbe[53](#_ftn248) can be and will be without measure!

(Before he gave wine to the students of the Yeshiva, he said:)

#### 47

I too am a student of the Rebbe, and therefore I will join with the students, and certainly they will not complain about me... (And he added with a smile: And even if they complain—I don't care).

**14.** [The Rebbe gave wine to one of the Shochetim, and afterwards said:]

The Sages said[54](#_ftn249), "The word 'v'shachat' [and he shall slaughter] means only 'v'mashach' [and he shall pull]," meaning, that the action of slaughtering (in avodah) is analogous to the acquisition of pulling, that one pulls the object from one domain to another, through which it exits the previous domain and is elevated to another domain.

By way of introduction:

In slaughtering—there is a difference between an animal and a bird[55](#_ftn250), for with a bird, the slaughtering of the majority of one sign is sufficient, and that is the esophagus [veshet], which is the special one of the signs[56](#_ftn251), whereas with an animal there is a need for the slaughtering of the majority of two, not only the esophagus but also the trachea [kaneh]; "an animal that was created from the dry land is made kosher with two signs... a bird that was created from the marsh is made kosher with one sign"[57](#_ftn252). And the explanation for this is that "the animal... from coarse material... with two signs (esophagus and trachea) that are slaughtered, its material, which is more coarse, will be refined," whereas "birds that were created from the marsh need refinement with one sign"[58](#_ftn253), the esophagus alone.

And its meaning in avodah:

The difference between the esophagus and the trachea—that the esophagus serves for eating and drinking, and the trachea serves for the spirit of life. And therefore, one who is not so materialistic (like a bird), the slaughtering of one sign is sufficient for him, the esophagus, meaning, to be careful from materialism regarding his eating and drinking so that it should be as it ought to be; and one who is more materialistic (like an animal), needs the slaughtering of two signs, not only the esophagus but also the trachea, meaning, that he needs caution from materialism (not only regarding matters of eating and drinking, but) also regarding his spirit of life, his *spiritual* matters, that they should be as they ought to be ("he needs to protect also his spiritual matters").

And for example—regarding the study of Torah—to be careful from studying not for its own sake, beginning from the simple interpretation of "not for its own sake," in order that he be called a Rav, and the like, but rather to study for its own sake[59](#_ftn254). And similarly regarding the dissemination of Torah—that when one studies with children, one must endeavor to teach them (not only Torah alone, but) Torah and fear

#### 48

of Heaven, through the study of Chassidus, including also endeavoring to act upon parents that they should send their children to a Talmud Torah where they teach Torah and fear of Heaven, and to bring close also the parents themselves—first to Judaism in general, and afterwards also to Chassidus.

**15.** (And the Rebbe concluded:) One must involve oneself in the dissemination and spreading of Torah in general, and in the dissemination and spreading of the Torah of Chassidus in particular,

— To our sorrow, only a few involve themselves in the dissemination of Torah, and regarding the spreading of the Torah of Chassidus, there is almost no one at all who involves himself—

And through this, one hastens and brings closer the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu[60](#_ftn255).

The truth is that Moshiach is already here ("he is already here"), and this is only your fault...—it is forbidden to say about Jews a matter of fault, but...

Moshiach is already "standing behind our wall"[61](#_ftn256), and is waiting to go out and redeem the Children of Israel and is not delayed even for the time of tying two knots (but "he unties one and ties one")[62](#_ftn257), the moment they do teshuvah, he will redeem them immediately[63](#_ftn258), and consequently, from his side he is already here, and the matter depends only on us.

And therefore one must involve oneself in the spreading of the Torah of Chassidus outward,

And as the words of the Alter Rebbe[64](#_ftn259)—that because he is a Nasi, certainly his will will be fulfilled ("he will certainly carry it out")—that the Torah of Chassidus is not a matter of a party, but will be the inheritance of all of Israel,

And when they involve themselves in the spreading of the Torah of Chassidus, they will bring the coming of Moshiach one moment sooner!

[The Rebbe commanded to play the Nigun of the Alter Rebbe of four stanzas, and to repeat the fourth stanza—seven times].

***

**16.** After the festival of Sukkos there is the Yom Tov of Shemini Atzeres, as explained in the Midrash[65](#_ftn260), the analogy to a king who said to his children, "I request of you, stay with me one more day, your departure is difficult for me";

#### 49

but after the festival of Pesach there is no additional Yom Tov, and the reason for this is because on the night of the second day of Pesach we begin to count the Sefiras HaOmer, and all the days of the Sefirah are a continuation of the festival of Pesach, and after the festival of Pesach comes the festival of Shavuos, which is the "Atzeres" of the festival of Pesach[66](#_ftn261) (which is why it does not have a fixed time in the days of the month—"sometimes on the fifth, sometimes on the sixth, sometimes on the seventh"[67](#_ftn262), but its fixed time is on the fiftieth day of Sefiras HaOmer[68](#_ftn263)).

And since the festival of Pesach continues and goes on, one must endeavor that the maamar of Chassidus and the farbrengen should act also afterwards, in actual deed: actual deed in the study of Torah, and simply—to study Nigleh and Chassidus, and actual deed in the fulfillment of mitzvos.

"Action is above"[69](#_ftn264). Through actual deed specifically—we will merit the revelation of Moshiach, at which time there will be a revelation of the essence of the essence and being of the Ein Sof, blessed be He.

(After Grace After Meals and the evening prayer, the Rebbe said:)

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, was accustomed to wish after Pesach: A healthy summer.

**********

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Acharei, Mevarchim HaChodesh and Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5711

#### 50

(An unedited transcript)

**"And Jonathan said to him, 'Tomorrow is the new moon, and you will be missed, for your seat will be empty.'"**[1](#_ftn265) This Haftorah is read on the Shabbos of Erev Rosh Chodesh. The reason for this is that Jonathan’s words to David were spoken on Erev Rosh Chodesh, as he said, "Tomorrow is the new moon." However, this requires understanding: on the face of it, this is a very weak connection, especially since the entire length of the Haftorah itself has no relevance to Erev Rosh Chodesh, and the only link is the two words "tomorrow is the new moon." Furthermore, it is even more difficult to understand because the law is that the Haftorah must be related to the subject of the Torah reading, and not just the general subject of the Parsha, but specifically the conclusion of the Parsha.[3](#_ftn267) This is why on Shabbos Chanukah that falls on Rosh Chodesh, we read "Sing and rejoice,"[4](#_ftn268) because the conclusion of the reading is the Parsha of Chanukah.[5](#_ftn269) If so, it is all the more difficult why we read the Haftorah of "tomorrow is the new moon" on every Shabbos of Erev Rosh Chodesh, as it has no similarity to the reading of the Parsha—for we read it on every Shabbos of Erev Rosh Chodesh, regardless of which Parsha it is. We must therefore conclude that the connection of this Haftorah to Shabbos Erev Rosh Chodesh is so powerful that it overrides the obligation to read a Haftorah related to the Torah reading. We must understand the matter. We also need to understand the details of the Haftorah, where Jonathan said to David, "If the arrows are from you and beyond, then go, for Hashem has sent you,"[6](#_ftn270)—why did he give him a sign specifically with arrows, and not in another, clearer way?

2) **To understand** all this, we must first preface what has been explained previously[7](#_ftn271) regarding the greatness of Moshiach, for it is written about him,[8](#_ftn272) "He shall not judge by the sight of his eyes, nor decide by the hearing of his ears," but rather, "He will smell with the fear of Hashem," for he "smells and judges."[9](#_ftn273) Furthermore, our Sages said[10](#_ftn274) that Moshiach comes to bring the righteous to teshuvah. And it was explained there[11](#_ftn275) that these two matters in Moshiach—

#### 51

regarding the essence of Moshiach, whose primary greatness is "he will smell with the fear of Hashem," and regarding the activity of Moshiach, that he comes to bring the righteous to teshuvah—are connected to one another. For the matter of "smelling and judging" means that he will not judge by the sight of his eyes, as a person sees with his eyes,[12](#_ftn276) seeing only the revealed matters, but rather in a way that he knows the matters and the causes that brought the person to his undesirable state. As the saying goes,[13](#_ftn277) "Do not judge your fellow until you reach his place." The truth of this matter is when one reaches the level of the *etzem* (essence). As has been explained, the status and situation of the revealed powers is not an indication of the *etzem*.[14](#_ftn278) As we find with Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai, that even though he did not leave, etc.,[15](#_ftn279) nevertheless, due to his great humility, he said, "I do not know to which path they are leading me."[16](#_ftn280) Therefore, in order for the judgment to be true, one must know all matters down to the level of the *etzem*, and only then can he "judge the poor with righteousness." This is the matter of "smelling and judging," because the sense of smell touches the essence of the soul, as has been explained[17](#_ftn281) that the nose is the gate to the brain, meaning the interiority of the *mochin* (intellects). Especially according to what is explained in *Idra Rabba*, [18](#_ftn282) that the left nostril reaches the level of the "life of lives," the level of the interiority of *Atik*, which is the *etzem*. Therefore, through the sense of smell, he reaches the point of knowing all the matters of the other person down to his *etzem*. This is also the matter of Moshiach coming to bring the righteous to teshuvah; since the judgment of Moshiach will be from the perspective of the *etzem*, he will therefore effect teshuvah even in the righteous. For the revealed powers do not indicate the state of the *etzem*, and even if the revealed powers are in a state of goodness, it is still possible that the *etzem* is in the depths of the *kelipos* (as proven by the aforementioned statement of Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai), and therefore, the matter of teshuvah must exist even in the righteous.

**However**, it still needs to be understood: it is understandable regarding ordinary righteous people—that is, righteous people from the perspective of their revealed powers—that since their revealed powers are not an indication of the *etzem*, they need the matter of teshuvah. But the matter that Moshiach comes to bring the righteous to teshuvah refers to all the righteous, even those who are righteous from the perspective of the *etzem*. This is why they bring an example of this from Moshe Rabbeinu, who before his passing reached the level of teshuvah,[19](#_ftn283) because the revelation of Moshiach shone within him. And certainly, Moshe Rabbeinu was righteous even from the perspective of the *etzem*, for it is impossible to say, Heaven forbid, that his *etzem* was in the depths of

#### 52

the *kelipos*; certainly, his *etzem* was at the highest level of holiness. It is not understood what the matter of teshuvah is at this level. And even though it was explained that the matter of teshuvah means that one is not satisfied with his previous state—a matter that applies even to the righteous, for since the essence of the soul is always in *dveikus* (cleaving) to the Essence of the *Ein Sof*, as it is written,[20](#_ftn284) "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today," and the *Ohr Ein Sof* is infinitely higher,[21](#_ftn285) therefore the matter of teshuvah is constant, that at every level one stands, one wants to ascend to a higher level—nevertheless, it is still not understood, for this matter in its general sense exists even before the coming of Moshiach. If so, what is the greatness of the innovation (such a tremendous thing) that will be brought about specifically by Moshiach?

3) **But the matter is**[22](#_ftn286) that the general work of *birurim* (refinement) is "to include the left in the right,"[23](#_ftn287) which is the general matter of Torah: to refine and elevate all the undesirable things that come from the left, so that they are included in the right. There are two ways to do this: *iskafya* (subjugation of the *sitra achra*) and *is'hapcha* (transformation of darkness into light). Each has an advantage over the other. The work of *iskafya* is through the good dressing itself in the seed and fighting with it. This is the work of the *beinonim* (intermediates),[24](#_ftn288) which is the measure of every person, "and after him every person will be drawn."[25](#_ftn289) The work is by way of war, as it is written,[26](#_ftn290) "And a man wrestled with him," whereby the evil is nullified, whether by sixty, or by a thousand, or by a myriad.[27](#_ftn291) The advantage of work in this manner is that through it, the evil itself recognizes and knows the greatness of the good, and that it should be good, and it agrees to become good. But nevertheless, the disadvantage is that the evil itself is not transformed into good; it is only nullified by the good, but the evil itself remains in its previous essence. Another disadvantage is that in order to refine the evil, the good must dress itself in the evil—for the refiner must dress in the garments of that which is being refined—and through this, the evil causes a weakening in the good, as the good knows of the reality of the evil, etc. An example of this is the sweetening of bitter water by adding a large amount of sweet water. It is simply understood that the bitter water has not been transformed into sweet water, but remains in its previous essence, and is only nullified by the abundance of sweet water. Likewise, it is understood that the bitter water causes a weakening in the sweet water, as its sweetness is not as it was before, for there is a slight mixture of bitter water in it. However, the work of *is'hapcha* is that due to the abundance of the revelation of light, which is a most exalted light, the evil itself is transformed into good. The advantage of this manner is that the evil itself becomes good (and not just nullified by the good), and furthermore, it does not cause a weakening in the good, for the good does not dress itself in it to transform it; rather, it is transformed automatically through the revelation of a most exalted light. But the disadvantage is that the evil from its own perspective does not know and recognize this, for since its transformation into good is through the revelation of light, the evil itself does not agree to be nullified to the good, but is transformed automatically by the revelation of the light.

**This can be understood** by an analogy[28](#_ftn292) from a courtroom that has a prosecutor and a defender. The nullification of the prosecutor can be in two ways. The first is through the arguments of the defender, who presents his arguments for the defense until his arguments affect not only the judges but also the prosecutor, who, because of the arguments, is nullified. It is understood that this is not in a way that the prosecutor is transformed to argue for the defense, but rather that because of the defender's arguments, his own arguments are blocked and he does not argue for the prosecution. It is also understood that in such a way, a weakening is created in the defender, since he hears, for a short time at least, the arguments of the prosecutor, at which point he hears that even though he is arguing for the defense, there is someone else arguing for the prosecution. But there is a more exalted way to nullify the prosecutor, and that is through the revelation of "in the light of the King's face is life,"[29](#_ftn293)—that is, when the King enters the courtroom, then both the prosecutor and the defender are nullified (there is no more prosecutor and no more defender), and even the prosecutor argues for the defense. However, even though in this way the prosecutor himself becomes a defender, this matter is only from the perspective of the revelation of the light of the King's face, and not from his own perspective at all, for he does not understand or grasp the light of the King's face, but is nullified automatically by the revelation of the light of the King's face, while from his own perspective, he remains a prosecutor.

**However**, there is another way of *is'hapcha* that has both advantages: the evil is transformed into good completely, and this matter is done also from its own perspective, and not only from the revelation outside of it. This is when the evil itself grasps and recognizes (hears) that it is evil, and it is distressed (it becomes narrow for him) by its status and situation, and therefore it leaves its evil and is transformed into good. This matter is through the revelation of the *he'elem atzmi* (essential concealment), meaning that this is not a matter of a revelation of light, as in "in the light of the King's face is life"—light specifically, which is only a radiance and illumination—but the level of *he'elem atzmi*, which is from the perspective of the King's own essence.

#### 54

4) **This is** what is written,[30](#_ftn294) "And they came to Marah and could not drink the water of Marah for they were bitter... and Hashem showed him a tree, and he cast it into the water, and the water became sweet." Regarding the tree, we find two opinions. The opinion of the *Zohar*[31](#_ftn295) is that the tree refers to the Torah, as it is written,[32](#_ftn296) "It is a tree of life to those who grasp it," and the opinion of the *Midrash*[33](#_ftn297) is that this tree was the *hardufni*, which is a poison.[34](#_ftn298) These two opinions are the two aforementioned ways of *is'hapcha*. For according to all opinions, the bitter water was not nullified by adding a large amount of good water (in which case they do not change in their essential nature, as above), but rather, by casting the tree, the bitter water itself was transformed, as it is written, "and the water became sweet." But within this itself, there are two opinions. According to the *Zohar*, that the tree refers to Torah (for the Torah is the "tree of life," which does not belong to the "tree of death," and does not belong to the mixture of good and evil), it follows that the sweetening of the water was through the revelation of the light of Torah, and because of this revelation, the bitter water was turned into sweet water. However, according to the *Midrash*, that the tree itself is a bitter tree, it follows that the action of casting the tree into the water was to reveal to the water their own bitterness, etc., and through this, the sweetening is accomplished from the perspective of the bitter water itself. And even though this matter was done specifically by Moshe, as it is written, "And Hashem showed him a tree, and he cast it into the water," this is because the evil from its own perspective cannot feel that it is evil, but there must be a revelation from above specifically. Nevertheless, this is not a matter of a revelation of light, but the action is to show them their own bitterness, through which the evil itself leaves its reality and is transformed into good. That is, this is not a matter of a revelation of light, but a revelation of the *he'elem atzmi*, the "concealment of all concealments," about which it is written,[35](#_ftn299) "He made darkness His hiding place."

5) **The explanation** of this matter in the work of man: it is written,[36](#_ftn300) "As Hashem, the G-d of Israel, lives, before whom I have stood," which refers to the soul as it is above, which grasps G-dliness and stands in love and fear, and does not know at all about other matters besides G-dliness. However, upon its descent below to be dressed in a body and an animal soul, it already belongs to human intellect, to grasp a physical thing, and below that, for through the descent of the soul into the body, concealment is created in two ways. The first is that the body conceals the light of the soul, and the second is the concealment of the body itself. And these are the two matters that exist in darkness: its being the absence of light, and its being a creation in its own right. That is, the concealment of the light of the soul is the matter of the absence of light, and the concealment of the body itself is the matter that the darkness is a creation in its own right. For the absence of light exists only when there is a reality of light, and then the darkness effects the absence of light or

#### 55

a weakening and concealment in the light. From this it is understood that the concealment of the body itself cannot be a matter of the absence of light, for the creation of the body preceded the creation of the soul,[37](#_ftn301) and this is also why the root of the body is not from the level of light, but from the level of the *reshimu*.[38](#_ftn302) Rather, the concealment of the body itself is the matter that the darkness is a creation in its own right.

**Now**, regarding the two matters of darkness mentioned above, there must be the work of *iskafya* and the work of *is'hapcha*. The work of *iskafya* is the work that is according to reason and knowledge, meaning that through the many ways of contemplation that are explained in the books, and especially in the books of Chassidus, one effects the evil so that it is nullified to the good. And the work of *is'hapcha* is in a way that one does not want to enter at all into arguments and excuses, etc., and in the words of the Rebbe Rayatz[39](#_ftn303) in the name of the Alter Rebbe: "A Jew, he does not want and he cannot be separated from G-dliness." The general matter of this is from the perspective of the powers that are given from above, powers that a Rebbe gives—meaning, this is not from the perspective of his own exertion (*oisgehoreveto koichos*), but powers that the Rebbe gave him, and from the perspective of these powers, he does not enter into matters of argument at all. However, there is an even more exalted matter in *is'hapcha*, which comes from the perspective of the revelation of the *he'elem atzmi*. This matter is above any definition of understanding, etc., for we have in this neither understanding nor grasp, nor recognition nor feeling, neither internally nor by way of *makif* (encompassing), but because of the soul's *dveikus* to the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, no matters prevent him, and they give him also the revelation of the *he'elem atzmi*, which cannot be drawn down either in internal powers or in *makif* powers. This matter finds expression in the feeling of "evil and bitter is your forsaking Hashem your G-d."[40](#_ftn304) That is, even though he has no knowledge at all of "Hashem your G-d," and he does not know at all about matters of holiness, nevertheless he feels that "evil and bitter is your forsaking Hashem your G-d," and furthermore, even though he does not know why it is evil and bitter, nevertheless he feels that it is evil and bitter, and he feels that this is a matter that touches the essence of his soul in this world and the next, and it is impossible that it should continue this way, and it is necessary that there be a change from here on,[41](#_ftn305) for even though he does not know what it is to draw close to Him, nevertheless he knows that it is impossible to continue in such a way. And specifically in this work, the *he'elem atzmi* is revealed, because in this work the body itself is transformed into good, meaning that the cause of its transformation into good is not from the perspective of the revelation of light, but from the perspective of the body itself, and this matter is from the perspective of the revelation of the *he'elem atzmi*, since the revelation of the true *Yesh* (Being) is specifically in the created *yesh*.[42](#_ftn306)

#### 56

6) **With this** we can understand[43](#_ftn307) the matter of Moshiach coming to bring the righteous to teshuvah. For the innovation of the days of Moshiach is that the *yesh* itself will be transformed into good, and specifically from its own perspective. This is the greatness of the revelation of Moshiach over the revelation of the splitting of the Red Sea; for although at the splitting of the Red Sea there was also the transformation of darkness into light, that the darkness itself shone, as it is written,[44](#_ftn308) "And the cloud and the darkness were there, and it lit up the night," nevertheless, this matter was from the perspective of a revelation of light,[45](#_ftn309) as it is said, "The King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, was revealed to them,"[46](#_ftn310) "I, and not an angel," etc., "I am He and no other,"[47](#_ftn311) that this revelation lit up the darkness. However, regarding the future to come, it is written,[48](#_ftn312) "And the night will shine like the day," meaning that even though the night is darkness, nevertheless, it will shine like the day from its own perspective. This matter can be through the revelation of the true *Yesh* specifically, which is the greatness of the revelation of the future to come, unlike the splitting of the Red Sea, which was only a revelation of the aspect of the *Ayin* (Nothingness) of the true *Yesh*. This is also the innovation of Moshiach coming to bring the righteous to teshuvah. For even a righteous person who serves Hashem with great love and delights is in the category of *yesh*—"there is one who loves,"[49](#_ftn313) "there is one who loves,"[50](#_ftn314)—for even though the *yesh* is "what he loves," nevertheless he is in the category of *yesh*. The innovation of Moshiach, that he will effect that even the righteous will come to the matter of teshuvah, is that the righteous person will feel his *yesh* (beingness) and will automatically want to leave his *yesh*, and this is because the aspect of the true *Yesh*, besides whom there is nothing, will be revealed in the created *yesh*.

7) **And according to** all the above, the matter of "And Jonathan said to him, 'Tomorrow is the new moon,'" etc., will be understood. For "tomorrow is the new moon" is the matter of the renewal of the moon, which is like the revelations of the future to come, as we say in the blessing of *Kiddush Levanah* that the light of the moon will be like the light of the sun, like the light of the seven days of creation,[51](#_ftn315) as it was before its diminution, etc. This is also the precision of the language "tomorrow is the new moon," similar to what our Sages said,[52](#_ftn316) "Today is to do them,"[53](#_ftn317) "tomorrow to receive their reward." That is, the general work in this time is like the work of Erev Rosh Chodesh, upon which all the revelations of the future depend,[54](#_ftn318) which is the matter of "tomorrow is the new moon." This matter is also hinted at in the details of the matters that Jonathan said to David: "If the arrows are from you and beyond, then go, for Hashem has sent you." For the matter of shooting arrows with a bow points to the general matter of the work of *birurim*,

#### 57

as explained in the additions to *Torah Or*, [55](#_ftn319) that the pulling of the bow is so that the arrow will be thrown further, for the more one pulls the bow downward, the further the arrow goes. So it is in the work of *birurim* (the work of *ohr chozer*—returning light), that the involvement with the lowest things reaches the highest. This is what Jonathan said to David: "If the arrows are from you and beyond," meaning that the work of *birurim* had already been completed, then "peace be to you," meaning peace in the heavenly retinue and in the earthly retinue,[56](#_ftn320) "there is no matter," there is no more work of *birurim*, "Hashem lives," and it is possible for there to be the revelation of the "day that is entirely Shabbos and rest for eternal life."[57](#_ftn321) But if "the arrows are from you and beyond," that the *birurim* have not yet been completed, then "go, for Hashem has sent you"—go and engage in the work of *birurim*, and do not say from where you will take the strength for this, for "Hashem has sent you," meaning that you are not doing this by your own strength, but on the mission of the Holy One, blessed be He, for the entire matter of the work is His mission, similar to what our Sages said,[58](#_ftn322) "Be respectful of the mitzvos, for they are messengers." And this matter itself (whether the work of *birurim* had been completed) Jonathan needed to clarify specifically with Saul. For three mitzvos were commanded to Israel upon their entry into the land: the appointment of a king, the cutting off of the seed of Amalek, and the building of the Chosen House.[59](#_ftn323) And since the first mitzvah of the appointment of a king was fulfilled in Saul, as he was the first king in Israel, and if he had cut off the seed of Amalek, then the matter of the building of the Chosen House would have also been accomplished then [and only because he did not cut off the seed of Amalek and kept Agag alive[60](#_ftn324) did the entire length of the exile come about], therefore he needed to clarify with him specifically if the work of *birurim* had already been completed, for with him was the matter of *birurim*, etc. And the sign for this was specifically the matter of the bow. The matter of this[61](#_ftn325) is that it is stated in the *Zohar*, [62](#_ftn326) "Do not look for the footsteps of Moshiach until you see this bow in the world decorated with bright colors, etc., and then look for Moshiach." On the face of it, it is not understood; for the bow is a sign of the covenant that there will not be a flood,[63](#_ftn327), and the need for this sign is an undesirable matter, and therefore Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai said that one of his merits was that the bow was not seen in his days.[64](#_ftn328) If so, what is the connection of the bow to the footsteps of Moshiach? But the matter is that the precision is in the matter of the bow in "bright colors" specifically, as explained by the Tzemach Tzedek,[65](#_ftn329) that this is the revelation of the interiority of *Atik*, through which the darkness itself shines, which is that the clouds themselves

#### 58

cause the abundance of colors, similar to the revelation of the future to come, that "the night will shine like the day." Therefore, "when the bow is seen in bright colors, then look for the footsteps of Moshiach." However, the precision in this is "look for the footsteps of Moshiach," because the matter of Moshiach himself is that the darkness will shine from its own perspective, as above, unlike the matter of the bow in bright colors, where the illumination of the darkness is due to the abundance and strength of the sunlight, and therefore it is only in the category of the "footsteps of Moshiach." And it concludes,[66](#_ftn330) "And they kissed one another and wept one another, until David grew." For Jonathan son of Saul is the matter of understanding (*hasagah*), which is the matter of "Saul from Rechovos HaNahar,"[67](#_ftn331) the level of *Binah*. Unlike David, whose matter is that he "established the yoke of Torah"[68](#_ftn332) and the "yoke of teshuvah,"[69](#_ftn333) *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) specifically. And this is "until David grew," until the matter of "Hashem has done great and wondrous things on earth"[70](#_ftn334) will be in revelation, the revelation of the *he'elem atzmi*, speedily in our days.

**********

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Acharei, Mevarchim HaChodesh and Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5711

#### 59

(Unedited)

**A.** Maamar beginning with the words, "And Yonasan said to him, tomorrow is the new moon."

***

**B.** Regarding the spelling of the name of the month (which is blessed this Shabbos)—as there is a doubt whether it should be written "Iyar" with one *yud* or "Iyar" with two *yuds*—the well-known allusion is that "Iyar" is an acronym for *Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, Rochel*. Therefore, it should be written with two *yuds*.

One must understand: What is the special connection of Rochel to the Patriarchs, such that we find her enumerated together with them—Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, and Rochel?

This is all the more puzzling when considering the distinction between the Patriarchs and the Tribes:

It is known that the Patriarchs ("We only call the three 'Patriarchs'") belong to all of Bnei Yisrael, as they are the "fathers" of all Bnei Yisrael, and all of Bnei Yisrael are called "the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov." This is not the case with the Tribes; each tribe comprises only a portion of Bnei Yisrael—the children of Reuven, the children of Shimon, etc. The same applies to *avodah*: the *avodah* of the Patriarchs is required of every member of Bnei Yisrael ("The level of the Patriarchs must exist within every person, as they are the root and source of all the souls of Israel"), whereas the *avodah* of the Tribes is different: "Each and every tribe shall ascend on its own path," and from each tribe, the specific *avodah* unique to that tribe is required (from the children of Reuven, the *avodah* of Reuven is required; from the children of Shimon, the *avodah* of Shimon is required, and so on for the other tribes).

Since the children of Rochel are only *two* tribes—Yosef and Binyamin—it is most puzzling what the connection of Rochel (from whom only Yosef and Binyamin descended) is to Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, who are the "Patriarchs" *of all Bnei Yisrael*.

**C.** This can be understood by first explaining the reason why Rochel is the only one of the Matriarchs who was not buried in the Me'aras HaMachpeilah. We find two reasons for this, which on the face of it appear to contradict one another:

#### 60

1) "Because she belittled the *mishkav hatzadik* (the conjugal union with the righteous one—by saying to Leah, 'This night’s union was mine, and I will give it to you in exchange for your son’s mandrakes'), she did not merit to be buried with him."

2) "So that she would be of help to her children when Nevuzaradan would exile them and they would pass by there. Rochel would emerge from her grave, weep, and plead for mercy for them, as it is written: 'A voice is heard on high, etc.,' and the Ribono shel Olam replies to her: 'There is a reward for your labor, says Hashem, etc., and the children shall return to their border.'"

One can say that the bridge between these two reasons is that the reason *Rochel*—out of all the Matriarchs—is able to be of help to her children, to weep and plead for mercy for them, and to bring about that "the children shall return to their border," is precisely because she possesses the *zchus* connected to *waiving the mishkav hatzadik*.

It is stated in the Midrashim of Chazal that "The Patriarchs and Matriarchs went to appease the Ribono shel Olam... but He was not appeased. Rochel entered and said before Him: 'Ribono shel Olam, whose mercy is greater—Yours or the mercy of flesh and blood? You must say that Your mercy is greater. And did I not bring my rival into my home? For all the labor that Yaakov worked for my father, he worked only for me. When I came to enter the chuppah, they brought in my sister. And not only was I silent, but *I handed over the signs to her*. You, too, if Your children brought Your rival into Your home, be silent for them.' 'And if I, who am flesh and blood... did not become jealous of my rival... then You, the living and eternal King... why are You jealous of idolatry, which has no substance?'"

[Especially since, regarding the Ribono shel Olam, the concept of jealousy does not apply at all, for the Ribono shel Olam is the true reality, whose existence is from His own essence, unlike a created being, for whom it is only *felt* that his existence is from his own essence.]

And it concludes there: "Immediately, the mercy of the Ribono shel Olam was stirred, and He said: '*For your sake, Rochel*, I will return Israel to their place.' This is what is written: 'A voice is heard on high, lamentation, bitter weeping, Rochel weeping for her children because they are not,' and it is written: 'Thus says Hashem: Restrain your voice from weeping and your eyes from tears, for there is a reward for your labor, etc.,' and it is written: 'And there is hope for your future, says Hashem, and the children shall return to their border.' 'You have learned well how to plead as a defense attorney; there is a reward for your labor and your righteousness in that you handed over your signs to your sister.'"

#### 61

Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: Rochel’s act of handing over the signs to her sister signifies *waiving the mishkav hatzadik*, which is a matter of *deficiency* [to the point that she was punished for waiving the *mishkav hatzadik* (for the mandrakes) for one night only]. How can this act be considered a *ma'alah*, to the point that in its merit the Ribono shel Olam will return Israel to their place?

The explanation for this is that this is precisely the point: Since the "mishkav hatzadik" is a spiritual matter of the highest order, which one should never waive, and nevertheless, Rochel agreed to waive it and handed the signs to her sister—meaning she gave up not only her physicality but also her spirituality—and all this was in order "to be of help to her children," so that she could plead for mercy for them—this is considered the *greatest ma'alah*. And the Ribono shel Olam promises: "*For your sake, Rochel*, I will return Israel to their place," "and the children shall return to their border."

**D.** Based on the above, we can explain the connection and affinity of Rochel with the Patriarchs—Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, and Rochel:

Just as the "Patriarchs" belong to all of Bnei Yisrael, so too does Rochel belong (not only to the two tribes, Yosef and Binyamin, who descended from her, but) to *all of Bnei Yisrael*—because Rochel sacrificed herself so that she could plead for mercy for all of Bnei Yisrael, and in her merit the Ribono shel Olam promises "the children shall return to their border," which is a matter that pertains to all of Bnei Yisrael.

It should be added that beyond Rochel’s efforts on behalf of *all of Bnei Yisrael*, in that she "weeps and pleads for mercy for them," she also exerts herself for the *Shechinah*—as hinted in the language of the verse, "Rochel weeping for her children because they are *not*." Although, on the face of it, it should have said "because they are *not* [plural]," the Zohar explains, "Because the *husband*... has departed from her, etc." That is, Rochel is (also) weeping over the *absence of the revelation of the Shechinah*, and consequently, she brings about (in addition to "the children shall return to their border") the restoration of the revelation of the Shechinah, which will take place in the future Redemption.

***

**E.** In the *sicha* printed in the *Kuntres* for the holiday of Pesach, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, says that before the revelation of Moshiach there are "birth pangs," and in order to hasten the birth, there must be a breaking of boundaries. This is achieved through joy, for joy breaks boundaries.

#### 62

He explains there that the joy must be regarding the good of the other, for the other is certainly good.

—It should be noted that in these days, we have already emerged from the birth pangs, and now there needs to be only the matter of joy, and through this, one can even in a short time bring about the coming of Moshiach.—

In accordance with this, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was accustomed on the last day of Pesach to instruct that a dance of Moshiach ("Moshiach’s tantz") be danced.

—Due to various reasons, I did not want to do so on the last day of Pesach itself... In any case, this should be completed on this Shabbos, which is still a continuation of the last day of Pesach, and therefore, we shall now dance "Moshiach’s tantz."

May it be Hashem’s will that through this, all matters will be drawn down in the manner of "And I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no room for more."

[The Rebbe danced with the entire congregation in a circle—"Moshiach’s tantz."]

***

**F.** My father-in-law, the Rebbe, was accustomed to wish (during this period) a healthy summer ("A gezuntn zumer").

—In the early years, he was accustomed to preface this by saying that in Poland it is customary to wish a healthy summer, but in recent years he would not say any introduction or justification, but would simply wish: "A healthy summer."

It should be added that the intention here is not only regarding physical matters, but also regarding spiritual matters:

It is the way of the world—and this is also true among Bnei Yisrael—that during the summer days, one occupies oneself with matters of bodily health. And since "the body being healthy and whole is one of the ways of (the service of) Hashem" (as per the ruling of the Rambam), it is understood that the health of the body during the summer days must be in a manner that also adds to spiritual matters.

#### 63

(And the Rebbe concluded:) A healthy summer in both physical and spiritual matters.

***

**G.** [After Mincha, the Rebbe said:]

I once entered my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the first Shabbos between Pesach and Atzeres, after Mincha, and he said to me: "Now one must take a Gemara from the Vilna Shas and learn Pirkei Avos." [And when I remarked that learning Pirkei Avos from the Vilna Shas would take a long time, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, replied and added,] "Saying or learning ('gezogt oder gelernt'), but not at length."

(And the Rebbe concluded:) Now one must say or learn Pirkei Avos.

**********

## With the help of Hashem. Lag B’Omer, 5711

#### 64

(Unedited transcript)

**"And you shall count for yourselves from the morrow after the Shabbos, from the day you bring the omer of the waving"**[1](#_ftn356). This means that first there is the mitzvah of bringing the omer of the waving, and afterwards the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer—a mitzvah to count the days and a mitzvah to count the weeks[2](#_ftn357)—since this mitzvah falls between the bringing of the omer and the festival of Shavuos. However, we must understand why the verse says "from the morrow after the Shabbos." On the face of it, since the intention is the morrow after Pesach[3](#_ftn358), it should have said "from the morrow after Pesach." Why is it stated as "from the morrow after the Shabbos"? Especially since the Tzedukim erred and claimed it meant the morrow after the weekly Shabbos, and the Sages of Israel had to debate them and bring proofs that the verse refers to the morrow after Pesach[3](#_ftn358). If so, why was "the morrow after Pesach" not explicitly stated in the text, but rather "the morrow after the Shabbos"?

b) **This can be understood** by first explaining the general concept of Sefiras HaOmer. It is stated in the Mishnah[4](#_ftn359) that all meal-offerings come from wheat, but this one (the meal-offering of jealousy) comes from barley, and likewise the omer meal-offering comes from barley. Now, the reason the meal-offering of jealousy comes from barley—animal fodder—is explained in the Mishnah there: just as her deed was an animal act, so too her offering is animal food. But it still requires explanation why the omer meal-offering differs from all other meal-offerings in that it specifically comes from barley. The explanation for this is known[5](#_ftn360): it is because the avodah of the omer meal-offering is the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis*.

**The explanation of the matter**[5](#_ftn360) is that the revelation that occurred on the first day of Pesach was in the category of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) on His own initiative[6](#_ftn361). As it is written[7](#_ftn362), "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Hashem on this mountain"—meaning that the avodah from below to above began only after the Exodus, whereas at the time of the Exodus, the arousal was from above to below. This is the meaning of the verse[8](#_ftn363), "Draw me, we will run after you; the King has brought me into his chambers." "Draw me" refers to the revelations of the Exodus, which were by way of *is'arusa d'le'eila*, for the King of Kings was revealed to them.

#### 65

This means that while the Jewish people were themselves mired in the forty-nine gates of impurity[10](#_ftn365), He was revealed to them, and so on—this is the concept of "Draw me," from above to below. This is also why it says "Draw me" in the singular, because the revelation from above effected a shift only in the *nefesh elokis*, for only the *nefesh elokis* senses the revelation from above, whereas the *nefesh habehamis* remained in its status and position. This is also the meaning of the verse[11](#_ftn366) regarding the Exodus, "For the people fled." Our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains[12](#_ftn367) that this seems puzzling: why was this necessary? If they had told Pharaoh to let them go free forever, would he not have been forced to let them go? Rather, it was because the evil in the souls of the Jewish people was still in its full strength. That is, since the revelation from above effected a shift only in the *nefesh elokis*, while the *nefesh habehamis* remained in its strength, the *nefesh habehamis* necessitated the matter of haste and flight. All of this is because the revelation of the Exodus was by way of from above to below, and the Jewish people, on their own, were not vessels for this; therefore, the revelation was felt only in the *nefesh elokis*. However, after the revelation of the Exodus, there was the matter of Sefiras HaOmer, which is the avodah from below to above. Regarding this it says, "We will run after you"—meaning that this is not in the manner of "Draw me," from above to below, but in a manner where the running is from one's own self (*allein loifen*), which is the avodah from below to above. And since the avodah is from below to above, it pertains also to the *nefesh habehamis*; therefore, it says "we will run" in the plural, for this effects a shift also in the *nefesh habehamis*. This is also the precision of "we will run" (*nerutzah*), specifically from the word *merutzah* (running/haste). For when the avodah is also from the side of the *nefesh habehamis*, it is by way of *merutzah*, because the nature of the *nefesh habehamis* is that when it is drawn to something, it is specifically by way of *merutzah*. That is, for the *nefesh habehamis*, there is no such thing as going slowly; it is only by way of *merutzah*. It is a matter of "either/or": either it is not drawn to matters of *Elokus* at all, or it is drawn to them by way of *merutzah* (meaning, when one influences it to be drawn to *Elokus*, it happens for it by way of *merutzah*). Furthermore, when the *nefesh habehamis* is drawn to *Elokus* by way of *merutzah*, this effects the quality of *merutzah* also in the *nefesh elokis*. That is, the *nefesh elokis* on its own does not have the quality of *merutzah*, and its attraction to *Elokus* is with measure and limitation; but through the *nefesh habehamis*, an addition of light is added to it, so that the quality of *merutzah* is created within it, above measure and limitation. This is why it says "we will run" in the plural—that the quality of *merutzah* is (not only in the *nefesh habehamis*, but) also in the *nefesh elokis*. The general concept of "We will run after you" refers to the avodah of refining the *nefesh habehamis*, which is the general avodah of Sefiras HaOmer, which is from below to above, and this is the preparation for the matter of the Giving of the Torah: "The King has brought me into his chambers."

#### 66

c) **More specifically**, in the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis* there are two matters: the refinement of the *mochin* (intellect) and the refinement of the *midos* (emotions), and these are the two matters of the offering of the omer and the counting of the omer[13](#_ftn368). The offering of the omer is the refinement of the *mochin* of the *nefesh habehamis*. For in addition to the general concept that the omer meal-offering comes from barley—animal fodder—which indicates the refinement of the *nefesh habehamis*, the offering comes from grain even within the category of animal fodder, which indicates the *mochin*, as is understood from the words of our Sages[14](#_ftn369), "A child does not know how to call 'Abba' until he tastes the taste of grain." This is the *mochin* of the *nefesh habehamis*, for since its essence is *midos*, its *mochin* are also connected and related to the *midos*. This is why the grain (*mochin*) is also animal fodder (*mochin* that belong to the *midos*). After the offering of the omer, which is the refinement of the *mochin* of the *nefesh habehamis*, comes the avodah of refining the *midos* of the *nefesh habehamis* through Sefiras HaOmer: to count the days and to count the weeks. That is, the offering of the omer, which is the refinement of the *mochin* that belong to the *midos*, is on the first day only, the 16th of Nissan. But Sefiras HaOmer, which is the refinement of the *midos* themselves—for this, a general refinement is not enough. Rather, there must be a specific refinement: to refine each *midah* individually. Furthermore, the refinement must be in the finest detail: to refine each *midah* as it is comprised of all seven *midos*. That is, the general refinement is only by way of *makif* (encompassing) and does not touch upon the practical, and the essence is the avodah done slowly, specifically through one's own power. This is the refinement in the finest detail, as each *midah* is comprised of all seven *midos*, through which the avodah is done in such a way that "in all your ways you shall know Him"[15](#_ftn370), so that all the details of thought, speech, and action will be as they should be. This is why the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer is not just to count the weeks—which is the refinement of each *midah* in a general sense—but the essence is to count the days, which is the refinement of the *midos* in detail: *Chesed* of *Chesed*, and so on, *Hod* of *Hod*, and so on, until *Malchus* of *Malchus*. In this, we can explain the opinion of Rabbeinu Yeruchem[16](#_ftn371) that in this time there is a distinction between the mitzvah to count the days and the mitzvah to count the weeks. There are those who say[17](#_ftn372) that even in the time of exile, the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer is *d'oraisa* (Torah law), and there are those who say[18](#_ftn373) that in the time of exile, it is only *d'rabanan* (Rabbinic law). However, Rabbeinu Yeruchem[16](#_ftn371) distinguishes between counting the days and counting the weeks: that the counting of the days, even in this time, is *d'oraisa*, but the counting of the weeks is *d'rabanan*. One can explain this based on the above: that the counting of the weeks is the refinement of the general *midah*, and the counting of the days is the refinement of every detail

#### 67

and detail within each *midah*. Accordingly, the counting of the days, which is the refinement of all the details of the *midos*, since this matter pertains to the avodah in practice—in thought, speech, and action (as mentioned above)—which must be and is present at all times and in all seasons, therefore the obligation of counting the days is *d'oraisa* even in this time. This is not the case for the counting of the weeks, which is the refinement of the general *midah*, which does not pertain to the avodah in practice in thought, speech, and action. Even though there is a higher quality in this regarding the avodah of counting the days—since it is the refinement of the *midah* in its totality, which is a higher level—on the other hand, since it is a higher avodah that does not pertain to practical action, in this time we do not have the power to refine the general *midah*, and the power given to us is only for that which pertains to the avodah in practice.

d) **The explanation of the matter of the inclusion of the *midos***[19](#_ftn374)—how each *midah* is comprised of the seven *midos*. For example, in the *midah* of *Chesed*: in addition to the general *midah* of *Chesed* itself, whose essence is the love of Hashem, it is also comprised of all the *midos*. The concept of *Chesed* of *Chesed* is that because of his love for Hashem, he loves those who love Hashem; when he sees someone engaged in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with fear of Heaven, he is aroused with love for him. Likewise, because of his love for Hashem, his engagement in all matters pertaining to Torah and *mitzvos* is with alacrity. The concept of *Gevurah* of *Chesed* is that his love for Hashem is expressed in the opposite line: he hates those who oppose Hashem. The concept of *Tiferes* of *Chesed* is the beauty that comes from *Chesed*: when he sees someone learning Torah and fulfilling *mitzvos* with pleasantness and sweetness (*mit a geshmak*), he glories in the beauty of Torah and *mitzvos*, to what extent (*oif wifil*) the Torah can affect a person. In addition to the inclusion of the primary *midos* (*Chagas*), the branches of the *midos* (*Nehi*) are also included in *Chesed*. *Netzach* of *Chesed* means that because of his love for Hashem, even when there are obstacles and hindrances, he overcomes himself to stand against every obstacle, and so on. Furthermore, when there is opposition from the outside and he lacks the strength, and so on—"for many rise up against me"[20](#_ftn375)—because of his love for Hashem, he fights the opponents, and so on; this is the concept of *Hod* of *Chesed*. The concept of *Yesod* of *Chesed* is that even when, for some reason, he has no attraction to Torah and *mitzvos*, because of his love for Hashem, he connects to it with all the movements of his soul, until he is aroused with a desire for Torah and *mitzvos*, and until all his thoughts, speech, and action are only in Torah and *mitzvos*; this is the concept of *Malchus* of *Chesed*. Just as the *midah* of *Chesed* is comprised of all the *midos*, so it is with all the *midos*: each *midah* is comprised of all the *midos*.

#### 68

**Now, just as** in the *nefesh elokis* each *midah* is comprised of the seven *midos*, so it is also in the *nefesh habehamis*, for "Hashem has made one corresponding to the other"[21](#_ftn376). Just as in the *midah* of *Chesed*: *Chesed* of *Chesed* means that his love for material things is expressed in an open desire for materiality. *Gevurah* of *Chesed* means that because of his love for material things, he hates anyone who opposes him in this matter; when they say to him, "How does it befit you to be immersed in animalistic matters that are not according to the dignity of man?", he hates them. *Tiferes* of *Chesed* means that in addition to his attraction to material things, he also glories and boils (*er barimt zich un kokt zich*) in the fact that he is attracted to material things. The concept of *Netzach* of *Chesed* means that even when, for some reason, he lacks the attraction to material things, he overcomes himself to generate desire, and so on. Furthermore, even when there is opposition from the outside—that they shame and disgrace him, saying, "See how a Jew, a son of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, is immersed in animalistic matters, and even more so in forbidden matters"—he fights so that this will not disturb his desire; this is the concept of *Hod* of *Chesed*. And his desire grows so much that he comes to a state of connection with the desire; this is the concept of *Yesod* of *Chesed*, until even his thoughts, speech, and action are in material matters, and thus he goes from bad to worse, until he comes to forbidden matters; this is the concept of *Malchus* of *Chesed*.

e) **The essence** of the refinement of the details of the *midos* is completed on the day of Lag B’Omer[22](#_ftn377), which is the level of *Hod* of *Hod*, which is the end of the primary *midos*. The concept of this is that *Hod* of *Hod* is the lowest level in the matter of *hoda'ah* (acknowledgment/gratitude) itself—that he acknowledges that it is so, even though he does not understand it with his intellect. An example of this: there is a great sage whose wisdom is wondrous to the eyes of all people, and there is also a small sage who, although he has a general connection to the matter of intellect, also does not understand the wondrous wisdom of the great sage. Nevertheless, since he has a connection to intellect, even though he does not understand the wisdom he hears from the great sage, he sees that this is a most wondrous intellectual matter. Therefore, it is true that one cannot say he knows or grasps the thing, but in any case, he acknowledges (even though he does not understand) that he must nullify himself before him. This is because he feels that this is a most wondrous intellectual matter, and since he has a connection to intellect, he understands that he must nullify himself before him, even though he does not know or grasp it. But a very simple person who has no connection to intellect at all—it is not appropriate to say of him even that he understands that he must acknowledge and nullify himself to the great sage. That he acknowledges and nullifies himself—this matter itself is for him by way of *hoda'ah*. This is the concept of

#### 69

*Hod* of *Hod*, acknowledgment of acknowledgment, that the matter of *hod* (*hoda'ah*) itself is not from *Chabad* or from *Chagas*, but from *hoda'ah* alone. As we say in the *Modim D'Rabanan* prayer: "We acknowledge You... for that we acknowledge You"—acknowledgment of acknowledgment. This is the final level in holiness, regarding which our Sages said[23](#_ftn378), "Whoever does not bow during *Modim* will not rise for the resurrection of the dead." For even when he does not have the matter of knowledge, since he knows at the very least that he must acknowledge, then he has hope. And even if he does not have this knowledge either, but can effect in himself to acknowledge from *hoda'ah* alone without knowledge, he is at the very least at the level of *Hod* of *Hod*, and he has hope. But "whoever does not bow during *Modim*," who lacks even the matter of acknowledgment of acknowledgment, then his spine turns into a snake[23](#_ftn378)—meaning he has no connection to matters of holiness.

**With this** we can understand the connection of Lag B’Omer to Rashbi. The work of Rashbi was to connect the "depth of the height" with the "depth of the depth" (as explained above[24](#_ftn379)). Therefore, the revelation of the "depth of the height" up to the root of its root, above and beyond, was on Lag B’Omer, which is the counting of *Hod* of *Hod*. This is the lowest level in avodah, in which the avodah of refining the primary *midos* is completed, and then the opening of the channel can occur for the drawing down and revelation of the root of its root, above and beyond, through which a revelation of the inner dimension of the Torah will reach all of Israel. The power to effect the opening of the channel for this is through the avodah of *Hod* of *Hod*, which is the concept of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), the yoke of Torah[25](#_ftn380) (as explained above[26](#_ftn381)). That is, he does not take into account the limitations of time and place, and his general avodah is entirely not according to reason and intellect. Therefore, not only do place and time not conceal and hide from him, but on the contrary, even in time and place he effects the matter of "And you shall count for yourselves."

f) **This is also** the meaning of "And you shall count for yourselves from the morrow after the Shabbos" specifically. The concept of this is that the general order of *hishtalshelus* (the chain of progression) is established in the level of priority and delay, *mati v'lo mati* (reaching and not reaching)[27](#_ftn382), and in general terms, this is the matter of times and the order of times[28](#_ftn383). However, in order for the matter of "And you shall count for yourselves" to be possible—to refine the entire order of *hishtalshelus* down to the very bottom, into the depth of the depth—the power for this is "from the morrow after the Shabbos," a level that is above the general concept of time[29](#_ftn384). The highest level in the matter of time is

#### 70

Shabbos, for after the six days of the week comes the day of Shabbos, which is sanctified above all days, for "Shabbos is sanctified and exists"[30](#_ftn385). But even so, this is still a matter within time, as it is written[31](#_ftn386), "For six days... and on the seventh day He rested and was refreshed." And since this is still within the category of time, even though it is a time of holiness, it is sufficient to elevate oneself, but it is not enough to overturn the foolishness of the *sitra achra*. Therefore, when there needs to be "And you shall count for yourselves," which is the refinement down to the depth of the depth, the power for this is *from the morrow* after the Shabbos, a level even above the matter of "Shabbos is sanctified and exists," a level that is above the order of *hishtalshelus*.

**The concept of this** is that at the time of the Exodus from Egypt, there was an arousal from above regarding the matter of "For the people fled," and regarding the general preparation for the Giving of the Torah, through the power that the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, was revealed to them and redeemed them. As the author of the Haggadah says[32](#_ftn387), "I, and not an angel; I, and not a seraph; I, and not a messenger; I am He and no other"—the Holy One, Blessed be He, in His glory and essence. This means[33](#_ftn388) that since they were mired in the forty-nine gates of impurity, if someone else had come—even from the highest levels of holiness—not only would he not have been able to bring the Jewish people out from there, but on the contrary, and so on. Therefore, it was necessary for the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, Himself to come, for He has no connection at all to the order of *hishtalshelus*. This is what is meant by[34](#_ftn389) "And Hashem passed over," which is the concept of the leap above the order of *hishtalshelus*[35](#_ftn390). Likewise, when the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer was given to the Jewish people for all times, they were told that the empowerment to be able to have "And you shall count for yourselves"—that all forty-nine days will be counted, refined, and purified[36](#_ftn391)—is from the morrow after the Shabbos, from a level that is entirely above the order of *hishtalshelus*, even in the levels of holiness, above even the Shabbos that is sanctified and exists. And when it is drawn from the morrow after the Shabbos, and the avodah of "And you shall count for yourselves" is performed, then one finally arrives at "The King has brought me into his chambers," which refers to the Giving of the Torah, at which time there was the matter of "I wrote and gave My own self"[37](#_ftn392), that the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (Essence and Being) of the *Ein Sof* was given to us (*m'hot unz opgegebn*).

g) **However**, as a preparation for this, there is in the meantime the matter of Lag B’Omer, at which time there is a revelation of the inner dimension of the Torah[38](#_ftn393). That is, even though the order of *hishtalshelus* in the study of

#### 71

Torah is that one first studies the revealed dimension of Torah and afterwards arrives at the study of the inner dimension of Torah, nevertheless, one must know that the power to be able to have this order itself is through the fact that there is first the matter of Lag B’Omer. This is the concept of the revelation of the inner dimension of Torah, which gives the power so that the study of the revealed dimension of Torah will be as it should be, and also that through the revealed dimension of Torah, one will arrive at the inner dimension of Torah. The concept of this is that King David requested, "Open my eyes, that I may behold wonders from Your Torah"[39](#_ftn394). Even though he studied not only the revealed dimension of Torah but also the inner dimension of Torah, nevertheless, he did not reach the matter of "wonders from Your Torah," because this is a matter that will be revealed only in the time to come[40](#_ftn395), as it is written[41](#_ftn396), "As in the days of your coming out of the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders," *Nun* (50) wonders[42](#_ftn397), which is the concept of the fiftieth gate that will be revealed in the time to come[43](#_ftn398). However, the beginning of this exists already starting from Lag B’Omer, through Rashbi, who opened the channel to be able to "Open my eyes, that I may behold wonders from Your Torah." Especially on the day of his passing, *Lag* B’Omer[44](#_ftn399), at which time there was the matter of "Open my eyes," for even though all his days he studied the secrets of the Torah, on the day of his passing he revealed hidden secrets that had not been revealed until then[45](#_ftn400], saying that there would not be a generation like his until the generation of Moshiach[46](#_ftn401), at which time the matter that Rashbi opened will be revealed.

**And according to** the known principle that every year all the matters and the general status and situation that occurred the first time are aroused once again[47](#_ftn402), when we stand on Lag B’Omer in a movement of connection to the study of the inner dimension of Torah, to walk in the path that Rashbi opened, and to draw this into the entire year, this is a preparation and introduction to the matter of the Giving of the Torah, "The King has brought me into his chambers." This is also the appropriate time to request and effect (*oisbetn*) that King David's request be fulfilled: "Open my eyes, that I may behold wonders from Your Torah"—that also in Your Torah, the study of the revealed dimension of Torah and the study of the secrets of the Torah, there will be a revelation of wonders, until the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, who will teach the inner dimension of Torah with all the Jewish people together[48](#_ftn403).

## Sicha of Lag B’Omer, 5711

#### 72

**A.** Lag B’Omer is the day of the Hilula of Rashbi.

While there has been discussion among the Rishonim and Acharonim regarding the general nature of Lag B’Omer—beginning with the dispute concerning the calculation of the *thirty-three days* during which mourning is observed for the death of the students of Rabbi Akiva, with some saying they are from the beginning of the Sefirah until Lag B’Omer (which leads to debate regarding the day of Lag B’Omer itself, and especially the night of Lag B’Omer), and others saying they begin after Rosh Chodesh Iyar until the end of the Sefirah, as R’ Nechemiah of Dubrovna brings in his well-known responsum regarding the many differences of opinion among the Poskim—

The conclusion, however—as stated by R’ N. of Dubrovna —is that "all the pressure and distress that all the aforementioned Poskim felt and were entangled in is only because they did not find a reason and root for the greatness of Lag B’Omer... But it is already known through the holy one of Hashem, the Arizal... that on that day Rashbi, of blessed memory, died... Matters that are well-known do not require proof, for the matter of the Hilula of Rashbi on Lag B’Omer has already been publicized throughout the world for many generations."

**B.** We must explain the unique greatness of Rashbi (the master of the Hilula of Lag B’Omer) by first explaining the greatness of the five great students of Rabbi Akiva (of whom Rashbi is one), who "established Torah" and through whom "the world was sustained".

The precision of the phrase "established Torah" should be explained in the manner and likeness of the Sages' statement (regarding Dovid) that he "established the yoke of Torah". "Yoke" (*ol*) specifically denotes the concept of *kabalas ol* (accepting the yoke) in the study of Torah. For even though Torah is "your wisdom and your understanding in the eyes of the nations", even according to human intellect, nevertheless, Torah study must be not from the perspective of intellect, but specifically from the perspective of *kabalas ol*.

As the Sages said (regarding Dovid), "And Hashem was with him, that the Halacha is according to his view"—meaning, in order for the "Halacha to be according to his view," there must be "Hashem was with him," to be connected with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of Hashem, the Name *Havayah*, He who was, is, and will be as one. Then, Torah study is performed not from the perspective of intellect, but out of *kabalas ol* and fear of Heaven, knowing that the Torah is the *wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He*.

And through the fact that "they established Torah" ("the yoke of Torah," studying Torah through *kabalas ol*), "the world was sustained" through them:

The Sages said, "The Holy One, Blessed be He, looked into the Torah and created the world; a person looks into the Torah and sustains the world." This means that the existence of the world depends on Torah. From this, it is also understood regarding those who study Torah, that the manner of their study (their feeling in Torah) acts upon and influences the manner of their conduct in the world.

Therefore, when Torah study is through *kabalas ol*, "Hashem is with him," this also acts upon his conduct in the world—that even when he goes out to engage in the affairs of the world (after davening and Torah study), from the high roof to the deep pit, the state and condition of "Know before Whom you are standing" (during davening) and "Hashem is with him" (during Torah study) is drawn down for him.

**C.** This matter is especially connected with the study of the inner dimension of Torah (*Pnimiyus HaTorah*):
