The primary difference between the study of the revealed Torah (*Nigleh*) and the study of the inner Torah is that in the study of *Nigleh*, even though one knows that this is the Torah of the Holy One, Blessed be He (as emphasized in the text of the blessing over the Torah: "Who chose us from all the nations and gave us His Torah"), His wisdom and His will, nevertheless, in the study itself ("*lernendik*"), he is studying about *physical matters* (for the Torah "traveled and descended... until it was clothed in physical matters and affairs of this world, which are the majority of the mitzvos of the Torah and their laws"), such as "two holding a garment," "one who exchanges a cow for a donkey," and the like. Consequently, there is

#### 74

a need for great exertion ("*horeven un areinkneln mit zich*") so that it is felt in the study that this is His wisdom and His will. This is not so in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, where the study itself is regarding *matters of Elokus*.

It should be added that the difference between the study of *Nigleh* and *Pnimiyus HaTorah* is also hinted at in the difference of language between the Shas (*Nigleh*) and the Zohar (*Pnimiyus HaTorah*). The common language in Shas is "*Ta shema*" (Come and hear), and the common language in the Zohar is "*Ta chazi*" (Come and see)—analogous to the difference between hearing (*Ta shema*) and seeing (*Ta chazi*), for "hearing is not like seeing". This hints that in the study of *Nigleh*, the feeling of *Elokus* is only in the manner of *hearing* (knowledge and understanding), while in the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the feeling of *Elokus* is in the manner of *seeing*.

Correspondingly, there is a difference in the feeling of *Elokus* in the affairs of the world ("looks into the Torah and sustains the world")—that through the study of *Nigleh* without *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the feeling of *Elokus* in worldly affairs is only in the manner of hearing, meaning that he hears, knows, and understands that worldly affairs are also permeated with *Elokus*, but he lacks the *seeing* of the matter. Only through the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* does the feeling of *Elokus* in worldly affairs become in the manner of *seeing* ("*Ta chazi*"), that even in worldly affairs he *sees* *Elokus* tangibly, through seeing *Hashgacha Pratis* at every step ("*wou er shteit un wou er geit*"), in the world in general and in his portion of the world in particular, seeing with physical eyes the manner of the Holy One, Blessed be He’s conduct with him for the good, in children, life, and abundant sustenance.

**D.** Based on this, it is understood that among the five students (who "established Torah" and through whom "the world was sustained") themselves, the greatness of Rashbi is the greatest:

The primary innovation of Rashbi is in the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the "Tree of Life". Certainly, Rashbi also studied *Nigleh*, to the point that "in every chapter of the tractates in Shas, Rabbi Shimon is mentioned" (an anonymous "Rabbi Shimon" is Rashbi), but his primary

#### 75

study was in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, to the extent that even his study of *Nigleh* was connected with *Pnimiyus HaTorah* —that he would find the inner dimension in all matters of *Nigleh*, or that his study of *Nigleh* was from the outset from the perspective of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (analogous to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding the study of *Nigleh* in the time to come, "that they will know from the inner Torah all the bodies of the revealed Torah").

From this it is understood that the essence and perfection of the matter of "they established Torah," through which "the world was sustained" (which is connected with *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, as mentioned in section G), was accomplished by Rashbi.

**E.** And in this, there is an added emphasis on Lag B’Omer—the day of the Hilula of Rashbi:

The nature of the day of the Hilula is that all the *avodah* he performed during his lifetime in this world is elevated on the day of the Hilula to its root and source. From this it is understood that on Lag B’Omer, an ascent is made "to the beginning and head of all his levels (in the category of attainments in the secrets of Torah)... the root of his root in the heights of greatness in the most elevated level, above and beyond".

And this matter is accomplished on Lag B’Omer, the *Sefirah* of *Hod sheb'Hod*, which is the lowest level—for "every light that is most elevated cannot come into revelation below except in the most lowest level specifically... for the value of the depth of the bottom is according to the value of the depth of the height".

From this it is understood that the nature of Rashbi is to connect and join the *depth of the height* (the ultimate ascent in all his *avodah* in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*) with the *depth of the bottom* (*Hod sheb'Hod*)—due to the greatness and intensity of his connection with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He (as he said about himself, "I am bound in one knot with the Holy One, Blessed be He..."), Who is above and beyond without end, and below and below without limit, which is why it is in his power and ability to connect and join the depth of the height with the depth of the bottom.

In the terminology used above—that through Torah study out of *kabalas ol*, the study of

#### 76

*Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the connection of the depth of the height with the depth of the bottom is accomplished, starting from the depth of the bottom of the intellect, and reaching the depth of the bottom of worldly affairs, so that even in worldly affairs there will be the feeling of *Elokus*.

**F.** It should be added that after the action of Rashbi in opening the channel for the revelation of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, what was said above is relevant to the *avodah* of every Jew:

In the time of Rashbi, the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* was relevant only to individuals of distinction, and only in a hidden manner, not in public. But in these days, the "heels of Moshiach," the Arizal writes that "in these last generations, it is permitted and a mitzvah to reveal (in public) this wisdom".

And all this was added to even more in the time of the Baal Shem Tov, through whom *Pnimiyus HaTorah* was clothed in the light of the general Torah of Chassidus, and in the time of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, in the light of the Torah of Chabad Chassidus, until it became a paved path for all the Children of Israel, as the words of the Rebbe Rayatz that the Alter Rebbe did not want to make the Torah of Chassidus into a faction, but rather an inheritance for all the Children of Israel.

And after the opening of the channel and the paving of the path in the revelation of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* as it was clothed in the Torah of Chassidus, certainly the power and ability is given to every Jew to reach the state and condition of "*Ta chazi*," that even in worldly affairs he can see *Elokus* tangibly, and even to the recognition ("*derhern*") that "Hashem is One", and "there is nothing else besides Him".

However, for this, a person must exert himself a little ("*a bisel tzu-horeven*"), as the Sages said, "A person sanctifies himself a little below, they sanctify him much from above." This means that through a person's *avodah* in the manner of *is'arusa d'lesata* (below) to sanctify himself even "*a little*" only, then an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (from above) is drawn down to sanctify him "*much*."

And more than this—"A person sanctifies himself a little below in this world, they sanctify him much from above *for the World to Come*". It can be said that the meaning of this is that even *now in this world* (and even in the double and redoubled darkness of the time of exile) the level of holiness of the *World to Come* is drawn down to him, analogous to what the Sages said regarding the Patriarchs, that "the Holy One, Blessed be He, gave them a taste in this world of the World to Come." Similarly, we find among several Amoraim that they would be blessed with "May you see your world in your lifetime". From this it is understood that a taste of this is relevant also to every Jew.

***

**G.** *Maamar* on the verse "And you shall count for yourselves..."

***

**H.** The custom of Israel is known (which is "Torah") that on Lag B’Omer, the Jewish children, students of the *cheder*, go out to the field and play with a bow.

In explaining the reason for the custom, we must preface:

It is stated in the *sefarim* that since "all the days of Rashbi the rainbow was not seen in the cloud," because "his merit protected the generation and there was no need to show the rainbow in the cloud", therefore, on the day of the passing of Rashbi, Lag B’Omer, they play with a bow, to show that since the passing of Rashbi there is a need for a rainbow.

However, according to this reason, it turns out that playing with a bow on Lag B’Omer is a sign *for the worse* (since the need for a rainbow indicates an undesirable state and condition).

There is an explanation of the sign of the rainbow *for the better* —based on what is written in the Zohar (and in *Tikkunei Zohar*), "Do not look for the feet of Moshiach until this rainbow is seen... in bright colors... and then look for him for Moshiach." This means that seeing the rainbow in bright colors is a sign that the time for the coming of Moshiach has arrived, the feet of Moshiach ("*s'iz shoin do afilu di 'regalim' fun Moshiach'n*").

And since Lag B’Omer is the day of the Hilula of Rashbi, through whom there was

#### 78

the opening of the channel for the revelation of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (as mentioned in sections D-F), and even to the manner of "your springs shall spread outward," which is the preparation, the introduction, and the vessel for the coming of Moshiach —therefore, it is customary to play on this day with a bow, to hint at the rainbow in bright colors, the sight of which is the sign for the feet of Moshiach.

**I.** It should be added and explained that the relevance of the custom of playing with the bow on Lag B’Omer is *specifically to the students of the cheder*:

It will be understood by prefacing another matter regarding Lag B’Omer in connection *to the students*—that on Lag B’Omer the students of Rabbi Akiva (the teacher of Rashbi) stopped dying, for they did not treat each other with respect. Therefore, this day was established as a day of joy and remembrance for all the students, children of Torah, those who study Torah, to know and remember that they must treat each other with respect (the appropriate conduct through which the accusation against the students of Rabbi Akiva ceased).

**J.** The matter in this is that the two manners of conduct mentioned above (treating each other with respect or the opposite) come as a result of two manners of Torah study. There is a manner of study that leads to treating each other with respect, and there is a manner of study that leads to not treating each other with respect:

When the approach to Torah study is out of the knowledge and recognition that the Torah is the *wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He*, and consequently, the vitality and enthusiasm ("*der koch*") in the study is (not from the feeling itself, *yeshus* and pride, Heaven forbid, but) from the fact that he learns, understands, and innovates *in the wisdom of the Holy One, Blessed be He*—he will certainly not be resentful that his friend succeeds in Torah study no less and perhaps even better than him. Furthermore, even if his friend refutes his words and proves to him that he erred in his words, he will not only not be upset and angry at him, but on the contrary, he will thank him for saving him from error, falsehood, and lies (because the *Yetzer Hara* misled him to a crooked path, and his friend returns him to the straight path), and established him on the truth of the Torah of Hashem.

And when Torah study is in such a manner—then the conduct among the students is in a manner (that not only is there no room for jealousy and hatred, but on the contrary) that they adorn one another, and treat each other with respect.

Not so when the approach to Torah study is out of the thought that "my power and the strength of my hand made me this wealth", the *feeling itself*, ("*er tut oif*"), *he* asks a question, answers an answer, and challenges the words of so-and-so, and as a result, a feeling of *yeshus* is created in him, and sometimes also pride—then when his friend comes and corrects his error, or even just proves that he is able to say a better answer, which thereby diminishes his stature, he will certainly *be upset and angry at him*. For until now he thought that by his power and the strength of his hand he accomplished great things and made wealth in Torah, and he went around proclaiming "rejoice, my innards." And since so-and-so comes and shows that he had an error from the outset, that his wealth in Torah is nothing but imagined wealth, an imagined logic, a false logic, he is upset and angry at him.

And when Torah study is in such a manner—then the conduct among the students is in a manner of a lack of giving respect (they did not treat each other with respect).

—It should be noted that the above certainly does not apply to the students of Rabbi Akiva, for with them the conduct of a lack of giving respect to each other was from the root of the *Gevuros* and *Dinim* of *Katnus* as they are above, but after the *hishtalshelus* of the levels below, it came in a manner of simple resentment.

**K.** From this it is also understood regarding the study of Lag B’Omer—the remembrance regarding the students of Rabbi Akiva that must arouse the students to treat each other with respect:

When we say that there is a rule in Torah that Torah study must be in a manner that they treat each other with respect—it does not mean that Torah study can remain in the same manner as before and the change will only be in the detail of the custom of treating each other with respect. For the lack of the custom of treating each other with respect is *caused* by an undesirable manner of Torah study. Rather, it is necessary to establish ("*avekshteln*") the Torah study in such a manner that from the outset there will be no possibility for a state and condition of a lack of the custom of treating each other with respect, as mentioned, through the approach to Torah study being out of the knowledge and recognition that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He.

**L.** And the advice for this—the matter of the "bow":

It is explained in Chassidus that weapons are divided generally into two types—as the language of the verse in the words of Yaakov Avinu: "which I took from the hand of the Emorite with my sword

#### 80

and my bow"—*sword and bow*. And the difference between them is that with a "sword" one can strike only an enemy who is in close proximity (and one sees him with physical eyes), whereas with a "bow" one can strike even a hidden enemy who is in a distant place.

And its meaning in the *avodah* of Hashem—that it is not enough to be careful, to fight, and to defeat the enemy who is in close proximity, which refers to such matters that everyone knows clearly without any doubt that they are the counsel of the *Yetzer Hara*, from the *sitra achra*. Rather, one must also be careful of the hidden enemy in a distant place, and for this there is a need for a "*bow*," through which one can shoot an arrow at the enemy who is in a *distant place*.

And regarding our matter:

In order to ensure ("*bavwarenen*") that Torah study will be as it should be—Torah study specifically out of fear of Heaven (as explained in Tractate Shabbos)—there is a need to be careful and particular also regarding matters that are in a *distant place*, that is, such matters that seemingly *do not belong* to Torah study,

—as the Rebbe says that in order for Torah study to be out of fear of Heaven, there is a need for several preparations, such as, purification in a *mikveh*, giving *tzedakah*, davening at length, saying *Tehillim*, studying *Chumash* with Rashi (for this study opens the heart, and similarly regarding the study that opens the mind)—

Which seemingly is not understood: what is the relevance of all the aforementioned matters to Torah study?! On the contrary: if instead of these matters he would add another half hour in the study of Gemara, he would certainly accomplish more!

And the answer to this—that specifically through the aforementioned matters, whose action is seemingly far from Torah study, one can ensure that Torah study will be as it should be, like the parable of the bow, whose action (not only on an enemy standing close by, but also) on an enemy standing far away.

**M.** And another matter in the parable of the "bow":

We see tangibly—as is brought in the Torah of Chassidus —that in order for the shooting of the arrow by the bow to be in a more distant place, one must pull the string further down, closer to oneself, and the more the pulling of the string will be further down, and closer to oneself, the further the arrow will reach.

—The reason for emphasizing that this matter is brought in the Torah of Chassidus, in addition

#### 81

to the fact that we see it tangibly, is because in things that we see tangibly we do not know if they are true matters or untrue matters, and only when the matter is brought in Torah (and in this case, in the Torah of Chassidus), it is a sign that it is indeed the truth, or that this is a matter from which one can learn, etc.—

And its meaning in the *avodah* of Hashem—that the pulling of the bowstring further down and closer to his heart, indicates *bitul* and self-abasement, and through this the arrow reaches further, to nullify and subdue also the enemy who is in a distant place.

And similarly regarding Torah study—that the preparation for Torah study is *bitul* and self-abasement, to know that this is not "my power and the strength of my hand," but through the power of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and through this, Torah study becomes as it should be, as it is written, "And my soul shall be as dust to all (and through this) open my heart in Your Torah." And consequently, the more one adds in the fulfillment of the matter of "my soul shall be as dust to all," the more one will add in the fulfillment of the request that follows, "open my heart in Your Torah," in a better and faster manner ("*beser un shneler*").

**N.** Based on this, we can explain the content of the custom that the students of the *cheder* play with a bow on Lag B’Omer:

In the playing of the students of the *cheder* with a bow, it is hinted that there must be the matter of the bow in order to ensure that Torah study will be as it should be, as mentioned above at length.

And the empowerment for this is on Lag B’Omer, the day of the Hilula of Rashbi, whose primary matter is *Pnimiyus HaTorah*—for, through *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the approach ("*der tzugang*") to the study of *Nigleh* is created out of knowledge and recognition that the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He (and it goes without saying—the negation of the matter of "my power and the strength of my hand," through *bitul* and self-abasement), and out of fear of Heaven, for then the study is as it should be.

**O.** It should be added that when Torah study is as it should be (through *Pnimiyus HaTorah*), this is drawn down and acts in all matters—for with a Jew, all influences are drawn down through Torah—that all his affairs are accomplished with success, and without concealments and hiddenness, and furthermore, even undesirable matters are transformed for the good.

And it is hinted at in the story of the Gemara (in Tractate Moed Katan) regarding Rashbi:

"He (Rashbi) said to his son (R’ Elazar)... go to them (to two of his students)

#### 82

that they should bless you... They said to him, etc. When he came to his father, he said to him, not only did they not bless me, but they caused me distress (for they said to him words whose meaning is the opposite of a blessing). He said to him, what did they say to you? He said to him, this and this they said to me. He said to him, all of these are blessings, etc."

And it must be understood:

A) What is the need for the greatness of Rashbi specifically in order to interpret the words of the students that their intention is for a blessing, and why could R’ Elazar himself (even if he was still young) not interpret the words for the good?

B) And the main wonder is on the students of Rashbi: why did they need to bless him in such language that could lead to fear and panic, until he heard the interpretation of the words from his father?

And the answer to this—as explained in *Likkutei Torah* that "the blessing in such a manner is from the category of the *stum* (hidden)," which is a most elevated blessing, and therefore there is a need for caution against the *evil eye*, through hiding it in such language that is not understood even to the recipient of the blessing himself (for fear of the *evil eye* of the recipient of the blessing himself).

And only from the perspective of the greatness of Rashbi—whose matter is *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, and as mentioned above (section E) that his matter is to connect the depth of the height with the depth of the bottom, that even in the depth of the bottom the depth of the height is revealed—there is no place and need to fear and be careful of an undesirable matter, for, in the level of Rashbi, everything is good.

—Regarding *Nigleh*, the Sages said, "If he merits, it becomes for him a potion of life; if he does not merit, etc.," meaning, that there is also a possibility of a state and condition of "if he does not merit," for then it is the opposite of a potion of life, Heaven forbid. But regarding *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, the "Tree of Life", the matter of the opposite of a potion of life is not relevant at all (as explained at length in *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*)—

And therefore it is in the power and ability of Rashbi specifically to draw down the matter of the blessing even in the language of *Targum* and in language that appears openly as the opposite of a blessing—to reveal that this is the matter of a blessing, and a most elevated blessing.

**P.** (And the Rebbe concluded:)

This day, the day of Rashbi ("*Rashbi's tog*"), "the day of his joy",

#### 83

—It is told in *Pri Etz Chaim* (and brought in the *Acharonim*) regarding R’ Avraham Halevi (a student of the Arizal) who was accustomed to saying the prayer of *Nachem* every day. And when he did so on Lag B’Omer, the Arizal said to him in the name of Rashbi: "He said to me (Rashbi—many years after his passing! For this event was in the time of the Arizal, while Rashbi was in the time of the Tannaim), tell this man why he says *Nachem* on the day of my joy." Meaning, that Rashbi does not tolerate matters of the opposite (or even the lack) of joy, on Lag B’Omer, the day of his joy—

It is a day capable of conducting oneself in the order of the conduct of Rashbi (since then one can hold on ("*anhaltn zich*") to him)—that even such a matter that openly and in the language of *Targum* one could err and think that it is the opposite of a blessing, Rashbi transforms it and interprets it—below ten *tefachim*, and also in the language of *Targum*—in a manner of the ultimate good.

And therefore: even if at one time there was for someone room for a mistake or fear regarding a certain matter "that it is somehow not so"...—then they draw down for him the interpretation of the words in a manner of the *ultimate good*!

And the content of the interpretation—that now is the time of "Open my eyes and I will behold wonders from Your Torah", which is the matter of being above the order of *hishtalshelus*, and therefore, this is drawn down and revealed also in the depth of the bottom, that even a matter that appears as the opposite of a blessing, it is transformed into a blessing, as it is written, "And He transformed, etc., into a blessing," and one sees openly that this is the ultimate of blessing and the ultimate of good.

***

**Q.** *Maamar* on the verse "And you shall count for yourselves..."

***

**R.** It is known from the custom of Israel (which is "Torah") that on Lag B’Omer the Jewish children, students of the *cheder*, go out to the field and play with a bow.

And in explaining the reason for the custom—we must preface:

It is stated in the *sefarim* that since "all the days of Rashbi the rainbow was not seen in the cloud," because "his merit protected the generation and there was no need to show the rainbow in the cloud", therefore, on the day of the passing of Rashbi, Lag B’Omer, they play with a bow, to show that since the passing of Rashbi there is a need for a rainbow.

But, according to this reason, it turns out that playing with a bow on Lag B’Omer is a sign *for the worse* (since the need for a rainbow indicates an undesirable state and condition).

There is an explanation of the sign of the rainbow *for the better* —based on what is written in the Zohar (and in *Tikkunei Zohar*), "Do not look for the feet of Moshiach until this rainbow is seen... in bright colors... and then look for him for Moshiach." This means that seeing the rainbow in bright colors is a sign that the time for the coming of Moshiach has arrived, the feet of Moshiach ("*s'iz shoin do afilu di 'regalim' fun Moshiach'n*").

And since Lag B’Omer is the day of the Hilula of Rashbi, through whom there was

#### 78

the opening of the channel for the revelation of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (as mentioned in sections D-F), and even to the manner of "your springs shall spread outward," which is the preparation, the introduction, and the vessel for the coming of Moshiach —therefore, it is customary to play on this day with a bow, to hint at the rainbow in bright colors, the sight of which is the sign for the feet of Moshiach.

**S.** It should be added and explained that the relevance of the custom of playing with the bow on Lag B’Omer is *specifically to the students of the cheder*:

It will be understood by prefacing another matter regarding Lag B’Omer in connection *to the students*—that on Lag B’Omer the students of Rabbi Akiva (the teacher of Rashbi) stopped dying, for they did not treat each other with respect. Therefore, this day was established as a day of joy and remembrance for all the students, children of Torah, those who study Torah, to know and remember that they must treat each other with respect (the appropriate conduct through which the accusation against the students of Rabbi Akiva ceased).

**T.** The matter in this is that the two manners of conduct mentioned above (treating each other with respect or the opposite) come as a result of two manners of Torah study. There is a manner of study that leads to treating each other with respect, and there is a manner of study that leads to not treating each other with respect:

When the approach to Torah study is out of the knowledge and recognition that the

## 100

It is well known that our Sages of blessed memory state: "And you shall make them known to your children... the day that you stood before Hashem your G-d at Chorev." Just as there it was with awe, fear, trembling, and quaking, so too here (in every place and at every time) it must be with awe, fear, trembling, and quaking.

The Arizal explains: "Awe" refers to the mind of the person; "fear" to his heart; "trembling" to his internal organs; and "quaking" to his external limbs.

This means that when a person reads, reviews, or studies Torah, his entire being—his mind and heart, his internal and external self—must be in the same state that he was in at the time of the Giving of the Torah at Chorev.

And even though at that time they "saw the sounds and the torches," and "Hashem spoke with you face to face," how can every person draw this fear upon himself at all times? The answer is: when a person takes to heart that the Torah he is studying is an extension of *Chochmah Ila'ah*, and that the light of the *Ohr Ein Sof*—which is far above the category of *Seder Hishtalshelus*, where "before Him, darkness is as light," and where above and below, spirituality and physicality are equal—dwells and is *revealed* there, then it will be that just as it was there, so too here; everything is equal.

This means that it will be here below, in a revealed manner, to the ultimate degree, to hear from the mouth of the *Atzmus HaMatzil* Himself, "I am Hashem your G-d..." That it is here just as it was then—the possibility and the capacity for

## 101

this were granted at the time of the Giving of the Torah, when the decree was nullified that the upper realms should remain for the upper ones and the lower realms for the lower ones, for "Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai," and to Moshe He said, "Ascend to Hashem".

This matter recurs, and this empowerment is awakened every single year during the days of the festival of Shavuos, the "Time of the Giving of Our Torah"—"Giving" being in the present tense.

As a preface to this, it is incumbent upon us—upon each and every one of us—to accept upon ourselves that we will "do and we will hear," and to prioritize "doing" over "hearing"—as is well known and explained thoroughly in the teachings of the *Divrei Elokim Chayim*.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*21 Iyar, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## 102

**A.** It was discussed regarding the superiority of the mitzvah of milah over other mitzvos, in that the drawing down of holiness occurs within the physical limb of the human body, and in a manner of a continuous action that remains in the human body at all times — spoken by the Rebbe, and printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 3, pp. 759-760.

**B.** And one should add to this:

It is explained in the discourses of Chassidus that the mitzvah of milah is (unlike all positive mitzvos, where the act of performance is the "vessel" for drawing down the light, but rather) like negative mitzvos, through which extremely lofty lights are drawn down that cannot be contained within "vessels." Therefore, it is impossible to draw them down through [positive] action, and the person’s act is merely the negation of the opposing element. A parallel to this is the mitzvah of milah—the act of milah is nothing more than the removal of the orlah, that is, the removal of the obstructing element, rather than an act that serves as a "vessel" for drawing down the light.

And based on what was stated, that the mitzvah of milah is a continuous mitzvah that remains in the human body at all times—it is understood that this is also the case regarding the drawing down of the lofty lights that are not contained within "vessels." This is not a one-time drawing down, but a drawing down that remains in the human body at all times, and it acts not only in the spiritual realm, but also in the physical (just as the act of milah is in the physical flesh), in children, life, and ample sustenance.

***

**C.** In anticipation of the holiday of Shavuos, two maamarim are being published, which follow the maamarim published for the holiday of Pesach. And in the first maamar—the discourse beginning "Vayehi Bayom Hashmini"—the matter of milah is also discussed:

In the aforementioned maamar, the Rebbe Rayatz asks what is the concept of the "eighth day" for the inauguration (miluim), "For it is written, 'And you shall not go out from the door of the Tent of Meeting for seven days, until the day of the completion of the days of your inauguration, for seven days He shall fill your hand.'" From this it is implied that "the seven days themselves are the days of inauguration." What is the concept of the "filling" that fills the days of inauguration, and with what does it fill them, given that they themselves... are the days of inauguration? Why is there a need for an additional day of completion to fill them, beyond the fact that they are already full?

And the point of the explanation is—that even though the seven days of inauguration are themselves full days, full of light (for "day" denotes light), nevertheless, the eighth day of inauguration is added to them, which fills them (in addition to the fact that they are already full) *with a loftier light*.

And he brings a parallel to the concept of the "eighth" of inauguration—like the *eighth* of milah:

Regarding milah on the *eighth* day specifically—Chazal said, "So that one Shabbos may pass over it." This means that milah is higher than Shabbos, and therefore milah overrides Shabbos, because, being higher than Shabbos, it also includes the concept of Shabbos (similar to the principle that "a hundred is included in two hundred").

The explanation for this is—that the day of Shabbos, even though its level is greater than the six days of the week, as it is "holy and established," is still within the seven days of Bereishis, the seven days of creation [as is understood from what is written in the Midrash Rabbah on the verse "And Elokim finished on the seventh day: What was the world lacking? Rest. Shabbos came, rest came"], which are the *seven days of the cycle* that repeat in a loop ["For seemingly it is not understood why we always count day one, day two, day three, etc., for from the creation of the world until now there have already been thousands and myriads of days. Rather, they are the days of the cycle that repeat in a loop"—meaning, that every Shabbos a complete cycle is finished, and afterwards a new cycle begins, a new era]. In contrast, milah is on the *eighth* day, which is higher than the seven days of the cycle, *guarding the cycle*.

And he adds in the maamar that we find something similar regarding *Sefiras HaOmer*—a matter that is time-dependent, for we are now in the days of Sefiras HaOmer—that we count seven weeks, which are like the seven days of the cycle, and afterwards we arrive at the holiday of Shavuos, which is like the eighth day that guards the cycle.

**D.** And one should connect the concept of milah on the eighth (which is higher than the seven days of the cycle) with the act of drawing down holiness into the flesh of the physical body:

And by way of introduction to what was explained previously regarding the verse "And you shall count for yourselves *from the morrow of the Shabbos*"—for seemingly it is not understood why it says "from the morrow of the Shabbos," which leaves room for error (as the Tzadukim erred) that the intention is to the Shabbos of Bereishis, and it does not say explicitly "from the morrow of Pesach"—in order for the avodah of Sefiras HaOmer ("And you shall count for yourselves") to be possible, which is the clarification and refinement of the *animal soul* [which is the concept of the waving of the omer from the barley, which is *animal* food], there is a need for the granting of strength from a *level* that is extremely lofty, above the Seder Hishtalshelus. This is the concept of "from the morrow of the Shabbos," for Shabbos is within the Seder Hishtalshelus, and "from the morrow of the Shabbos" (higher than Shabbos) is higher than the Seder Hishtalshelus.

And the point of this is—that specifically the revelation that is higher than the Seder Hishtalshelus has the power and ability to descend and act in the lowest of the low. Therefore, only the revelation of "from the morrow of the Shabbos" (higher than Shabbos, higher than the Seder Hishtalshelus) gives the strength for the clarification of the animal soul. This is not the case for the level of holiness of Shabbos ("holy and established"), which does not have the power to descend and act below, as is emphasized by the fact that on Shabbos, mundane work is forbidden.

From this it is also understood regarding the mitzvah of milah—that in order for there to be a drawing down of holiness to the lowest point, to the *flesh of the physical body*, there is a need for the granting of strength from an extremely lofty level. This is the concept of the *eighth* of milah, the level of "eighth" that is higher than the seven days of the cycle, the guardian of the cycle.

**E.** And one should add that the mitzvah of milah, the sign of the holy covenant, is connected with the level of Yesod, whose concept is the connection of the *mashpia* (the one who influences) with the *mekabel* (the one who receives)—because the power to descend and influence below comes from the revelation of the light that is higher than the Seder Hishtalshelus (the eighth), and through it, the action is accomplished even in the lower matters, so that they become connected to Above.

***

**F.** This matter also pertains to the connection to the Rebbe—"The Tzaddik is the *Yesod* (foundation) of the world":

The Rebbe—his concept is the intermediary that connects, as is said regarding Moshe Rabbeinu, "I stand between Hashem and you."

In these days, when we are in the double and redoubled darkness of the final galus, the need and necessity for a special connection ("a special hiskashrus") to the Rebbe, the "Tzaddik Yesod Olam," is emphasized most strongly. This is the granting of strength to be connected to Above at all times, without being affected by changes in time or status and situation, Shabbos or weekday, day or night, the darkness of the galus, etc.

—It is told about the holy Tzaddik R' Meir of Premishlan, that the mikveh in his city was behind a high mountain. When the ground would become muddy and slippery, the townspeople would have to walk around the mountain so as not to slip, whereas the holy Tzaddik R' Meir would walk through the mountain even then. Once, some young men were visiting the city who did not hold by matters of miracles, and seeing that R' Meir walked through the mountain, they also tried to walk through the mountain, and immediately they slipped and were injured. They asked R' Meir how he walks through the mountain even at a time when no one can walk through the mountain without falling? And he replied: "Az m'iz tzugebundn oybn falt men nit untn" (When one is tied Above, one does not fall below).

(And the Rebbe concluded:) Whoever is connected Above, for him there is no difference between walking on top of the mountain or below the mountain and the like, since in every status and situation he does not fall below.

Whoever is connected Above through the "Tzaddik Yesod Olam" is connected Above (not only during davening and Torah study, and not only in the Chabad of his soul, but) even with the *heel of the foot*—as per the saying of the Rebbe Rashab regarding the interpretation of "Ekev asher shama" (which was said regarding Avraham Avinu): "Di pyate hot derhert" (The heel heard), and consequently, for a Chossid, even the "heel" is in a different manner ("a Chassidishe pyate").

And similarly regarding the entirety of the avodah of Sefiras HaOmer ("And you shall count for yourselves from the morrow of the Shabbos")—that through the connection Above (the level of "from the morrow of the Shabbos" which is higher than the Seder Hishtalshelus) to the Tzaddik Yesod Olam, not only does the animal soul not hide and conceal, but on the contrary, one effects in it a clarification and refinement in the manner of "U'sefartem lachem," from the word *behirut* (clarity), that the animal soul itself should be shining ("di behemah alein zol leichten"). And then one can also elevate it onto the mountain—Mount Sinai, where the Torah was given (after the preparation through the avodah of Sefiras HaOmer), and through this, the decree is nullified, the partition that separated the higher realms from the lower realms, until they become entirely one.

**G.** And furthermore, and this is the main point—that through the connection to the Tzaddik Yesod Olam, one merits that he (the Tzaddik Yesod Olam) will take us out of galus and lead us to our Holy Land, to the complete Geulah through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

And in the language of the blessing common among our Sephardic brethren: "Yireh Kohen b'Tzion" (May a Kohen see in Tzion), which also includes the newly circumcised infant, who is a Kohen, that "this small one shall become great," and he will merit, together with his brother Kohanim, to offer sacrifices in the Third Beis Hamikdash, which will be built by the Ribono shel Olam ("binyana d'Kudsha Brich Hu") Himself.

*

[Before Mincha, the Rebbe gave the father of the child five dollars, and said: These funds are for the yeshiva, tuition for the child's learning, that he should learn in Tomchei Temimim.]

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Bechukosai, Mevarchim HaChodesh Sivan, 5711

#### 107

(An unedited transcript)

**"And I will walk**[1](#_ftn590) among you, and I will be to you for Elokus, and you will be to Me for a people..." and "I will lead you upright" [komemiut][2](#_ftn591). It is necessary to understand what is the greatness of the level of "And I will walk among you," such that it is written[3](#_ftn592) regarding it, "If you walk in My statutes... then I will walk among you." Yet it is written[4](#_ftn593), "After Hashem your Elokim you shall walk," and it is written[5](#_ftn594), "To walk in all His ways and to cleave to Him." Our Sages said[6](#_ftn595), "Just as He is compassionate, so too you be compassionate; just as He is merciful, so too you be merciful," etc. If so, the matter of walking in the ways of the Ribono shel Olam is always present. What, then, is the innovation in the matter of "And I will walk among you," that it should be specifically when "you walk in My statutes"? Furthermore, it is necessary to understand the matter of "I will lead you upright" [komemiut], which is explained as "with an upright stature" [koma zekufa][7](#_ftn596). In the Gemara[8](#_ftn597), two opinions are brought regarding this: the first opinion, like the measure of the Heichal, which is one hundred cubits; and the second opinion, like the two statures of Adam HaRishon—that is, two hundred cubits. It is necessary to understand the matter and the level of this[9](#_ftn598).

**Furthermore,** it is necessary to understand that we find a superior level in these promises—"And I will walk among you" and "I will lead you upright"—compared to the other promises stated in this parsha. All the other promises are not dependent on a specific time—specifically the future—but can occur at any time. That is, at any time that "you walk in My statutes," then "I will give your rains in their time," and all the other promises. Proof of this is found in Maseches Taanis[10](#_ftn599), that in the days of Shimon ben Shetach, wheat was the size of kidneys, just as it will be in the future[11](#_ftn600). True, regarding wheat the size of kidneys, one could say that this is only a semblance and example of what will be in the future. However, we also find[12](#_ftn601) regarding the promise, "And I will grant peace in the land... and no sword shall pass through your land,"[13](#_ftn602) that because of this, Yoshiyahu did not allow Pharaoh to pass through Eretz Yisrael for war, because he interpreted "no sword shall pass through your land" to mean that it does not refer to a sword of non-peace—for it was already said "I will grant peace in the land"—but rather, it means even a sword of peace. This matter was so simple to him that he did not even consult Yirmiyahu the Prophet about it. Even though he was punished for this, the punishment was not because he did not interpret the verses correctly, but because his generation was not viewed favorably by the Makom. But were it not for that, this promise should have been fulfilled at that time as well. From this, it is understood that the promises in the parsha are not dependent on the time of the future specifically. However, regarding the promises of "And I will walk among you" and "I will lead you upright," the Ramban[14](#_ftn603) and Rabbeinu Bachya[15](#_ftn604) write: Know that Yisrael never attained these blessings in their completeness (neither in the time of the First Beis Hamikdash nor in the time of the Second Beis Hamikdash), neither the masses nor the individuals among them (meaning even those individuals who were complete). They will only be in the future Redemption, in the time of the Third Beis Hamikdash. Based on this, it is necessary to understand even more: what is the greatness in the matter of "And I will walk among you" (relative to the matter of walking that is always present) and "I will lead you upright" (upright stature, and two statures), such that this matter will be in its completeness specifically in the future, when the complete Redemption comes, speedily in our days.

**The general** concept of this[16](#_ftn605) is that the precision of the language "And I will walk" [va'ishaleich]—rather than "And I will go" [va'eileich]—indicates a habit of walking, that He returns and walks, etc. Included in this are two modes of walking: walking from above to below, and walking from below to above, as both are present simultaneously. This is also the interpretation of the matter of "I will lead you upright" [komemiut]—in the plural—that they are two statures, and both come simultaneously.

b) **To understand** the level of the matter of "And I will walk," the two walkings simultaneously, one must first preface the difference between the two modes of walking, and the advantage that each has over the other. The matter of this is, as is known by the parable[17](#_ftn606) of two people, one standing above on a high mountain and one standing below in a valley, whose connection can be in two ways: the one above descends below, or the one below ascends above. The difference between them is that when the one below needs to ascend above, there are several conditions[18](#_ftn607). The first: he must know all the paths and ways to ascend the mountain. The second: he must be a person of strong power to be able to ascend the mountain. The third: he must have the appropriate garments—that is, not only that the garments do not prevent him from ascending the mountain, but they even assist him in his ascent. Its matter in the avodah of man is as it is written[19](#_ftn608), "Who shall ascend the mountain of Hashem," etc., and for this, there must be several conditions. The first: that he knows the paths to ascend the mountain. This means that in the way of Hashem itself—which is the general matter of Torah and mitzvos—he must know the correct paths. That is, that the study of Torah should be as it ought to be, and furthermore, that it should be *lishmah* and not for the sake of any ulterior motives, etc.[20](#_ftn609). This is also what is said in the Gemara[21](#_ftn610): "What is the meaning of the verse[22](#_ftn611), 'And the faith of your times shall be a strength of salvations,' etc.—'faith' is the Order of Zeraim, etc., and yet, 'the fear of Hashem is His treasure.'" The main thing is the fear of Hashem. As it is stated in the continuation of the Gemara there, that when they bring a person to judgment, they say to him, "Did you conduct your business with faith? Did you set times for Torah?" etc., and yet, "If the fear of Hashem is his treasure—yes; if not—no." It is like a man[23](#_ftn612) who said to his messenger, "Bring me up a kor of wheat to the attic." He went and brought it up. He said to him, "Did you mix into it a kav of salt?" He said to him, "No." He said to him, "It would have been better if you had not brought it up." For a kav of salt means salty earth that preserves the produce from becoming wormy (as per Rashi's commentary). That is, he has no taste, understanding, or comprehension in this, etc.—this is the matter of fear and acceptance of the yoke. And all the more so, that it should not be in a way where he learns but does not fulfill what he learns (and similarly, one who learns in order to provoke[24](#_ftn613)), about whom the verse says[25](#_ftn614), "But to the wicked, Elokim said, 'What right have you to recite My statutes?'" And if he does not merit, it becomes for him the opposite of a potion of life[26](#_ftn615), and it increases vitality in the *kelipah* for the moment, as Admur HaZaken writes in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*[27](#_ftn616). And so it is also in the fulfillment of mitzvos, that it must be as it ought to be specifically. As it is stated in the Gemara[28](#_ftn617) that there is one who fulfills the mitzvah of honoring father and mother and inherits Gehinnom, because he honors them in a way that degrades them. And so it is in the fulfillment of other mitzvos, that their fulfillment must be as it ought to be, and also *lishmah*, without ulterior motives, etc. And in addition to knowing the paths, he must also know the *netivos* (tracks). The difference between them is[29](#_ftn618) that a *derech* (path) is a paved road for the many, while a *nativ* (track) is a narrow path. That is, the *netivos* to ascend the mountain of Hashem are the matters of the comprehension of Elokus, through which a person will come by way of nature to love and fear, and through this, he will ascend the mountain of Hashem. All this is from the side of the *nefesh elokis*. However, in order to be able to bring with him also the *nefesh habehamis*, for this the second condition is required: that he be a person of strong power, that is,

#### 110

that he not be crushed under his burden[30](#_ftn619), but on the contrary, that he take with him also the *nefesh habehamis*. And the third condition is that he be dressed in the appropriate garments. That is, not only that the garments do not confuse[31](#_ftn620), but furthermore, that they assist him in his ascent. The matter of this is that the garments are the letters of thought, the letters of speech, and the letters of action[32](#_ftn621). There are two aspects in them: the vitality and the feeling that is in the letters, and the body of the letters. The rectification of the vitality that is in the letters is through the avodah of love and fear, for through contemplation on the comprehension of Elokus, he gives birth to love and fear, which are the wings through which it flies upward[33](#_ftn622). But the rectification of the letters themselves is through the matter of tears, as it is written[34](#_ftn623), "O wall of the daughter of Tzion, let tears run down like a river." The matter of tears is from the side of the constriction of the mind [kivutz hamochin][35](#_ftn624). That is, through this—that he contemplates how he was separated from the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof Baruch Hu* [and even though this was for only a brief moment, nevertheless, it does not concern him what happened after that, because at that moment he could have been connected with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the *Ein Sof Baruch Hu* and he was separated from the *Atzmus*]—then there is created in him a constriction of the heart and a constriction of the mind (the heart is constricted and the head is squeezed), from which come the tears. That is, because he cannot express the matter in letters, and the mind cannot bear it, etc. Through this, the rectification of the body of the letters is accomplished—that is, he breaks the wall of the *sitra achra* and builds the wall of the daughter of Tzion. And specifically when these three conditions mentioned above are present—that he has the appropriate garments, his power is strong, and he knows the paths and tracks—specifically then can he ascend the mountain of Hashem.

**And so it is** also in the matter of the ascent to Gan Eden, which is called the mountain of Hashem[36](#_ftn625). Just as a mountain in its literal sense is inanimate, yet it ascends upward[37](#_ftn626), so too the matter of Gan Eden is the ascent from below to above. For the ascent from this world to Gan Eden to take place, it is specifically through the *Nahar Dinur* (River of Fire), because one must forget the sight of this world[38](#_ftn627). Similarly, the ascent from the Lower Gan Eden to the Upper Gan Eden is through the *Nahar Dinur*, in order to forget the sight of the Lower Gan Eden, for even the sight of the Lower Gan Eden confuses the Upper Gan Eden. Similar to[39](#_ftn628) what we find regarding R.

#### 111

Zeira, who fasted one hundred fasts in order to forget the Babylonian Talmud when he needed to ascend to Eretz Yisrael and learn the Jerusalem Talmud[40](#_ftn629). Since the Babylonian Talmud is in a manner of "He has set me in dark places,"[41](#_ftn630) it confuses the Jerusalem Talmud. And similarly in Gan Eden, the ascent from the Lower Gan Eden to the Upper Gan Eden is through the *Nahar Dinur* in order to forget the sight of the Lower Gan Eden, which confuses the revelation of the Upper Gan Eden. And in addition to the matter of the *Nahar Dinur*, there is also the matter of the pillar between the Lower and Upper Gan Eden, through which the pillar he becomes one with the higher level[42](#_ftn631). This matter is in all the multitude of levels in the Lower and Upper Gan Eden, as is known[43](#_ftn632) that even though only two levels are mentioned in Gan Eden, in truth there is an infinite multitude of levels in it. This is the matter of the three ascents every day in the three prayers, because there are a multitude of levels in which they ascend from level to level, after the prerequisite of the nullification of the previous level, through which is the ascent to the higher level, to infinity, as the saying goes[44](#_ftn633), "The righteous have no rest," etc., for it is said[45](#_ftn634), "They go from strength to strength." The general matter of the ascent in Gan Eden depends on the manner of the avodah below, for according to the manner of the soul's avodah while it is below, so is the manner of its ascent in Gan Eden. There are souls that merit to ascend only to the Lower Gan Eden, and there are souls that ascend to the Upper Gan Eden. And even those souls that merit to ascend to the Upper Gan Eden must first pass through the Lower Gan Eden, etc. All this is in the walking from below to above, which depends on the manner of the preparation and avodah of the one below.

c) **However,** the matter of the walking from above to below is in a manner that does not require the aforementioned conditions. For the one above, who is found above, knows the paths and tracks. Similarly, he is a person of strong power. That is, besides the fact that for the descent from above to below, great power is not needed—for the need for power is only so that he can constrict himself and descend—furthermore, the power of the one above is strong. Also, the matter of garments does not apply to the descent below. And not only does it not apply from the side of the one above, but it also does not apply from the side of the one below—that is, the garments of the one below do not apply either. As in the Giving of the Torah, which was in a manner of an *hemshech* (drawing down) from above to below, as it is written[46](#_ftn635), "And Hashem descended on Mount Sinai," which did not concern the state of the one below. For at the Exodus from Egypt, it is written[47](#_ftn636), "For the people fled," and it is explained regarding this (in *Tanya*[48](#_ftn637)) that seemingly it is puzzling why this was so.

#### 112

For if they had told Pharaoh to send them free forever, would he not have been forced to send them? Rather, it is because the evil in the souls of Yisrael was still in its strength, etc., and from the side of the body and the *nefesh habehamis*, there had to be a matter of fleeing. And even though afterwards there was the avodah of *Sefiras HaOmer*, nevertheless, the revelations of the Giving of the Torah are incomparable to the avodah of *Sefiras HaOmer*. Thus, it is found that the general revelation of the Giving of the Torah was by way of from above to below, which did not concern the state of the one below. And the revelation from above to below acted upon them so that their filth ceased[49](#_ftn638), as it was before the sin, and the *hemshech* below was in a manner that the speech "I am Hashem your Elokim" was heard from all four directions[50](#_ftn639). And similarly, we find regarding the matter of the resurrection of the dead, that it will be in a manner of an *hemshech* from above to below. That is why our Sages said[51](#_ftn640), "All Yisrael have a portion in the World to Come" (except for those enumerated there). That is, the matter of the resurrection of the dead will be for all the Children of Yisrael, and it is not like in Gan Eden, which has differences in levels as mentioned above, but in a manner that all Yisrael have a portion in the World to Come. This is because the matter of the resurrection of the dead is in a manner of the descent of the One above to below, which is why it does not concern the level and state of the one below[52](#_ftn641).

**This will be understood**[53](#_ftn642) through a parable of a great king who sits in his royal palace in royal garments and a royal crown, and all the people stand outside, and all their requests reach the appointed officials or the ministers, who convey the requests to the king, because it is impossible for them to enter to the king themselves. And even when there is someone who merits that they allow him to enter, there are limitations as to how far he can enter—to the outer courtyard, or to the inner courtyard, or to the king's room itself. But sometimes the king wants to reveal himself to the people, and then he goes out from his palace and stands at the gate of the palace and reveals himself to all the people. That is, the king himself, as he is in his purity, in royal garments and a royal crown, in great splendor and glory, reveals himself to all. But in such a manner, fear and dread fall upon the people, and they are completely nullified, to the point that it is not at all relevant that they should speak with him about their affairs and request their requests. But there is another mode in the revelation of the king, and that is when the king dresses in simple garments, and also speaks with the people about simple matters. Then he is relative to them, so that they can speak with him about their affairs and request their requests. That is, even though the people know that he is the same king who a short time ago was dressed in royal garments

#### 113

and a royal crown, nevertheless, since now he dresses in simple garments and speaks with them simple words, this acts upon them so that they can speak with him about their private affairs and request their requests. And behold, when the king reveals himself as he is dressed in simple garments, in this specifically is his *Atzmus* and *Mahus* revealed more than when he is in royal garments and his royal crown. For the reason that the king dresses in simple matters is because his desire is that the people speak with him about their affairs according to their level, and to such an extent that for this he forgoes royal garments and a royal crown. That is, in this specifically is his *Atzmus* (essence), and therefore also the union of the people with the king is with the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* of the king. The example of this will be understood above: that the revelation of the Giving of the Torah is, for example, the revelation of the king in great splendor and glory, which is why this revelation caused complete nullification, as the saying goes[54](#_ftn643), "At every word, their soul flew away, and He had to return it to them specifically with the dew of resurrection." But the matter of the fulfillment of mitzvos in physical things after the Giving of the Torah is like the revelation of the king as he is dressed in simple garments. This is that the mitzvos were dressed in physical things, but specifically in this is found His *Atzmus* and *Mahus*, as the saying goes, "No thought can grasp Him at all,"[55](#_ftn644) except when it grasps and is dressed in His Torah and mitzvos[56](#_ftn645). That is, in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* itself is grasped, which is not grasped even in the primordial thought of *Adam Kadmon*. Therefore, the matter of the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos in physicality specifically is the vessel for the resurrection of the dead, which will be from the side of His *Atzmus* specifically.

d) **And behold,** in each of the two aforementioned modes of walking—from below to above and from above to below—there is a level and advantage that is not in the other. For in the walking from below to above, one can walk only according to his power, only according to the measure of his avodah, and generally, the walking is only until the root of the *Memalei* (the immanent light). And in this is the advantage in the walking from above to below, that then the One above is drawn down as He is, and this is the matter of the revelation of the *Sovev* (the encompassing light). But on the other hand, there is a deficiency in the descent of the One above to below, that He does not come into union with the one below, because this is not from the side of the avodah of the one below. And in this is the advantage in the walking from below to above, that the one below absorbs the One above internally. Based on this, the elevation in the matter of "And I will walk among you" is understood, which includes both modes of walking, two types of walking—from above to below and from below to above—that both are included in one word and in one matter. This is through the revelation of a level that is above both of them.

**And the explanation** of the matter is that in the two aforementioned modes of walking, the existence of the one below occupies a place. That is, not only in the ascent of the one below from below to above,

#### 114

the raising of the *Memalei* into the *Sovev*, which is the matter of raising *Mayin Nukvin* (feminine waters), where then the *hemshech* is also according to the measure of the raising—that is, that the one below is a vessel for the *hemshech*—but also the walking from above to below, the drawing down of the *Sovev* into the *Memalei*. For even though this does not require the raising of *Mayin Nukvin*, nevertheless, there must be a refinement of the recipient. That is, since the root of this *hemshech* is from the level of the revelation of the light as it is in itself[57](#_ftn646), behold, with it being the light as it is in itself and above relation to the worlds, nevertheless, from this itself—that one must negate in it the relation to the worlds (which is what they say, that its matter is the revelation of the light as it is in itself)—it is understood that it has some relation to the worlds, only that it is negated from them. Therefore, it is appropriate to say that the one below is a vessel for this light by way of negation at least, and because of this, there must be in it a matter of refinement at least (even though the matter of raising *Mayin Nukvin* does not apply to this). This is what we find, that even in the future, when the revelation will be from above to below, there will be differences in levels, as it is written[58](#_ftn647), "From their smallest to their greatest." That is, even though the revelation will be in a manner of "as the waters cover the sea,"[59](#_ftn648) nevertheless, there will be differences in levels of "their smallest and their greatest." That is because even in the mode of walking from above to below, there must be a refinement of the one below. Furthermore, even in the mode of walking from above to below, there are the definitions of above and below, and the above is revealed in the below. That is because the root of the *hemshech* is from the level of the light as it is in itself, which, with it being as it is in itself, nevertheless, because it is light alone, it has a relation to the worlds, and there are in it the definitions of above and below. However, the matter of "And I will walk" in one word is in a manner that has no division of above and below, that both are equal. That is because the root of this *hemshech* is from the *Atzmus*, which is the source of the light, and more than that, that in truth it is not appropriate to describe it even as the source of the light, and from its side, everything is truly equal. From this, it is understood that for this, there does not need to be even a refinement of the recipient, but it can be revealed to all. And this revelation will be in the future, in the resurrection of the dead specifically, when the revelation will be to all equally, to the point that even in the created *yesh* (existence), it will be revealed that its existence is the true *yesh*. That is, that even the created *yesh* whose feeling is that its existence is from itself, this itself is because its creation is from the *Atzmus* whose existence is from the *Atzmus*[60](#_ftn649), and in the future, it will be revealed in the created *yesh* that it itself is the true *yesh*.

**And this is also** what they say[61](#_ftn650) regarding the four praises: "There is none like You," "There is none besides You," "There is none but You," and "Who is like You." "There is none like You, our Elokim" in this world; "There is none besides You, our King" for the life of the World to Come; "There is none but You, our Redeemer" for the days of Mashiach; and "Who is like You, our Savior" for the resurrection of the dead. For[62](#_ftn651), the interpretation of "There is none besides You" (for the life of the World to Come) and "There is none but You" (for the days of Mashiach) is that there is no existence besides Him. That is, even though there is some existence, nevertheless, it is in nullification, whether in the nullification of "none" (none besides You) or in the nullification of "none but" (none but You). Not so "There is none like You" (in this world) and "Who is like You" (for the resurrection of the dead), for the interpretation of this is that there is a "besides," only that it is in a manner of "There is none like You" and "Who is like You." That is, because the created *yesh* itself is the true *yesh*, only that in this itself there are two modes that are two extremes from one end to the other. "There is none like You" in this world: even though the created *yesh* itself is the true *yesh*, nevertheless, in this world, this is *in concealment and hiding*. But through the avodah in this world to remove all the concealments and hidings, etc., then there will be the revelation of "Who is like You," etc., for the resurrection of the dead, when *it will be revealed* in the created *yesh* that it itself is the true *yesh*.

e) **And this is also** what is said, "I will lead you upright" [komemiut], the two statures of Adam HaRishon, which is the matter of the stature of *Ohr Yashar* (direct light) and the stature of *Ohr Chozer* (reflected light), the avodah of the *nefesh elokis* with the *nefesh habehamis*, and the avodah of the *nefesh habehamis* from its own side. And in the future, both will unite in one word, which is the matter of the inclusion of above and below as one, from the side of the revelation of the *Atzmus*. As explained above, that even the individuals who were complete did not attain this level, for even the stature of Adam HaRishon before the sin was only one hundred cubits, and specifically in the future it will be two hundred cubits, like the two statures of Adam HaRishon, which is the matter of the inclusion and unification of the two matters of above and below, from the side of the revelation of the *Atzmus*.

**********

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Bechukosai, Mevarchim HaChodesh Sivan, 5711

#### 116

(Unedited)

**A.** The beginning of the weekly parsha—Parshas Bechukosai—deals with the blessings.

Since the beginning of any matter is the essence of the entire matter (which is why one should always look at the beginning of a thing), it follows that the essence of the parsha is the concept of the blessings.

This is further clarified by what is explained in *Likutei Torah* that even the matters later in the parsha which seemingly are the opposite of blessings are, "in truth, nothing but blessings"—just like the beginning of the parsha, which is the essence.

The verse introduces the condition for receiving the blessings: "If you walk in My statutes", and Rashi explains: "that you should be toiling in Torah."

—And it can be said that the very fact that it is written in the verse "If you walk in My statutes" is itself a *granting of strength* to fulfill the matter—

And through this, one merits all the blessings mentioned in the parsha, "I will give your rains in their time, etc.", up to what is written at the conclusion of the matter : "I will walk among you, etc., and I will lead you upright."

***

**B.** Maamar beginning with the words "And I will walk among you, etc."

***

**C.** It was discussed above (in the maamar) that in the time to come (at the resurrection of the dead), there will be an *hemshech* of the *Atzmus*—which has no connection at all to the worlds, and in relation to which everything is equal—and consequently, there will be no need for the *avodah* of refining the recipient. However, as long as the *hemshech* is from a level of *Elokus* that has value and connection to the worlds, it is proportional to the refinement of the recipient, and consequently, there is a need for the *avodah* of refining the recipient.

And in continuation of this—there is a story about the Chossid R' Mordechai of Horodok (as follows in section 6).

#### 117

—The Chossid R' Mordechai of Horodok was born after his parents had gone many years without being blessed with children, until his father received a blessing from R' Mordechai the Tzaddik—one of the hidden Tzaddikim—that a son would be born to him, and he instructed him to name him Mordechai, after him, even though he was still alive in this world. The aforementioned R' Mordechai was among the distinguished Chassidim of the Mitteler Rebbe, and the Mitteler Rebbe appointed him to be a *mashpia* in the city of Horodok.

**D.** Parenthetical note:

Among the sayings of R' Mordechai the Tzaddik—after whom R' Mordechai of Horodok was named—in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: A *neshamah* waits Above for thousands of years to descend below and be clothed in a body, in order to do a favor for a Yid in physical matters, and especially in spiritual matters. A *neshamah* toils ("matert zich op") in a body for seventy or eighty years in order to do a favor for a Yid in physical matters, and especially in spiritual matters.

—A *bochur* came to me and complained that he is experiencing a "fall of spirit" because he does not see that he is accomplishing anything ("er zeet nit vos er tut oif"), saying that I should make him a detailed accounting of what he has already accomplished on this day and that day, etc.

But the matter is a *kal v'chomer*: If a *neshamah* descends into the world to do a favor for a Yid in physical or spiritual matters—even one single favor for one single Yid—then he, who is in a place where there are many Yidden, all the more so! And furthermore, even if he is in a place where there are no Yidden, when a non-Jew sees his conduct (regarding the observance of Shabbos, putting on tefillin, and the like, that he is not moved by anything, etc.), it acts upon him such that because of this, he will refrain from doing something contrary to the good of a Yid!

**E.** And we will return to our subject—the story about R' Mordechai of Horodok :

Once, the holy Tzaddik R' Mordechai of Chernobyl came to Horodok.

R' Mordechai of Horodok, as a Chossid of the Mitteler Rebbe, was not impressed by him, but, being a Chabadnik... he did not want to miss ("durchlozn glat") the opportunity to see who this person was about whom they said he was a Tzaddik, his body pure, and holy from his mother's womb, and all the more so since he was a *mechutan* of the Mitteler Rebbe; and after he settled his mind, he went to him.

#### 118

When R' Mordechai of Horodok entered to see the holy Tzaddik R' Mordechai of Chernobyl, the Tzaddik spoke about the greatness of Tzaddikim, and said that Tzaddikim have no need for *avodah*. When R' Mordechai of Horodok heard this, he remarked and said: Even Tzaddikim have a need for *avodah*. *Avodah* is something everyone needs.

Seeing that the Tzaddik of Chernobyl was offended by his words—R' Mordechai of Horodok added and said: It is written "which Hashem created to do," "to rectify", meaning, that even *Elokus* which is clothed in the worlds ("Hashem created") requires *avodah* (rectification). And when the Tzaddik of Chernobyl heard this—that even *Elokus* requires *avodah*—his mind was put at ease.

**F.** And regarding us:

Even though in the time to come (when there will be an *hemshech* of the *Atzmus*) there will be no need for the matter of *avodah*, and we are already standing in immediate proximity to the *Geulah* and speaking about the status and situation that will be in the *Geulah*,

—By *kal v'chomer* from the prophecy of Yirmiyahu, that although the essence of his prophecy was regarding the destruction, nevertheless, he already prophesied about the return of the ten tribes, "Go and proclaim, etc., 'Return, O backsliding Yisroel,' etc.", which is the beginning of the ingathering of the exiles—

Nevertheless, *now* there is still a need for the matter of *avodah*, to remove all the concealments and hiddenness.

And among the essential matters in this—is the *avodah* of removing the concealment and hiddenness that is in the matter of *yishus* (selfhood), through the matter of *bitul*.

**G.** And regarding this matter—how pressing and necessary the matter of *bitul* and the negation of *yishus* is—there is a lesson and instruction from the *Haftorah* of the weekly parsha:

Even before it is said "Blessed is the man who trusts in Hashem, and Hashem shall be his trust" —the verse precedes it with "Cursed is the man who trusts in man, and makes flesh his arm, and from Hashem his heart turns away".

And by way of the introduction explained in the *maamarim* of Chassidus regarding the four names by which the speaking species is called—*Adam, Ish, Gever, Enosh*—which are divided into two types: *Adam*

#### 119

and *Ish*—these are essential names that describe the essence of the person, whether he is a possessor of *mochin* (intellect) or a possessor of *midos* (emotions); *Adam* is the title of *mochin*, and refers to the *nefesh elokis*, whose essence is intellect, and *Ish* is the title of *midos*, and refers to the *nefesh habahamis*, whose essence is *midos* (and even his intellect is only for the sake of the *midos*). And *Gever* and *Enosh*—these are descriptive titles that describe the essence of the names *Adam* and *Ish* and measure the quantity and quality of them, whether they are in a manner of strength and overcoming or in a manner of weakness; *Gever* indicates the overcoming and strength of the intellect and *midos*, and *Enosh* indicates the weakness of the intellect and *midos*.

And according to this, one can explain the content of the verse "Cursed is the *Gever* (the strong one) who trusts in *Adam* (the intellectual one)"—that it seems to him that his strength ("the *Gever*") is from the side of his intellect, his *nefesh elokis*, whose essence is intellect ("*Adam*"), and afterwards "and makes flesh his arm," that it seems to him that his strength ("his arm," "his power") is from the side of the "flesh," that he has a refined and purified body ("an eidelere guf"),

Meaning: The beginning is in a manner of "trusting in *Adam*," that he thinks he has a high *neshamah*, and thus he goes from bad to worse until it seems to him that his body has also been refined and purified, and consequently, he is not in need of the matter of *avodah*,

Until he reaches a status and situation where "from Hashem his heart turns away"—that even regarding his physical matters it seems to him that "my strength and the might of my hand have made me this wealth".

And the advice for this—that even when he is at a lofty level, a high *neshamah*, and a refined and purified body, he should not trust in himself, but in the *Ribono shel Olam* ("Blessed is the *Gever* who trusts in Hashem"), and he should ask the *Ribono shel Olam* to help him in his *avodah*.

And in the language of the verse at the conclusion and seal of the *Haftorah* : "Heal me, Hashem, and I shall be healed; save me, and I shall be saved, etc.," meaning, that when the *neshamah* descends below to be clothed in a body, and especially when it is in *galus* among the nations—the *neshamah* cries out to the *Ribono shel Olam*, "Save me"....

***

**H.** [During the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe spoke about one of those present who had been in military service, and said:]

It is in the power of the Rebbe to make even a "block of wood" ("a bulach")—a Chossid.

#### 120

A Chossid—is one who fulfills the will of the Rebbe. And consequently, one who fulfills the will of the Rebbe, regardless of his appearance and his external clothing, is a Chossid.

He might argue that since his external appearance is such-and-such, and he is among the nations, etc., how can he be called by the name Chossid?! But the truth is, as mentioned, that by the fact that he fulfills the will of the Rebbe, *the Rebbe makes him* a Chossid even while he is in his external appearance and clothing, and consequently, it is like the Rebbe himself, in his royal attire, being clothed in simple garments.

And regarding the fulfillment of the will of the Rebbe—there is the well-known letter of the Rebbe to the Jewish soldiers, in which he explains that all the events during a person's life, such as (in this case) going to the army, were determined by Divine Providence for the sake of an intention and purpose connected with the matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, even when on the surface it appears that there is another reason for it [and all the more so since the external reason is only temporary, whereas the matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos* are eternal, and through them the connection of *Bnei Yisroel* with the *Ribono shel Olam* is made in an eternal manner], and consequently, one must strive to utilize the going to the army for the matters of *Torah* and *mitzvos*.

And all this—in addition to the instruction of the Rebbe (in his letters) that every soldier should strive every day to put on tefillin, say a chapter of *Tehillim*, study a verse of *Chumash* with the commentary of Rashi, *maamarim* on matters of *emunah* that have been published in the language of the country, and the like.

And the conduct according to the will of the Rebbe also adds to the confidence that the *Ribono shel Olam* will protect him even while he is at the front, and will return him healthy and whole, and consequently, he can go with joy, like the well-known saying about soldiers who, even when they go to war, march with a "march" (song of walking) of victory.

## B’s”d. Sicha of Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5711

#### 121

– Following Mincha –

*Unedited*

**1.** The significance of Rosh Chodesh Sivan is explicitly stated in the verse[1](#_ftn678): "In the third month... on this day (Rosh Chodesh[2](#_ftn679)) they came to the wilderness of Sinai... and Israel encamped there opposite the mountain"—for it was then that the preparation for Matan Torah began[3](#_ftn680).

"These days are remembered and observed"[4](#_ftn681)—meaning that every single year, on this day, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, the preparation for Matan Torah begins anew.

**2.** However, there is a distinction between the preparation for Matan Torah on the first Rosh Chodesh Sivan and the preparation for Matan Torah each and every year:
