On the first Rosh Chodesh Sivan, being *before* Matan Torah, the preparation could not be through the Torah itself; it necessarily had to be through other matters, such as the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear" [as they learned from the ministering angels, as our Sages say[5](#_ftn682): "When Israel preceded 'we will do' to 'we will hear,' a Heavenly voice went forth and said to them: 'Who revealed to My children this secret, which the ministering angels utilize?'"]. Conversely, on Rosh Chodesh Sivan of every year, being *after* Matan Torah, the preparation for (the innovation in) the Matan Torah of that year can and must be through the *Torah itself*.

That is to say: Even though the Matan Torah of this year will be in a more sublime manner than ever before—as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh[6](#_ftn683) (regarding Rosh Hashanah, from which it is understood regarding all other matters as well) that "every year, a new and renewed light descends and shines... a higher light that has never shone since the days of the world"—and in relation to this unprecedented elevation in Matan Torah, it is as if we are "before" Matan Torah; nevertheless, since we are already *after the general concept of Matan Torah*, the preparation for this unprecedented elevation in Matan Torah is also accomplished through the *Torah itself*.

#### 122

It is understood that when the preparation for Matan Torah is through the Torah itself, then the receiving of the Torah is in an entirely different manner.

This is also the difference in the receiving of the Torah: the first time, the receiving of the Torah was in the manner of "the Holy One, blessed be He, coerced them with the mountain like a barrel," whereas the receiving of the Torah each and every year is—in the words of the blessing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—with joy and in an internalized manner.

**3.** It should be added that this concept—that the preparation for Matan Torah must be through the Torah itself—applies to all Bnei Yisrael, both those involved in business and those who "dwell in the tents" (full-time scholars).

This is emphasized even more strongly for those who "dwell in the tents," the students of the yeshivos—for since their entire occupation is *the study of Torah* ("that is their business"), and in the words of our Sages[7](#_ftn684), "Were it not for this day that causes [it]...", it is certain that for them, the preparation for Matan Torah must be through the Torah itself.

And as stated, the preparation for Matan Torah begins from this day, Rosh Chodesh Sivan.

## B"H. The text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send to Anash sheyichyu throughout the world in anticipation of the festival of Shavuos, 5711

#### 123

Please convey to Anash the blessing of receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and surely they will organize a Chassidishe farbrengen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## With the help of Hashem. 4 Sivan, Shabbos Parshas Bamidbar, Erev Chag HaShavuos, 5711

#### 124

(Unedited)

(Following davening, the Rebbe said:)

Regarding this day—the fifth of Sivan—there is an opinion that it was on this day that the precedence of *na'aseh* (we will do) to *nishma* (we will hear) took place (as is found in the Mechilta[1](#_ftn685) and cited in the commentary of Rashi[2](#_ftn686)).

From this, it is also understood regarding the preparation for *Matan Torah* in every single year—that on the fifth of Sivan, the *avodah* of the day must be related to the content of the concept of the precedence of *na'aseh* to *nishma*.

**********

## Sicha of the First Day of Shavuos, 5711

#### 125

– After Mincha –

(Unedited)

**A.** The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related[1](#_ftn687) that on the first day of Shavuos, the Tzemach Tzedek would hold a "nigleh tish."[2](#_ftn688)

The custom was that rabbis and halachic authorities who were unable to leave their communities for Pesach or Sukkos due to the volume of questions and the like, would habitually come to Lubavitch for Shavuos. During the dairy meal, the rabbis would present their halachic questions to the Tzemach Tzedek, and within fifty moments, the Tzemach Tzedek would respond to all their questions.

In order to maintain (*anhaltan*) this custom, I wish to share a concept in the nigleh of Torah.

**B.** Regarding the order in which the Torah Shebichtav (Written Torah) was given, there is a dispute in Maseches Gittin[3](#_ftn689) as to whether the "Torah was given scroll by scroll"—meaning, "when a section was stated to Moshe, he would *write it down*, and at the end of forty years, when all the sections were completed, he joined them with sinews and sewed them together"[4](#_ftn690)—or whether the "Torah was given as a completed whole," meaning "finished, defined, and complete," and "it was not written until the end of forty years, after all the sections had been stated; those stated to him in the first and second years were arranged in his memory *orally* until he wrote them down."[4](#_ftn690)

However, regarding the Aseres Hadibros (Ten Commandments) that were stated at the Giving of the Torah at Har Sinai—since the Tablets upon which the Aseres Hadibros were *written* were not given to Moshe until the end of forty days, it follows that at the time of the Giving of the Torah, the Aseres Hadibros were in the category of *Torah Shebaal Peh* (Oral Torah).

**C.** Now, regarding the manner of studying Torah Shebaal Peh, our Alter Rebbe brings in Hilchos Talmud Torah[5](#_ftn691) that we find a dispute among the poskim as to whether the primary obligation is to know the halachic rulings themselves, even without their underlying reasons, or whether the obligation is to also know the reasons for the halachos, to reason through them and engage in pilpul:

#### 126

The opinion of the Rosh[6](#_ftn692) is that the obligation is to also know the reasons for the halachos, to reason through them and engage in pilpul. The study of the reasons for halachos is so essential that without it, it is impossible to issue halachic rulings, as the Sages say[7](#_ftn693) that those who "issue halachic rulings based on their Mishnah" (the Mishnah alone, halachic rulings without reasons) are called "destroyers of the world," "for since they do not know the reasons for the Mishnah, they sometimes cause [errors] by comparing a matter to something that is not similar to it."[8](#_ftn694)

However, according to the Rambam, the primary obligation is to know the halachic rulings themselves, even without the reasons. This is evident from the fact that "he compiled his work, Mishneh Torah, without providing the reasons for the halachos at all, and intended it to be used for issuing rulings on its own, as he writes in his introduction there, that a person will not need any other compilation in the world, etc., that a person should read the Torah Shebichtav first and then, etc."[9](#_ftn695) [And for this reason, he writes in the introduction to his work[10](#_ftn696), "All the mitzvos that were given to Moshe were given with their explanation, as it is stated[11](#_ftn697), 'And I will give you the stone tablets, and the Torah and the mitzvah'—'Torah' is the Torah Shebichtav, and 'mitzvah' is its explanation"—which is the exposition of the Sages in Maseches Berachos[12](#_ftn698). However, the Rambam *omitted* the end of the exposition regarding the conclusion of the verse: "(which I have written) to teach them—this is the Gemara" ("the reasoning behind the Mishnayos, from which the ruling is derived"[13](#_ftn699)), because the primary obligation is to know the halachic rulings, even without the reasons, through the study of the Mishnah alone, "and the mitzvah is the Mishnah"]. The reason that those who "issue halachic rulings based on their Mishnah" are "destroyers of the world" is because "there are many Mishnayos where we say, 'Whose opinion is this? It is So-and-so, and it is an individual opinion, and the halacha does not follow him'"[8](#_ftn694); this reason does not apply to the Rambam's work, "which he compiled based on the final conclusion of the Talmud."[9](#_ftn695)

**D.** The distinction between these two modes of studying Torah Shebaal Peh is also expressed in the difference between the Talmud Bavli and the Talmud Yerushalmi—the primary focus of the Talmud Bavli is pilpul, involving questions and resolutions in the depth of reasoning and the reasons for the halachos, whereas the primary focus of the Talmud Yerushalmi is definitive halachic rulings.

From this, it is understood that there is a superiority in studying definitive halachos over studying the reasons for halachos and engaging in pilpul in the depth of reasoning—as is known[14](#_ftn700) regarding the great superiority of studying the Talmud Yerushalmi over the Talmud Bavli.

#### 127

It should be added and noted from what is explained in Hemshech Tarsav[15](#_ftn701) that within the study of reasons and reasoning themselves, there are two modes: The first mode—where one exerts great effort in study to know and grasp the reason and logic on their own terms; and the second mode—which is better and reaches a higher level—where the primary exertion and study is not merely to know and grasp the intellect, but that the halachic ruling should be aligned with the true Will of the Almighty. This study is performed specifically out of yirah and kabbalas ol, and through this, one aligns with the truth of Torah.

From all this, we understand the great elevation of studying and knowing definitive halachos (the approach of the Rambam)—for this is study born of kabbalas ol, to know the true Will of the Almighty as it is contained in the halachos of the Torah.

**E.** Based on the above, we can explain what is stated in the Gemara[16](#_ftn702) that "Rav Yosef, on the day of Atzeres, would say... 'Were it not for this day that causes [this, etc.]'"—that Rav Yosef specifically emphasizes the special quality of "this day" of the Giving of the Torah:

It is stated in the Gemara[17](#_ftn703) that "Rav Yosef was a 'Sinai'" (meaning "Mishnayos and Braisos were arranged for him as they were given from Har Sinai"[18](#_ftn704)), and "Rabbah was an 'uprooter of mountains'" ("sharp and skilled in pilpul in Torah"[18](#_ftn704)). That is to say, Rabbah’s strength was in sharpness and pilpul, whereas Rav Yosef’s strength was in the knowledge of halachos.

And since Rav Yosef’s primary strength was (not in the pilpul of the reasons for halachos, but) in the knowledge of the halachos themselves, therefore Rav Yosef emphasizes the quality of the *day* of the Giving of the Torah, "this day" specifically, for on this day only the *Aseres Hadibros* were stated, which are *simple matters*[19](#_ftn705), also because they are *halachos without reasons* [for all the matters of the Torah, including the reasons for the details of the Aseres Hadibros, Moshe learned from Hashem during the forty days, whereas on "this day" only the Aseres Hadibros were stated—halachos without reasons][20](#_ftn706). This is the strength of Rav Yosef, "Sinai"—the knowledge of halachos.

## Sicha of the Night of the Second Day of Shavuos, 5711

#### 128

**A.** We find a dispute regarding the date of the Giving of the Torah: "On the sixth of the month the Ten Commandments were given to Israel; Rabbi Yosi says on the seventh of the month." "Rabbi Yosi said to you: Moshe added one day of his own accord" ("On the fourth [of the month] he was told to separate for four days, and he added one day, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, agreed with his opinion")[1](#_ftn707).

The Halacha follows the Sages[2](#_ftn708), that "on the sixth of the month the Ten Commandments were given to Israel"[3](#_ftn709). Therefore, we celebrate the "time of the giving of our Torah" on the sixth of Sivan. Even in the Diaspora, where we observe two days of Yom Tov, we read the Ten Commandments on the first day of Shavuos, the sixth of Sivan (and not on the second day, the seventh of the month).

**B.** Regarding the explanation of why the Halachic ruling is such that we do not say "Moshe added one day of his own accord"—for seemingly, based on the well-known greatness of the concept of *avodah* of the lower realms by their own power—to the extent that because of this "the words of the Scribes are more stringent[4](#_ftn710) than the words of Torah"[5](#_ftn711)—Rabbi Yosi’s opinion, that "Moshe added one day of his own accord," would be more fitting, as the *avodah* of the lower realms by their own power is emphasized in the Giving of the Torah itself[6](#_ftn712)—it can be said:

It is known that the innovation of the Giving of the Torah is the connection of the higher realms and the lower realms. For, prior to the Giving of the Torah, there was the decree that "the people of Rome (from the word *romemus* [exaltation][7](#_ftn713), which denotes the higher realms) shall not descend to Syria (from the word *surah* [turning away], which denotes the lower realms), and the people of Syria shall not ascend to Rome." The higher realms were above and the lower realms were below. At the Giving of the Torah, "[The Holy One, Blessed be He] nullified the first decree and said: The lower realms shall ascend to the higher realms, and the higher realms shall descend to the lower realms"[8](#_ftn714).

This matter was accomplished through an *hemshech* from a place most exalted, above the definition of higher and lower realms; therefore, it is within His power and ability to effect the connection of the higher and lower realms[9](#_ftn715).

Since the *hemshech* of the Giving of the Torah is from a level above the definition of higher and lower realms, above any connection to the worlds, therefore, the concept of "he added of his own accord" (*avodah* of the lower realms by their own power) does not apply to the Giving of the Torah, since the *avodah* of the lower realms cannot reach such an exalted level.

**C.** We must explain the lesson from this regarding *avodah*, as with every matter that must be brought into actual *avodah*.

Someone asked the Rebbe Rayatz two questions: one regarding *ahavah* and *yirah*, and one regarding the *avodah* of the angels. The Rebbe Rayatz answered his first question regarding *ahavah* and *yirah*, but regarding his second question about the *avodah* of the angels, he did not answer, saying that the *avodah* of the angels does not concern him[10](#_ftn716).

Regarding our subject:

The Giving of the Torah exists also in the present—that every year, on the festival of Shavuos, the "time of the giving of our Torah," the event of the Giving of the Torah is renewed.

The point of this is: Seemingly, since the Torah already existed beforehand, what is the innovation in the "time of the giving of our Torah" this year? It is that the Torah which existed beforehand *has already descended below* to the level of the created beings[11](#_ftn717), and the innovation in the "time of the giving of our Torah" is that a new *hemshech* is effected *from above*.

In relation to the innovation in the Giving of the Torah through this new *hemshech* from above, the concept of "Moshe added one day of his own accord" does not apply, since the *hemshech* is from such an exalted level that *avodah* does not reach there.

#### 130

**D.** From this, it is also understood in the opposite direction: since we are speaking of an *hemshech* from such an exalted level that *avodah* does not reach there, one should not take into account his own standing and state—that he is not yet worthy and needs to make preparations, etc.—but rather, *snatch whatever is possible* ("*areinkhapn vos m'ken*"), or in the words of Chazal[12](#_ftn718), "Snatch and eat, snatch and drink."

We should add an explanation for the reason for the order of "snatch and eat, snatch and drink"—"for the world from which we are departing is like a wedding feast"—in connection to our subject:

"*Azleinan*" (we are departing/going), a term of movement—denotes a level that is *b'ein-eruch* (incomparable), *bli-gevul* (infinite)[13](#_ftn719).

Since one is passing over ("*m'shtelt zich iber*") and elevating himself to a level that is *b'ein-eruch* ("*azleinan minei*")—like at the time of the Giving of the Torah, when a new *hemshech* is made from a level above the worlds—the person's standing and state from the perspective of his *avodah* does not matter, and he has nothing to think about regarding preparations, but rather, to snatch whatever is possible, "snatch and eat, snatch and drink."

Simply put: each and every person must snatch as much as possible *in the study of Torah*, both regarding the revealed aspects of Torah and (especially) regarding the inner dimensions of Torah.

**E.** There is an extra emphasis regarding the *bochurim* of the *yeshivos*[14](#_ftn720), whose entire occupation is the study of Torah; they certainly must conduct themselves in the manner of "snatch and eat, snatch and drink," to snatch as much as possible in the study of Torah.

My desire[15](#_ftn721) was that in preparation for the festival of Shavuos, every *bochur* would inform me, via a *petek*, what he had accomplished ("*vos er hot oifgeton*") in the study of Torah.

Regarding the actual outcome—there are "wise men" who did not submit *peteklach* at all,

[Although I do not understand what the "wisdom" is in that... as is known the saying of the Rebbe Maharash[16](#_ftn722): The Holy One, Blessed be He—one certainly cannot deceive; and even the world—one cannot deceive; rather, whom does one deceive? Himself ("*zich alein*"). And is it a "trick" to deceive a fool?!],

and it is understood that the non-submission of the *peteklach* in itself constitutes a "sign" and "proof" of their standing and state[17](#_ftn723)...

#### 131

And even those who did inform me in a *petek* about their standing and state in the study of Torah, it does not reach—incomparably—what was expected from the outset! Rather, they at least have the concept of "he who confesses and abandons [his ways] will be shown mercy"[18](#_ftn724).

In any case, from here on, all the *bochurim* should endeavor to increase in the study of Torah in the manner of "snatch and eat, snatch and drink," to snatch as much as possible.

**F.** It should be added that the concept of "snatch and eat, snatch and drink" (to snatch as much as possible and not wait for preparations, etc.) applies especially to the study of the inner dimensions of Torah:

There are those who think that in order to study the inner dimensions of Torah, one needs preparations in order to be worthy of it.

—Someone asked me regarding his order of study in the Zohar [Chassidus—he does not study, because it is not to his spirit, only Zohar...], whether he must first immerse in a *mikveh* every time he studies.—

Therefore, we must emphasize that one should not make calculations as to whether one is suited for the study of the inner dimensions of Torah or not, and one should not wait to make preparations, but rather, snatch and study as much as possible.

The truth is that he will be "whipped" ("*m'vet im shmeisn*") for studying the inner dimensions of Torah while in an undesirable standing and state, for how is it possible to study the inner dimensions of Torah with human intellect?! But nevertheless, even in this standing and state, it is better that he snatch and study the inner dimensions of Torah, the Torah of Chassidus, because through this he connects with the Rebbes, the *nesi'im* of the Torah of Chassidus, and they will already pull him out from wherever he may be ("*di rebbeyim veln im shoin aroisshlepn fun umetum*").

The early *Chassidim*[19](#_ftn725) would prepare themselves to enter for *yechidus*; one *Chassid* would prepare for three years, and another *Chassid* for seven years (and there were those who prepared for an even longer time), but today there is no time to wait until one makes preparations; rather, one must snatch and connect to the Rebbe, and then the Rebbe will pull him out of his standing and state.

In any case, one must know that a *Chassid* who is "blemished" ("*a kaliker*") is better than one who is not a *Chassid tamim* (and the Rebbe explained: I mean *tamim* in the sense of the negation of being "blemished").

#### 132

**G.** Regarding the practical application:

One must snatch and study the inner dimensions of Torah; snatch a *maamar* from *Torah Or*, a *maamar* from *Likutei Torah*, a *maamar* from this *nasi* and a *maamar* from that *nasi*, for through this one connects with our Rebbes, the *nesi'im*, and they will already pull him out of his standing and state[20](#_ftn726).

It should be added regarding the connection to the Rebbe Rayatz—that because he is now in a standing and state of holiness most exalted even to physical eyes, *Chassidim* must also be in a standing and state appropriate to this, and since this is how it must be, it is so in truth[21](#_ftn727).

## Second Day of Shavuos, 5711

#### 133

(Unedited transcript)

**"Two thousand years before the creation of the world, the Torah preceded it,"** as it is stated[1](#_ftn728), "I was His confidant (amon), and I was a delight (sha’ashuim) day by day," and a day of the Ribono shel Olam is a thousand years[2](#_ftn729). My sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe[3](#_ftn730), raises a point of precision here: one must understand the nature of these two thousand years that the Torah preceded the creation of the world. After all, the entire concept of time is a new creation that was brought into being via *yesh me’ayin* during the creation of the world, just like the totality of the creation that the Ribono shel Olam created *me’ayin l’yesh*[4](#_ftn731). If so, what is the meaning of the statement that the Torah preceded the creation of the world by two thousand years?

**By way of introduction,** we find[5](#_ftn732) that even in earlier seforim, they questioned this statement of our Sages. How can the concept of "two thousand years" exist prior to the creation of the world, given that the measurement of time is determined by the luminaries, the stars, and the constellations, etc., as it is written[6](#_ftn733), "They shall serve as signs, for seasons, for days, and for years"? If so, how can there be a concept of two thousand years prior to the creation of the luminaries? The answer provided is that the "two thousand years" refers to the measurement as we know it now; had we imagined that the luminaries—which are the vessels that measure time—existed then, this measurement of time would have been equivalent to two thousand years of our current time. However, on a deeper level, the difficulty concerns the very essence of time, the nature of which is the changes of past, present, and future[7](#_ftn734). In a short span of time there are few changes, and in a long span of time there are many changes. This concept is only relevant when there is an existence of created beings, for then there is the matter of changes. But prior to the creation of the world, since there was no existence at all, and consequently there was no matter of changes, what then is the meaning of the "two thousand years" of time? This implies that the absence of changes—which is the concept of eternity—is such that even while being within the parameters of time, time does not exert any weakening effect upon it. From this, it is understood that just as time does not exert a negative effect upon it,

#### 134

it also does not exert a positive effect upon it. If so, it makes no difference whether the measure of time is two thousand years, more, or less. The answer to this is that although it is eternal and is not changed by time, nevertheless, since it exists within time and has a relationship with other matters that are within the category of time, therefore, in relation to those other matters, we attribute the concept of time to it[8](#_ftn735). However, in truth, the difficulty is even deeper, for time itself is a new creation that was brought into being via *yesh me’ayin*. Just as the existence of space is a new existence that did not exist previously, so too is time a new creation that did not exist prior to its creation, as is well known[9](#_ftn736) that time and space are interconnected. According to this, it is even more difficult to understand the meaning of the two thousand years that the Torah preceded the creation of the world.

**My sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, explains[10](#_ftn737)** that this does not refer to a precedence in time, but rather a precedence in stature. This precedence is in the manner of "two thousand years," *b'alpayim*—*aalfecha chochma, aalfecha binah* (I will teach you wisdom, I will teach you understanding)[11](#_ftn738). This refers to the level of the *mochin* (intellects), which are above the worlds[12](#_ftn739). As is known, the beginning of the worlds is from the level of the *midos* (emotional attributes), which are for the sake of the worlds, as it is written[13](#_ftn740), "For in six days Hashem made the heavens and the earth." This means that before the creation of the heavens and the earth, there first had to be the creation of the "six days," which are the six *midos*[14](#_ftn741), through which He made the heavens and the earth—where "heavens" refers to all the higher worlds, and "earth" refers to all the lower worlds. But the *mochin* are above the worlds, for they are "for Himself." Just as it is in a person below, where the *midos* are for the sake of the "other"—meaning that the entire concept of *midos* is relevant only when there is an "other," which is true even regarding the arousal of the *midos* within oneself, and certainly regarding the activity of the *midos*, for which the existence of an "other" is strictly necessary. This is not the case with *mochin*; not only is an "other" not needed for the arousal of the *mochin*, but even for the activity of the *mochin*, an "other" is not required. Furthermore, the "other" actually disturbs the *mochin*, since the nature of *mochin* is "for Himself." Similarly, it is understood above: the nature of the *midos* is for the sake of the worlds, and the nature of the *mochin* is "for Himself." And although the *Etzem* (Essence) above does not need to descend to the level of the light as it is above *Atzilus*, and certainly does not need the *mochin* of *Chochma* and *Binah* (the two thousand years), nevertheless, this is the order of *hemshech* (drawing down): first

#### 135

there must be the light as it is for itself (the concept of *mochin*), and only afterwards can there be the light as it is for its "other" (the concept of *midos*). This is the meaning of "two thousand years the Torah preceded the creation of the world," for it is said, "I was a delight day by day," for the Torah has its root in the level of the *mochin* that are above the worlds.

b) **However,** one still needs to understand the statement of our Sages that "the Torah preceded the world by two thousand years." Why do they consider the stature of the Torah as it is "a delight day by day" (which is the concept of two thousand years, for a day of the Ribono shel Olam is a thousand years), and not as it is in a more exalted level, regarding which it is written previously, "I was His confidant (*amon*)"? The order in this verse is from above to below: the verse begins with "I was His confidant," which refers to the Torah as it is in His Essence; then "I was a delight day by day," which refers to the Torah as it is drawn down into the level of the *mochin* (*Chochma* and *Binah*); and then it counts further levels, concluding with "and my delights are with the children of men," which refers to the Torah as it descended below. Thus, the most exalted stature of the Torah is what is written, "I was His confidant." What is the reason that in this statement of our Sages, the stature of the Torah is explained as it is in the level of "a delight day by day," and not the more exalted stature, "I was His confidant"?

**Seemingly,** one could say that the order of the verse is from below to above. For regarding the interpretation of "I was His confidant," it is stated in the Midrash[15](#_ftn742) that the Torah says, "I was the artisan's tool of the Ribono shel Olam," for He would look into the Torah and create the world. Based on this, it turns out that the beginning of the verse, "I was His confidant," is the level of the Torah as it relates to the creation of the world, and afterwards it counts the stature of "a delight day by day," which is the Torah as it is in the level of the *mochin* (*Chochma* and *Binah*) that are above the world [and it concludes with "and my delights are with the children of men," as the Torah was given below, which is the most exalted level, since it is specifically through the *avodah* below that one reaches the highest level, as will be explained]. But in truth, the matter of "I was His confidant" is the most exalted level of the Torah, as understood from Rashi’s commentary: *amon* means "greatness with Him." It must be that the fact that the Torah is the "artisan's tool of the Ribono shel Olam" is also a most exalted matter. The explanation is[16](#_ftn743): sometimes it is written, "By the word of Hashem the heavens were made"[17](#_ftn744), meaning the creation is from the level of speech; and sometimes it is written[18](#_ftn745), "All that Hashem desired, He did," meaning the creation is from the level of Hashem’s desire and will. It is explained[19](#_ftn746) that every created being is composed of matter and form. The matter, which is the body

#### 136

and the tangibility of the creature, is made by the "word of Hashem," while the form of the creature is made by the "desire and will of Hashem," from which level the *bitul* (nullification) of the created beings is drawn. The fact that the Torah is the "artisan's tool of the Ribono shel Olam" means that through it, the form is created, which is connected with the *bitul* in the created beings. Furthermore, it can be said that the creation through the Torah (the "artisan's tool of the Ribono shel Olam") also relates to the creation of the matter. This is based on what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*[20](#_ftn747), that the creation of *yesh* (existence) is specifically through the power of the *Etzem* (Essence), which is not caused by any cause or reason that preceded it, *chas v'shalom*. Therefore, He alone has the power and ability to create *yesh me’ayin* and from absolute nothingness. This is why the creation of the world is through the Torah, since its root is in His Essence, *yisbarach*[21](#_ftn748). From all this, it is understood that the order of the verse is from above to below, meaning that the most exalted level of the Torah is "I was His confidant." According to this, it is not understood why our Sages chose the stature of the Torah that preceded by two thousand years—which is what is written, "I was a delight day by day"—and not the first and more exalted matter, "I was His confidant."

**Also,** one must understand the phrase "I *will be* (*ehyeh*) His confidant," etc. *Ehyeh* is in the future tense. Yet this matter was stated (in the aforementioned statement of our Sages where this verse is mentioned) in the time of the Amoraim, or at the very least in the time of the Giving of the Torah, for everything that a veteran student is destined to innovate was already given to Moshe at Sinai[22](#_ftn749). If so, it should have been stated in the past tense ("I was"), and why is it stated in the future tense ("I will be")? According to the rules of grammar, the *vav* (*v'ehyeh*) transforms the future tense into the past tense[23](#_ftn750) (*v'havah*). However, in the *Zohar*[24](#_ftn751) it states that what is written, "I will be His confidant," is similar to "I will be what I will be" (*Ehyeh Asher Ehyeh*)[25](#_ftn752)—that "I am destined to be revealed" in the time to come. From this, it is understood that the precision is specifically in the future tense, "I will be." One must understand why this matter is stated in the future tense.

c) **To understand this,** we must first explain the five matters enumerated in the verse: "I was His confidant," "I was a delight day by day," "playing before Him at all times," "playing in the world of His earth," and "my delights are with the children of men." It is explained[26](#_ftn753) that "I was His confidant" refers to the Torah as it is in His Essence, *yisbarach*—"with Him." "I was a delight day by day" refers to the Torah as it is drawn down into the level of the *mochin*, *Chochma* and *Binah*, which is the totality of intellect. Regarding this level, the term

#### 137

"delight" (*sha’ashuim*) is used (even though it does not say *sha’ashuai*—my delights—which refers to the essential delights, but rather just *sha’ashuim*), because even as the Torah is in the level of *mochin*, it contains the element of *taanug* (pleasure). It is known[27](#_ftn754) the precision in the language of our Sages[28](#_ftn755), "The Torah emanated (*nafkat*) from *Chochma*." *Nafkat* is precise: its revelation is through *Chochma*, but its root is above *Chochma*, in the level of the higher *taanug*. Therefore, even when it comes to be revealed in the *mochin* of *Chochma* and *Binah*, it contains the element of *sha’ashuim*. As is known, the revelation of *taanug* is specifically in *Binah*, as the saying goes[29](#_ftn756), "The revelation of *Atik* is in *Binah*." This is what is meant by[30](#_ftn757), "And the Levite shall serve (*v'avad*)," *avad* is *Atik*—that the revelation of *Atik* is in *Binah*. Furthermore, the beginning of the revelation of *taanug* and the essence of *taanug* is in the level of *Chochma*. This is why the face of Rabbi Avahu glowed when he found a new *Tosefta*[31](#_ftn758); the matter of a new *Tosefta* indicates innovation and invention, which is the essence of *Chochma*[32](#_ftn759), and from this came the *taanug* that caused his face to glow. This is also the concept of the Garden of Eden, as is known[33](#_ftn760) that *Chochma* is called *Eden*, and *Binah* is called *Gan Eden*. This means that although *Binah* is the level of the river[34](#_ftn761) regarding which it is said[35](#_ftn762), "And a river goes out from *Eden* to water the garden" (which is above the level of the garden), nevertheless, from this itself it is understood that *Binah* is not the level of *Eden* itself, but is only the river that goes out from *Eden*, while *Chochma* is the level of *Eden* itself. All this is because the root of the Torah is above *Chochma*; therefore, even as it is in the level of *Chochma*, and even as it emanates from *Chochma*, it contains the element of *sha’ashuim*. The verse continues, "playing before Him at all times," which refers to the Torah as it is drawn down into the level of the *midos*, which is the concept of "at all times"—it is within the parameters of time and "time," but it is in the state of "at all times," without changes. Regarding this level, it says "playing before Him," etc. The concept of "playing" (*sechok*) is the revelation of *taanug* [and this is what[36](#_ftn763) our Sages said[37](#_ftn764), "It is forbidden for a person to fill his mouth with laughter in this world"—specifically laughter—meaning that even though the *avodah* of Hashem must be with joy, as it is written[38](#_ftn765), "Because you did not serve Hashem your G-d with joy," and furthermore, it must be with a "good heart," as the verse continues, "and with a good heart," nevertheless, it is forbidden to fill one's mouth with laughter, for this indicates an excessive feeling of joy]. This concept is specifically in the *midos*, because the drawing down of *taanug* into the *mochin* is not in such a state of revelation, and is felt only in the glowing of the face,

#### 138

whereas it is specifically in the *midos* that the *taanug* comes in a revealed and felt manner. The verse continues, "playing in the world of His earth," which refers to the Torah being clothed in the *sefirah* of *Malchus*, the level of "earth," for *Malchus* is the root of the created beings of *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*. The verse concludes, "and my delights are with the children of men," which refers to the Torah as it is drawn down specifically below. In this level specifically, the term *sha’ashuai* (my delights) is used, which refers to the essential *sha’ashuim*, because it is specifically through the study of Torah below that one reaches the level of the *sha’ashuim* of the King in His Essence[39](#_ftn766).

d) **The explanation of this matter[40](#_ftn767)** is that it is known that in the drawing down of *Elokus* in general, there are two modes: *Ohr Yashar* (direct light) and *Ohr Chozer* (reflected light). So too is it in the study of Torah[41](#_ftn768): there is the study of Torah in the manner of *Ohr Yashar*—where one studies and understands, etc.—and study in the manner of *Ohr Chozer*, when one studies and does not understand, or has questions from elsewhere, and overcomes the concealments and questions, etc. This is the difference between the Talmud Yerushalmi and the Talmud Bavli[42](#_ftn769): in the Talmud Yerushalmi there is not a multitude of questions and lengthy *pilpul* and back-and-forth, and the study is in the manner of *Ohr Yashar*; in the Talmud Bavli there are questions, etc., and as our Sages said[43](#_ftn770), "He has placed me in darkness"[44](#_ftn771)—this is the Talmud of Bavel—which is study in the manner of *Ohr Chozer*. It is known that study in the manner of *Ohr Chozer* reaches a level incomparably higher than the study of *Ohr Yashar*. This is similar to what we find regarding the superiority of the Talmud Yerushalmi over the Talmud Bavli, to such an extent that Rabbi Zeira had to fast one hundred fasts in order to forget his learning of the Talmud Bavli[45](#_ftn772). From this, it is understood that the Talmud Bavli is not in the same category as the Talmud Yerushalmi; for if the ascent from the Talmud Bavli to the Talmud Yerushalmi were a matter of order and gradation, he would not have needed to forget the Talmud Bavli in order to learn the Talmud Yerushalmi. Since he had to forget the *chizah* (vision/grasp) of the Talmud Bavli to learn the Talmud Yerushalmi, it is understood that this is an incomparable ascent. From this, it is also understood regarding the superiority of the Talmud Bavli over the Talmud Yerushalmi—the superiority of *Ohr Chozer*—that this superiority is completely incomparable.

**Now,** within the study of *Ohr Chozer* itself, there are two modes[46](#_ftn773). The first mode is that one exerts himself in his study in order to understand the subject. Although there is tremendous exertion here,

#### 139

and the matter of exertion is not a matter of intellectual understanding—for the nature of intellect is from above to below and not from below to above, and the very matter of exertion is not a matter of intellect but above it—nevertheless, his exertion is within the realm of intellect. The second mode is that one studies in order to know the action that he must perform, for he wants to grasp the higher intent of the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, *baruch Hu*, and he fears that he might not align with the higher will. Therefore, awe and fear fall upon him, and he stands in a state of constriction to exert himself even more, etc. This exertion is not a matter of intellect at all. Seemingly, it would appear that in the second mode, it is not possible for the study to be with *taanug*. For in the first mode, even though he studies with great exertion and is surrendered to the study with his entire essence (*ingantzen ibergegeben*) to the point that his life is not worth anything, nevertheless, since his exertion is to grasp the intellect, it is possible for there to be *taanug* in this. This is not the case in the second mode, where he is not in a state of intellect at all, but his entire existence is in constriction; seemingly, there is no possibility for *taanug* in this. But in truth, even in this mode of study, there is the matter of *taanug*. This can be understood through a parable[47](#_ftn774) of a minister and a servant who are carrying out the King's command. The minister knows how the King governs the country for the good, and therefore he carries out the command also because of the minister's love for the country; since he knows that carrying out the King's command is a benefit to the country, he carries out the command and has vitality and *taanug* in it. This is not the case with the servant who carries out the King's command; the servant is not an existence for himself at all, and his entire existence is only to carry out the master's command. He has neither intellectual understanding nor emotional feeling in this, and seemingly he has no *taanug* in it at all. But in truth, it must be that the servant also has a (hidden) *taanug* in carrying out the King's command. The proof of this is that we see the servant wants to beautify the King's command, to carry it out with *hiddur* (embellishment) and beauty. From this, it is proven that he has *taanug* in it, for from the perspective of his own *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) and servitude, he should only carry out the King's command as it is and nothing more, for the King's command is only the fulfillment of His will and nothing more, and there is no matter of beauty and embellishment in that. From the fact that the servant wants to beautify and embellish the carrying out of the King's command, it is proven that he has a (hidden) *taanug* in carrying out His command. It can be said that the servant's *taanug* is the *taanug* of the King Himself, for since the servant is not an existence for himself at all—*er alein iz gornit*—and his entire existence is only to fulfill the master's will, therefore his *taanug* is the master's *taanug*, meaning that the master's *taanug* is found within him. So it is also in the analogy: the one who studies specifically "in order to do," even though his study and exertion are from a state of constriction of the soul, nevertheless, in truth, he has a (hidden) *taanug* in this. On the contrary, since he himself has nothing in this study,

#### 140

for the study is only "in order to do," it turns out that his *taanug* in this is the *taanug* from above, in which the *taanug* from above is felt.

**The point of this is** that through the second mode of study in the manner of *Ohr Chozer*, one reaches the essential *taanug* from above, the level of the inner dimension of *Atik* itself[48](#_ftn775). This is not the case in the first mode, through which one reaches only the level of the inner dimension of *Abba*—the inner dimension of *Atik*[49](#_ftn776). Although the intention here is not that the inner dimension of *Abba* clothes and covers the inner dimension of *Atik*, nevertheless, this is as the inner dimension of *Atik* is drawn into the inner dimension of *Abba*, and it is not the level of the inner dimension of *Atik* itself. The difference between them is like the difference between felt and complex *taanug* and simple *taanug*. As is explained[50](#_ftn777) also regarding the revelation in the time to come, sometimes it is stated[51](#_ftn778) that the Ribono shel Olam will make an *ariston* (meaning a morning meal[52](#_ftn779)) for His righteous servants in the time to come, and sometimes it is stated[53](#_ftn780) that in the World to Come there is no eating or drinking, etc. It is explained that these are two levels in the revelation of the time to come: at first, there will be the revelation of the complex and felt *taanug*, and this is the concept of *ariston*; and afterwards, there will be the revelation of the simple *taanug*, the essential *taanug* that is not felt at all, which is the concept of "in the World to Come there is no eating," etc.

e) **This is** "and my delights are with the children of men," that specifically through the study of Torah below (the "children of men"), where the study is in the manner of *Ohr Chozer*, and in the aforementioned second mode, one reaches the level of *sha’ashuai*—the essential *sha’ashuim*, the *sha’ashuim* of the King in His Essence—which is the concept of the Torah as it is in His Essence, *yisbarach*, "I will be His confidant"[54](#_ftn781). With this, we can understand what is said, "I will be His confidant," etc.—*ehyeh* is specifically in the future tense—because this matter will be revealed specifically in the time to come. This means that now the *hemshech* (drawing down) of the Torah as it is in His Essence, *yisbarach*, is *being accomplished*, and there are also additional lights in *Atzilus*[55](#_ftn782), but the *revelation* will be specifically in the time to come. This is also why, in the aforementioned statement of our Sages, they count the stature of the Torah that preceded the world by two thousand years—which is the concept of "I was a delight day by day"—and do not count the stature of "I will be His confidant," because the matter of "I will be His confidant" is the Torah as it is in His Essence, *yisbarach*, which is not the matter of the Torah as it is in itself, for this matter is from the perspective of His Essence, *yisbarach*, and not from the perspective of the Torah.

#### 141

**This is also** what my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, said[56](#_ftn783) in the name of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, that at the Giving of the Torah, three things were given: the revealed Torah, the secrets of the Torah, and the power for *avodah*. The explanation is that the revealed Torah is in revelation now. The secrets of the Torah are the reasons for the Torah that will be revealed in the time to come, which is the level of the felt *taanug* mentioned above. And the power for *avodah*, which is in the manner of *Ohr Chozer*, is a matter that is above even intellect and hidden reason, above even the reasons for the Torah that will be revealed in the time to come, since this matter reaches His Essence, *yisbarach*, and as mentioned above, this matter will be revealed specifically in the time to come. However, this matter was also given at the Giving of the Torah, for since there will not be another Giving of the Torah[57](#_ftn784), it is understood that all matters were already given at the Giving of the Torah, only that the revelation will be in the time to come.

\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

## Sicha of the Second Day of Shavuos, 5711

#### 142

The Rebbe washed his hands for the meal and instructed that a *nigun* be played.

**A.** My father-in-law, the Rebbe, used to wish people in his blessing for Shavuos: "May you receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness (*pnimiyus*)."

The explanation of this phrasing is as follows:

The Giving of the Torah (*Matan Torah*) was such that "Hashem suspended the mountain over them like a barrel and said to them: If you accept the Torah, good, and if not..." [1] ("They accepted it under duress" [2]), which is not a state of joy.

[This is also emphasized in the text of the *tefillah* and *Kiddush*, where only on a *Yom Tov* that falls on Shabbos do we say "with love, a holy convocation," whereas on a *Yom Tov* that falls on a weekday we do not say "with love"—because, "the holy convocation of Shabbos, the Jewish people accepted upon themselves with love at Marah before they came to Sinai, and He did not suspend the mountain over them like a barrel; but the other *mitzvos* they accepted at Sinai, and Hashem suspended the mountain over them like a barrel" [3], and consequently, it is not "with love"].

Furthermore: Since *Matan Torah* is a process from above to below, it is not in a manner of inwardness.

It should also be noted what is explained in the *Midrash* [4] that "in the days of Moshiach there will be a marriage," but *Matan Torah* was only a matter of betrothal (*erusin*) ("the betrothal was of this world").

The difference between betrothal and marriage is that in betrothal, she is only "forbidden to all others" [5], and it is only in a manner of *makif* (encompassing) [6], whereas the union in inwardness is achieved specifically through marriage, as it is written [7], "Therefore a man shall leave his father and his mother and cleave to his wife, and they shall become one flesh"—through the matter of the birth of a child [8].

And although the matter of marriage (union in inwardness) will only be in the time to come—the preparation, the introduction, and the qualification for this must be even in this present time. Similar to the well-known concept

#### 143

regarding the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, whose purpose is to add lights in *Atzilus*, except that now it is in a state of concealment [9], and the revelation will be in the time to come.

This is the content of the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the blessing of a *Tzaddik*, which is not merely a blessing, but also a *granting of strength*—that the receiving of the Torah should be (not out of coercion, but) *with joy*. And when the receiving of the Torah is with joy, which breaks through boundaries [10], then it can be (not only from above to below, but also) a receiving *with inwardness*.

And through this, one merits the perfection of the matter of receiving the Torah with inwardness—the matter of the marriage of the time to come, with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, truly.

***

**B.** In anticipation of Shavuos, two *maamarim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, were published [11].

—The *maamarim* were published in good time [12], so that they were surely studied everywhere: on-site, out of town, in all countries, overseas, and also in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—

The second *maamar* is based on the teaching of our Sages [13], "Two thousand years before the world, the Torah preceded it."

The Rebbe delivered the *maamar* entitled "Two thousand years before the world, the Torah preceded it."

***

**C.** I was asked what the innovation of *Matan Torah* was. Since the questioners were such that they were not capable of understanding the content of "And I was with Him as an *amon*," "And I was His delight day by day" [14], as per all the details mentioned above (in the *maamar* [15])—I explained to them that *Matan Torah* effected the connection of the created beings with the Creator.

The matter is as follows:

A created being and the Creator are infinitely distant from one another, and consequently, it is impossible

#### 144

in any way for the created being to ascend to the Creator. To what can this be compared? To two things between which a deep chasm is opened, which it is impossible to cross in any way.

Among *created beings* themselves, there are different types that are distant from each other, but nevertheless, there is some connection and relevance between them. For example: the four categories—inanimate, vegetative, animate, and speaking—although there is a disparity of value between them, there is also a connection between them, for the inanimate provides benefit to the vegetative, the vegetative to the animate, and the animate to the speaking; from this itself it is proven that there is some connection between them. Moreover, through the inanimate serving the speaking, the inanimate is elevated—to a certain degree—to the level of the speaking [16].

Not so with *created being and Creator*—there is no value or relevance between them at all, and there is no possibility for a created being to ascend to the Creator.

However, at *Matan Torah*, the greatest innovation took place—the connection of the created being with the Creator, that through the Torah, the created beings can ascend to the Creator.

And although even before *Matan Torah* there were souls in the world, which are *Elokus*, the souls are as *Elokus* becomes in the category of a created being, or as *Elokus* becomes in the category of *yesh* (as in the two expressions in the *drushei Chassidus* [17]). Not so the Torah; even when it is below, it is *Elokus* itself, and therefore, specifically through it, the connection of the created beings with the Creator is effected.

*

**D.** Among the reasons [18] that the Torah was given specifically in the desert is to teach and instruct [19] that just as the desert is a "place of *hefker* (ownerless property)" [20], without a master, so too regarding the Torah—it has no master, and consequently, every Jew has a connection to the Torah, and when he studies the Torah, it becomes his [21] ("the Torah becomes his").

However, it still requires explanation:

The study and instruction mentioned from the giving of the Torah in the desert (which is a place of *hefker*)—explains the giving of the Torah in a place that is not subject to the authority of a master, but rather in (a desert which is) a *place of hefker*; but this reason is not sufficient to explain why the Torah was given specifically in a *desolate wilderness* ("in a desolate desert"), and in the words of the verse [22], "a land of drought and deep darkness, without water," a place that lacked clothing, food, and even water, for which reason, while they were in the desert, their clothes grew with them (as it is in the *Midrashim* of our Sages [23]), and their food was only the *manna* that descended for them from heaven [24], and water Hashem gave them through a rock [25]—in such a place specifically was the Torah given?!

And especially according to the known principle that in a parable of the Torah, *all* the details of the parable are intended to correspond to the subject [26], and since, according to the aforementioned explanation, the matter of the desert serves as a parable for the Torah (that just as the desert is a place of *hefker*, so the Torah belongs to every Jew), it must be said that all the details that were in the desert (the parable) are connected and relevant to *Matan Torah* (the subject). Seemingly, the aforementioned reason is relevant only to one detail of the desert (the parable)—that it is a place of *hefker*, and not to the additional details (mentioned above) that existed in the desert?

**E.** The point of the explanation is this—that the giving of the Torah in a place of desolation specifically, which lacked all the physical necessities required for human existence, comes to teach and instruct that a person who studies Torah must remove from his heart all worries and rely entirely *on Hashem* to fulfill all his needs, both physically and spiritually.

More specifically:

Regarding the engagement in Torah study—there are those who justify their lack of engagement in Torah with various strange claims and excuses, saying that there are several obstacles hindering them from Torah study, both physical obstacles and spiritual obstacles.

For example—regarding spiritual obstacles and distractions:

#### 146

When one demands of a businessman to set aside times for Torah, he argues that this is not his business: he is a businessman, and consequently, he is connected to giving *tzedakah* and similar matters, but not to Torah study.

And especially since he knows that one of the special *avodos* belonging to a businessman is "detaching himself" ("*oprayzn zich*") from his business in the middle of the day for the *Mincha* prayer, as is known [27] that this is the special virtue of the *Mincha* prayer, to the extent that even "Elijah was answered only in the *Mincha* prayer" [28]. Since that is so—the businessman argues—he already has a most significant matter, and why do they pressure him ("*farvos yogt men im*") to engage in Torah study specifically [29]?

Similar to this is his argument regarding the study of the *Chitas* lessons:

When one demands of a businessman to study the *Chumash* portion with Rashi’s commentary, and especially ("*ver redt noch*") the lesson in the *Tanya*—he argues that since the *Toras HaChassidus* demands *avodah* in an orderly and gradual manner, he will first fulfill all his matters in perfection, including and especially—the *avodah* of the *Mincha* prayer, until it is (as above) like the prayer of Elijah the Prophet... and after that—he will continue to ascend to a higher level in his *avodah*. He does not refuse ("*er zogt zich nit op*"), Heaven forbid, to study *Chumash* with Rashi, or *Tanya*, but in his opinion, everything must be in its time ("*altz mit der tzeit*"), after he is free from all his other matters, in an orderly fashion.

And likewise is the attitude of the *yoshev ohel* (the full-time student)—regarding his matters:

When one demands of him the *avodah* of "All my bones shall say" [30], "It shall not depart, etc." [31], and the like, he does not refuse this ("*zogt er zich nit op fun dem*"), but he argues that first of all, there is a need for preparations for this: first he must rest ("*prier darf er zich oisshlofn*") so that his mind will be calm, and likewise he needs to guard himself [32], to eat refined foods ("*eidele macholim*"), etc.,

#### 147

—as it is in the *Alshich* [33] (and likewise in the *Responsa* of the Rambam [34]) that "the proper conditions... for learning wisdom... are eating and drinking refined and good things, because coarse food imparts thickness and coarseness to the brain"—

And only after all this—the *yoshev ohel* argues—will he sit down to study in the appropriate manner...

**F.** And this is the lesson and instruction from the giving of the Torah in the desert, "a land of drought and deep darkness, without water"—that regarding Torah study, a person must rely entirely on Hashem. Therefore, even though it seems to the person studying that he lacks the necessities required for Torah study (like the situation in the desolate desert), physical needs or spiritual needs—he should not take that into account, and he must dedicate himself entirely to Torah study.

In other words:

Just as the first *Matan Torah* came specifically through the fact that the Jewish people left the land of Egypt [35] into a desolate desert, "a land not sown" [36], without knowing

#### 148

with what and how their needs would be provided ("*nit vissendik vi un mit vos zei velen oisskumen*"),

—and as it was in practice, that the *manna* was given to them in the merit of Moshe, the pillar of cloud in the merit of Aharon, and the water in the merit of Miriam [37], which is to say, that in order to obtain their needs they were required to rely on the merit of three *Tzaddikim* [38]—

And specifically then were they prepared and worthy for the receiving of the Torah;

Likewise is the lesson and instruction for every Jew, including and especially—the instruction to us in this time of ours, that one must sit down to study Torah ("*men darf zich zetzin lernen Torah*"), and rely entirely on Hashem, and then Hashem will bestow everything necessary in both physical and spiritual matters [39].

*

**G.** The difference between the *Omer* which permits the new grain in the country and the Two Loaves which permit the new grain in the *Mikdash*, the details of the explanations of this according to the revealed Torah, and the content of their matters in the *avodah* of Hashem—was edited by the Rebbe and printed [40] in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 2, p. 134 and onwards.

*

**H.** Shavuos is the *Yom Hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov [41].

Once, there was a doubt whether the passing was on the first day of Shavuos or the second [42]. However, from the *maamar* of the Alter Rebbe [43] regarding the passing of the Baal Shem Tov, "On the *fourth* day the luminaries were taken," it is proven that he passed away on the first day of Shavuos, since the second day of Shavuos cannot fall on a Wednesday (as is known [44] the mnemonic for the calendar of the holidays "A"T B"S," that the calendar of Shavuos (S') is on the same day that the second day (B') of Pesach falls, and since "Pesach does not fall on D"V" [45], Shavuos will not fall on a Tuesday, and consequently, the second day of Shavuos will not fall on a Wednesday).

#### 149

And since the passing was on the first day of Shavuos, the burial was on the second day of Shavuos, as only then is it permitted to perform all the needs of the deceased by Jews [46] (and the law that it is forbidden to delay and one must bury immediately (on the first day) by a non-Jew [47]—does not apply here, since the Baal Shem Tov commanded the "Chevra Kadisha" that *they* "should engage in his burial" [48], and one delays the deceased in order to fulfill his words [49]).

Thus, the *Hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov belongs to *both days* of Shavuos: to the first day—on account of the passing, and to the second day—on account of the burial (and it may be said that because of this, the doubt arose whether the *Hilula* is on the first day or the second).

To add, that the passing of Moshe Rabbeinu also belongs to both days, because: we find that Moshe passed away on Shabbos (which is why we say on Shabbos "Your righteousness is righteousness") [50], and we find that on the day of his passing he wrote thirteen Torah scrolls [51], from which it is proven that he passed away on a weekday. And among the resolutions to this [52]—is that his passing was on both days: the beginning of the passing—on Friday, and its end—on (the *Mincha* of) Shabbos.

**I.** It is necessary to explain the connection and relevance of the *Yom Hilula* of the Baal Shem Tov to Shavuos:

By way of introduction to what is explained in the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from the 2nd of Nissan (which was published in anticipation of the 2nd of Nissan this year) [53] that "it must be understood why the day of the passing of a *Tzaddik* is called *Yom Hilula*... for *Hilula* is joy like the joy of a bride and groom," and he also brings the teaching of our Sages [54] "on the day of his wedding, this is *Matan Torah*," "that *Matan Torah* is called a wedding, which is the matter of *Hilula*," and he explains that the matter of *Hilula* is the revelation of the power of the *Ein Sof* in created beings, both regarding the matter of procreation which is through marriage, and regarding the day of the passing of a *Tzaddik*, the completion and perfection of his *avodah* in drawing down *Elokus* into the world.

And it is explained elsewhere [55] that this matter belongs specifically to the day of the passing of a *Tzaddik* whose *avodah* was in the revelation of the *pnimiyus haTorah* (inner dimension of Torah), which is why we find specifically regarding Rashbi that the day of his passing is called by the name *Hilula*.

#### 150

And if these things are said regarding Rashbi who revealed the *pnimiyus haTorah* only to select individuals [56]—regarding the Baal Shem Tov who revealed the *pnimiyus haTorah* *to all*, it is all the more so.

*

**J.** Regarding the passing of Moshe Rabbeinu (mentioned above)—we find in the *Midrashim* of our Sages [57] that the reason he remained outside the Land is because he wanted to remain with the people of his generation, in order to take them and come together with them to the Land of Israel.

The explanation for this—is that the existence of Moshe Rabbeinu as he is in his entire essence and being, is in his being with the people of his generation ("*mit zeine iden*") [58], and if he cannot be together with the people of his generation, what is the benefit for him in entering the Land of Israel, or other lofty matters?!... Therefore, if the people of his generation remain in the desert, he also remains with them.

And so it is with my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation—that the reason he remains for the time being outside the Land, is because he does not want to separate from the Chassidim who are connected to him, and therefore he remains with them, in order to take everyone—the connected Chassidim and also those who have some connection to him (and even those who for the time being are in a state and situation of sinners and rebels against the *Talmidei Chachamim*, for even they receive their vitality from the *Talmid Chacham*, from the aspect of "back" at least [59])—to take them together with him to the Land of Israel to the complete and true Redemption.

**K.** Knowledge of this matter—that the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation remains outside the Land in order to take each and every one of us to the Redemption—adds to the recognition of the value and importance of the *avodah* of each and every one of us:

Sometimes the *Yetzer Hara* comes to a person and argues: What does it matter to Hashem [60] if you behave in this way or that way?! For the verse explicitly states [61], "If you are righteous, what do you give Him, and if your transgressions are many, what do you do to Him, etc."! We find indeed that the *avodah* of created beings effects pleasure above, but this matter—the *Yetzer Hara* argues—is said only regarding *perfect Tzaddikim*, who have no connection to physicality, etc., and on account of the greatness of their level, their *avodah* effects pleasure above; but

#### 151

you—the *Yetzer Hara* argues—who are in a lowly state, etc., who are you that your *avodah* should matter above?!... Regarding you it is said, "If you are righteous, what do you give Him"!...

To this, one must answer him: How can you—the *Yetzer Hara*—confuse me! I myself was present at the standing at Mount Sinai, and to me Hashem said, "I am Hashem your G-d, etc." [62], in the singular! Moshe Rabbeinu, and likewise the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation—are waiting for me, and without me the train will not depart... And since that is so, then surely my *avodah* matters above.

**L.** And it should be noted, that although these things (regarding the importance of his *avodah*) have in them a feeling of pride, and pride is the root of all undesirable matters [63]—nevertheless, one must utilize this matter itself in order to bring benefit in *avodah*.

By way of introduction—regarding the matter of pride, we find a contradiction (seemingly) in the words of our Sages: on the one hand—"He is under a ban who has in him arrogance, even a little bit" [64], "neither of it nor of a part of it" [65], meaning, that the conduct in this cannot be in the way of moderation (as in all matters of character traits where the good way is the middle path [66]), but one must distance himself from it "to the furthest extreme" [67]; and on the other hand—"A *Talmid Chacham* must have one-eighth of an eighth" [65].

And among the resolutions to this [68]—is that when one is in the middle of *avodah*, at a higher level, then one must negate the matter of pride entirely, "neither of it nor of a part of it," not so *at the beginning of the avodah* one must have "an eighth of an eighth," "for if he will not be in a state of self-elevation at all, *his heart will not dare to approach the *avodah*, saying *who am I and what is my *avodah*" [69].

Thus, for the sake of *avodah*, one utilizes even an undesirable matter, like the matter of pride, to know the value and importance of his *avodah* which matters above, so that through this his *avodah* will be as it should.

The point of the matter—that even an undesirable thing can and must be utilized for benefit in holiness, and all the more so from the fact that from a matter of holiness can come a thing

#### 152

undesirable, Heaven forbid, like the formation of harsh *gevuros* from holy *gevuros*, as our Sages said [70], "From the sweat of the *Chayos*, a river of fire issues, etc.," and similarly in the *avodah* of man, anger at the wicked after the enthusiasm in prayer [71], and likewise in the line of *Chesed* [72], that from the love of Hashem one can fall into strange desires, Heaven forbid, and all the more so that an undesirable matter can bring benefit in holiness.

**M.** And it should be added that this is a fundamental matter in the general *avodah*:

"*Avodah*"—is from the language of tanning hides [73], that the hides in themselves are in a state and situation that requires tanning and fixing, and moreover, the action of tanning and fixing is *contrary* to the nature of the hides in themselves ("*zei lozen zich nit*"), but this state itself is *for the good*—since only in such a state is the general matter of *avodah* relevant.

And likewise regarding the general existence and strength of the *Klipah*—that this matter itself is in order to bring benefit in *avodah*, for the strength of the *Klipah* arouses and brings about a greater overcoming in the general *avodah*.

It may be said that this matter is hinted at in the language of our Sages [74] (regarding the beautiful woman that "the *Yetzer Hara* incites him") "The Torah spoke only against the *Yetzer Hara*"—that the need for "the Torah spoke" is specifically at a time when there is a fear of the incitement of the *Yetzer Hara* (when the *Yetzer Hara* is at its strength), and then "the Torah spoke *against* the *Yetzer Hara*"—not to concede to him, but on the contrary, *to fight against him* [75]. Thus, the incitement of the *Yetzer Hara* itself is for the sake of the war against him, which is the content of the matter of "And you shall take captive its captives" [76].

**N.** From this it is also understood regarding all the concealments and hiddenness in the world—that one must know that the intention in this itself is for the sake of the *avodah*.

By way of introduction—that according to what is understood *by our own intellect*, there should not have been so many concealments and hiddenness, for if not for the concealments and hiddenness, one could have completed the Divine intention much better than in a situation where there is a multitude of concealments and hiddenness. And all the more so if there were no concealments and hiddenness at all, and one would see *Elokus* in revelation—that then the matter of pleasure would not be in matters

#### 153

spiritual and matters of holiness alone [similar to the story [77] about the *Tzaddik* R. Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl who was fat in his body because of the greatness of the pleasure in saying *Amen, Yehei Shmei Rabba*]—then surely the *avodah* would be in a loftier manner.

However, since in practice the conduct is—not as it is accepted by our intellect, but in another manner—as it was determined *from above*,

—to what can this be compared? To a ship traveling in the sea [as explained in *Likkutei Torah* [78] that the matters of *Torah* and *Mitzvos* are compared to ships in which and through which one passes in the sea, and it is also known that in the time of exile, the Jewish people are compared to a woman whose husband went to a distant land [79]], that the order of things is that on the upper deck the sailors walk in white clothes, and hold feasts, etc., and below in the belly of the ship is a man wearing the simplest clothes (not even regular clothes, and certainly not white clothes), and his role is to operate the machines that move the ship and to supervise them so that they perform their function properly [80]. And although the action of the ship's movement is done through the *avodah* of the *mechanic*, nevertheless, the *sailors* steer the ship (to this side or that side) *according to their opinion*, without taking into account the opinion of the mechanic. And similarly in the subject, that although the *avodah* in practice to complete the Divine intention in the creation of the world is done *by us* specifically, nevertheless, our opinion is not taken into account regarding the conduct of the world, which is determined *from above*—

That not only are there no concealments and hiddenness at all, but on the contrary, there is a multitude of concealments and hiddenness—then one must know that the intention in this itself is *for the sake of the avodah*, that in a state and situation of a multitude of concealments and hiddenness (not only is there no weakening in the *avodah* of Hashem, but on the contrary) a greater overcoming is effected in the *avodah* of Hashem.

**O.** The point of the matter—that when a Jew sees a certain thing in the world, he must know that there is a Divine intention in it, and the intention is to utilize this thing in the *avodah* of Hashem [81].

Similar to the story [82] about the *Tzaddik* R. Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl who was once served (by mistake) non-Jewish milk, and he did not see it, and afterwards he explained this according to

#### 154

the statement of the *Mishnah* [83] "Milk that a non-Jew milked and a Jew does not see it, etc.," that the meaning of this is, that "milk that a non-Jew milked," then "a Jew does not see it," *a Jew does not see this*, for what he does not need to see, he does not see.

The explanation for this—is that the seeing of the thing is in order to elevate it to holiness, and consequently, a forbidden thing, for example, which cannot be elevated, a Jew does not see.

And since that is so, then regarding all the matters that a Jew *does* see in the world—he must fulfill the Divine intention—to utilize every single matter in the *avodah* of Hashem.

**P.** From this it is also understood regarding every place where a Jew is found, even when he is in a remote corner that has only a few Jews, he must know that the Divine intention brought him to this place [84] in order to act in strengthening Judaism, to bring these Jews closer to Judaism.

Someone might argue that in such a situation, when a few Jews are among non-Jews, one can be lenient, Heaven forbid, in the observance of *Torah* and *Mitzvos*, for this situation—he argues—is similar to a situation of war where it is permitted to eat even pig's trotters [85]!...

First of all, one must know that non-Jews are not the masters over Jews! They may have ownership regarding physical matters only, but not regarding spiritual matters!

And as the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, before his departure to his city of refuge, Kostroma [86]: "Only our bodies were given into exile and the subjugation of kingdoms, but our souls were not handed over to exile and the subjugation of kingdoms... everything that concerns our religion... there is no one who can force his opinion upon us, etc."

—In our town (Yekaterinoslav) lived a Jew, a refugee from Poland. This Jew received a draft notice for the army, and a few days after he reported to the army I saw him again in the *Beis Medrash*. When I asked him how he was released from the army, he told me that since he did not know Russian, they ordered him to say everything they told him. "I am a Jew who does not know wisdom," he continued to tell me, "so I did as they ordered me: when the commander said '*Na prava*' (go right), I repeated and said '*Na prava*'; when he said '*Na leva*' (go left), I repeated and said '*Na leva*'. Seeing this, he said to me: '*Ti durak*' (you are a fool), I also repeated and said '*Ti durak*'..." When the commander heard

#### 155

this, he became full of anger, gave me a blow with his rifle, and shouted: "*Pashol durak*" (get out of here, fool), I repeated and said "*Pashol durak*", and I ran away...

Over the soul of a Jew—no one in the world has ownership, not the "Draft Board," not General Hirsch, and not even President Truman!—their honor is in its place, but they have no ownership over the soul of a Jew to bring him to a place where there is difficulty in the observance of *Torah* and *Mitzvos*.

And since that is so, then even when he is in a place that has only a few Jews in an environment of non-Jews, not only do they not have ownership to cause weakening, Heaven forbid, in spiritual matters, so that even in such a situation he can observe and fulfill (to a certain degree) all matters of Judaism, *Torah* and *Mitzvos*, but more than that, he must know that Divine Providence brought him to this place in order to act in strengthening Judaism.

*

**Q.** Following what was said above—until now we spoke in a hidden and unclear manner ("*m'hot geredt oif a farshteltn oifen*"), and now we must add and speak openly ("*m'darf redn ofn*"):

When a Jew arrives and is in a certain place, he must know that Divine Providence brought him to this place in order to act in strengthening Judaism, to create a connection with the Jews found in this place, and to bring them closer to Judaism.

(The Rebbe turned to one of those sitting [87] and said to him:) Since two ships arrived here with Jews, you must know that the two ships were handed over to your responsibility, so that you will endeavor to create a connection with these Jews, to speak with them about matters of Judaism, and to bring them closer to Judaism! (And he added:) If you are embarrassed—say the things *in my name*: tell them that there is one Jew whose name is... (The Rebbe said his holy name), who does not speak fluent English, and speaks with a very heavy accent ("*mit a moradign akcent*"), so that his words are understood only half or a quarter, and speaks things that are not appropriate to what is accepted in America... you can speak in my name, and the things will have their effect.

One must speak with Jews about matters of Judaism, putting on *Tefillin*, observing *Shabbos*, and the like, and not be affected by the fact that there is someone who does not want to hear

#### 156

his words, or even mocks him—as the ruling in the first law in the *Shulchan Aruch* (in the glosses of the Rema, who brings from the words of the Tur): "He should not be embarrassed before people who mock him"!

The truth is that even one who mocks and does not want to hear—his soul hears the things being said [and all the more so from the known instruction [88] regarding the speaking of *Chassidus*, that even one who does not understand deep intellectual matters, there is a benefit in that his soul hears the things, and all the more so when speaking simple things regarding the observance of *Torah* and *Mitzvos*, surely his soul hears], and on the contrary: the very fact that he mocks proves that the things touched him ("*es hot im ongerirt*"), only that for the time being his reaction is in a manner of mockery, and surely in the end the things will have their effect ("*es vet im dernemen*").—One must therefore endeavor not to be affected by the mockers, and to fulfill the mission of strengthening and spreading Judaism.

**R.** One must remember the *mesiras nefesh* for the strengthening of Judaism that was in Russia!

In that [89] period, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, called ten of the Chassidim, and made a *covenant* with them for the *avodah* of spreading *Torah* and strengthening Judaism, without being affected by anything, to the point of *actual mesiras nefesh*!

—There are some of those ten Chassidim here, and therefore I do not mention names, for even without mentioning names, a feeling of *yeshus* (selfhood) has already been created in them...

When [90] the Rebbe at the time made a covenant for the spreading of *Torah* and the strengthening of Judaism, it was in a manner connected and touching the aspect of the *Yechidah* in the soul—both regarding the *Yechidah* of the Rebbe, and regarding the *Yechidah* of those with whom the Rebbe made the covenant (even if they themselves did not know it). And since the aspect of *Yechidah* is above limitations, then the covenant that is from the aspect of *Yechidah* is in a manner that has no limitations, and consequently, the covenant

## 161

At the beginning of the weekly parsha, it is stated: "When you kindle the lamps, the seven lamps shall give light toward the face of the Menorah." 

The significance of this in avodah is that one must kindle and illuminate the souls of Yisrael ("The candle of Hashem is the soul of man") with the light of Torah and mitzvos ("For a mitzvah is a candle, and Torah is light").
