The verse emphasizes: (a) "*Beha'alosecha* (when you kindle) the lamps," which implies "until the flame rises by itself" —that the kindling of the souls of Yisrael must be done in such a way that they burn and shine *by themselves*; (b) "Toward the *face* of the Menorah shall they give light," which relates to the word *pnimiyus* (inwardness) —that they should shine with the light of the *pnimiyus* of Torah, the teachings of Chassidus.

This is the task of a shaliach: to kindle and illuminate the Jews in every place he travels and visits, until they, too, shine on their own with the light of the teachings of Chassidus.

*

Regarding the anash who are in the places you are currently traveling to and visiting—Canada, Paris, London, and Manchester—convey my greetings to them.

Tell them that the work remaining to be completed is merely a matter of "small vessels". However, because of the intensification of the darkness, we require—and therefore have been given—the greatest lights, which is the light of the teachings of Chassidus, beginning with the general Chassidus revealed by the Baal Shem Tov, and specifically the Chassidus of Chabad revealed by the Alter Rebbe and our Rebbes who followed him.

— "The Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures", and "He only asks [of them]

## 162

according to their capacity". The same applies to the Tzaddikim (who "are like their Creator"), our Rebbes, who demand and require of us according to our capacities. And since they demand and require it of us, they have certainly given us the strength necessary to accomplish it.

For this reason, there must be hiskashrus to our Rebbes—to the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, etc. (The Rebbe paused in tears, and then continued) up to the Rebbe, my father-in-law.

*

It is worthwhile and proper to conduct a Chassidishe farbrengen, with love, unity, and joy, for through a farbrengen one can accomplish much more than the efforts of an individual sitting alone and learning from a book.

One should arouse—at the farbrengen—the need for self-agitation and movement ("der eigener treissel un hazazah"), and emphasize that for this, one does not need a three-day fast... rather, one can achieve this by reciting a kapitl of Tehillim properly, by studying a verse of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary, by studying a few lines of Tanya, or a bit of Chassidus ("a shtikel Chassidus") properly.

— The farbrengen can take place at different times ("vi amol"): sometimes before this, sometimes after, and sometimes in the middle.

The main thing is that everyone should strive in this once, twice, and three times; and if it has not yet helped, one should not be discouraged, but do it a fourth time. If there is an interruption, one should resume and continue, and then he will suddenly realize ("mitamol vet er zich chappen") that he is standing in a place of light.

*

To succeed in all of this, one must find the appropriate letters ("pasike osiyos") regarding everything mentioned above.

— The Rebbe (Rashab) said in the name of his father, the Rebbe Maharash, that the letters are drawn from the *yechidah* in the soul [The Rebbe Maharash said this regarding the delivery of Chassidus by a Rebbe: "The *yechidah* in the soul draws letters for him"].

Likewise, one must be authoritative ("hobn in zich a tokifus")—

## 163

so as not to be affected by all the concealments and hiddenness, and certainly not to be affected by trivial matters.

It is also worthwhile that you endeavor to write good news from every place you visit, especially since the desire to report good news will encourage and hasten the finding of additional opportunities to act in the aforementioned matters, and much more.

*

(Afterward, he said:)

Travel in peace ("fart gezunterheit"), and may we hear good news from you.

Travel in peace, kindle and illuminate the souls of the children of Yisrael, and—thereby—hasten the Geulah.

## B's"D. Shabbos Parshas Shelach, Mevarchim HaChodesh Tammuz, 5711

#### 164

(An unedited transcript)

**"Send** for yourself men, that they may scout the land of Canaan..."[1] Rashi explains: "For yourself—according to your own judgment. I am not commanding you; if you wish, send." Now, from the fact that Moshe sent spies (as it is written, "And Moshe sent them to scout..."), it is evident that it was his opinion that it was necessary to send spies. And although it is stated in the verse, "And you all approached me and said, 'Let us send men... and the matter was good in my eyes,'" and our Sages said[4] that this is like a person who says to his friend, "Sell me [this item]..."—once he saw that he did not hold him back at all, the buyer thought to himself, "He is confident that I will find no blemish in it; he immediately told me, 'Take your money, I am not testing it.'" So too, "I agreed to your words, thinking perhaps you would retract when you see that I am not holding you back, and you did not retract." This implies that Moshe agreed to send the spies so that Bnei Yisrael would see that he was not holding them back and would retract (and since they did not retract, he had no choice, etc.). Nevertheless, since Hashem left the sending of the spies to Moshe’s judgment, by saying "Send for yourself—according to your own judgment," it is understood that if it had not been Moshe’s opinion that it was necessary to send spies, he could not have sent them. Since he did send them, it must be that it was his opinion that it was necessary to send them. This matter is a very great wonder: why was it in Moshe’s opinion to send spies?

For it is stated in the Gemara, Maseches Berachos,[5] regarding the verse,[6] "Until Your people pass over, Hashem, until this people You have acquired passes over"—"Until Your people pass over, Hashem" refers to the first entry (when they came in the days of Yehoshua); "until this people You have acquired passes over" refers to the second entry (when they ascended from the Babylonian exile in the days of Ezra). From here the Sages said: "Yisrael were worthy that a miracle be performed for them in the days of Ezra just as it was performed for them in the days of Yehoshua..." Rashi explains: "A miracle be performed for them to enter with a high hand," meaning that the entry of Yehoshua was through a great miracle and with a high hand. From this it is understood *a fortiori* that if the entry into the land had been through Moshe [for the incident of the spies was in the second year after their departure from Mitzrayim, meaning before the sin of Mei Merivah, at which time they would have entered the land through Moshe], it would certainly have been with a great miracle and with a high hand, for the entry into the land through Yehoshua was through

#### 165

an angel, as our Sages said[7] regarding the verse,[8] "Now I have come," but not in the days of Moshe your teacher, since Moshe did not agree to an angel, but said,[9] "If Your Presence does not go, do not take us up from here." If so, if the entry of Yehoshua, which was through an angel, was with a great miracle and with a high hand, then certainly the entry through Moshe (not through an angel) would have been with a great miracle and with a high hand. Based on this, it is not understood why it was in Moshe’s opinion to send spies; for when the entry into the land is through a great miracle, there is no difference whether "it is strong or weak," "whether in open cities or in fortresses,"[10] and the like.

b) **This will be understood** by first explaining the general concept of the entry into the land, through which the need for sending the spies will also be understood. The innovation of the entry into the land is that then the essential matter of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* (practical mitzvos) began.[11] For although even while they were in the desert their conduct was according to Torah, nevertheless, the fulfillment of the mitzvos then was only temporary, and only a small fraction of the whole; the essential matter of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* was innovated when they entered the land. Like the thirty-nine labors of Shabbos, where the Tanna lists the order of bread,[12] "plowing, sowing, reaping," etc.—all of this was not applicable while they were in the desert, for they ate bread from heaven,[13] and this matter was innovated only upon their arrival in the land, at which time the essential matter of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* was innovated.

**To understand** the virtue of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* that was innovated upon entering the land, one must preface what is explained in *Likutei Torah*[14] that the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* is divided into two types: *Livyasan* and *Shor HaBar*. *Tzaddikim* who are in the category of *Livyasan*, which is a term of connection (*chibur*), as in "This time my husband will be joined (*yileveh*) to me,"[15] their essential *avodah* (in fulfilling the mitzvos) is to unify supernal unifications, which is a spiritual *avodah*. This is also why *Livyasan* in its literal sense is a fish, "the fish of the sea," which is the concept of the *neshamos* of the *alma d'is-kasiya* (the hidden world),[16] similar to the creatures in the sea that are not separated from their root and source; therefore, their *avodah* below is a spiritual *avodah* to unify supernal unifications. It is stated in *Likutei Torah* there as an example of this, Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai when he was in the cave for thirteen years,[17] that certainly he could not fulfill many *mitzvos maasiyos*. And although according to the law he was exempt from these mitzvos, because he was under duress due to danger to

#### 166

life, and "the Torah exempts one under duress,"[18] nevertheless, it is impossible to say that the matter which is effected through the fulfillment of the mitzvos was lacking in him. It must be that he drew down the *hemshechos* (drawings) through spiritual *avodah* in supernal unifications. And *Likutei Torah* continues: "And likewise the Arizal was also in this category." And in the gloss of the Tzemach Tzedek:[19] "And likewise the Baal Shem Tov." The concept of *Shor HaBar* is the *tzaddikim* whose *avodah* is in physicality, in the fulfillment of *mitzvos maasiyos*. It is explained in *Likutei Torah* there[20] that although the *tzaddikim* who are in the category of *Shor HaBar* need the elevation that is effected by the *tzaddikim* who are in the category of *Livyasan*, nevertheless, there is an extra virtue also in the *avodah* of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* in physicality specifically, the category of *Shor HaBar*. It is analogous to what is written,[21] "And much produce is by the strength of the ox (*shor*)," meaning that there is an advantage in the *neshamos* that are called "the beast of the earth," that their strength is greater and more powerful, as is stated regarding the *chayos* of the *Merkavah*:[22] "And the *chayos* carry the throne," for their strength is immense to be the ones carrying the throne, and through this[23] they are also carried, etc.[22] It is analogous to what is explained[24] in the interpretation of the verse,[25] "For not by bread alone does man live, but by everything that comes from the mouth of Hashem does man live," which refers to the "mouth of Hashem" that is within the bread,[26] meaning the Divine vitality within the bread. Seemingly, it is not understood: why does man need the "mouth of Hashem" that is in the bread? After all, there is the "mouth of Hashem" that is in man himself! It is explained regarding this that the "mouth of Hashem" (the Divine vitality) that is in the bread has a root that is higher than the Divine vitality in man, for since it fell lower, it is understood from this that its root is higher above, for everything that is higher descends lower,[27] and therefore specifically the "mouth of Hashem" that is in the bread effects the connection of the *neshamah* to the body. From all this is understood the virtue of the *avodah* of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* in physical things specifically; therefore, even the *tzaddikim* who are in the category of *Livyasan* must fulfill the mitzvos in physical things specifically [and only when there is a special instruction from above, like with Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai who was under duress and could not fulfill the mitzvos in physicality, this is an instruction from above that his *avodah* is a spiritual *avodah* of supernal unifications], for this is due to the virtue of the *avodah* of the category of *Shor HaBar* specifically.

**Based on this,** the virtue of the *avodah* in the entry of Bnei Yisrael into the land relative to their *avodah* while they were in the desert will also be understood. For while they were in the desert, they had bread from heaven, and water

#### 167

from the well of Miriam (which would roll and come with them[28]), and also the garments, which are a separate thing, were cleaned and pressed by the Clouds of Glory, and furthermore, the garments would grow with them,[29] meaning that the growth in the *neshamah* which brought about growth in the body caused, in a natural way, growth also in the garments; for although in themselves they are a separate thing, nevertheless, they would grow with them. And since while they were in the desert they did not need to engage in physical things, therefore their *avodah* was only in the category of thought[30] or speech,[31] as is also hinted at in the concept of the desert (*midbar*), which is also from the word for speech (*dibur*), as it is written,[32] "And your speech (*midbarech*) is comely," which is the mitzvah of Torah study, whose essence is in the mouth, as our Sages said[33] regarding the verse,[34] "They are life to those who find them (*lemotze'eihem*)"—to those who bring them out (*le-motzi'eihem*) with the mouth. But upon their entry into the land, the matter of fulfilling *mitzvos maasiyos* in physicality specifically was innovated, which is a higher concept.

c) **However,** in order that the *avodah* of fulfilling mitzvos in physicality specifically could exist, through which one reaches higher as mentioned above, there needed to be a giving of strength from above specifically. That is, in addition to the giving of strength regarding which our Sages said,[35] "If not for Hashem helping him..."—which is the giving of strength after the matter of *avodah* already exists, at which time one needs assistance from above to overcome the concealments and hiddenness—there is more than this: even at the beginning of the *avodah*, in order that the general matter of *avodah* in physicality can exist, there is a need for a giving of strength from above, and after this comes the *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below) [which brings about] an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above), and through this one reaches the highest level.

**Prefacing** that these three matters in the general *avodah*—the giving of strength from above for the *avodah* of fulfilling mitzvos in physicality, the *avodah* itself, and the drawing down of the *is'arusa d'le'eila* which comes through the *is'arusa d'lesata*—we find also in the matter of Torah, for since "the Holy One, Blessed be He, looked into the Torah and created the world,"[36] it is understood that all matters exist first in the Torah. The matter of this is, as is known, that there are three levels in Torah: inheritance, toil, and gift.[37] For it is written,[38] "Torah that Moshe commanded us is an inheritance for the congregation of Yaakov," meaning

#### 168

that the Torah is in the category of inheritance. And we also find that Torah study is through the toil of man specifically, as our Sages said,[39] "Prepare yourself to study Torah, for it is not an inheritance to you," except in a manner of toil specifically. And likewise we find that Torah is in the category of a gift, as the common expression "the giving of Torah," and likewise our Sages said[40] that Moshe would study Torah and forget it until it was given to him as a gift. The matter of this is that there is a matter in the Torah that is in the manner of an inheritance to every single one of Yisrael, who is a son of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. And this is also that "Yisrael" is an acronym for "there are sixty myriad letters to the Torah,"[41] that every single one of Yisrael has a letter in the Torah through which he receives his vitality.[42] And in addition to this, Torah study must be in a manner of toil specifically, meaning that these matters which one can grasp through toil, one cannot arrive at except through toil specifically. And higher than this is the concept of the gift that is in the Torah, which is what is given from above specifically, since it is impossible to arrive at this through *avodah*. And as explained above[43] regarding the matter of "Then I was with Him as an *amon*... and my delights were with the sons of man,"[44] that in the Torah below, the category of essential delights is drawn down—the delights of the King in His essence—which is "delights" specifically, referring to "Then I was with Him as an *amon*," as the Torah is in His essence, may He be blessed; this matter is in the category of a gift specifically. However, in order to arrive at the category of the gift that is in the Torah, there must first be the preface of the matter of toil, analogous to what our Sages said,[45] "If he had not made rest for himself, He would not have given him the gift," meaning that through the preface of toil in the levels that one can reach through toil, then they give afterwards the category of gift that is in the Torah. And with this, it will also be understood what our Sages said,[46] "Whoever sits and reviews Torah, the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and reviews opposite him," and likewise they said[47] "The day is twelve hours; the first three hours the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and engages in Torah." Seemingly, what is the matter of the Torah engagement of the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the first three hours specifically? After all, the Holy One, Blessed be He, always sits and reviews opposite the person who sits and reviews! But the matter is that the concept of "the Holy One, Blessed be He, sits and reviews opposite him" refers to the level of Torah that comes through toil, but the matter of the study in the first three hours refers to the category of the gift that is in the Torah, and this is the concept of the first three hours, which refers to the *Gimel Rishonos* (three firsts) of *Atik*, for this matter is drawn down in the category of a gift from above specifically.

#### 169

**And just as** there are these three matters in Torah, so too it is drawn down in a natural way also in the fulfillment of mitzvos. For the formula of the blessing of the mitzvos is "Blessed are You, Hashem our G-d, King of the world," and the Rebbe Rayatz explained[48] in the name of the Alter Rebbe, that *Elokeinu* (our G-d) is a term for strength (*koach*),[49] and "Hashem our G-d" means that Hashem is our strength and our vitality,[50] and this matter is the giving of strength for the fulfillment of the mitzvos,[51] whose matter is "Who has sanctified us with His mitzvos," meaning that one takes the physical thing and makes of it a thing of holiness. And this is the formula of the blessing of the mitzvos which must be "prior to their performance."[52] And afterwards is the body of the mitzvah, through which there comes an *is'arusa d'lesata* [which brings about] an *is'arusa d'le'eila*, until one reaches higher, which is what our Sages said,[53] "The reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah," that the most elevated matter in the mitzvah is the mitzvah itself, that a *tzavta* and connection[54] is made with the Commander of the mitzvos, the category of the "Owner of the Will."

**Based on this,** it will also be understood regarding the entry into the land, that in order that they could arrive at the elevation that is effected through the fulfillment of mitzvos in physicality specifically, for which the person performing needs to descend from his level and clothe himself in physical things, etc., there needed to be a giving of strength from above. And this is the matter of the sending of the spies, which is the giving of strength from above for the *avodah* in physicality in the entry into the land. And regarding this it is said, "Send for yourself men, that they may scout the land of Canaan"—*yaturu* (that they may scout) is also from the word *yisron* (advantage/virtue),[55] as it is written,[56] "And the advantage of the land in everything is...," which is the giving of strength from above so that there can be the advantage that is through the *avodah* in physicality specifically.

d) **Based on this,** it will also be understood what Moshe requested, "Let me pass over, I pray You, and see the land...,"[57] "see" specifically. Seemingly, the essence of his request was "Let me pass over," that he should pass over and be there, and what is it that he requested "and see" specifically? And especially according to our Sages,[58] "For what reason did Moshe Rabbeinu desire to enter Eretz Yisrael? Was it to eat of its fruit that he needed? Rather, that the mitzvos (that are in the land) should be fulfilled through him." If so, the essence of his request should have been that he enter the land and fulfill the mitzvos, and what is the precision of "and see," the matter of seeing specifically, for which he prayed 515 prayers, the numerical value of *Va'eschanan*?[59] But the matter is[60] that Moshe wanted to effect the giving of strength from above for the *avodah* in physicality through his seeing the land, to draw down the category of "seeing," which is the category of Moshe, as it is written,[61] "And He saw the first for him...," through which is the *bitul* of *Chochma*, as is stated regarding Moshe, "And what are we?"[62] And therefore, when he could not draw down the matter of "seeing" through his seeing the land, he then said,[63] "And now, Yisrael, listen," meaning that now there could be for them only the matter of listening alone, regarding which they said,[64] "Seeing is not like hearing," for even when a person hears a certain matter in all its details, it is specifically after he sees that thing that he will delight with great delight. And the reason for this is because in seeing there is a drawing down from the inwardness of the *nefesh* more than in hearing. And likewise, seeing effects self-nullification more than hearing; for although when one hears that there is a great king in a distant land to whom many noble and honored ministers are nullified, this causes him to be nullified to the king and fulfill his command, nevertheless, it is not at all like one who enters the king's courtyard and sees himself many noble and honored ministers nullified to him,[65] through which there is effected in him greater self-nullification. And this is what Moshe wanted to effect in Yisrael, that there should be in them the matter of "seeing."

e) **Based on this,** it will also be understood what is explained in *Likutei Torah*[66] regarding the difference between the spies that Moshe sent and the spies that Yehoshua sent, that Moshe sent the spies to scout the entire land of Canaan, whereas Yehoshua sent the spies to scout only Yericho. For Yericho is a term for *rei'ach* (scent/smell), which refers to the garments of the *nefesh*—thought, speech, and action—which are in the category of scent only. Meaning, the sending of the spies by Yehoshua was a giving of strength for the clarification of the garments only, whereas the spies that Moshe sent to scout the entire land of Canaan, the land of the seven nations, was the concept of the giving of strength for the clarification of the seven *midos* themselves, whose essence is love and fear. And as it is stated in *Likutei Torah* there in the gloss:[67]

#### 171

"And see in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 14," where it is explained that the level of the *beinoni* is the level of every person, and after it every person will be drawn. For the *avodah* of the *beinonim* is in thought, speech, and action,[68] meaning, it goes without saying that one is careful in action and speech, but that one is careful even in thought, knowing that "thoughts of transgression are harder than transgression,"[69] and this is the matter of the level of the *beinoni*, that he has never committed a transgression in his life and never will.[70] And this matter is the level of every person, and after it every person will be drawn, meaning that they demand this from every single one of Yisrael. And for this is the giving of strength of the sending of the spies by Yehoshua. However, the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* is in the category of the *midos*, love and fear, that every matter in holiness is most beloved, and a matter of *kelipah* is loathsome and hated in the extreme; this *avodah* is not applicable to everyone, but this is a concept that comes from above, as it is said,[71] "You have created *tzaddikim*," and it is a concept of a gift, as it is written,[72] "I give your priesthood as a service of gift." And for this is the giving of strength of the sending of the spies by Moshe.

**The matter of this** is that since Moshe was from the category of "seeing," and was in the category of self-nullification (as mentioned above), therefore it was in his power to send spies to the entire land of Canaan, meaning, to effect the clarification in the *midos* themselves, since from the perspective of "seeing," the matter of the opposite of holiness is not applicable. Just as in the time to come, when there will be the seeing of G-dliness, then the matter of the opposite of holiness will not be applicable at all (and only now is it said,[73] "I have set before you life and good, and death and evil... and you shall choose life," meaning that it is possible that the choice should be also in the opposite, G-d forbid, and nevertheless he chooses life). And this matter has an analogy also in the *avodah* of man now, as the Rebbe Rayatz brings in the name of *Sifrei Mussar*[74] regarding the matter of "Who is wise? He who sees the outcome,"[75] that when a person cannot overcome his desire, the advice is that he should picture for himself (see) what will be after the fulfillment of the desire (the outcome), that then nothing will remain of it, for since it is a physical thing that is finished and lost, nothing will remain of it, and then he will also be pained by this act; when he pictures this for himself, he will be able to overcome his desire. And as explained above in the explanation of Moshe’s request "Let me pass over, I pray You, and see" specifically, that he wanted to effect the matter of "seeing," through which the *avodah* in physicality could exist in the entry of Bnei Yisrael into the land.

#### 172

f) **And this is** "Send for yourself men, that they may scout the land of Canaan...," that the sending of the spies is the concept of the giving of strength so that the *avodah* in physical things can exist. And this giving of strength is through Moshe, which is what is written "Send for yourself—according to your own judgment," for, although the spies in themselves were righteous,[76] their *avodah* was only in spirituality, whereas the giving of strength for *avodah* in physicality is drawn down through Moshe specifically, because with Moshe there was the matter of "seeing" and self-nullification,[77] as explained[78] also regarding the matter of "six hundred thousand footmen of the people in whose midst I am,"[79] that although they were in the category of "feet," through them specifically is drawn down the category of "in whose midst I am," which indicates his *bitul*, and from this he felt (*er hot derhert*) the virtue of the *avodah* in physicality in the entry into the land, and he effected in it a giving of strength. However, the spies did not have in them this category of *bitul*, and therefore they did not feel the virtue of the *avodah* in physicality, but said "the land is one that consumes its inhabitants,"[80] that through *avodah* in physicality, not only will they not elevate the physical, but on the contrary, etc. And this is what they said,[81] "Even the householder, as it were, cannot remove his vessels," for it is true that there are in physical things sparks higher than the breaking of the vessels, nevertheless, their argument was that from the perspective of the greatness of the descent, the householder cannot remove his vessels, meaning, that despite being the householder, he cannot remove his vessels. However, Yehoshua and Kalev, who had in them the category of *bitul* to Moshe, said, "Their protection has departed from them, and Hashem is with us; do not fear them,"[82] that the householder *can* remove his vessels, for "householder" refers to the G-dliness that is associated with the worlds, and He can remove His vessels, meaning to elevate the physicality. And therefore they said, "The land is very, very good,"[83] two times "very"; the first "very" is your "very," and the second "very" is the "very" of above. And all this comes from the perspective of their *bitul* to Moshe. And this is also what is written,[84] "And Kalev silenced (*vayahas*) the people," and *vayahas* is a matter of *bitul*, since through *bitul* specifically is drawn down the giving of strength for the entry into the land. And this is that also regarding the spies of Yehoshua it is said,[85] "And Yehoshua sent... spies secretly (*cheresh*)," for *cheresh* is a term for silence,[86] like a deaf person (*cheresh*) who does not hear and does not speak,[87] which is the concept of *bitul* in the extreme, meaning that also with Yehoshua there was the matter of self-nullification, at least

#### 173

in matters of thought, speech, and action, and all this is because the giving of strength for the entry into the land depends on the self-nullification of Moshe, for which reason it is said "Send for yourself—according to your own judgment." And so it is also in the future redemption, that through the *bitul* to Moshe, the "extension of Moshe in every generation,"[88] and in our generation this is the Rebbe Rayatz, who is the shepherd of our generation, the entry into the land will be in simplicity, and it will be felt that "the land is very, very good."

## B's"d. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Shelach, Mevarchim HaChodesh Tammuz, 5711

#### 174

(Unedited)

**A.** This farbrengen is the first farbrengen after Mattan Torah—after which the second Luchos were also given—following the events that transpired in the interim, including the sin of the Meraglim (which is in our parsha). As is known, were it not for the sin of the Meraglim, the entry into Eretz Yisrael would have been accomplished by Moshe in a manner of complete Geulah. However, because of the sin of the Meraglim, the entry into Eretz Yisrael was accomplished by Yehoshua[1](#_ftn989), and it was not a complete Geulah.

We must understand the matter of the Meraglim, as follows.

***

**B.** Maamar on the verse "Shelach lecha anashim, etc."

***

**C.** It was discussed above (in the maamar[2](#_ftn990)) that the sending of the Meraglim by Moshe is the power bestowed by Moshe Rabbeinu so that entry into Eretz Yisrael could be possible. For, the land in and of itself is an "eretz ocheles yoshveha" (a land that consumes its inhabitants)[3](#_ftn991); therefore, there is a need for a special power bestowed by Moshe Rabbeinu so that the entry into the land will be in the appropriate manner[4](#_ftn992).

It must be added that this matter is relevant to our days as well:

By way of introduction—even though the entry into the land already occurred in the past, nevertheless, after the Churban and the Galus, we are in a standing and state *before* the entry into the land in a manner of permanence and eternity, in the future Geulah.

Since this is so, we must know that it is impossible to ascend to Eretz Yisrael without the power bestowed by the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, because the land in and of itself is an "eretz ocheles yoshveha"[5](#_ftn993).

#### 175

One can make "calculations" regarding the greatness of the merit of ascending to Eretz Yisrael, to the extent that "anyone who walks four amos in Eretz Yisrael is guaranteed to be a ben Olam Haba"[6](#_ftn994). And all the more so if he also "speaks Lashon HaKodesh"[7](#_ftn995), surely his merit is even greater ("there is no comparison at all"...). But, one must know that the standing and state today is such that it is an "eretz ocheles yoshveha," and consequently, one should not ascend there without the power bestowed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation.

Those whom my father-in-law, the Rebbe, sent to Eretz Yisrael—they possess the power bestowed by the Moshe Rabbeinu of our generation so that their entry into the land will be in the appropriate manner.

**D.** There are those who think that there is no need to ask the Rebbe about every matter.

He has—he argues—the Shulchan Aruch, and he also has a brain in his head ("he has a good head, may no evil eye harm him"...), and consequently, he can himself—Baruch Hashem—clarify ("durchton") every matter to its truth, and he does not need to ask the Rebbe.

Regarding such a person, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, once used the expression[8](#_ftn996) "sam sapozhnik" (he himself is a cobbler):

There is a story about a gentile into whose house a Yid entered and saw there... Tefillin, and he decided immediately to buy them from him. When he asked the gentile—with excitement—where did you get these from? The gentile replied—not knowing if the Yid’s intention was to buy them, or if his main intention was to clarify from where he had stolen them—"*Ya sam sapozhnik*," meaning, I myself am a cobbler, and I sewed them myself!...

It goes without saying—concluded my father-in-law, the Rebbe—how can a gentile be involved in the making of Tefillin!

And the parallel in the analogy—is he who thinks that he, too, can clarify every matter by himself, and does not need to ask the Rebbe[9](#_ftn997).

## 176

In his letter[1](#_ftn998) for the first celebration of Yud-Beis and Yud-Gimmel Tammuz—in the year 5688—the Rebbe Rayatz explained the significance of this redemption, stating that "Hashem did not redeem me alone on Yud-Beis Tammuz, but also all those who cherish our holy Torah, those who observe the mitzvos, and even those who are merely called by the name of Yisrael."

This encompasses all types of Jewish men and women: those who possess both Torah and mitzvos, those who possess either Torah or mitzvos, and those who possess neither Torah nor mitzvos, but are simply "called by the name of Yisrael."

As is known, a *kinuy* (appellation) is a term or name that obscures and covers the essence of the person being called by this name, to the extent that it might not be their actual name, nor an abbreviation of their name, nor an interpretation of their name, nor even in the language in which they are named, and not even a description of the person themselves, but rather a name used only because of their family lineage[2](#_ftn999).

Yet, despite all this, they are at least called by the name *Yisrael*[3](#_ftn1000), because, in the language of the aforementioned letter, "every person of Yisrael (regardless of their personal state regarding the observance and fulfillment of the mitzvos) has a heart that is whole with Hashem and His Torah."

And to *all* these categories, a redemption was drawn down on this day in that year (the year 5687), and this influence is reawakened every single year at this time.

## 177

Redemption means an exit from the *meitzar* (constriction)—the measurement and limitation of material and physical matters, and of the body and the *nefesh habehamis*.

However, we must prepare ourselves to be a *keli* (vessel) to receive this influence, to absorb it internally, and consequently—to bring it into practice, in thought, speech, and action, in the days that follow this *chag hageulah*.

And then, the redemption will be ours, for all of the Jewish people, the complete and true redemption, speedily in our days, Amen.

**Menachem Schneerson**

*Motzaei Shabbos, Gimmel Tammuz, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## B"H. The text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send to Anash, may they live, throughout the world, in anticipation of 12-13 Tammuz, 5711

#### 178

To be conveyed to all Anash: L’chaim, l’chaim and for a blessing, and for an awakening toward success in strengthening Yiddishkeit and disseminating the revealed Torah and Chassidus.

**Menachem** **Schneerson**

## 13 Tammuz, 5711

#### 179

(Unedited transcript)

**"You have given those who fear You a banner to be raised for the sake of truth, Selah."** In the maamar (which he sent to the country of Russia and which has just now been printed), the Rebbe Rayatz brings the interpretation of the Targum: "You have given to those who fear You a test to be tested by," etc. He explains that this refers to the avodah of mesiras nefesh in matters of *nisyonos* (tests) specifically—which are given to Bnei Yisrael in order to effectuate through them an elevation. In this, this final galus differs from the previous ones, in that it contains a greater abundance of concealments and hiddenness, and a greater abundance of *nisyonos*.

In truth, this itself is an indication of the strength and power given from Above to each and every person, so that they can withstand the test. This is the advantage of the strength and power given in this final galus over the galus of Mitzrayim (which was the root of all the galuyos). For regarding the galus of Mitzrayim, it is written: "But they did not listen... because of shortness of breath and hard labor"—meaning that the avodah of *nisyonos* only confused them. In contrast, in this galus, the strength and power are given to recognize the truth: that they are merely *nisyonos* and nothing more.

He continues to explain that the *nisayon* consists of the fact that the Elokis spark is extremely hidden and concealed. The nature of a *nisayon* is not like other physical matters that are being clarified, where the clarification is through engaging with them, whereby the spark is clarified and included in Elokus. In contrast, in a *nisayon*, the mode of clarification is not through engaging with the object itself, but rather the person’s engagement with himself. The *nisayon* is not a thing in its own right; rather, a thing was set up to conceal and prevent. Therefore, the person’s entire engagement is with himself—to awaken the essential power within him, etc., until

#### 180

all obstacles and delays are nullified. (Thus far, the words of the Rebbe Rayatz at the beginning of the maamar, in brief). The core of the matter is that specifically in this final galus—the double and redoubled darkness of *ikvesa d’Meshicha*, which is the end of the concealment and hiddenness—Bnei Yisrael have been given the powers not to be affected by the *nisyonos*. This is achieved by awakening the essential power, which is both essential strength and *bitul atzmi* (self-nullification). (It can be said that this is the reason why the avodah of *nisyonos* specifically effects the greatest elevation and ascent). Automatically, the *nisayon* is nullified and becomes as if it never existed.

b) **The explanation** of this matter: In every avodah—both in the avodah of *birurim* (clarifications) and in the avodah of *nisyonos*—there are three elements: the object in which the avodah must take place; the Jewish person upon whom the avodah is incumbent; and the manner in which the avodah is performed with the object being clarified or the object in which the *nisayon* is clothed. In all three of these elements, there is a distinction between the avodah called "the avodah of *birurim*" and the avodah called "the avodah of *nisyonos*."

**The matter** of this is that the avodah of *birurim* is performed in a way that clarifies the spark that exists within the reality of the object being clarified itself. In contrast, in the avodah of *nisyonos*, the object itself in which the *nisayon* occurs has no reality (as mentioned above, that the *nisayon* is not a thing in its own right, but was only set up to conceal and prevent). Nevertheless, since there is a matter of *nisayon* here, it is necessary to say that there is a spark of holiness in it; for without a spark of holiness, there could not even be a reality that is merely a semblance to conceal and prevent. This is also understood from what is brought in the maamar regarding the matter of *nisayon*—what is said regarding the galus of Mitzrayim, "But they did not listen... because of shortness of breath and hard labor." For in the backbreaking labor that took place in Mitzrayim, there were many sparks of holiness clothed [within it] that were clarified and elevated at the time of the Exodus. As is known regarding the interpretation of the Sages on the verse "And they emptied out Mitzrayim"—that they made it like a trap that has no grain and like a deep sea that has no fish; meaning, they extracted all the sparks of holiness that were there. However, the spark of holiness in a *nisayon* is in a state of extreme concealment and hiddenness. This is also why the primary matter of *nisyonos*

#### 181

is in this final galus, in *ikvesa d’Meshicha*, because then we must clarify the smallest and final sparks, in which the concealment and hiddenness are the greatest. That is, the spark of holiness in the matter of *nisyonos* is clothed and swallowed up in such concealment and hiddenness that it does not shine at all. Therefore, it is impossible to call it by the name "light," and it even reaches the point where it is sometimes said that the spark of holiness itself becomes darkness, similar to the concept of "the piece of meat itself becomes *neveilah* (carrion)." This is the difference between the object being clarified and the object in which the *nisayon* occurs: in the object being clarified, there is a spark that can be called a "spark of light," since it is in the mode of light, etc. In contrast, in a *nisayon*, nothing remains of the spark except its mere reality, because all other aspects (besides its essential reality) are in the category of "the piece of meat becomes *neveilah*."

**Due to** the aforementioned difference between the object being clarified and the object in which the *nisayon* occurs, a difference also arises in the person performing the avodah and the manner of the avodah. In the matter of *nisyonos*, a person must work with his reality, his essence, and his being, and not with the other aspects that are merely his extensions (as with the spark of holiness in the object in which the *nisayon* occurs, where only its essential reality remains in its entirety). Furthermore, the mode of avodah is not through a path of war and debate, claim and counter-claim, until he effects clarification and elevation, but rather by awakening essential strength and *bitul atzmi* specifically.

c) **More specifically**, the beginning of the avodah of *birurim* is at the time of *tefillah*, as the saying goes: "The time of prayer is a time of battle." This means that although the general avodah of *birurim* is at the time of eating and drinking or utilizing all physical matters, nevertheless, in order that the physical object should not only fail to pull the person down, but on the contrary, that the person should be able to act upon it, clarify it, and elevate the spark clothed within it—he must first effect a general weakening, both in himself (in his body and animal soul) and in the physicality and materiality of the world. This is the matter of the avodah of *tefillah*, the "time of battle," which effects a general weakening in the body and animal soul. This is done through the *hisbonenus* (contemplation) before *tefillah*, and afterwards through the *hisbonenus* during *tefillah* itself, in the avodah of the *Ofanim* and *Chayos HaKodesh*, which are the root of the animal soul. Through this, he effects a general weakening in his body and animal soul, and automatically

#### 182

also in his portion of the world. This is the reason why before *tefillah* it is forbidden to eat or engage in one's needs, because before he has effected a general weakening in himself and in his portion of the world, there is room to fear that not only will he be unable to elevate the physical object, but on the contrary, the physical object will pull him down and draw him lower. Only after the avodah of *tefillah* does the order of avodah of *pas shachris* (breakfast) and all other matters connected with the avodah of *birurim* follow. For after he has effected a general weakening—which is the beginning of the war—he can go and continue in the second war, "Eat bread with salt," to engage in the clarification of physical matters.

Now, the beginning of the avodah of *birurim*, which is in the avodah of *tefillah* (as mentioned), is in the mode of *hisbonenus*, etc. The reason for this is that the sparks in the objects being clarified are in such a state that, aside from their essential reality, all other aspects remain in them as well, which are a matter of light and holiness, etc. Therefore, it is possible to wage war with them through a path of debate, claim and counter-claim, until he effects clarification and elevation in them. In contrast, in the avodah of *nisyonos*, since the spark of holiness in the *nisayon* is in such a state that "the piece of meat itself becomes *neveilah*"—where the spark itself becomes darkness, like the darkness of *Gah"T* (the three impure *kelipos*) entirely, to distinguish—then it is impossible to proceed in the path of war and debate, since he has no foothold at all with which to begin the war. Rather, the mode of avodah is through the awakening of essential strength and *bitul atzmi*, which is impossible otherwise, and he is compelled to withstand the *nisayon* because there is no other path before him. And since his avodah is from the side of essential strength and *bitul atzmi*—meaning, not from the side of matters of extension, illuminations, and revelations, or avodah according to *taam v’daas* (reason and intellect), but from the side of the essence—then from the side of the essence, it is within his ability to extract the spark clothed in the object of the *nisayon*, since even in the spark, the essence remains in its entirety, as mentioned above.

d) **This is also** why the avodah of *nisyonos* is connected with the level of *yechidah* in the soul, which has the power to transform the level of *yechidah* of the *sitra achra*, the level of *yechidah* of the animal soul. It is sometimes explained that when the level of *yechidah* in the soul shines, then it is not even in the mode of a *nisayon* at all. And the fact that there is nevertheless a *nisayon* is expressed by the fact that he must be awakened and come to the avodah that is from the side of the revelation of the *yechidah* in the soul. But after

#### 183

the level of *yechidah* in the soul is revealed, then the avodah is not even in the mode of a *nisayon* at all. The matter is that the levels of *nefesh, ruach,* and *neshamah*, which are the internal powers of the soul, are from the level of intellect and below. Above them is the matter of the *makif* (encompassing light) of *chayah* and the *makif* of *yechidah*; the *makif* of *chayah* is the matter of *ratzon* (will), and the *makif* of *yechidah* is the matter of *taanug* (delight). The matter of avodah in the path of war and debate is relevant only to avodah from the side of intellect and below. In contrast, in avodah from the side of *ratzon* and *taanug*, the matter of debate is not relevant, for by necessity, either one delights in this thing or one does not delight in it. This means that when the avodah is from the side of *yechidah* in the soul—the power of *taanug*—since it is simple to him that he delights in this matter, there is no room for claims, counter-claims, and debate in the path of war. And since the avodah is from the side of the *yechidah* of the Elokis soul, which transforms into holiness even the *yechidah* of the animal soul—meaning, it extracts the *taanug* of the animal soul from physical matters, and certainly from material matters—then all physical and material matters become completely equal to him, and through this, all matters of *nisyonos* are nullified. As our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, that the believer will not feel any suffering in the world, and in all matters of the world, "yes" and "no" are equal to him in true equality. This means that the reason a person is distressed and worried about a lack of children, life, and abundant sustenance is because these matters are not in a state of equality for him. But when he is in a standing and state where all matters of children, life, and abundant sustenance are in a state of equality for him—because what concerns him is only the matter of Torah and *mitzvos*, and from the perspective of Torah, "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good" —then all matters with which he is tested become equal to him, and automatically the *nisayon* is nullified. This is also the interpretation and explanation of what was stated above: that when the avodah is from the side of *yechidah* in the soul, it is not in the mode of a *nisayon* at all, because he has effected in himself that whatever happens will be in a state of complete equality for him.

e) **Now**, although it was stated above that the spark in a *nisayon* is in a state of complete concealment and hiddenness until nothing remains but its mere reality (which is the general difference between *nisyonos* and *birurim*, from which all specific differences come automatically), on the other hand, it is known that "everything that is highest of the high descends to the lowest of the low." Since this spark descended so low that nothing remains but its mere reality, it is understood that therein lies the highest of the high. By way of example, regarding what is explained as the reason

#### 184

that the matter of *mesiras nefesh* is in the final generations specifically: because in the first generations, matters of intellect were in a state of revelation, and intellect conceals *mesiras nefesh*, whereas in the final generations, etc. Just as it is easier to effect the matter of *mesiras nefesh* on the heel of the foot than on the head, so too it is easier to effect the matter of *mesiras nefesh* in *ikvesa d’Meshicha* than in the first generations, which were on higher levels. Similarly, it can be said regarding the spark in a *nisayon* that since nothing remains in it but its mere reality, therefore the highest of the high is found within it.

f) **With this**, we can understand what is written: "For Hashem your Elokim is testing you to know," etc. This means that in order for there to be a matter of *daas* (knowledge) and vision in Elokus ("to know"), which is the purpose of the coming of Mashiach, this is specifically through the matter of *nisyonos* ("For Hashem... is testing you"). The reason for this is that in the matter of *nisyonos*, the spark is in a state of extreme concealment and hiddenness, so it is impossible to effect the clarification in it through a path of war and debate, etc. Rather, the avodah must be in the mode of proceeding with essential strength and *bitul atzmi*, which is reached specifically through the revelation of the *yechidah* in the soul. And when the level of the *yechidah* of the Elokis soul is revealed, it transforms the *yechidah* of the animal soul, and automatically he effects in himself that all matters of children, life, and sustenance are in a path of complete equality, and through this, the *nisayon* is nullified (as mentioned above). Then the spark within it is revealed and returns to holiness, and furthermore, it is elevated to the highest level, for that which descended to the lowest of the low was specifically the highest of the high.

g) **This is also** the reason why specifically after the *nisyonos* in the double and redoubled darkness of this final galus (after which the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth"), in which we clarify the final sparks that are in the greatest concealment and hiddenness, then the prophecy will be fulfilled: "The earth will be full of the knowledge of Hashem." The promise of the Torah will be revealed: "For Hashem your Elokim is testing you to know"—meaning, the purpose of the *nisyonos* is so that the matter of *daas* in Elokus will be revealed: "Know the Elokim of your father." Therefore, the avodah of *nisyonos* has been given to us now—not in the manner that it was in the galus of Mitzrayim, which was only a matter of confusion, but as the Rebbe Rayatz explains in the maamar, that "in this galus, the strength and power are given to recognize the truth: that they are merely *nisyonos*," and in a way that they can withstand the *nisayon* through the awakening of essential

#### 185

power, essential strength and *bitul atzmi*, and withstand the *nisayon* in a way that they extract the sparks. Through this, they will merit to come to "know Hashem your Elokim." This means that the *nisayon* is not a matter in its own right, but everything that "Hashem your Elokim is testing you" is only "to know," to come to the standing and state of "the earth will be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

Therefore, when we withstand all the concealments and hiddenness, and we proceed in the path of avodah not to enter into debate in the path of war, but to approach every matter with essential strength and *bitul atzmi*—meaning, that it is true that I myself am not a reality at all, but since I am engaged in the avodah of Hashem, I am not affected by anything, and I know that it is impossible otherwise, *der inyan muz zich durchfihrn* (the matter must be carried out)—then we nullify the *nisayon*, and we clarify and elevate the spark that is hidden within it. Through this, we effect in the world the revelation that will soon, in our days, be in open reality through the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu. The preparation for this must be through the avodah of each and every one during the time of galus, and especially in the final galus, and in this galus itself, in the *ikvesa d’ikvesa d’Meshicha*. When each and every one does his avodah with essential strength and *bitul atzmi*, then soon we will all merit that in our immediate time, all the revelations and lights and the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof* will be revealed through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

## Sicha of 13 Tammuz, 5711

#### 186

**A.** Surely everyone is familiar with the story of the days of 12-13 Tammuz [1](#_ftn1034) — the days of the *geulah* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, from his imprisonment for his work in disseminating Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit.

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related [2](#_ftn1035) that initially he was sentenced to death, *rachmana litzlan* [3](#_ftn1036). Afterward, this sentence was commuted to ten years of exile in Siberia, then to five years of exile, and finally to three years of exile in the city of Kostroma.

On 3 Tammuz, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was released from prison and set out for his place of exile, Kostroma, where he remained for several days, until 12 Tammuz.

On 12 Tammuz — the birthday of the Rebbe, my father-in-law — when he arrived at the G.P.U. institution to report as required, the office was closed because it was their holiday. However, he was informed [4](#_ftn1037) that an order had arrived from the capital, Moscow, to release him. The following day, 13 Tammuz, they informed him at the office that the order for his release had arrived the previous day, and they gave him his certificate of freedom.

Being flustered by the release order, they wanted him to sign for the certificate in such a way that it would be evident that it was not their fault that the news of the release had been delayed for twenty-four hours.

Understandably, then, the *magnitude of the leap and jump* was immense — from a death sentence, *rachmana litzlan*, to a release (a complete one, and) with a high hand, to such an extent that they feared the authorities’ displeasure over the twenty-four-hour delay in notifying him of the release!

**B.** At that time, it was seen with physical eyes that the conduct with the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was *miraculous conduct*.

#### 187

The truth is that the conduct with the Rebbe is *always* miraculous conduct; however, there were times when it was not as evident to physical eyes.

From that time on, it was seen tangibly that all matters regarding the Rebbe’s leadership are conducted in a way that is *above nature*.

By way of nature, there was no way out for the Rebbe’s rescue, and certainly not for the continuation of his work, and even more so for the expansion and broadening of his work in disseminating Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit — due to the many obstacles, concealments, and hidden factors. And yet, the appropriate path was always found, such that in every country he reached, he began his work there — work that was contrary to the visible status and the possibility of continuing work in that country — and nevertheless, the work proceeded successfully.

**C.** And we must know that this conduct continues even now — and this is the lesson for us:

To preface with what has already been discussed [5](#_ftn1038) regarding the questions asked about the matter of *histalkus*, etc. — we find in the Yerushalmi [6](#_ftn1039) (and it is also cited in *Yalkut Shimoni* [7](#_ftn1040)) regarding Shimshon, that "one verse says, 'And he judged Israel forty years' [8](#_ftn1041), and one verse says, 'And he judged Israel twenty years' [9](#_ftn1042)... this teaches that they were... in awe of him for twenty years after his death just as they were in awe of him during his lifetime." That is to say, since his leadership and authority continued even after his death, such that they were in awe of him for another twenty years, this is considered as if he had judged Israel for forty years.

And if this is true regarding a judge in Israel, how much more so regarding a *Rebbe*, whose entire essence is the *yechidah sheb’nefesh* (except that the *yechidah sheb’nefesh* extends into all parts of the soul and all parts of the body). And regarding the level of *yechidah*, the matter of *histalkus* is not as relevant ("there, the matter of *histalkus* has much less relevance"). It is certainly a matter of complete simplicity that his leadership can continue even after the *histalkus* just as in his lifetime.

There [10](#_ftn1043) are indeed matters where the *histalkus* is relevant, but there are also matters

#### 188

that, just as they were conducted until now — two, three, and four years ago, and before that — with success above the way of nature, because the Rebbe stood at the head... so too from here on... the Rebbe stands at the head and leads all matters.

For there is no issue here of a cessation... or an inheritance that requires division, where "this is wanted and this is not wanted"... rather, "he is alive" [11](#_ftn1044), and consequently, he continues to lead all matters.

Therefore, just as until now all matters were with extraordinary success above the way of nature... so too from here on — when now "he is found... more than in his lifetime" [12](#_ftn1045) — all matters will be with extraordinary success above the way of nature.

Consequently, the choice given to us is that we have the privilege... to choose to participate... together with him... in the matters under his leadership.

It is a clear matter that in any case, all matters will continue from here on as before, and like any living thing, it will be in a manner of "increasing in holiness" [13](#_ftn1046), going and growing, in expansion and spread. However, just as the Rebbe said [14](#_ftn1047) regarding the writing of the Sefer Torah (for the welcoming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu), that it is not his desire to take the merit for himself... but his desire is that all Bnei Yisrael participate in it... so too in all matters — [some of which appear as public affairs, but their purpose and inwardness is the work of disseminating Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit] — the Rebbe gave, gives, and will give everyone the possibility to participate in them.

And he also added and promised that participation in this will be a vessel for the drawing down of blessing and the receiving of blessing, in children, life, and ample sustenance.

**D.** And all this is emphasized most strongly on 12 Tammuz, the Rebbe’s birthday, when "his *mazal* is strong" [15](#_ftn1048), when it was seen with physical eyes that all matters are in a way that is completely above nature.

And so it is every year, that the days of 12-13 Tammuz are an auspicious time for this — that everyone should insert and cast himself ("*arein-varfen zich*") into one of the areas or several of the areas with which the Rebbe led, leads, and will lead

#### 189

("with which the Rebbe led... and leads... and will lead")... and should also include and involve his household members in this.

And then the Rebbe will draw down for them — in addition to the merit of participating in the Rebbe’s work itself — for each and every one, everything they need, in children, life, and ample sustenance.

***

**E.** In the *maamar* that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, sent — at the time — to the country of Russia to be studied during the days of 12-13 Tammuz, and which was printed in preparation for 12-13 Tammuz of this year [16](#_ftn1049), the Rebbe begins with the verse [17](#_ftn1050), "You have given to those who fear You a banner to be displayed, etc."

The Rebbe *shlita* said a *maamar* on the topic "You have given to those who fear You a banner to be displayed, etc."

***

**F.** It is related in the Gemara [18](#_ftn1051), "Rabbi Alexandri would proclaim, 'Who wants life? Who wants life?' Everyone would gather and come to him, saying, 'Give us life.' He said to them, 'Who is the man who desires life, etc.? Guard your tongue from evil, etc. Turn from evil and do good, etc.'" [19](#_ftn1052)

And from this, there has evolved, in opposition and in an opposite manner, a trade ("business") of "life insurance" [20](#_ftn1053):

Instead of going and proclaiming that there is a possibility to acquire life, "Who is the man who desires life," that there is advice for long life and good years (as in the story of the Gemara) — there is someone who walks around and proclaims the *opposite* — that one must worry and arrange from now what will happen after one hundred and twenty years... and therefore it is worthwhile for everyone to purchase a life insurance policy: by paying a small sum each year, they promise him that when the time comes, they will arrange all the necessary matters, etc., in accordance with his wishes.

**G.** Such a task requires very hard work, as it is the opposite of intellect: why should one talk to a person about what will happen after one hundred and twenty years — when one can talk to him about something joyful!

#### 190

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, related in one of his *sichos* (which has already been printed [21](#_ftn1054)) about a certain Jew who came to his father, the Rebbe *Adoneinu*, to consult with him on how to arrange his will regarding the distribution of his money after his long life, saying that his desire was that part of his money should be — in the language of the world — "*oyf oylomos*" (that is, that they should distribute it to charity after his long life). And *Adoneinu* said to him: Regarding the charity that one leaves for *oylomos* — it is better to do it in a manner of "you shall see your world in your lifetime" [22](#_ftn1055)! That is to say, instead of worrying and arranging "worlds" regarding the time after his long life — it is better that out of long life and good years, he should do, see, and enjoy *in his lifetime* the giving of charity for the work of disseminating Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit!

What, then, is the reason they engage in this? — It is nothing but for the sake of *parnassah*:

If he were not in need of *parnassah*, he would not trouble himself at all to engage with so-and-so as to whether he will purchase a policy or not. But since he is in need of *parnassah*, and thinks he has the power of speech so great that he can "sell" to so-and-so anything, both something that exists in the world and something that does not exist in the world... therefore he utilizes the power of speech to convince so-and-so to purchase a life insurance policy in order to arrange from now what will happen if, *chas v'shalom*, he does not live a long life.

The truth is that the insurance company itself wants and desires that its clients *live long lives* — for (in addition to the fact that the sum the clients pay will go and increase year after year) the payment that the insurance company commits to is after one hundred and twenty years. Consequently, when the clients live long lives, everyone (both the clients and the insurance company) will be satisfied... And since this is so, all the effort that the insurance company agent invests to explain to the client that he must also worry lest it be *in a different manner* (contrary to the desire of both...) is nothing but *mere talk* — for the sake of his *parnassah*, to convince the client to agree to pay a certain sum each year for the purchase of the insurance policy, and he promises him one of two things: either that he will live long and good years, or — if *chas v'shalom* not — that the insurance company will pay for him, and the "choice" is in his hands to choose the good path!...

**H.** And one must explain the lesson and instruction from this in the service of Hashem:

The service of the *nefesh elokis* with the *nefesh habahamish* can be in two ways:

#### 191

Way one — to "kill" the body and the *nefesh habahamish* (as our Sages said [23](#_ftn1056), "Words of Torah only endure in one who kills himself for them"), by "reminding him of the day of death" [24](#_ftn1057), and he does not suffice with reminding him in speech, but behaves so in practice — that he kills himself through fasts and afflictions ("here he has a fast, and here he has an affliction"), etc., according to all the details of the matters explained in the *mussar* books.

And way two — that the reminding of the day of death is only *from time to time*, when there is a need to frighten the body and the *nefesh habahamish*, such as in *Tikkun Chatzos*, or after he has fulfilled all the other advice mentioned in the Gemara before that [24](#_ftn1057) ("he should engage in Torah," "he should recite *Krias Shema*") and has not succeeded, then *as a last resort* "he should remind him of the day of death." And even when he reminds him of the day of death — after that, when he comes to actual practice — his work is through maintaining the health of the body for long life and good years.

As is known from what the Maggid said [25](#_ftn1058), that when a small pore is made in the body, a large hole is made in the *neshamah* ("when a small hole is made in the body, a large hole is made in the *neshamah*"), and consequently, one must guard the wholeness of the body due to the preciousness of the *neshamah*. And furthermore, that the body itself is one of the most precious things ("one of the most precious things"), as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, related [26](#_ftn1059) about his father, the Rebbe *Adoneinu*, who showed him his hand, saying: See how precious the body of a Jew is, for which "they poured out" so much ("for him they poured out so much") Torah and *mitzvos*!

And the entire purpose of the frightening regarding the "day of death" is only to "extract" from the body and the *nefesh habahamish* the "payment" that must be paid to the *Ribono shel Olam* day by day through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. But the true desire of the *neshamah* is (not for the death of the body, *chas v'shalom*, but on the contrary) for the continuation of the work and the use of the *nefesh habahamish* and the body for long life and good years — like the parable of the life insurance agent who reminds the client of the day of death solely to extract from him the pennies ("the few cents") designated for the insurance payment, but he too is interested in the client living long and good years.

And regarding the lesson — there is also advice on how to bring about long life and good years for the "clients," which are the 248 limbs of the body — as it is in the *maamarim* of

#### 192

Chassidus [27](#_ftn1060) that the action of *bitul* in the body draws down *the life of the body literally*, as it is written [28](#_ftn1061), "The fear of Hashem is for life."

Consequently, he can serve as an agent of an insurance company, to walk around and proclaim (to the body and *nefesh habahamish*) that they must remember the day of death, but he must know that after that, his work must be in such a way that for all those who belong to him (the clients), there will be added long life and good years in spirituality, and consequently also long life and good years in physicality.

And then they fulfill and complete the intention and the mission of the *neshamah* in its descent below for the sake of the work — in the good way, with expansion, peace of mind, and peace of body, and in a manner of "you shall see your world in your lifetime," with the *neshamah* being clothed in a physical body, and acting with it in this physical world, for long life and good years.

***

**I.** Regarding the establishing of a *yom tov*, *hillula*, or *yoma d'pagra* — since according to the *nigleh* of Torah there is an entire topic in the Gemara (in Tractate *Rosh Hashanah* [29](#_ftn1062)) regarding the nullification of the *yomim tovim* mentioned in *Megillas Taanis*, and the negation of establishing additional *yomim tovim*, as the Gemara says, "The *Megillas Taanis* is nullified; the former are nullified, the latter we add" (in *Taanis*) — therefore, before one establishes a new *yom tov*, *hillula*, or *yoma d'pagra*, one must seemingly first come to an agreement ("come to terms") with the topic of the Gemara...

On the other hand, we see in practice the custom in all the dispersions of Israel — "the custom of Israel is Torah" [30](#_ftn1063) — that many days have been added that were established as a *yom tov* for a miracle that happened to the community, or for a miracle that happened to a specific person, or for a miracle that happened to a *tzaddik*.

And this has already been discussed at length in the *Responsa Chasam Sofer* [31](#_ftn1064), and the conclusion of the matters — according to the second answer in the Gemara there [32](#_ftn1065), "At the time the *Beis Hamikdash* exists, they are forbidden (these days written in *Megillas Taanis*, from eulogy and fasting), because it is a joy for them; when the *Beis Hamikdash* does not exist, they are permitted, because it is mourning for them" [that is to say: those days that were established as *yomim tovim* because of events connected with the building of the *Beis Hamikdash*,

#### 193

remind and emphasize more the destruction] — that the rule that "the former are nullified... the latter we add" does not apply to the establishing of *yomim tovim* for a miracle that occurred *in the time of exile and in the Diaspora* (or even for a miracle that happened in Eretz Yisrael, but) that is not connected with the *Beis Hamikdash* or with Jerusalem in its building [33](#_ftn1066).

And this matter fits with what is explained in the *maamarim* of Chassidus [34](#_ftn1067) that there are matters that after the destruction one can attain specifically in the Diaspora, unlike in Eretz Yisrael, because the concealment and hiding that comes from the destruction is greater in Eretz Yisrael, because everything that is most holy is most destroyed (as the Ramban wrote [35](#_ftn1068)). And an example of this in our case — that *yomim tovim* that were established for miracles that occurred in Eretz Yisrael at the time the *Beis Hamikdash* existed were nullified after the destruction, and yet, we establish a new *yom tov* for a miracle that occurred specifically in the Diaspora, in the time of exile, and in a situation of the decree of annihilation — like the *yom tov* of 12 Tammuz, which is spreading in the communities of Israel more and more, until the time comes when it will spread to all of Israel, with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

**J.** And the explanation of the matter [36](#_ftn1069):

It was explained above (in the *maamar* [37](#_ftn1070)) regarding the matter of trials, that the Divine spark in the trial is in *the greatest concealment and hiding*, to the point that it is as if "the piece itself becomes *neveilah*," but on the other hand, when one reveals the Divine spark that is hidden and concealed in the trial — not through work in a way of debate, but by a Jew awakening his self-nullification and self-strength, then the breaking of the *kelipah* occurs, and consequently the Divine spark is revealed — this is *the greatest light*.

As we see that the greatest light breaks through and shines even inside a mortar, for despite it being a dark place, and the air in it being most foul, nevertheless, it is in the power of a great light to break through ("pass through") and illuminate the greatest darkness.

And similarly regarding the miracle that occurred after the destruction, in the time of exile, in the Diaspora, and in a situation of the most difficult decrees, etc. — that such a miracle points to the greatness of the light, like the advantage of light from darkness, that it has the power to penetrate and shine even

#### 194

in the place of darkness, and consequently, it is no wonder that specifically in the time of exile, in double and redoubled darkness, another *yom tov* is added.

And in the style of the teachings of Chassidus: from the side of the light in the *seder hishtalshelus* — which shone at the time the *Beis Hamikdash* existed — it is not relevant to add new *yomim tovim* after the *yomim tovim* from before were nullified ("the former are nullified, the latter we add"), but from the side of the light *that is above the seder hishtalshelus* — which is revealed through the nullification of the concealment and hiding that is in the darkness of the exile specifically — it is no wonder that another *yom tov* is added in the darkness of the exile.

**K.** And more specifically — regarding the *yom tov* of 12-13 Tammuz:

At that time there was the greatest concealment and hiding, as is also emphasized by the fact that the imprisonment of the Rebbe was connected specifically with a *Jew* — as is known [38](#_ftn1071) the saying (which they would repeat at the *farbrengens* of the elder Chassidim ("in the old *farbrengens*")) regarding 19 Kislev, that since there was concealment and hiding on the *inwardness of the Torah*, therefore it could not be through a gentile, for "the reflection of the reflection (*yechidah*) they do not have" [39](#_ftn1072), but specifically through a *Jew*. And similarly, one can say regarding 12 Tammuz, that even then the hand of Jews was involved, due to the greatness of the concealment and hiding on the inwardness of the Torah.

However, from the side of the revelation of the Rebbe’s essence, self-nullification, and self-strength (as mentioned that this is specifically the way to overcome a trial) — the concealment and hiding in the trial were nullified in such a way that the G.P.U. themselves came to the realization that they must release him (and not just a simple release, but) with a high hand (as above, section A), and furthermore, that after some time they admitted that specifically through them another *yom tov* was added for Chassidim — 12 Tammuz!

— Some [40](#_ftn1073) time after the *geulah* of 12 Tammuz, one of the prominent Rabbis was arrested by the G.P.U., and when he spoke to them to prove to them that they had arrested him without any guilt, the G.P.U. men answered him and said to him [they spoke to him in Russian, but, since not everyone here understands Russian, I will tell the content of their words in the spoken language]: Why are you afraid of the imprisonment? On the contrary, through this another *yom tov* will be added for Chassidim! When they arrested the Lubavitcher — they explained their words — the *yom tov* of 12 Tammuz was added, and when they arrest you and afterward release you — another *yom tov* will be added!...

#### 195

This is similar and analogous to the admission of Yisro: "Now I know that Hashem is greater than all the gods" [41](#_ftn1074), through which the greatest elevation was added [42](#_ftn1075).

**L.** We find this matter also at the time of the imprisonment itself:

The Rebbe related [43](#_ftn1076) that while he was in prison, they entered his prison room on *Shabbos* in order to photograph him,

— according to the law of the government, there must be a picture of every prisoner in the prison office. And since for some reason they did not photograph the Rebbe before they put him in his prison cell (called a "*tzele*"), they came to photograph him in his prison cell on *Shabbos*.

At that time — it was the second, third, or fourth hour after midday — the Rebbe was praying with his *tallis* covering his face ("with the *tallis* over the head"), and when they entered his cell and saw him sitting with his *tallis* covering his face — they left. After some time — an hour or an hour and a half (the Rebbe did not say how much time) — they came again. The Rebbe was still in the middle of prayer, but his *tallis* was not covering his face, and when he noticed them as they entered with all the photography equipment ("with all the clatter-gear"), he made some motion with his hand ("made a motion with the hand") showing that he could not stop now, and they were flustered and left. After another period of time — an hour or an hour and a half — they came a third time, and then the Rebbe told them that since today is *Shabbos*, he is forbidden to be photographed. And when they heard his words, they left, and postponed the photography to another time.

This event is a wonder, and according to intellect it has no place at all:

These people — they do not need to be impressed by a "*tallis*," and they are not impressed by a "*tallis*," and on the contrary: they arrested the Rebbe *because* of his being a Rabbi, a Rebbe, *who covers himself with a tallis*!...

What, then, is the reason that when the Rebbe was with them, in their four cubits, an environment that is entirely teeming with their people, and within their four walls, a place that has no *mezuzos* [44](#_ftn1077) — *they were impressed and flustered* upon seeing the Rebbe sitting with his *tallis* covering his face, to such an extent that they withdrew, realizing that they had nothing to do here!... — Where is there room for such a thing in intellect?!...

Rather, what is it — from the side of the Rebbe’s essence (who stood in self-nullification

#### 196
