and self-strength) it was effected even in such a reality that the Divine spark in it is hidden and concealed completely to the point that the piece becomes *neveilah* (except that nevertheless the reality of the spark remained), that when this reality sees [45](#_ftn1078) *essence and being* [46](#_ftn1079) *as he sits wrapped in a tallis over the head*... then there is no room for them at all (not from the side of intellect, since for them themselves this is a matter that does not belong to intellect) to try to disturb, since here their reality is nullified ("their reality becomes here a non-reality"), and not only do they not disturb, but furthermore, they withdraw from the place, seeing that they have nothing to do here ("one has here nothing to do")!...

**M.** And this power the Rebbe gives to each one of us:

In his letter for the *Chag HaGeulah* [47](#_ftn1080), the Rebbe writes: "Hashem did not redeem only me on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, observers of *mitzvah*, and also those who are called by the name of Israel."

And since "He did not redeem only me... but also all... who are called by the name of Israel" — such a type *that everyone* belongs to him — therefore, all those who belong to the Rebbe [48](#_ftn1081), "those who hold onto his door handle" [49](#_ftn1082), must know that they have nothing to be impressed by concealment and hiding, and they have nothing to be impressed by obstacles and delays, and they have nothing to be impressed even by the concealment and hiding from those who also have the "reflection of the reflection"!

If only they will not pay attention to the concealments, the hiding, the obstacles, and the delays, and will make a motion of nullification with the hand ("one will make a motion with the hand") out of self-nullification and self-strength — then all the concealments, the hiding, the obstacles, and the delays will be nullified by themselves, *above the way of nature* (just as the Rebbe’s *geulah* was above the way of nature), and furthermore — as the Rebbe concludes in the *maamar* [50](#_ftn1083) — that the above-nature is drawn down *into nature itself* (just as the release from prison was in nature), and then they can fulfill and complete the mission that was placed upon us in this physical and material world below ten *tefachim*.

And as mentioned above (in the *maamar* [51](#_ftn1084)) — the approach to all matters of

#### 197

this world must be in a manner of equanimity, from the side of the knowledge and recognition that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good" [52](#_ftn1085), and then one merits the revelation of the good in all matters, as explained in *Tanya* [53](#_ftn1086) regarding the matter of "and those who love Him are like the sun going forth in its might" [54](#_ftn1087), that even the matters that were initially in a manner of hidden kindnesses — come and are revealed in visible and manifest good.

***

**N.** According to what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, wrote in his letter for the *Chag HaGeulah*: "Hashem did not redeem only me on 12 Tammuz, but also all, etc." (as above, section 13) — all the types he details in his letter, among whom we are all included — it is understood that for each one there must be a matter of *geulah* in the spirituality of things.

And the matter of this:

*Geulah* — means an exit from exile, an exit from constraints and boundaries, including also the exit from the constraints and boundaries of oneself [and on the contrary: in order to exit from the constraints and boundaries that are outside of him ("foreign constraints and boundaries"), the advice is to exit from the constraints and boundaries of oneself ("from the own constraints and boundaries"), and by way of consequence, there will be no control for the constraints and boundaries that are outside of him], an "exit" and a "journey" from his previous place (status and situation) to a new place (status and situation).

And all this — even when he is in a good status and situation (place) (and not only that it seems so to him, but that it is so in truth), nevertheless, he should not suffice with this and remain standing in that place, but must exit from this "place" and go to a new "place," and therefore every Jew is called by the name "walker" [55](#_ftn1088), since from day to day and from hour to hour he must walk further and ascend to a higher level, as the command of the Torah, "increasing in holiness" [13].

**O.** And more specifically:

Standing in one place causes his work to be done in a manner of *habit*, and habit becomes nature [56](#_ftn1089), and consequently, his work lacks the matter of pleasure, as is known that constant pleasure is not pleasure [57](#_ftn1090).

And furthermore, that from the side of habit, he lacks the entire matter of *work* —

#### 198

as explained in *Tanya* [58](#_ftn1091) the difference between "one who serves Hashem" and "one who has not served Him" [59](#_ftn1092), that "one who serves Hashem is one who reviews his chapter one hundred and one times, and one who has not served Him is one who reviews his chapter one hundred times only" [60](#_ftn1093), "because in their days it was the *habit* to review every chapter one hundred times," and since the study is according to habit (even when the habit is the best, but) without toil and labor, then he is called "*one who has not served Him*," and only when he toils — in a manner of war — to change the nature of his habit, then he is called "one who serves Hashem."

[And furthermore, even one who is a "servant of Hashem" who "has already served and finished completely the work of war with evil, etc." [61](#_ftn1094) — since from here on his work is done without toil and labor and without concealments and hiding, he is not called "one who serves Hashem" in the present tense, but rather, "one who has not served Him."

— This is also the content of the story that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, related [62](#_ftn1095) about the *Tzemach Tzedek*, that a young man came to him for *yechidus* and complained that he had no desire to study, saying, "What shall I do that I have no desire to study?" And the *Tzemach Tzedek* answered him: "*Petach, petach*, what shall I do (the *Tzemach Tzedek* himself) *that I have* a desire to study!"... since the study of Torah must be (like all matters of the service of Hashem) in a way of war, labor, and acceptance of the yoke specifically].

Furthermore:

Since there is a command to go and add and ascend in holiness, therefore, if he does not go and add and ascend in holiness, *he is transgressing the fulfillment of the will of Hashem*, like one who transgresses, *chas v'shalom*, the fulfillment of the will of Hashem regarding a *mitzvah* from the Torah!

— From the side of the content of the matters themselves, there are indeed levels of difference regarding the severity of the matters: a Torah prohibition, a Rabbinic prohibition, a slight detail of the words of the Scribes, up to a matter that is only beyond the letter of the law; but from the side of Hashem, the Commander of the *mitzvos* — everything is the will of Hashem equally, and His will, may He be blessed, is that a Jew should not suffice even with conduct that is beyond the letter of the law, "they spoke here of a measure of piety" [63](#_ftn1096), but should go and add always more and more, and

## With the help of Hashem. Reshimus Devarim, Tuesday, Parshas Pinchas, 20 Tammuz, 5711

#### 222

(Unedited)

**A.** Regarding the mitzvah of nedarim (vows), which is explained at the beginning of Parshas Matos, it is stated [1](#_ftn1225): "And Moshe spoke to the heads of the tribes of the children of Israel, saying, etc." This implies that in this specific mitzvah, Moshe and the heads of the tribes are mentioned.

The significance of this is as follows [2](#_ftn1226):

The essence of the matter of nedarim is the creation of *gedarim and s'yagim* (fences and safeguards) in order to add strength and vigor to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos [3](#_ftn1227).

Based on this, we can explain the novelty found in the mitzvah of nedarim compared to all other mitzvos of the Torah [4](#_ftn1228): The obligation for all mitzvos of the Torah does not begin until the age of thirteen, whereas the obligation of nedarim applies even to a "mufla hasamuch l'ish" [5](#_ftn1229)—a child who is twelve years and one day old [6](#_ftn1230) (and according to many opinions [7](#_ftn1231), this obligation is *min haTorah*). This is because the content of the mitzvah of nedarim is the addition of fences and safeguards as a *preparation and introduction* to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, this mitzvah begins for the "mufla hasamuch l'ish"—at the time of *preparation* for the commencement of the obligation in all mitzvos of the Torah.

There is a moral lesson to be added here: before a person begins their obligation in all the mitzvos of the Torah (when they turn thirteen), there must be a preparation and introduction of adding fences and abstinence regarding things that the Torah has permitted (which is the concept of nedarim), through which they will be able to fulfill the mitzvos *kideba'i* (as they should be fulfilled) [8](#_ftn1232).

**B.** Now, regarding the matter of *adding* to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, which includes the concept of nedarim as mentioned above, we find two extremes:

#### 223

On one hand, it is an undesirable matter, as our Sages have said [9](#_ftn1233): "Whoever adds, subtracts, as it is stated [10](#_ftn1234), 'God said, you shall not eat of it, and you shall not touch it'" ("The Holy One, blessed be He, did not warn them about touching it, and through this addition, they subtracted, etc." [11](#_ftn1235)). Consequently, as a result of Chava *adding* a prohibition of her own volition (which they were not commanded by the Holy One, blessed be He), the *sin of the Tree of Knowledge* was caused (Heaven forbid).

On the other hand, we find that there are instances where the concept of nedarim (adding to the obligation of Torah and mitzvos) is a *desirable and lofty* thing [12](#_ftn1236), as Shimon HaTzaddik said to a certain nazir [13](#_ftn1237): "May there *increase* many nazirim like you in Israel" [14](#_ftn1238).

Therefore, "the heads of the tribes" are mentioned in the mitzvah of nedarim—because, in light of the two extremes mentioned above, in order to know *when* one should add a fence and safeguard to the mitzvos of the Torah, there is a need for the "heads of the tribes," the *nesi'im* (leaders) of Israel.

Yet, all of this is still not sufficient; there must also be the instruction of Moshe Rabbeinu ("And *Moshe* spoke to the heads of the tribes"). This is because specifically Moshe "prophesied with the language of *zeh* (this)" (as our Sages expound [15](#_ftn1239) on the verse at the beginning of our parsha—"Moshe spoke... *zeh* hadavar, etc."), and "Moshe Rabbeinu gazed through the clear glass" [16](#_ftn1240). Therefore, when the fulfillment of the mitzvah of nedarim is done according to the instruction of Moshe, we are assured that not only will no adverse result occur (Heaven forbid), but on the contrary, through this, *strength and completeness* will be added to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos [17](#_ftn1241).

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Thursday, Parshas Pinchas, 22 Tammuz, 5711

#### 224

– To the students traveling on the shlichus of the Melach, in his holy room –

You are surely aware that for several years now, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory[1](#_ftn1242), has instituted that students should travel for several weeks to outlying cities (and also within New York City itself) in order to engage in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and to effect a strengthening in the observance of Torah and mitzvos.

– Instead of utilizing this time for the sake of physical recuperation and restoration, as is the custom among others, the students shall utilize it to engage in the restoration and healing of the souls of Bnei Yisrael, both children and adults. Through this, there will be an addition to their own selves in the restoration and healing of their own souls and bodies, so that they will be healthy in both spirituality and physicality.

*

Since this journey is on the Rebbe’s shlichus, it possesses many advantages. We will now pause to consider two matters that are practically relevant[2](#_ftn1243):

1) Since this is the Rebbe’s shlichus, you will certainly succeed in it, provided that you do not ruin it yourselves ("men zol nor alein nit kalie machn"). When one travels on the Rebbe’s shlichus, by the power of the one who sends, it is as if *the Rebbe himself is traveling* ("der Rebbe fort"). Consequently, it is impossible for there to be obstacles and delays in the matter. The students only need to be a capable vessel, and as the capacity of the vessel grows, the shlichus will be fulfilled with greater speed and success.

2) Since this is the Rebbe’s shlichus, one must know the magnitude of the responsibility one is carrying. Those Jews to whom you are traveling will look at you as shluchim of the Rebbe, as a living example of Chassidim. Consequently, you must "fix yourselves" ("ois-richten zich") so that you appear in a manner appropriate for this.

– R' Shmuel Munkes[3](#_ftn1244) once walked with a group of Chassidim, upon their return from a farbrengen, past the courtyard of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe. R' Shmuel Munkes jumped onto

#### 225

the fence and hung from the courtyard gate. His fellow Chassidim—who were accustomed to his antics—asked him what the meaning of this new stunt was ("wos iz dos far a nayer shpitzel")? R' Shmuel Munkes replied to them: It is the way of the world that by a shoemaker, a shoe hangs; by a glazier, a piece of glass hangs, and so on. Likewise, it is fitting that by the *Rebbe’s courtyard*, a *Chassid* should be hanging... so that people should know that here is where the Rebbe’s courtyard is located.

And similarly in our case: Everyone who sees you will think that this is what a Lubavitcher Chassid, a Chabadnik, a Tamim, a yirei-shamayim yeshiva bochur (and so on with the other titles used to describe you) looks like. The impression will remain with them that this is how Chassidim, Temimim, and those who are mekushar—those who travel on the Rebbe’s shlichus to engage in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and the strengthening of Torah and mitzvos—should conduct themselves. Consequently, you must know that you bear a great responsibility[4](#_ftn1245).

However, since it is the Rebbe who instituted this matter, and he is the one sending you on this shlichus—it is within the power and ability of each one of you to fulfill this shlichus, such that not only will there be no chillul Hashem, Heaven forbid, but on the contrary, reports will be received regarding the magnitude of the amazement ("gwaldige hispaalus") regarding the essence of the Lubavitcher students ("wos a Lubavitcher bochur iz")!

*

I bless you that the blessings which the Rebbe has bestowed upon you in general, and specifically regarding the fulfillment of the shlichus, will be realized.

Travel in peace and return in peace ("fort gezunterheit un kumt zurik gezunterheit"), and may your journey be successful in both physicality and spirituality—both regarding the physicality and spirituality of *the Jews to whom you are traveling*, and regarding *your own* physicality and spirituality. For the Rebbe’s intent is not only for the benefit of the Jews to whom you are traveling, but also for the benefit of the travelers themselves, as per the teaching of our Sages[5](#_ftn1246) on the verse[6](#_ftn1247), "Hashem illuminates the eyes of both."

May you have a healthy summer, and following that a healthy winter, and so on, forever and ever[7](#_ftn1248).

Travel in peace, and in every place you arrive, convey a heartfelt greeting ("a hertzlichen grus") to our brothers, Bnei Yisrael. Tell them that even though we are in the midst of the Three Weeks, and approaching the month of Elul, the month of teshuvah[8](#_ftn1249), and after that the "Yamim Nora'im," nevertheless, they should not be alarmed ("zol men zich nit shreken"). Rather, "Serve Hashem *with joy*"[9](#_ftn1250), "*rejoice* with trembling"[10](#_ftn1251).

And likewise, tell them that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, said[11](#_ftn1252) that we are already at the time when "Behold, he is standing behind our wall"[12](#_ftn1253), "Behold, he is coming"[13](#_ftn1254) ("ot iz er")... and we must prepare for this through ahavas Hashem, ahavas HaTorah, and ahavas Yisrael[14](#_ftn1255). When you say these things calmly, yet with inner conviction, the words will surely be accepted by those who hear them, and through this, there will be an addition to their strengthening in Torah and mitzvos in general, and in ahavas Yisrael in particular.

Travel in peace.

## With the help of Hashem. Reshimos Devarim at the time of a Bar Mitzvah celebration, 22 Tammuz, 5711

#### 227

Unedited

The distinction between the titles "Ish" (man) and "Adam" (person) was discussed in relation to the definition of the obligation in mitzvos for one who is thirteen years old—whether this is due to the natural development of intellect and da'as, or due to Halacha L'Moshe MiSinai. Their significance in avodah was also discussed—avodah according to ta'am v'da'as (intellect and reason) versus avodah from a place of kabbalas ol (acceptance of the yoke) and mesiras nefesh that transcends ta'am v'da'as. This was edited by the Rebbe and printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 15, p. 289 and onwards.

(When speaking about avodah from a place of mesiras nefesh, the Rebbe related:)

My father-in-law, the Rebbe, told me about the greatness of the mesiras nefesh of his father, the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e., during his work regarding the Rabbinical Conference in Petersburg, which took place in the year 5670[1](#_ftn1256)—that his mesiras nefesh was in a wondrous manner, without any limitations whatsoever[2](#_ftn1257). He (my father-in-law, the Rebbe) added that once, he could not restrain himself, and he said to his father—in a lighthearted way—that his "mazal" is that the obligation of mesiras nefesh is not mentioned in the Shulchan Aruch. For, had the obligation of mesiras nefesh been mentioned in the Shulchan Aruch, it would have had limitations; but now that it is not mentioned in the Shulchan Aruch, one can practice mesiras nefesh without measure!

(And the Rebbe concluded:)

We must be Yidden of mesiras nefesh, provided that we utilize this mesiras nefesh in a good way.

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, Mevarchim HaChodesh Menachem-Av, 5711

#### 228

(An unedited transcript)

**"Command** the Children of Israel and say to them: My offering, My bread for My fire... you shall be careful to offer to Me in its appointed time." [1] The Sifri [2] states: What is written above? "May Hashem, the G-d of the spirits of all flesh, appoint a man over the congregation who shall go out before them and come in before them." [3] The Ribono shel Olam said to him (to Moshe): "Before you command Me regarding My children [which is something that is unnecessary], command My children regarding Me, etc." From the fact that before Moshe’s passing, the Ribono shel Olam told him to "command My children regarding Me" concerning the matter of the *korbanos*, it is understood that the matter of *korbanos* is the essence of *avodah*. Yet, we must understand this, for we find that the prophets argued to the Jewish people, "Is listening better than sacrifice, etc.?" [4] and it is written, [5] "For I desire kindness and not sacrifice." This implies that the essence is the matter of "listening" and the matter of *chesed*, not *korbanos* (*zevach*).

**Furthermore,** one must understand the matter of the *korbanos* themselves. The first *korban* that the Jewish people were commanded to bring through Moshe was the *korban tamid*. Regarding the *temidim*, our Sages said [6] that the morning *tamid* atones for the sins of the night, and the afternoon *tamid* atones for the sins of the day. The well-known question [7] is: How does the offering of an animal atone for the sin of a human being? This is similar to the language of Chazal, [8] "If a person sinned, what did the animal do?" It is explained [9] that the atonement comes through the person contemplating that everything done to the animal should have been done to him, etc. [10] This is also the concept of *tefillah*, which corresponds to the *korbanos*, as our Sages said, [11] "The *tefillos* were instituted to correspond to the *temidim*." As explained in *Likutei Torah*, [12] the matter of the *olah* offering—where they would offer the flesh, the sinews, and the bones—is that the formation of the bones is drawn from the *moach* (brain), and the formation of the flesh is from the blood, which draws into the heart, from which flesh is made. Its parallel in *tefillah* is that the contemplation regarding the *bitul* and the lack of

#### 229

independent existence of the worlds (the entire *Seder Hishtalshelus*) relative to the *Ohr Ein Sof*, how all is considered as nothing before Him, is the aspect of the "bones" that come from the *moach*. The arousal of the *midos*—*ahavah* and *yirah*—through this contemplation is the aspect of the "flesh" drawn from the blood in the heart. This is a light that is contracted, a tiny fraction of the *hasagah* (grasp) in the *moach*, which is drawn down to be enclothed in the heart through the sinews and arteries that connect the bones with the flesh. According to this, it would seem that *tefillah* has an advantage over *korbanos*, for the matter of *korbanos* is only *as if* everything done to the animal were done to the person, whereas in *tefillah*, the *avodah* of the *korbanos* is *actually* performed within the soul of the person, for the contemplation and the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah* are the actual offering of the flesh, sinews, and bones, as mentioned above. Based on this, *tefillah* should be on a higher level than *korbanos*. [13] Nevertheless, we find that the matter of *korbanos* is higher than *tefillah*, which is why we say in *tefillah*, [14] "May it be Your will... that the Beis Hamikdash be rebuilt speedily in our days," [15] where the offering of *korbanos* will take place. And what is explained—that the superiority of *korbanos* is because the *nitzotz Eloki* (Divine spark) within the animal has a higher root [16] (for everything that is higher descends lower [17])—would imply that the primary superiority should be in the *korbanos* of the First and Second Temples specifically, where the *nitzotz Eloki* in the physical animal is in a state of greater descent, and not in the *korbanos* of the future, when "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth." [18] Yet, we find that the primary superiority of *korbanos* is specifically for the future, as we say in the text of the *tefillah*, [19] "And there we will perform before You according to the command of Your will," which implies that specifically in the future, the offering of *korbanos* will be complete. We must understand this: from whichever perspective you look, due to the superiority of spirituality, the primary superiority should be in *tefillah*, and due to the superiority of physicality, the primary superiority should be in the *korbanos* of the First and Second Temples. Why, then, do we say that specifically the offering of *korbanos* in the future will be "according to the command of Your will"?

b) **To understand** all this, we must first preface [20] that it is known that the purpose of the creation of the worlds is because the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place below. [21] The meaning of a "dwelling place" is, for example, a person’s home, where he dwells

#### 230

with his entire essence and being. [22] So too is the matter of a dwelling place for Him below: that the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof* should be below. This is also the meaning of the statement of our Sages, "I have come into My garden, My private garden," [23] etc., that the *Ikkar Shechinah* (the essence of the Divine Presence) was below. The precision here is "the *Ikkar Shechinah*," meaning not just *Shechinah* in general—the aspect of revelations, etc.—but the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*. This is what is meant by "the *Ikkar Shechinah* was below," which is the concept of the Ribono shel Olam’s desire to have a dwelling place below. This is accomplished through the *avodah* below. Just as in the case of "the *Ikkar Shechinah* was below," there was also the matter of *avodah* then, as it is written, [24] "And He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it."

**The concept** is that it is written, [25] "Which G-d created to do," and our Sages said [26] "to do" means "to rectify." This means that in every thing there are two aspects: what it is from its own perspective, and what is added to it through the *avodah* of man. This is true even in the Garden of Eden, which is above the world (for the foundation of the Garden of Eden is the spirituality within the physicality of the world [27]), that there is the aspect of the Garden of Eden as it is from its own perspective, and there is what is added to it through the *avodah* of man. The point is that the Garden of Eden is higher than the world, [28] for the world is connected with the aspect of the *midos*, as it is written, [29] "For I said, the world is built with *chesed*," and the Garden of Eden in its entirety is the World of *Beriah*, in which the *Chabad* (*Chochma, Binah, Da'as*) of the *Ein Sof* shines, which is the aspect of the *mochin*. It is known that the *mochin* are higher than the *midos*; therefore, the drawing down of *mochin* into the *midos* is specifically through the "narrowness of the throat." That is, for the *midos* to come into being from the *mochin*, there must first be a concealment of the *mochin*, and only then can the existence of the *midos* be possible. From this, one understands the vast difference in value between the *midos* and the *mochin*, which is why there must first be a concealment of the *mochin*, creating a state that is neither *mochin* nor *midos*, and only then is the existence of the *midos* possible. From this, one also understands the vast difference in value between the world, whose formation is from the aspect of the *midos*, and the Garden of Eden, in which the aspect of the *mochin* shines. Furthermore, in the world there is only knowledge of existence, not a grasp of essence, [30] and this is true

#### 231

regarding both matters of *Elokus* and matters of the world. In all of them, one does not grasp the essence—not in spirituality and not in physicality—because the essence of every created being is the Divine power within it. For if the acting power were to withdraw from the acted-upon, it would become nothingness and void. [31] Since the essence of the created being is the Divine power within it, and in the Divine power there is no grasp whatsoever, it follows that even in physical things, there is no grasp of essence in the world, only knowledge of existence. In contrast, in the Garden of Eden, there is a grasp of the essence of *Elokus*, [32] as the saying goes, [33] "They derive pleasure from the radiance of the *Shechinah*," and pleasure is specifically from the grasp of essence. However, although the world is vastly inferior to the Garden of Eden, nevertheless, specifically through the *avodah* in the world, one effects an addition of light in the Garden of Eden. For the revelation of the Garden of Eden (that they derive pleasure from the radiance of the *Shechinah*) is the radiance of their Torah and *avodah*, [34] light and radiance alone [35] from what is effected by the *avodah* below. This is similar to what was explained in the *maamar* "Basi L'Gani" [36] regarding the addition of lights in *Atzilus* through the *avodah* below: that the lights in *Atzilus* are "as if placed in a box," for they are not for the sake of *Atzilus*, but for the sake of the lower world, and they are not revealed in *Atzilus*. It is the same regarding the Garden of Eden, that nothing is revealed in it except the radiance of their Torah and *avodah* alone. Nevertheless, the radiance of their Torah and *avodah* in this world adds light in the Garden of Eden. The matter of the renewal in the Garden of Eden through the *avodah* below is the drawing down of the *Ohr Sovev*, meaning [37] that in the Garden of Eden from its own perspective, only the aspect of *Ohr Memaleh* shines. This is why the Garden of Eden is called a "clear world," [38] where all matters are in an orderly arrangement, each thing according to its status. Therefore, the matter of *teshuvah* is not effective in the Garden of Eden, for *teshuvah* is the transformation from essence to essence, and this matter does not apply in the Garden of Eden, which is a "clear world" in which the *Ohr Memaleh* shines—whose nature is lights within vessels, lights that are according to the value of the vessels, so that the vessels can receive the light. This is the innovation effected by the *avodah* below: that the *Ohr Sovev* is drawn down.

c) **Now,** the primary *avodah* through which the dwelling place below is accomplished is specifically the *avodah* of *korbanos*. [39] This is also true regarding the *avodah* at the beginning of creation, as it is written, "And He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it," as our Sages said [40] that "to guard it" refers to the *avodah* of *korbanos*, as it is written, "You shall be careful to offer to Me, etc." The explanation is,

#### 232

as we stated above, that the matter of the dwelling place means that the *Atzmus* and essence of the *Ein Sof* should be below. Furthermore, the matter of the dwelling place is that the drawing down below should not be merely in the manner of a *makif* (encompassing light), but should be drawn into the created beings internally and in revelation. For this, one must remove the concealments and obstructions, because when there are concealments and obstructions, the drawing down is only in the manner of a *makif*, or the drawing down is internal but is hidden and not revealed. Therefore, one must remove the concealments and obstructions, and then the drawing down will be internal and in revelation, since there is no reason for it not to come into revelation. All this is accomplished specifically through the *avodah* of *korbanos*, because in them it was seen in revelation [41] that in a physical animal, *bitul* and inclusion in the fire above is effected—the aspect of "the lion that consumes the offerings." [42] *Korban* is a term for the drawing near of powers and senses, [43] meaning that it is drawn into the created beings internally. [44] Furthermore, the drawing down through *korbanos* is the drawing down of the *Atzmus*, as the saying [45] goes, "The mystery of the *korban* ascends to the mystery of the *Ein Sof*," meaning the mystery of the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, which is the precision of the phrase "mystery of the *Ein Sof*" and not "mystery of the *Ohr Ein Sof*." Therefore, the primary matter of a dwelling place for Him below is accomplished through the *avodah* of *korbanos*, because through this *avodah* one reaches the aspect of the *Atzmus*, and the drawing down is within the created beings and in revelation. This is the reason why the primary superiority of *korbanos* is in the offering of a physical animal specifically, and not in *tefillah*, because specifically in the offering of a physical animal it was seen in revelation that the animal is included in the fire above, as mentioned. Therefore, even at the beginning of creation, there was the matter of the *avodah* of *korbanos*, since specifically through this is the intention fulfilled that the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place below. This is also the precision of the phrase "And He placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it"—"placed him" (*vayanihehu*) specifically, since through the *korbanos* the matter of *neyacha* (rest/satisfaction) is accomplished, etc. [46]

d) **Now,** in the *avodah* of *korbanos* itself, there is an added superiority in the manner of the *avodah* that existed at the beginning of creation in the Garden of Eden. As we stated above, the Garden of Eden is the spirituality within the physicality of the world, meaning that while it is in the physicality of the world, it is the spirituality within that physicality, and there, the existence of evil did not exist at all (for evil was outside the Garden of Eden). From this, it is understood that the *avodah* of *korbanos* in the Garden of Eden was not in the matter of *birurim* (refinements), but in the matter of drawing down *Elokus* [similar to what existed in the days of Shlomo, of whom it is written [47] "He is a man of

#### 233

rest," for the matter of *birurim* was for him in a manner of "by itself" [48]]. However, after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, it is written [49] "And He drove out the man," that he was judged with expulsion, [50] and this is because in the Garden of Eden, the existence of evil is not applicable. [51] And although the simple reason stated in the verse is "and now, lest he reach out his hand, etc., and eat and live forever," [52] based on this reason alone, he did not need to be judged with expulsion (for there are many ways for the Omnipresent). Rather, the inner reason for the expulsion is because in the Garden of Eden, the existence of evil is not applicable. This is what is meant [53] by "And He sent him out... to work the ground from which he was taken," for since from the ground from which he was taken, the matter of sin was brought about for him, in exchange for the fact that while he was in the Garden of Eden his *avodah* was in drawing down *Elokus*, he now had to work the ground, which is the matter of the *avodah* of *birurim*. This is the superiority of the *avodah* of *korbanos* as it existed in the Garden of Eden: its matter is the drawing down of *Elokus*, without engaging with evil at all. This is also the case in the *avodah* of *korbanos* of the future, for since "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," there will be no need for the matter of *korbanos* for the *avodah* of *birurim*, but only for the drawing down of *Elokus*, just as it was in the Garden of Eden at the beginning of creation.

e) **However,** the primary perfection in the matter of *korbanos* will be in the future, when the *korbanos* will be even higher than the *korbanos* in the Garden of Eden. More specifically, regarding *korbanos* it is written, "My bread for My fire you shall be careful," which are three matters: "My bread" is the thing being offered; "you shall be careful" refers to the person offering; and "My fire" is the matter of the fire above. This means that according to the manner of the one offering and the thing offered, so will be the drawing down from above. In the future, all three of these matters will be in perfection; therefore, there will be the ultimate perfection in the matter of *korbanos*.

**The explanation** is that the *korbanos* in the Garden of Eden were before the Giving of the Torah, at which time there was the decree that "those of Rome shall not descend to Syria, and those of Syria shall not ascend to Rome," meaning that the upper realms would not descend below and the lower realms would not ascend above. [54] Therefore, all the *mitzvos* that the Patriarchs performed were "fragrances," [55] meaning that the essential drawing down of the Giving of the Torah had not yet been drawn down. As explained by the Rebbe (Rashab) [56] that the matter of "fragrances" applies also to Adam HaRishon, even though his *avodah* was higher than the Patriarchs

#### 234

because he was the "handiwork" of the Ribono shel Olam [57] and was in the Garden of Eden. One can explain the innovation in this: that even though he was the handiwork of the Ribono shel Olam, his *avodah* was nevertheless only in the aspect of "fragrances." For regarding the soul, all are equal, as our Rebbe explains in *Tanya* [58] that the *nefesh Elokis* is literally a part of G-d from above, as it is written, "And He blew into his nostrils a soul of life," [59] "And You blew it into me," [60] and as it is written in the *Zohar*, [61] "He who blows, blows from within himself," meaning from his innerness and from his interior. The superiority of Adam HaRishon was that even regarding the body, he was the handiwork of the Ribono shel Olam, meaning that his body, while being below ten *tefachim*, was the handiwork of the Ribono shel Olam, who is above ten *tefachim*. [62] Thus, he had the matter of the connection of the upper and lower realms. This is the innovation: that even so, his *avodah* was only in the aspect of "fragrances," because the decree had not yet been nullified by the drawing down of the Giving of the Torah, which is the drawing down of the *Atzmus* itself. This is the concept of "I [Anochi]...," [63] "I wrote and gave My soul." [64] Therefore, the entirety of the Giving of the Torah is higher than the status and situation of the Garden of Eden at the beginning of creation, as is understood from the statement of our Sages [65] regarding the verse [66] "the sixth day": "The Ribono shel Olam made a condition with the works of creation: If the Jewish people accept My Torah, it is good; and if not, I will return the world to *tohu* and *bohu*." This is because specifically at the Giving of the Torah was there the drawing down of the *Atzmus*. Therefore, although the superiority of the *avodah* of *korbanos* in the Garden of Eden was great—for its matter was not the *avodah* of *birurim* (since in the Garden of Eden there was no existence of evil), but the drawing down of *Elokus* below—nevertheless, since this was before the Giving of the Torah, it did not contain the drawing down that comes from the *Atzmus* itself. On the other hand, the *avodah* of *korbanos* during the time of the First and Second Temples, although it was after the Giving of the Torah (when there was the drawing down of the *Atzmus*), nevertheless, since it was after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, when a mixture of good and evil was created, the primary *avodah* of *korbanos* was in the matter of *birurim*. However, with the coming of Moshiach speedily in our days, both superiorities will exist. [67] In the future, it is written, "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," at which time there will be the nullification of the *sitra achra*. This is also what is written, [68] "And the wolf shall dwell with the lamb," that even the wolf (an impure animal), which is from the *sitra achra*, will have a matter of refinement, etc. From this, it is understood that even *kelipas nogah*, which is the intermediary between *kedushah* and the *sitra achra*, will be on a much higher level. Thus, in the future, the animal being offered and the person offering will be on an added level of superiority. Consequently,

#### 235

the matter of *korbanos* will not be for the *avodah* of *birurim*, but for the drawing down of *Elokus*, as in the Garden of Eden. In addition to this, they will also have the superiority of the drawing down of the *Atzmus* that is after the Giving of the Torah, higher than the *korbanos* in the Garden of Eden. Therefore, specifically regarding them it is said "according to the command of Your will," since through this, the primary matter of a dwelling place for Him below is accomplished.

f) **Now,** the perfection in the *avodah* of *korbanos* in the future comes specifically through the *avodah* during the time of *galus*. [69] According to the well-known principle [70] that the cause is higher than the thing caused by it, since it has the power to cause the thing, one understands the greatness of the superiority of the *avodah* during the time of *galus*, for specifically through it do we arrive at the perfection of the *avodah* of *korbanos* "according to the command of Your will." One can say that this is also what is meant [71] by "They reached her between the straits (*bein hametzarim*)," that when one is "between the straits," specifically then do they "reach her," reaching the most exalted attainments, until they reach the time when the *avodah* of *korbanos* of the future will take place, whose matter is the ultimate perfection of a dwelling place below, with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, Mevarchim Chodesh Menachem-Av, 5711

#### 236

(Unedited)

**A.** In the notes of the Tzemach Tzedek on Megillas Eichah—which are currently being printed[1]—all the matters in Megillas Eichah are interpreted *l’ma’aliusa* (for the better), ("in the same way that the curses will be transformed into blessings... one can also say that Eichah [is] for elevation"[2]), such as the verse[3] "All her pursuers overtook her between the straits (bein hametzarim)," which means that it is precisely from "between the straits" ("from the straits"[4]) that one arrives at even higher levels[5], and similarly with the other verses in Megillas Eichah.

Based on this, it is well understood why we read the parshiyos of Matos, Masei, and Devarim during the Shabbosos of "Bein Hametzarim," and in many years (like this year) also Parshas Pinchas, even though these parshiyos speak of matters related to *Geulah*, such as the topic of korbanos (in Parshas Pinchas), and the conquest, inheritance, and division of the Land (in the parshiyos of Matos, Masei, and Devarim)—because the true essence of the days of "Bein Hametzarim" is *l’ma’aliusa*.

Regarding the parsha of the week, Parshas Pinchas (which we read this year during the Shabbosos of Bein Hametzarim)—we read in it, as mentioned, the section of the korbanos: "Command the children of Israel and say to them, My offering, My bread for My fire, etc."[6]

***

**B.** Maamar beginning with the words "Command the children of Israel and say to them, My offering, My bread for My fire, etc."

***

**C.** In the aforementioned notes on Megillas Eichah, the Tzemach Tzedek explains the greatness of the fifteenth of Av, stating[7]:

"The matter of 15 Av... for on the 15th is the essence of the perfection of the moon ('the moon stands in its perfection'[8]), and 15 Av in particular has a higher level than the other 15ths of the month... the greater the descent below... through this is the greater ascent... because on Tisha B'Av is the essence of the descent of Malchus... therefore its ascent on 15 Av is higher, etc."

The lesson from this for a person's avodah is that even when one is in a state of descent [to the point that after engaging in avodah and entering for "yechidus," one is in a standing and state where "it did not touch and did not strike"...], one must not become overwhelmed or despair, Heaven forbid, from the descent. Rather, on the contrary, one must strengthen oneself further in avodah and aspire to reach a greater ascent that will come after and through the descent, as mentioned, that the greater the descent below, the greater the ascent will be through it.

This should be connected with the parsha of the week, Parshas Pinchas, in which it is told about the ascent that Pinchas attained through his mesiras nefesh—that even though there was a state of the greatest descent at that time (as told at the end of Parshas Balak), Pinchas was not overwhelmed by the magnitude of the descent, but on the contrary, he strengthened himself in his avodah through mesiras nefesh, and through this, a very great elevation was brought about for him: "Behold, I give to him My covenant of peace, etc."[10]

**D.** However, in this matter (overcoming the descent), one should not go in one's own ways ("mit aygeneh derech"), but one must come and *ask the Rebbe*, the Moshe Rabbeinu of the generation, and according to his instructions, one must strengthen oneself and aspire to the ascent that will come after and through the descent.

Furthermore:

Even when the Rebbe does not tell him explicitly what to do—whether because it is a matter that the Rebbe cannot instruct him on because it is a case of "one who comes to consult, we do not instruct,"[11] or because it is the Rebbe's desire that he arrive at this matter through his own strength—nevertheless, through *asking the Rebbe and dedicating oneself to him*, he will know and recognize ("vet er derheren") the Rebbe's opinion even in matters that the Rebbe does not tell him explicitly.

Similar to what we find regarding a pidyon nefesh—as is known among Chassidim that when one writes a pidyon and sends it to the Rebbe, the action is already accomplished even if the pidyon has not yet reached the Rebbe and consequently he has not seen it with physical eyes. The Chossid must do his part, dedicate himself to the Rebbe, and rely on him, and when he does his part and from his side there are no obstacles, then the matter is already accomplished by the Rebbe.

#### 238

And similarly in our case, when the Chossid asks the Rebbe, dedicates himself to him, and relies on him, so that from his side there are no obstacles—then he receives the "answer" of the Rebbe even when the Rebbe does not tell him explicitly.

**E.** We find an example of this in the conduct of Pinchas—that when "a halacha was hidden from him (from Moshe)," and Pinchas "remembered the halacha," "he said to him (Pinchas to Moshe) did you not teach me thus, etc." (in astonishment):[12]

Seemingly, since Moshe did not instruct him what to do, for "a halacha was hidden from him," and Pinchas's action was based on his own opinion (that he "remembered the halacha")—why did he need to go to Moshe and ask him "did you not teach me thus, etc."?

The explanation for this is that even at the time that "a halacha was hidden from him," this halacha (like all halachos) is taken *from the words of Moshe*, and therefore, even when Moshe does not say what to do—whether because in this matter the law is that "one who comes to consult, we do not instruct," or "so that Pinchas would come and take what is fitting for him"[13]—Pinchas goes and asks Moshe!

And an example of this in our case—that even when the Rebbe (the Moshe Rabbeinu of the generation) does not tell him what to do, one must ask the Rebbe, and through asking the Rebbe and dedicating oneself to him, one will align with the Rebbe's opinion even in matters that were not said explicitly.

*

**F.** What was said above, that at this time the ascent that comes after and through the descent is emphasized, also relates to the shlichus that the Rebbe placed upon the yeshiva students to dedicate of their time to engage in strengthening Yiddishkeit:

It was discussed at the farbrengen beforehand[14] regarding the yeshiva students—both the Rebbe's yeshiva students and the students of other yeshivos—that they must leave the yeshiva for a few weeks during the year and travel to the provincial cities (or even in the city of New York itself, outside the walls of the yeshiva) in order to engage there in strengthening Yiddishkeit.

And even though someone might argue that it is better to remain in the yeshiva and utilize even these few weeks for the study of Torah, and why should he travel from the yeshiva, at which point he will be forced to be idle from the study of Torah (relative to his study in the yeshiva), and not in every place will he be able to fulfill ("oysfiern") all the hiddurim, etc., so that leaving the yeshiva for a period of time is a *descent*—nevertheless, the truth is that precisely through this, a *greater elevation* will be added to the study of Torah throughout the entire year, as explained above at length.

And in the language of Chazal[15]—"Hashem did a kindness for Yisrael by scattering them among the nations":

The departure of the yeshiva students from outside the walls of the yeshiva is in the category of "scattering them among the nations," for any place that is outside the walls of the yeshiva is considered "among the nations" relative to the standing and state within the walls of the yeshiva.

And just as the matter of "scattering them among the nations" is a "kindness that Hashem did for Yisrael," through which they arrive at a greater elevation,[16] so too in our case, the departure from his four cubits outside the walls of the yeshiva in order to engage in strengthening Yiddishkeit is a "kindness" also for him, through which a greater elevation will be added to him in the study of Torah throughout the entire year.

**G.** However, in order to receive this elevation, it is necessary to go out and travel and fulfill the shlichus *in actual practice*, and not be satisfied with the thought that because he is a Chossid and is connected, he is *ready* to go with mesiras nefesh to fulfill the Rebbe's shlichus!...

—It is told[17] about the Maggid of Mezeritch, that he once met a childhood friend from the period before he was a student of the Baal Shem Tov, who even then would study (with his friend) Kabbalah, and pray according to the kavanos of the Arizal, and his friend asked him: What is the reason that you prolong your prayer for a long time? After all, I too—he explained his question—intend all the kavanos of the Arizal, and nevertheless, my prayer does not last so long, and why with you (the Maggid) does the prayer last so long?

The Maggid did not answer him on the spot, and began to inquire about what was happening with his friend, what he engages in, etc. And his friend told him that his main engagement—thank G-d—is in the study of Torah, and he earns a living from the store that his wife manages, except that once a year, when the "fair" takes place, his wife gives him a list of the merchandise needed for the store, and a bundle of money, to travel to the fair to buy the merchandise, and even when he travels to the fair—he continues to tell—he is not in a hurry (for when he is on the road, she has no control over him...), but he is careful to finish his fixed lessons every day and only

#### 240

then continues on his way, so that the trip to the fair lasts for him a few weeks, and then he returns to his home and continues to engage in Torah.

The Maggid asked him: I do not understand why you need to waste a few weeks for a trip to the fair—you can stay in your room and imagine in your mind the trip to the fair?! The road—is well known to you, since you travel there every year, and consequently, it is easy for you to imagine in your mind all the details of the trip: now I am at such-and-such station, and now at the next station, and now I am arriving at the fair, and I am holding the wallet with all the money in my hand, and now I am buying the merchandise, and checking that they did not cheat me... And thus, you could finish the whole business in a few short hours, and you would not need to waste a few weeks?!—His friend replied: But I need the *merchandise*!

When the Maggid heard his answer, he responded and said: "Azoy"?!—So it is also regarding prayer: when one needs the "merchandise"—one cannot be satisfied with the "kavanos" alone that one intends even in a short time, but one must come and be in every place, and for this, a great deal of time is necessary!...

And similarly regarding our matter:

He can sit in his four cubits *and think* about his connection to the Rebbe, and his readiness to go with mesiras nefesh to fulfill the Rebbe's shlichus, and for the perfection of the matter he will add *and imagine for himself* all the details of the trip: here he cannot obtain Chalav Yisrael, here they do not receive him with a friendly face, and here they mock the appearance of a yeshiva bochur with a beard and peyos, etc.—at which point he will finish the "trip" (in the imagination of the mind) in a very short time, half an hour or an hour—depending on the quality of the sense of imagination,

[And there are two ways in this: one whose sense of imagination is better—will do this in half an hour; or conversely, one whose sense of imagination is better—will deepen and drift in the imagination of the mind for a whole hour, and one whose sense of imagination is most developed ("er hot gor a gutn chush ha-tziyur")—will deepen and drift in the imagination of the mind until he faints...],[18]

But, in order to obtain the "merchandise"—one must *travel* and fulfill the shlichus *in actual practice*!

One must travel, therefore, and fulfill the shlichus in actual practice, and it will not help

#### 241

anyone to argue ("zich ois-taneh'n") with Rabbi Hodakov[19]... or with himself, that because of various reasons it is not in his power to travel, for, from all the arguments of various kinds, he will not obtain the "merchandise"; in order to obtain the "merchandise"—it is necessary to travel in actual practice, and to engage in strengthening Yiddishkeit, to awaken Jews regarding the fulfillment of Torah and Mitzvos.

And to add, that the obligation to engage in strengthening Yiddishkeit is placed not only on yeshiva students and bnei Torah, but also on businessmen (as discussed at the farbrengen beforehand[20])—yeshiva students according to their matter, and businessmen according to their matter; and through their engagement in strengthening Yiddishkeit to influence others, a greater elevation will be added to them—yeshiva students according to their matter, and businessmen according to their matter.

*

**H.** Two Jews visited me this week, and raised a suggestion: since the date of the elections in Eretz Yisrael is approaching,[21] one should announce the recitation of Tehillim so that the elections will be in a good way ("es zol geyn gut").

—Reciting Tehillim is certainly a good thing at all times, and especially in such a matter (the elections in Eretz Yisrael), but, there is nothing to fear ("nito vos tzu shreken zich") from the elections. One must know and remember the statement of Chazal (mentioned above) "Hashem did a kindness for Yisrael *by scattering them among the nations*," and consequently, when the avodah in "scattering them among the nations" is as it should be, all matters will be as they should be, in a way that "*kindness* Hashem did for Yisrael."

One must know and remember that the "key" is found *with us*, and also the keys of all matters—"the key of life and of rain and of the resurrection of the dead"[22]—are found *here* (as discussed above at length[23]), and consequently, there is nothing to be overwhelmed by from all the matters, and the matter depends only on us.[24]

## Sicha of 20 Menachem-Av, 5711

#### 242

**A.** Generally, the established order (for a Yahrtzeit) is to first conduct a "Siyum" and afterwards say "L’chaim." However, since there are always "innovations" here, we will say "L’chaim" first, sing a nigun, and afterwards the "Siyum" will be conducted [1353], and following that, we will say "L’chaim" once more.

**B.** (After saying L’chaim and singing a nigun, the Rebbe said:)

The conclusion of Masechta Taanis (in the Mishnayos) is with the verse [1354], "On the day of his wedding and on the day of the gladness of his heart." The Mishnah explains: "On the day of his wedding—this is the Giving of the Torah (Yom Kippur, on which the second Tablets were given [1355]); and on the day of the gladness of his heart—this is the building of the Beis Hamikdash, which will be built speedily in our days."

By way of introduction: We now stand *after* the sad days (the Three Weeks) have already passed, which are the *opposite* of "the day of his wedding" and "the day of the gladness of his heart": the Seventeenth of Tammuz, on which "the Tablets were broken [1356]"—the *opposite* of "the day of his wedding, this is the Giving of the Torah"; and Tisha B'Av, on which "the First and Second Temples were destroyed [1356]"—the *opposite* of "the day of the gladness of his heart, this is the building of the Beis Hamikdash."

*After* these days pass, the joy is at its greatest, as is explicit in the Mishnah: "There were no better days for Israel *than the Fifteenth of Av* and Yom Kippur."

**C.** The truth is that the joy begins already *on Tisha B'Av itself*—after midday—on which the redeemer of Israel, the savior of Israel, was born [1357]. Therefore, it is customary to say "Nachem" in the Mincha prayer of Tisha B'Av [1358]. However, the perfection and revelation of the joy is on the Fifteenth of Av.

This is similar to what we find regarding the reason for the holiday of the 15th of Av, "that the dying of the desert generation ceased"—that in truth, the decree had already ceased on Tisha B'Av, but they were in doubt, "perhaps they erred in the month, until they saw the full moon, and then they *knew* that the decree had ceased [1359]," that the desert generation had already died out, and those who remained "were all whole and standing to enter the Land [1360]."

From this it is understood that on the 15th of Av it is *clarified* that all the decrees and all the undesirable matters have already ended, and the time has arrived to leave the "desert of the nations [1361]" and enter Eretz Yisrael, in the true and complete Geulah.

This can be further sweetened according to what is explained in the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes to Megillas Eichah [1362]: "On the 15th is the essential perfection of the moon, and the 15th of Av in particular has a higher level than other 15ths of the month... the more the descent is below... through this the ascent is higher... and therefore, similarly, because on Tisha B'Av is the essential descent of the Malchus, the face of the moon, etc., therefore its ascent on the 15th of Av is higher, etc." In other words: The virtue of the fifteenth day of the month is that the moon becomes full, and in this is hinted the perfection of Israel, who are compared to the moon [1363]. And there is a special virtue in the fullness of the moon (the perfection of Israel) in the month of Av—because it follows the greatest descent on Tisha B'Av, at which time the ascent is also the greatest; therefore, a special joy is created on the 15th of Av [1364].

**D.** And it should be added that "(on the day of his wedding, etc., and) on the day of the gladness of his heart, this is the building of the Beis Hamikdash which will be built speedily in our days," will be a *greater virtue* than how it was *before* "the First and Second Temples were destroyed"—because now all the matters of destruction and exile have already ended, and a complete Geulah is created *after which there is no exile* [1365].

The point of this is:

The difference between a complete Geulah after which there is no exile, and a Geulah after which there is exile, is not only at the *end* of the matter, at the end of time—meaning, that the deficiency in a Geulah after which there is exile is only that *after a time* another exile occurs, and the virtue of the future Geulah is that even at the end of all time there will be no more exile—rather, the difference exists already *at the beginning of the Geulah*. Meaning, that a Geulah after which there is exile is not a complete Geulah *from its inception*, and the virtue of the future Geulah is that *from its inception* it is a complete Geulah ("From the very beginning, the standing is already different").

Proof of this is from the verse [1366] (which is cited in Chassidus [1367]): "For this city has been to Me a cause of My anger and My fury *from the day that they built it*... to remove it from before My face." The explanation of this is that the cause of the destruction of this city is because its initial construction was not in perfection; had its initial construction been in perfection, it would never have been destroyed.

And similarly in our case: "In the First and Second Temples"—since *in the final analysis* (after four hundred and ten years, or after four hundred and twenty years [1368]) there was destruction and exile, it is proven *that from the outset* the entry into the Land (both in the first entry and the second entry) and the building of the Beis Hamikdash (both the First and Second Temples) were not *as they ought to have been*.

And this is the virtue of the future Geulah and the building of the future Beis Hamikdash ("on the day of the gladness of his heart, this is the building of the Beis Hamikdash which will be built speedily in our days")—a very great ascent (following a very great descent) whose beginning is on the Fifteenth of Av—that we are preparing for a Geulah that prevents and negates from the outset the possibility, and even the thought, of a state of destruction and exile, because the beginning ("the first standing") is in a manner that "I will remove the spirit of impurity from the land [1369]," and consequently, there is no land that could begin to sprout such a thing from which, in the final analysis, something not good would emerge.

**E.** Now [1370], the conclusion of the Mishnah, "on the day of his wedding and on the day of the gladness of his heart," comes in continuation of the beginning of the matter—"There were no better days for Israel than the Fifteenth of Av and Yom Kippur, on which the daughters of Jerusalem (Israel [1371]) would go out... and dance in the vineyards, and what would they say, 'Young man, lift up your eyes and see what you choose for yourself, etc.'"—that the purpose of the matter is the concept of matches and unions.

By way of introduction—that the entire concept of a match among Bnei Yisrael below is drawn down from the concept of the match above, between Hashem and Knesses Yisrael [1372].

—And to note what is explained in the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes to Eichah [1373] regarding the interpretation of "Lift up your eyes": "Similar to the time when Israel looks upward... and similarly here too, that he should not look at the physical desire in the woman, but rather at the root of the matter, the higher union and the drawing down of Elokus, etc.," and then, he will aim ("he will hit the mark") for the appropriate match (as they announced above: "The daughter of so-and-so to so-and-so" [1374]) without distractions from external things, which do not occupy a place for him, because he looks at the essence and root of the matter as it is above—

From this it is understood that the reason why the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur are a time of matches below is because they are a time of matches above, between Hashem and Knesses Yisrael, from which it was drawn down also below that these times are auspicious for matches.

The explanation of this is:

Yom Kippur, "in which there is forgiveness and pardon"—because it is after the descent of the sin of the Golden Calf, after which a greater ascent is created, the concept of the *marriage* of Hashem and Knesses Yisrael is renewed in it, in a manner more exalted than in the first Tablets—"the day of his wedding," "on which the second Tablets were given."

And the Fifteenth of Av—is after the descent of Tisha B'Av, on which there was the concept of *divorce*, as it is in the Midrash [1375] (and explained at length in the Maamar that was just printed [1376]) that the concept of destruction and exile is like the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, in which Adam HaRishon was judged with divorce, "I judged him with divorce... and I lamented over him 'Eichah,' as it is said [1377], 'And He said to him, Eichah'—'Eichah' is written (when it should have been written 'Aich' with a Kamatz without a Hey)... so too his children... I judged them *with divorce*... and I lamented over them 'Eichah,' 'Eichah [1378] sits solitary'"—similar to a bill of divorce, the opposite of the concept of marriage. And when the Fifteenth of Av arrives, on which the greatest ascent is created according to the measure of the greatest descent of Tisha B'Av (as mentioned in section 3)—the concept of the *marriage* of Knesses Yisrael and Hashem is created.

**F.** And it is explained in the Mishnah that for the sake of the matches, "the daughters of Israel would go out in borrowed white garments":

Since it is speaking about the match and the connection of Knesses Yisrael to Hashem after the soul descends *below*, to this physical and material world, in which it must fulfill the mission of Hashem, therefore, in its descent below, they give it from above "garments"—"borrowed white garments [1379]": "(garments of) *white*"—is an essential color, and its concept in avodah is a simple will, not complex in Chochma and intellect; and its drawing down into internal powers, in Chabad, etc.—in which the avodah must specifically be—is in a manner of "borrowing" ("white garments *borrowed*"), that this is not from their own selves, but rather, that it is drawn down to them by way of *borrowing* from a level *above* them, the level of Yechidah [1380].

From this it was drawn down also regarding the concept of matches in their literal sense—that in order to bring closer and hasten the completion of the match for the best, the daughters of Israel would wear special garments, beautiful garments—"*white garments*," and so as not to shame those who do not have, they enacted that the daughters of Israel should *borrow* garments from one another—"borrowed *white garments*."

**G.** And the details of the order of borrowing white garments are explained in the Gemara at the conclusion of the Masechta:

"The Sages taught: The daughter of a king borrows from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol, the daughter of a Kohen Gadol from the daughter of a Sagan, the daughter of a Sagan from the daughter of a Kohen Mashiach Milchamah, and the daughter of a Kohen Mashiach Milchamah from the daughter of a common Kohen." In other words, not only the "daughter of a king," who must borrow from one below her because there is none above her (since "a king precedes a Kohen Gadol" [1381]), but even the daughter of a Kohen Gadol, who has the choice to borrow from one below her ("the daughter of a Sagan") or from one above her ("the daughter of a king")—she borrows from the one *below* her specifically: "The daughter of a Kohen Gadol from the daughter of a Sagan," and similarly "the daughter of a Sagan from the daughter of a Kohen Mashiach Milchamah, and the daughter of a Kohen Mashiach Milchamah from the daughter of a common Kohen," that each one borrows from the one *below* her.

But at the conclusion of Masechta Taanis in the *Yerushalmi*—we learned in a different way: Regarding the "daughter of a king" who has none above her—"The daughter of a king borrows from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol" (as in the Bavli), but regarding the "daughter of a Kohen Gadol" who has the choice to borrow from one below her or from one above her—it is in the Yerushalmi that she borrows from the one *above* her: "The daughter of a Kohen Gadol borrows from the daughter of a king." And from this it is understood also regarding the daughter of a Sagan who borrows from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol, and so on, that each one borrows from the one *above* her [1382].

By way of introduction, although this matter is in the *Aggadah* portion of the Torah (like many matters in Masechta Taanis and especially at its conclusion), and in general people are accustomed to think that in the Aggadah portion of the Torah one should not debate with logical arguments, etc., because it pertains more to the inner dimension of the Torah, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe wrote [1383] regarding the study of the Aggadah in "Ein Yaakov," that "most of the secrets of the Torah are hidden within it"—the truth is that also in the Aggadah portion of the Torah there are *many logical arguments* that can be used (not only in the inner dimension of the Torah, but) also *in the revealed* Torah, and even regarding matters that touch upon the Halachic portion of the Torah [1384].

From this it is understood also in our case—that there is certainly in this matter [the order of borrowing white garments, from one below her or from one above her] a logic for here and a logic for the opposite, and there is a reason and logic for why the opinion of the Bavli is in one way and the opinion of the Yerushalmi is in the opposite way, as follows.

**H.** Explanation of the matter:

Since the (borrowing and) wearing of the "white garments" is in order to *adorn oneself* in garments, for the benefit of the match, "Young man, lift up your eyes and see, etc." (that by way of nature, beauty leads to marriage)—it is more logical that each one should borrow from the one *above* her [1385], so that she will receive more beautiful garments, and consequently be more beautiful, for the benefit of the match.

However, since the enactment that they should "go out in borrowed white garments" is in order "*not to shame* those who do not have," then, in order to negate the shame that is in the borrowing itself—that the borrower is ashamed before the lender that she needs to borrow from her and receive from her without giving her anything—it is more logical that each one should borrow from the one *below* her.

By way of introduction—that we find in the laws of Kiddushin that although generally the man who is betrothing must *give* to the woman being betrothed, nevertheless, an "important person" (who is not accustomed to receiving gifts) can betroth a woman by *receiving* from her, "because of the pleasure that she receives a gift from him (the pleasure that has the value of a Prutah), she decides and acquires herself to him" [1386], meaning, that for an important person, *receiving* (from one below him) is considered *giving*—the giving of the *pleasure* that an important person agrees and is willing to receive a certain thing from one below him.

And similarly in our case: when the daughter of a king borrows from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol (who is below her)—the very fact that the daughter of a king agrees to receive and wear the garment she received from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol causes *pleasure and honor* to the daughter of a Kohen Gadol, such that the receiving of the daughter of a king (from one below her) is also considered *giving* (the giving of pleasure and honor). And similarly for each one who borrows from one below her—that the receiving of the borrower from the lender is also *giving* to the lender, that she gives her the pleasure and honor that she agrees and is willing to receive from her.

From this it is understood that there is a virtue in borrowing from one *below* her compared to borrowing from one above her—that in borrowing from one above her, the borrower is *only receiving* from the one above her, and is not giving her anything, and consequently *is ashamed* by the borrowing; whereas in borrowing from one *below* her, the borrower is not only receiving, but also *giving* [1387]—the pleasure and honor that she agrees and is willing to receive from one below her, and consequently *there is no shame* in the borrowing, because each of them is *also receiving and also giving*: the borrower—receives garments and gives pleasure and honor, and the lender—receives pleasure and honor, and gives garments.

And based on this, it is possible to explain the logic of the Bavli and the Yerushalmi: the logic of the Bavli, that each one borrows from the one below her—so that there should be no shame in the borrowing; and the logic of the Yerushalmi, that each one borrows from the one above her—even though in such a manner there will be shame in the borrowing—so that she will wear more beautiful garments, for the benefit of the match.

**I.** And it is necessary to explain the reason for the dispute between the Bavli and the Yerushalmi—what is the reason that the opinion of the Yerushalmi is that the benefit in the match outweighs the deficiency of the shame in the borrowing, and the opinion of the Bavli is that the deficiency of the shame in the borrowing outweighs the benefit in the match:

In borrowing from one above her—the deficiency of the shame (that she is only receiving and not giving) is for a short time, for the moment only, whereas the benefit in the match (through which she receives and wears more beautiful garments) is for a long time, because through the match the marriage is created, which is an eternal matter, "a building that lasts forever"; but on the other hand, the slight deficiency (shame for a short time) is *immediate* (at the time of borrowing), whereas the great benefit (the match and marriage for a long and eternal time) is *after a time* (when the match is completed which will lead to marriage).

And in such a case a question is asked—is there an obligation to burden oneself even with a slight matter now, for a great benefit that will come after a time, as in our case, that she will have to suffer now the shame and unpleasantness in borrowing from one above her, for the benefit of the match and marriage after a time [1388].

And in this we find a difference between the Bavli and the Yerushalmi in several laws—that the opinion of the Bavli is that since the benefit is only after a time, there is no obligation to burden oneself now, and the opinion of the Yerushalmi is that since the benefit is great, even though it is after a time, there is already an obligation from now to burden oneself with a slight matter.

**J.** And among the examples of this [1389]:

At the end of the book Yam Shel Shlomo by the Maharshal, he brings all the differences in law between the people of Eretz Yisrael and the people of Bavel, and the first difference is regarding Krias Shema: "The people of Eretz Yisrael stand during Krias Shema, the people of Bavel sit, this is the reason, 'when you sit in your house.'"

And the explanation for the conduct of the people of Eretz Yisrael that they stand during Krias Shema—although the Halacha is according to Beis Hillel that "every person recites in his own way (either standing or lying or sitting or walking) as it is said [1390], 'and when you walk on the way' [1391]," "they stand and recite, sit and recite, recline and recite, walk on the way and recite [1392]"—is because they are stringent upon themselves in Krias Shema like in prayer, which must be in a standing position, so that through this there will be an addition in the intention of the heart, even though the Torah did not obligate to exert oneself and stand in Krias Shema, but only in prayer.

And since the exertion in standing in Krias Shema is for a moment only (at the moment one stands), but this exertion is immediate (before Krias Shema), whereas the benefit in the intention of the heart is for a duration of time (the entire duration of Krias Shema), but this benefit is after a time (after one stands and begins Krias Shema)—it is found that the people of Eretz Yisrael (the opinion of the Yerushalmi) obligate to exert oneself now a little for a great benefit after a time, whereas the people of Bavel (the opinion of the Bavli) do not obligate to exert oneself now for a benefit that will come after a time.

And another difference between the people of Eretz Yisrael and the people of Bavel—which the Maharshal brings—that "the people of Eretz Yisrael bathe from impurity even on Yom Kippur, for they expound that those who have experienced a seminal emission bathe privately on Yom Kippur as is their custom, and the people of Bavel do not bathe, etc., for they expound that we are in an impure land."

In other words: this bathing, since it is not for the sake of pleasure but because of the impurity, is not included in the prohibition of bathing on Yom Kippur [1393], but nevertheless, since Yom Kippur is forbidden in bathing, it is impossible to force him to exert himself to bathe because of impurity, rather the matter depends on his will.

And since the exertion in bathing is for a short time, for the duration of a Tevilah, but this exertion is immediate (at the beginning of the day), whereas the benefit in the matter is for a long time, for the duration of all the prayers throughout the day, but the benefit is after a time (after the Tevilah, when the time of prayers arrives)—it is found that the people of Eretz Yisrael (the opinion of the Yerushalmi) obligate to exert oneself now a little for a great benefit after a time, whereas the people of Bavel (the opinion of the Bavli) do not obligate to exert oneself now for a benefit that will come after a time.

And similarly, another example was brought there regarding marriage [1394]—that also in this we see the aforementioned difference, that the people of Eretz Yisrael take upon themselves a not-good thing, a burdensome thing, for a short time, so that afterwards there will be a benefit for a prolonged time, whereas the people of Bavel do not.

And they follow their opinion also at the conclusion of Masechta Taanis regarding the borrowing of white garments: according to the opinion of the Yerushalmi that one should burden oneself with a slight matter so that afterwards there will be a benefit for a long time—each one borrows from the one above her, even though she will be ashamed in the borrowing, because the burden that is from the shame is for a short time, and the benefit in the match is for a long time; and according to the opinion of the Bavli that one should not burden oneself now (even with a slight matter) for a benefit (even a great one) that will come after a time—she should not be ashamed in borrowing from one above her, even though the shame is for a short time, and the benefit is for a long time (and therefore she borrows from the one below her, at which time there is no shame in the borrowing, because the borrower is not only receiving but also giving, as mentioned in section 8).

**K.** And it is necessary to explain the *reason and explanation* for the dispute between the Yerushalmi and the Bavli—according to what is explained in Chassidus [1395] regarding the general difference between the Talmud Yerushalmi and the Talmud Bavli:

In order to obligate a burden in a slight matter, for a short time, for a great benefit, for a long time—one must know *clearly and with certainty* that the burden is indeed in a slight matter, and for a short time only, and the benefit is indeed a great benefit, and for a long time, and then one can *weigh* that the great benefit for a long time *outweighs* the slight burden for a short time.

And therefore: in the Talmud Yerushalmi, whose manner of study is by way of *direct light*, without the obscurities and concealments that are in the multitude of questions and debates, in the manner of "I saw a *clear* world" [1396]—one can know *clearly and with certainty* that this matter is for a short time and this matter is for a long time [not only in the sense of time in its literal sense ("on the clock"), but also and primarily from the content of the matters with which one "fills" the time], this matter is a slight thing and this matter has in it a great benefit, and consequently one can be sure *that it is worth* the burden in the slight thing for a short time (a few moments) for the great benefit for a long time (throughout days and good years);
