Whereas in the Talmud Bavli, "He has made me dwell in *darkness*, this is the Talmud of Bavel" [1397], whose manner of study is by way of clarifying the obscurities and concealments of questions and answers (reflected light), in the manner of "I saw an *inverted* world" [1396]—it is impossible to know and determine clearly and with certainty the value and relation of the matters to one another (for it is possible that even a matter that is in a short time exceeds in its value and importance another matter that is in a long time), and consequently, when a slight matter for a short time is on the agenda now, it is impossible to postpone it because of the consideration of a great benefit for a long time that will come after a time.

**L.** And this matter touches upon the avodah in practice:

Since we are currently in a time of exile, in a standing and state of double and redoubled darkness—we cannot always rely on the calculation and estimation of the magnitude of the value of matters, to compare and weigh which matter will bring a great benefit and which matter will bring a small benefit (according to value), and to determine based on this which matter to do first and which matter to do afterwards, which matter is worth doing and which matter is not worth doing, and the like; therefore, one must engage in every matter that comes to hand, and not make a calculation that it is worth it to forgo a slight matter for the sake of a benefit in a grave matter, for it is possible that this matter which appears to him as a "slightest of the slight" mitzvah is in truth—from the perspective of many matters—like the "gravest of the grave" mitzvah.

And as the Rebbe (Rashab) wrote in one of his letters (which is printed in the introduction to Kuntres U'Maayan [1398]): "Since now is the time of the final clarifications of the footsteps of Moshiach... there is now no order and gradation in the manners of the clarifications and the rectifications... and therefore... we cannot and also are not permitted... to clarify what is near or far according to our intellect... but rather what we find that needs rectification we must exert ourselves with tremendous powers, etc."

**M.** And here [1399], the conclusion of the Mishnah "on the day of his wedding and on the day of the gladness of his heart" comes in continuation of the beginning of the matter—"There were no better days for Israel than the Fifteenth of Av and Yom Kippur, on which the daughters of Jerusalem (Israel [1400]) would go out... and dance in the vineyards, and what would they say, 'Young man, lift up your eyes and see what you choose for yourself, etc.'"—that the purpose of the matter is the concept of matches and unions.

After it was explained (in the Bavli) the manner of borrowing white garments, that "the daughter of a king borrows from the daughter of a Kohen Gadol, the daughter of a Kohen Gadol from the daughter of a Sagan, etc.," meaning, that each one borrows from the one *below* her, in order to negate the shame in the borrowing itself, even though the shame is for a short time and through it a benefit will come in the match for a long time, because in the standing and state of "He has made me dwell in *darkness*" it is impossible to know and determine clearly and with certainty the value and relation of the matters to one another (as explained at length above)—it is necessary to clarify and add that all this is only when we are in an "inverted world," in the darkness of exile; whereas *in the time of the Geulah*, when the prophecy will be fulfilled "The sun shall no longer be your light by day, etc., but Hashem shall be your eternal light" [1401], then all matters will be *revealed and clear* (and consequently they will be able to compare and weigh every thing and matter according to its truth).

And this is the content of the conclusion—specifically in the Bavli—"In the future, Hashem will make a circle for the righteous, etc., and each and every one will point with his finger, etc.":

The innovation of the future to come—that for each and every one, in his standing and state, all matters will be in a *clear* manner, to such an extent, that even in matters of Elokus there will be *a vision of the essence*, that "he points with his finger" and says "Behold, this is our G-d, etc., this is Hashem, etc." [1402], a vision of Elokus in the ultimate clarity and verification in a manner that no doubt is possible in the matter.

[And it can be said that the revelation of the future ("each and every one points with his finger" and says "Behold, this is our G-d, etc.") is created specifically through the avodah of clarification from the darkness [1403]—which is the manner of avodah in the time of exile, in the standing and state of concealment, at which time there must be the engagement in the bringing closer and matching of Knesses Yisrael to Hashem, through this, that the daughters of Israel go out in borrowed white garments, etc.].

And from this it will be drawn down also below—as hinted in the continuation of the verse "This is Hashem *for whom we hoped*," as explained in Chassidus [1404] that "kivinu" (we hoped) is from the word *kav* (line), which descends and is drawn down below, and even below ten tefachim—that all matters entirely, even physical matters, will be in a manner of clarification, a "clear world."

And then there will be a very great joy—as the conclusion and seal of the verse: "We will rejoice and be glad in His salvation," in the complete and true Geulah, speedily in our days, Amen.

***

**N.** The conclusion of Masechta Taanis is connected specifically with the *Twentieth of Av* (and for this reason I chose to conduct the Siyum on Masechta Taanis specifically)—because the only place in Shas that I found (at present) in which the date Twentieth of Av is mentioned, is at the conclusion of Masechta Taanis in the Mishnah [1405]: "The time for the wood of the Kohanim and the people is nine (on these nine times the Kohanim and the people would volunteer to bring wood and they would offer a sacrifice)... on the Fifth of Av... on the Fifteenth of it... *on the Twentieth of it* the descendants of Pachat Moav son of Yehudah," and in the Gemara there [1406]: "The Tanna taught, the descendants of Pachat Moav son of Yehudah are the descendants of David son of Yehudah, the words of Rabbi Meir; Rabbi Yosi says they are the descendants of Yoav son of Tzeruyah."

[Explained at length was the special virtue in the wood offering of the Twentieth of Av, because it is after the 15th of Av, "the day of the breaking of the sickle," when they would not cut new wood, and nevertheless they volunteered their wood for the sake of the sacrifices of other Jews, including also those who had committed transgressions, etc., and they did so out of joy and a holiday. And the content of the dispute between R. Meir and R. Yosi [1407], whether this great virtue came to them by merit of their being descendants of David (self-nullification and self-sacrifice in the study of Torah), or by merit of their being descendants of Yoav (self-nullification and self-sacrifice in the clarification of the world)—was edited by the Rebbe, and printed in Likkutei Sichos Vol. 4, page 1103 and onwards [1408].

And at the conclusion of the matter—in continuation of the instruction regarding the conduct in Ahavas Yisrael, that when one has a good thing that he cannot obtain another like it, he must be prepared to give it for the sake of the other, even one who is on a lower level, and to do so out of joy—the Rebbe said:]

And this matter the Rebbe demanded from each one of us, and demands also now, and will continue to demand also in the future.

—The Rebbe did not "get tired"... he had dealings with many who were "stiff-necked," and when he would speak to them once, twice, and three times, it would not help, and nevertheless, he would return and speak a fourth time, and in the final analysis he would accomplish his goal ("he would carry out his own").

And like the well-known parable regarding learning an instruction in holiness from everything—that even from a "thief" one can learn several things, and among them, that even if he did not succeed the first time, he returns many times [1409].

Also the conduct of the Rebbe was in this order: even when he would speak once, twice, and three times, and the listener would not want to obey, and not only that, but sometimes he would kick ("he would sometimes give a kick")...—he would continue and speak so many times until he would accomplish his goal.

And in this order the Rebbe conducts himself also now!...

One must know, therefore, that in this matter is expressed *the primary demand* of the Rebbe—that even when it is speaking about a Jew who has a "taste" in the avodah of bringing a sacrifice on the altar, and he has in his hand a thing worthy for the altar, a most exalted thing that it seems to him that besides him no one has such a thing, and if he gives it to the other, he does not know from where he will be able to obtain another like it—it is required of him a feeling of *self-sacrifice* to be prepared to give it for the sake of the other, and not only that, but to go and search and inquire perhaps there is in a remote corner a Jew whom one can help and assist to become closer to Elokus—which is the concept of the sacrifice, from the word *kiruv* (bringing closer), bringing closer the powers and the senses [1410] to Elokus, to Yiddishkeit, to Torah and its Mitzvos—

## B’s”D. Shabbos Parshas Eikev, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 5711

#### 276

(Unedited transcript)

**“And it shall come to pass, because (eikev) you hearken to these ordinances, and keep and perform them, that Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness that He swore to your forefathers…”**[1](#_ftn1506) We must understand the content of these three matters: the covenant, the kindness, and the oath. According to the simple interpretation of the verse, this is a matter of a condition: if you hearken to the ordinances, then He will keep the covenant and the kindness that He swore. However, we must understand[2](#_ftn1507) that these matters are not dependent upon a condition at all. The concept of a covenant[3](#_ftn1508) is like two lovers who forge a covenant between them; even if something should arise to separate them or interrupt the love (for example, if one of them behaves improperly), it does not diminish their love in the slightest. Thus, the matter of a covenant is not dependent on a condition at all. Similarly, the matter of an oath is not conditional. Just as with the oath we take to fulfill the mitzvos[4](#_ftn1509)—even if there are obstacles and hindrances to fulfilling the mitzvos, the oath is precisely that one should not be affected by anything and should fulfill the mitzvah[5](#_ftn1510). It is the same regarding the oath from Above,[6](#_ftn1511) as it is written, “By Myself I have sworn,”[7](#_ftn1512) “which You swore to our forefathers from days of old.”[8](#_ftn1513) The meaning is that regardless of the standing and state of Bnei Yisrael, Hashem, as it were, compels Himself to fulfill His oath. Likewise, the matter of kindness is not dependent on a condition, for the nature of kindness is to bestow upon everyone—not only upon the worthy, but also upon the unworthy.[9](#_ftn1514) Furthermore, as is known, there is a distinction between the *midos* of Chesed, Gevurah, and Rachamim. The nature of Gevurah is to be exacting with everyone, even the worthy, etc. The nature of Rachamim is that even if one is unworthy, He has mercy and bestows upon him; nevertheless, the distinction between the worthy and the unworthy is still evident. Not so the matter of

#### 277

Chesed, which bestows upon all and does not distinguish at all between the worthy and the unworthy. Since these matters are not dependent on a condition, what is the meaning of the verse, “And it shall come to pass, *because* (eikev) you hearken to these ordinances,” implying that only then will He keep the covenant and the kindness? We must also understand[2](#_ftn1507) the precision of the language, “And it shall come to pass, *eikev* (because/heel) you hearken.” Since this is a matter of a condition, the language “if” would be more appropriate: “And it shall come to pass *if* you hearken,” similar to the verse,[10](#_ftn1515) “And it shall come to pass, *if* you will hearken.” Why does it say *eikev*? Rashi explains (based on the Midrash Tanchuma[11](#_ftn1516)) that this refers to the mitzvos that a person tramples with his heels (*eikev*). But according to this, it is difficult to understand why it says “these *ordinances* (mishpatim),” specifically ordinances.[12](#_ftn1517) It is known that there are three categories of mitzvos:[13](#_ftn1518) *eidus* (testimonies), *chukim* (statutes), and *mishpatim* (ordinances). *Mishpatim* are mitzvos that the intellect mandates. *Eidus* are mitzvos that have a place (at least) in the intellect—meaning, even if one would not fulfill them on his own, there is a basis to fulfill them due to the testimony they contain, such as mitzvos that are a remembrance of the exodus from Egypt. *Chukim* are mitzvos regarding which the nations of the world taunt Israel, saying, “What is this mitzvah?”[14](#_ftn1519) as they have no place in the intellect, and one says, “It is a statute I have enacted, a decree I have issued,” etc.[15](#_ftn1520) If so, when the verse mentions mitzvos that a person tramples with his heels—those he is not careful about—it should have said *chukim* or at least *eidus*. Why did it specify *mishpatim*?

b) **To understand** all this, we must first preface[16](#_ftn1521) the explanation of the statement in the Zohar:[17](#_ftn1522) “Three bonds are bound one to another: Yisrael to the Torah, the Torah to the Holy One, blessed be He, and all are levels upon levels, hidden and revealed.” This means that this connection is not only in the *satim* (hidden) aspect of Yisrael—the lofty powers of the soul—but also in the *galya* (revealed) aspect of Yisrael—the revealed powers. And this applies not only to the *nefesh elokis* (divine soul), but through it, the revealed powers of the *nefesh habehamis* (animal soul) are also bound to the Torah and the Holy One, blessed be He. The matter is as follows:[19](#_ftn1524) the term “connection” (*hiskashrus*) is only applicable to two things that are separate from one another. Conversely, regarding one thing, the term “connection” is not applicable, only the term *dveikus* (cleaving). For example, light and the luminary: the light

#### 278

is not a different thing from the luminary, but merely a revelation of the essence; therefore, *hiskashrus* does not apply to it, only *dveikus*, for it is cleaved and unified with the essence. Now, the soul Above is in a state of *dveikus* with Elokus, as is precise in the language of the Tanya[20](#_ftn1525) that even a *tzaddik gamur* who serves Hashem with fear and great love in *taanugim* will not reach the level of his *dveikus* in Hashem with *dchilu* and *rchimu* before his descent into this world, etc. Only when the soul comes below and becomes a *metzius* (an entity) does the term *hiskashrus* apply to it. That is, when the soul is in a state of “it is pure,”[21](#_ftn1526) it is in a state of *dveikus* with Elokus. But as it is in the state of “You created it, You formed it, You breathed it into me, and You preserve it within me,” where it is in the state of *yesh* and a *metzius* of a thing, then its connection with Elokus is in the state of *hiskashrus*. And this is the meaning of “Three bonds are bound one to another,” etc.

**However,** there is still a greater advantage in the *hiskashrus* below than in the *dveikus* Above, for it is precisely through the *hiskashrus* below that one arrives at a higher level. The matter is as follows: it is written,[22](#_ftn1527) “I am black and comely, O daughters of Yerushalayim.” “Daughters of Yerushalayim” refers[23](#_ftn1528) to the soul Above, which is called by the name “daughters of Yerushalayim” because they are in a state of perfection of fear (which is the concept of Yerushalayim, from *yirah shalem*—perfect fear[24](#_ftn1529)). As mentioned above from the Tanya, even a *tzaddik gamur* who serves Hashem with fear and great love in *taanugim* will not reach the level of his *dveikus* in Hashem with *dchilu* and *rchimu* before his descent into this world, etc.—meaning, only while they are Above are they in a state of perfection of fear, and for this reason they are called “daughters of Yerushalayim.” More specifically, “daughters of Yerushalayim” refers to the souls as they are in the state of *Malchus* of *Atzilus*.[25](#_ftn1530) For above the *sefirah* of *Malchus*, the matter of *ahavah* and *yirah* does not apply, as there is no “one who loves” and “one who fears.” Only in the state of *Malchus*, which is the state of revelation in *Atzilus*—the state of *yesh* that is emanated—does the matter of *yirah* apply. And this is what is meant by “I am black and comely, O daughters of Yerushalayim”: the soul below says to the souls Above (which are called daughters of Yerushalayim), “I am black”—in a state of blackness and concealment of light, because it is in a state of separation (*apgerissen*) from the essence and being of the *Ein Sof* B.H., and also in a state of separation from the daughters of Yerushalayim, as it is not in a state of perfection of fear. For even if one is a *tzaddik gamur*, etc., he will not reach the level of his *dveikus* in Hashem with *dchilu* and *rchimu*, etc., which the body cannot endure, etc. And since the soul is found and exists within the body, it is understood that it is far from the state of

#### 279

perfection of fear. Furthermore, it is found in a “dry and weary land without water,”[26](#_ftn1531) for one can, G-d forbid, transgress both a positive commandment and a negative commandment. Yet, despite this (“I am black”), it is “comely” (*naveh*), for precisely by being below it is in a state of the ultimate beauty and comeliness. Because, precisely due to the concealments and hiddenness that exist below, the soul is aroused with a thirst for Elokus and love like fiery coals, which is the ultimate beauty of love (unlike when it is Above, where there are no concealments and hiddenness, and it is not in a state of thirst for Elokus). Therefore, it is in the ultimate beauty (*naveh*).

c) **However,** we must understand: seemingly, the advantage gained by the soul in its descent below—that due to the concealments and hiddenness it is aroused with thirst and love like fiery coals—applies only to the matter of love. But the matter of *yirah* is in a more elevated state when the soul is Above. For the matter of *yirah* comes from the recognition and feeling of greatness, and precisely through this one is aroused to *yirah*. This matter exists precisely when the soul is Above, for since there are revelations there, the greatness of Elokus is felt, and through this *yirah* is created. This is not the case when the soul is below, where there are no revelations, etc. Furthermore, in love, the matter of understanding and comprehension alone is sufficient; when one understands and comprehends that a thing is good for him, he is aroused to love that thing, because by nature he is drawn to that which can bring him benefit. Therefore, when he comprehends that Elokus is good for him, he is aroused in love. However, in *yirah*, the matter of comprehension alone is not sufficient; there must be recognition and connection to the One from Whom he fears. The reason for this is that the essence of *yirah* is *bitul* (nullification), which is the opposite of a person’s existence. Therefore, understanding and comprehension are not enough for this; there must be recognition and connection. For this, one specifically needs *yigiah* (toil), as the Sages say,[27](#_ftn1532) “Woe to the flesh that did not toil in *yirah*” (unlike love, which comes through understanding and comprehension alone, where there is not such a need for *yigiah*). From this it is understood that the primary matter of *yirah* applies precisely when the soul is Above, for since there are revelations there, the recognition and connection to Elokus are created, through which the matter of *yirah* is created. This is not the case below, where there are no revelations through which one would come to the state of recognition and connection. If so, how can one come to the matter of *yirah*? Based on this, we must understand the matter of (“I am black and) comely” regarding *yirah*, that the ultimate beauty of *yirah* is precisely below. We must conclude that the matter of *naveh* must apply not only to love but also to *yirah*. For we stated above that the unification of the souls of Yisrael

#### 280

while they are below with Elokus is called *hiskashrus*, and it is known[28](#_ftn1533) that a lasting bond is in the manner of two knots, one upon the other, which are the two matters of love and *yirah*, as explained in the Tanya[29](#_ftn1534) that just as a bird cannot fly with one wing but only with two wings, so too it is impossible to be *parcha le'eila* (to fly Above)[30](#_ftn1535) except through the two matters of *dchilu* and *rchimu*. If so, we must understand what is the beauty (*naveh*) in the matter of *yirah* precisely below.

**However,** the matter is that although the essence of *yirah* is more intense when the soul is Above, nevertheless, the *nature* of *yirah* is in a more elevated state below. This is because the *bitul* is in the state of relinquishing one’s selfhood, which applies more to the soul below, which is in the state of an independent *metzius*. This is similar to what is explained elsewhere[31](#_ftn1536) regarding the difference between the *bitul* of “there is nothing else” (*ein od*) and the *bitul* of “everything is considered as nothing before Him” (*kula kama kela chashiv*). The *bitul* that is in the light is in the state of *kela chashiv*, while the *bitul* of *ein od* (which is more elevated) is in the state of *yesh* specifically. That is, when the soul is Above, its *bitul* is in the state of *kula kama kela chashiv*; through the contemplation that the Source constantly gives it life and it is incomparable to Him, it is completely nullified and *kela chashiv*. But nevertheless, since it is Elokus, it is not completely nullified from its existence (*er vert nit ois*) in the manner of *ein od*. However, when it is below, where there are concealments and hiddenness, when it comes to the recognition (*az er chapt zich*) that the truth is not so (*az es is nit azoi*), then it is completely nullified, and it knows that there is only the essence and being of the *Ein Sof* B.H., and “there is none else besides Him.” This is the advantage of *yirah* precisely below; although the essence of *bitul* is more intense Above, the *nature* of the *bitul* is in a more elevated state when the soul is below. Therefore, we say “I am black and comely” also regarding *yirah*.

d) **Now,** just as in the first bond of Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, there is an advantage in the *hiskashrus* of the soul precisely below, so too in the second bond of the Torah with the Holy One, blessed be He, there is an advantage in the *hiskashrus* of the Torah precisely below. For,[32](#_ftn1537) although the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, in its descent below it is merely in the state of “the withered remnants” (*novlos*) of the wisdom Above, as the saying goes,[33](#_ftn1538) “The withered remnants of the wisdom Above is Torah.” This is because the Torah is enclothed in human intellect and in worldly matters and in arguments of

#### 281

falsehood,[34](#_ftn1539) to the point that it is possible for a person to study Torah and forget the Giver of the Torah,[35](#_ftn1540) and furthermore, it is possible that the study is in a manner of “he did not merit,” in which case it becomes for him, etc.[36](#_ftn1541) All this is because the Torah, while it is below, is in the state of *metzius*. This matter applies not only to the *galya* (revealed) aspect of Torah, but also to the *satim* (hidden) aspect of Torah—that is, the hidden within the revealed—which is the study of Torah as the souls study in Gan Eden, such as the laws of *negaim* and sacrifices, and “one who exchanges a cow for a donkey,” and the like. In all these matters, the Torah explains the matters of the *hishtalshelus* (chain of progression), which is in the state of *metzius*. This means that the interpretation of the Torah’s descent below is not only below in this world specifically, but in the totality of the worlds that are after the *Tzimtzum*. For before the *Tzimtzum*, there was no place for the existence of the worlds,[37](#_ftn1542) and only after the *Tzimtzum* was a place made for the existence of the worlds, and there is the matter of the Torah as it explains the details of the matters in the order of *hishtalshelus*. Now, since the *Tzimtzum* was by way of total removal, it is understood that when the Torah is after the *Tzimtzum*, the term *dveikus* does not apply to it, only the term *hiskashrus*. And all the more so as the Torah is below in this world, surely the term *dveikus* does not apply to it. And although “words of Torah do not receive impurity,”[38](#_ftn1543) because the Torah is not in the state of enclothement—as is known the difference between Torah and prayer: the matter of prayer is in enclothement, for the contemplation in prayer is in the state of the Elokus that pertains to the worlds, and the contemplation is in a manner that the matter is well-grasped in his mind. Not so Torah, which does not come in actual enclothement. Similarly, this is the difference between Torah and mitzvos: the mitzvos are enclothed in actual physical things, whereas the Torah is not enclothed in physical things, but only speaks about them, which is not by way of enclothement but only by way of *makif* (encompassing). Therefore, words of Torah do not receive impurity. But nevertheless, since the Torah is drawn into worldly matters by way of *makif* at least, therefore it is not appropriate to use the term *dveikus* for it, only *hiskashrus*. However, precisely in the descent of the Torah below, when it is in the state of *hiskashrus* only, the essence of the *Ein Sof* B.H. is drawn into it (similar to the above regarding Yisrael). And this matter is drawn into the Torah precisely through Yisrael. That is, at first, it is the *hiskashrus* of Yisrael with the Holy One, blessed be He, through the Torah, and through this, an addition of light is made also in the Torah. For, “at first, when a person acts, he acts for his own sake,”[39](#_ftn1544) which is the matter of Torah study before prayer, which is the matter of contemplation, through which he effects in prayer the refinement and purification of his soul, and connects with

#### 282

the Essence of the *Ein Sof* B.H. And afterwards is the study of Torah after prayer, the study of Torah *lishmah* (for its own sake), for the sake of the Torah itself, to connect the Torah with the Essence of the *Ein Sof* B.H. That is, through the fact that the Torah worked in him the *hiskashrus* with the Essence of the *Ein Sof* B.H., he also works in the Torah the *hiskashrus* with the Essence of the *Ein Sof* B.H. And this is the matter of “Three bonds are bound one to another: Yisrael to the Torah, and the Torah to the Holy One, blessed be He.” This is the *hiskashrus* of the Torah and the souls of Yisrael as they are in the state of *metzius*, that even then they are bound to the Holy One, blessed be He. And furthermore, “all are hidden and revealed,” that the *hiskashrus* is not only in the revealed aspect of Yisrael, the revealed aspect of Torah, and the revealed aspect of the Holy One, blessed be He, but also in the state of *satim* and the inwardness—the inwardness of the souls of Yisrael, the inwardness of the Torah, and the inwardness of Elokus. This is the advantage of the *hiskashrus* that comes through the descent below specifically.

e) **And this is** “And it shall come to pass, *eikev* (because) you hearken… that Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness that He swore,” etc. The matter of the covenant is that even when one of the two lovers does not behave as he should, nevertheless the love remains as it was at first. Similarly, the matter of kindness is that He bestows even upon the unworthy, and this is the matter of *Chesed deKshot* (true kindness), which is the state of *Chesed* of *Atik*, for “there is no left side in this *Atik*.”[40](#_ftn1545) Similarly, the matter of the oath is in a manner that He compels Himself, etc., as if He has no choice, as it were (as above). That is, these matters are above *taam v'daas* (reason and knowledge), a state that is above the order of *hishtalshelus*. And one reaches this level precisely through the *avodah* of “And it shall come to pass, *eikev* you hearken.” The meaning of the verse is not a conditional statement, but rather that this is the order of *avodah*: the drawing down of a state that is above *hishtalshelus* is in the state of *eikev* specifically. The matter is as follows: there are two states in the soul, *Yisrael* and *Yaakov*.[41](#_ftn1546) *Yisrael* is the letters *li rosh* (for me is the head),[42](#_ftn1547) meaning the head of the soul. And *Yaakov* is the state of *yud eikev* (the heel),[43](#_ftn1548) the heel of the soul.[44](#_ftn1549) It is the same regarding time and place, for *eikev* refers to the time and place of the “heels of Mashiach” (*ikveta d’Meshicha*),[45](#_ftn1550) when “we have not seen our signs, and there is no one among us who knows how long,”[46](#_ftn1551) “I clothe the heavens in blackness.”[47](#_ftn1552) And nevertheless, there is the matter of *tishmeun* (you hearken), which is the matter of understanding and comprehension, etc. More specifically, as it continues in the verse, “these *ordinances* (mishpatim),” which refers[48](#_ftn1553) to

#### 283

the judgment that a person judges himself,[49](#_ftn1554) through which he contemplates the purpose of his creation and the manner of his standing and state. That is, he contemplates the root of his soul, which is hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory,[50](#_ftn1555) and higher still, in the state of “the soul that You have placed within me is pure,” and he contemplates “from where you came.”[51](#_ftn1556) And afterwards he contemplates his standing and state now, which is in the state of “He who dwells with them in the midst of their impurity,”[52](#_ftn1557) and “the *Shechinah* went into exile with them to Edom,”[53](#_ftn1558) that He takes with Him (*er schlept mit zich*) the divine spark. And after all this, at some time or another, he will be aroused in complete *teshuvah*, since there is the giving of strength from Above through the heavenly proclamations that proclaim, “Return, O wayward children.”[54](#_ftn1559) Through the contemplation of all this, which is the matter of the *mishpatim*, even while he is in the state of *eikev*—the heel of the soul, and the time and place of the heels of Mashiach, etc.—he will come to the standing and state of “you hearken… and keep and perform,” which refers to the three garments of thought, speech, and action.[55](#_ftn1560) *Tishmeun* is the matter of understanding and comprehension, which is in the garment of thought. *U’shmartem* is the matter of speech, as the Sages say,[56](#_ftn1561) “*Shamor* (keep) refers to Mishnah,” meaning Torah study, which is “equivalent to them all,”[57](#_ftn1562) which is in speech. And *va’asitem* (and perform) is action. Through this, “Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness that He swore,” which are the matters that are above *hishtalshelus*. This is also the connection of this *parsha* to the seven *haftoros* of consolation, as hinted at by the precision of the language “And it shall come to pass (*v’hayah*), *eikev*,” for “*v’hayah*” is only an expression of joy,[58](#_ftn1563) because even in the state of the heel—the heel of the soul and the time and place of the heels of Mashiach—there will be “you hearken,” etc., and then there will also be the drawing down from Above, “Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness that He swore,” a drawing down from above *hishtalshelus*. And all this will be drawn down below in physicality, as the verse continues, “And He will bless the fruit of your womb and the fruit of your land,” etc., “upon the land that He swore to your forefathers to give to you.”

## Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Eikev, Mevarchim HaChodesh Elul, 5711

#### 284

Unedited

**A.** The order of the "Shiva D'nechemta" —where the first Haftorah is "Nachamu Nachamu Ami", which is the Haftorah for Parshas Va'eschanan, and the second Haftorah is "Vatomer Tzion Azavani Hashem", which is the Haftorah for Parshas Eikev.

Regarding the explanation of the order of these Haftaros—as stated in Tosafos that "the way of the consolations is to go from strength to strength"—it is brought in the Abudraham in the name of the Midrash that "they ordained to say at the beginning of the Haftaros of consolation 'Nachamu Nachamu Ami,' meaning that the Ribono shel Olam said to the *prophets*, 'Comfort, comfort My people.' To this, Knesses Yisrael replies, 'And Tzion says, Hashem has forsaken me,' meaning, 'I am not consoled by the comfort of the prophets.'" This is the content of the subsequent Haftorah, "O afflicted one, storm-tossed, uncomforted", "meaning, the prophets return and say before the Ribono shel Olam, 'Behold, Knesses Yisrael has not been consoled by our comfort.' To this, the Ribono shel Olam returns and says, 'I, I am He who comforts you'".

In this, the greatness of the stature of Bnei Yisrael is emphasized:

Even though the entirety of the destruction and the galus was *due to the fault* of Bnei Yisrael, as we say, "Because of *our sins* we were exiled from our land," nevertheless, Bnei Yisrael received consolation, and not just any consolation, but "consolation *in double measure*" ("Nachamu Nachamu"), which is incomparable to what they had anticipated.

And after all this—*Bnei Yisrael come with the claim* that they are not satisfied even with a double consolation, because it is the consolation of *the prophets*, whereas the Ribono shel Olam Himself—claims Knesses Yisrael—"has forsaken me!"

And a greater novelty—that even though the consolation through the prophets is also the consolation of the Ribono shel Olam, for the prophet is in a state of total unity with the Ribono shel Olam, to the extent that he does not need to say "and Hashem will give," but can say "*I will give*" ("And I will give the rain of your land... and I will give grass...") as if speaking for Himself —nevertheless, *the Ribono shel Olam accepts*

#### 285

the claim of Bnei Yisrael that they are not satisfied with the consolation of the prophets, and He returns and comforts them Himself: "*I, I am He who comforts you*."

And this should be connected with Parshas Eikev, whose beginning is, "And it shall be, because (eikev) you will listen... and Hashem your G-d will keep for you the covenant and the kindness that He swore to your forefathers"—which is from the perspective of the connection of Bnei Yisrael with the Ribono shel Olam in a manner of covenant and oath that is above *ta'am v'da'as*.

***

**B.** Maamar beginning "Ve'hayah Eikev Tishme'un...".

***

**C.** It was discussed regarding the interpretation of "Ve'hayah Eikev Tishme'un," that it refers to "minor mitzvos... which they cast *under their heels*", that one should not differentiate and prioritize the mitzvos that are in the category of "head" over the mitzvos that are in the category of "heel" (as would be required according to intellect), since the foundation for the fulfillment of mitzvos is the matter of *emunah* and *kabbalas ol*—this was discussed by the Rebbe shlita, and is printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 17, p. 89 and onwards.

***

**D.** I wish to explain a matter, and my request is that everyone should publicize this in any way they can, and after Shabbos they should publicize this even in ways that cannot be used on Shabbos.

You are permitted to say these things in my name or not in my name, provided that it will be more effective for the publicity and, primarily, for the absorption of the words by the listeners.

**E.** Regarding the month of Elul, Chazal said that its name is hinted at in the acronym of the verse : "*A*nah *L*e'yado *V*esamti *L*ach" ("He caused it to come to his hand, and I will appoint for you").

#### 286

This verse is in the parsha where the Torah speaks of a person who killed his fellow unintentionally (without knowledge), and the Torah, the Torah of life, says that they should establish a place, cities of refuge, to which the murderer should flee, and in this way he will not fear the redeemer of blood, who wishes to take revenge for the spilled blood and kill him—as is explained at length in Parshas Masei and elsewhere.

Now, the acronym of "Elul" is not from the first words of the verse that speak of the *act* that the person committed, but rather from the words in the verse that speak of his *merit* ("Anah Le'yado"), and the *rectification* of the sinful person through the cities of refuge ("Vesamti Lach").

And to add, that cities of refuge were everywhere that Bnei Yisrael were, whether in the desert, whether in Eretz Yisrael, or whether across the Jordan—which was outside of Eretz Yisrael.

**F.** Now, this is the function of the cities of refuge in saving the *body* of one who killed a person unintentionally.

But surely his soul also needs rectification, for he committed a great and severe transgression. True, he did it unintentionally—but even those who act unintentionally are subject to punishment and require atonement.

And seemingly, this itself requires explanation: why is punishment due to one who acts unintentionally?

The reason is that, in truth, it is wondrous how a person of Yisrael could commit a transgression, even unintentionally. For not only the *neshamah* of a Yid, but even his body should flee and distance itself from this by its very *nature*, because it is a thing that harms him, harming the body and the soul, just as it is impossible to say that one would jump into fire unintentionally. And because of this, in truth, "No evil will befall the righteous".

However, the reason for this is because the *nefesh habehamis* is in a state of dominance within him; that is to say, the animal within him is in a state of dominance over the human within him. It covers over

#### 287

the human of the *nefesh elokis*, and over his feelings, and draws the Yid to do something that the animal within him is drawn to. And because the person allowed the *nefesh habehamis* to dominate, and usually even assisted this through improper conduct—therefore he is subject to punishment and requires atonement.

And this atonement is achieved through the cities of refuge, for the essence of the cities of refuge is—*galus*, and it is known that "*galus* atones".

**G.** There is another aspect to the cities of refuge—they also assist in the saving of one who killed a person intentionally, as Chazal say, "Both the unintentional and the intentional [murderer] precede to the cities of refuge." There he is, in the meantime, safe from the redeemer of blood. And only afterwards do the *beis din* send and bring him from there to the *beis din*, and when—"the congregation shall judge"—then "the congregation shall save". And as is known, that if they sentenced [someone] to death once in seven years, the Sanhedrin was called: destructive.

In any case, until the judgment, he is safe and saved. And in the meantime, he can do *teshuvah*.

**H.** Regarding this matter—there is an advantage in the time of *galus* over the time of the Beis Hamikdash. For in the time of the Beis Hamikdash, *teshuvah* did not avail to exempt from punishment one who killed a person unintentionally or intentionally, and even if he did *teshuvah*, they would punish him.

—And it is explained in the *She'eilos U'teshuvos Noda B'Yehuda* why *teshuvah* did not avail for the punishments of the *beis din* below. The reason is that *teshuvah* is a matter of the heart, and since a judge has only what his eyes see, the *teshuvah* of the heart does not avail to nullify the decree of the *beis din* (of man).

This is not the case after the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash—and also forty years before the destruction

#### 288

—may it be rebuilt speedily in our days—when the capital laws were nullified, and there remained only the judgment of the four deaths, for which one is punished *from above*, then *teshuvah* does avail, as Chazal say : "A person committed a transgression and became liable for death to the Omnipresent; what should he do to live? If he was accustomed to study one page, he should study two pages, etc."

**I.** And like all these things is also the matter of the month of Elul.

In the acronym of Elul, "*A*nah *L*e'yado *V*esamti *L*ach," it is hinted that this month is the city of refuge for the improper deeds that a person did throughout the entire year, through *cheshbon hanefesh* and *teshuvah*. For if, G-d forbid, he sinned and blemished and crossed the path, the path of Hashem—then with every transgression he committed, he is a murderer of a soul, "who sheds the blood of man

#### 289

in man", meaning that he "sheds the blood of man," the man of holiness; he *takes* and removes blood and vitality from his *nefesh elokis*, and delivers them "into man"—the man of Belial, which is the *yetzer hara*, shedding the blood of man unintentionally or intentionally.

And the month of Elul is the city of refuge; if the sinner *goes into galus* to the month of Elul—he disconnects himself and exits his *yeshus* and his own reality, "from your land, and from your birthplace, and from your father's house" —from his desires, his habits, and from the conclusions of his intellect, *ta'am v'da'as* —and he will be in the state of "and he shall flee there", that "there shall be his dwelling" —meaning that he decides in his soul "to settle there," to arrange the days of his life in the new order of *cheshbon hanefesh* and *teshuvah*, then—"*galus* atones."

And not only the improper matters that he did unintentionally will be atoned for, but also the improper matters that he did intentionally will be atoned for, for now the *teshuvah* of "shedding the blood of man" avails, as mentioned above.

And even if he cannot reach the level of *teshuvah me'ahavah* (out of love), where "willful sins become for him as merits", but he does *teshuvah me'yirah* (out of fear) at least, whether out of fear of punishment or fear of judgment, or out of the fear of the Days of Awe, out of the fear of "Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li" —the acronym of Elul —from his contemplation of the *tlat kishrin* (three bonds) that are bound one to another: Yisrael to the Torah, and the Torah to the Holy One, blessed be He, and he himself—through the transgression, where "your iniquities separate between you and your G-d", he is distanced and disconnected from the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*—then, when he contemplates and delves into this, he comes to *teshuvah me'yirah*, "willful sins become for him as unintentional," and "*galus* atones."

**J.** However, the intention here is not the matter of self-affliction and fasts—just as with the cities of refuge, the intention is not that the person in *galus* needs to afflict and torture himself.

#### 290

The essence of the cities of refuge is—*galus*, which *galus* itself atones. But they provide him in the city of refuge with the things he was accustomed to in his home.

Regarding the cities of refuge it is said : "And he shall live—provide him with something that will provide him with life." And therefore the law is that "a student who goes into *galus*, his teacher goes into *galus* with him." Even though the student is only secondary to the teacher, nevertheless, "his teacher goes into *galus* with him."

And when his teacher is with him, then regardless of the disparity in their stature—"provide him with *life*," meaning, that his teacher will bring him to *teshuvah*, until he reaches the level of "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are *alive* all of you today" —"Today, if you will listen to His voice".

**K.** Furthermore, by the fact that the person will fulfill the "and he shall flee there," to run into the month of Elul—he will be saved from the redeemer of blood, "he is the Satan," "he is the *yetzer hara*" that incites to sin, he is the accuser, "he is the Angel of Death", the redeemer of blood who wants to take revenge on the person.

The Satan is the redeemer of blood who claims: So-and-so killed the soul, killed the *nefesh elokis* within him, shedding the blood of the man of holiness into the man of Belial.

And the advice for this: "And the cities shall be for you as a refuge from the redeemer (of blood), and the murderer shall not die until he stands before the congregation for judgment".

And even if there were matters that he did intentionally, until the judgment and verdict of Rosh Hashanah, one can be exempted from this too through *teshuvah*, as mentioned above.

**L.** And this is the matter that needs to be publicized:

The Ribono shel Olam says to Yisrael:

*I am giving you twenty-nine, thirty days*, *during which, if you will disconnect yourselves from the habits and improper conduct that you have practiced until now—and flee there. Flee into the order and conduct of Elul to settle there—then you will be able to rectify everything that was not as it should have been until now, and consequently, it will be a refuge from the redeemer of blood from all the accusations.*

#### 291

*And through teshuvah,*

*Initially teshuvah me'yirah, where they become for him as unintentional, and afterwards teshuvah me'ahavah, where they become for him as merits—*

*You will be written and sealed—immediately in the Book of the Righteous*,

*For a good and sweet year.*

## B"H, 5 Elul, 5711

#### 292

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Torah institutions in general,
And the yeshiva students in particular,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

As we approach the beginning of the study term, which comes upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send you my warm and heartfelt blessing: May He who grants man wisdom, understanding, and knowledge shine His countenance upon you, and may the beginning and the entire school year be successful in every detail.

Every single action of the sons and daughters of Israel must have a desired intent and purpose. The vacation days that have just passed also have an intent and purpose: to renew your strength and increase your courage, so that you may continue—or, for those beginning, start—your study of Torah and proper education in yiras shamayim with greater diligence and greater vitality.

It is my hope, and my prayer, that you will bring from potential into actuality the diligence, persistence, and vitality required to acquire the Torah, which is a Torah of life, from the mouth of the Living G-d, an inheritance for the people of Israel, of whom it is said, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

And especially during these days of the month of Elul—the month that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was accustomed to call "the month of accounting," an accounting of the year that is passing, and good resolutions for the future—my confidence is strong that you will make a true accounting of what needs to be changed for the better and corrected regarding your conduct and order in the past. This is so that from here on, your studies and your conduct will be of the highest quality, for your benefit, both materially and spiritually.

I conclude with the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year for each and every one of you, for your parents, may they live, for your educators, may they live, and for the directors of your institutions, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## With the help of Heaven. Remarks at a Reception – 10 Elul, 5711

#### 293

**A.** It is well known [1] that "the custom of Israel is Torah."

One of the reasons for this is that the Jewish people are the children of the Holy One, Blessed be He, as it is written [2], "You are children to Hashem your G-d," and children resemble their father (and mother—in this context, Knesset Yisrael). Thus, the conduct of the Jewish people resembles the conduct of the Holy One, Blessed be He. Since the conduct of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is expressed in His Torah, it follows that "the custom of Israel is Torah."

From this, it is understood that the specific details of the "custom of Israel" regarding marriage are in accordance with the content of the concept of marriage as it exists between the Holy One, Blessed be He, and Knesset Yisrael, as will be explained below [3].

**B.** It is a custom of Israel that the groom and bride are brought to the chuppah, and under the chuppah, the bride circles the groom, and the groom gives her a ring and betroths her with this ring.

(It should be noted that, according to the strict letter of the law, it is not necessary to betroth specifically with a ring. In the Gemara and Halacha, we do not find that betrothal must be with a ring, but rather with money or its equivalent [4]. However, it has already become the custom of Israel to betroth with a ring [5], and the source for this is in the Tikkunei Zohar [6], which states that betrothal is specifically with a ring, which is like a *mem setumah* [6a].)

The concept behind this is as follows:

Regarding the matter of marriage, it is said that "it is as difficult to pair them as the splitting of the Red Sea" [7]. Therefore, in order to accomplish this, there is a need for an *hemshech* (drawing down) from a most exalted level—specifically, the level of *makif* (encompassing light) [8].

#### 294

Since in the matter of marriage (the purpose of which is union and procreation, etc.) there are three partners—"There are three partners in a person: the Holy One, Blessed be He, his father, and his mother" [9]—there must be three *makifim*: the *makif* of the bride, the *makif* of the groom, and the *makif* of the Holy One, Blessed be He.

Based on this, we can explain the content of the aforementioned custom:

The bride *circles* the groom—this is the *makif* provided by the *bride* [10], which is her dedication from the level of *makif* to build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

The groom gives a *ring* (which is round) to the bride—this is the *makif* provided by the *groom* [11], which is his dedication from the level of *makif* to build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

And as a *natinas-koach* (empowerment) for the groom and bride to be able to dedicate themselves from their level of *makif* to build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, they are led to the *chuppah*—which is the *makif* provided by the *Holy One, Blessed be He*, a level of *makif* that is above the *Seder Hishtalshelus* [12]. Through this, their home will be an everlasting edifice [13] on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, and they will be granted abundant success in material matters as well.

**C.** The same applies to the marriage between the Holy One, Blessed be He, and Knesset Yisrael—which is particularly relevant to the month of Elul [during which this wedding is taking place, by Divine Providence], as it is the month of preparation for Rosh Hashanah. During this time, the process of *nesirah* (separation) takes place for the sake of building the *Malchus*, as it is written [14], "And Hashem G-d caused a deep sleep to fall upon the man... and He built... the rib," through which the union of *Ze'er Anpin* and *Nukvah* can occur above [15] (similar to the concept of marriage below).

By way of introduction: In the marriage of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and Knesset Yisrael, there are two modes [16]: (1) The *avodah* of the month of Nissan—"My beloved is mine and I am his" [17]—from above

#### 295

to below, where the revelation occurs first from above, "My beloved is mine," and in the course of time, "I am to my beloved" also happens automatically; (2) The *avodah* of the month of Elul—"I am to my beloved and my beloved is mine" [18], the acronym for Elul [19]—from below to above, meaning that the beginning is specifically through the *avodah* of man, "I am to my beloved."

Regarding our subject—the marriage that takes place in the month of Elul, "I am to my beloved and my beloved is mine":

The *avodah* of "I am to my beloved" (the *avodah* of man) is similar to the law in betrothal that it must be "with her consent," meaning that she "agrees to the betrothal of the man... nullifies her own mind and will, and considers herself as something ownerless before her husband" [20]. This is the *bitul* and dedication ("*di ibergegebenkeit*") to the Holy One, Blessed be He, which comes from the level of the *makifim* in the soul (*chayah* and *yechidah* [21]), which are above the internal powers (*nefesh, ruach, neshamah*), similar to the *makif* provided by the bride.

And in order for this dedication to the Holy One, Blessed be He, to exist from the level of the *makif* in the soul ("I am to my beloved"), there is a need for empowerment from the higher *makif*—this is the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy that shine in the month of Elul [22], similar to the *makif* of the chuppah that gives strength to the dedication of the groom and bride from their own levels of *makif*.

**D.** It should be added that the *avodah* of the month of Elul—"I am to my beloved and my beloved is mine"—is from the *essence of the soul*, which is even above the level of *yechidah*:

"I am to my beloved and my beloved is mine" are the initial letters of "Elul," and the final letters are four *yuds*. Since "Elul" is in the *initial* letters, and the four *yuds* are only in the *final* letters, it is understood that "Elul" is *above* the four *yuds*—similar to what is explained in *Torah Or* [23] regarding the verse "Who shall go up for us to heaven?" [24], where the initial letters spell "milah" (circumcision) and the final letters spell the Tetragrammaton [25], meaning that "milah" is *above* the name *Havayah*, to the extent that it is in the *initial* letters and the name *Havayah* is in the *final* letters.

#### 296

Now, the four *yuds* are in the name *Av* [26] [for only in the name *Av*, the name *Havayah* filled with *yuds*, are there four *yuds*, unlike the other names *Sag, Ban, Mah*, which do not have four *yuds*], and its meaning in the human soul is the level of *yechidah*, as explained in the discourse *Maskil L'Eisan HaEzrachi* [27]: "Eisan is the essence of the soul... for the soul that You have placed within me is pure; You created it, You fashioned it, You breathed it into me... In the Midrash [28], five levels are counted: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*, and in the Zohar [29], they are included in four levels: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah*, and *neshamah l'neshamah*, corresponding to the four letters of the name *Havayah*. And *Eisan* is the strength of the soul that comes into revelation through the power of *mesiras nefesh*, and *Eisan* is ancient and uncreated, and it is the name *Av* which is uncreated" (unlike the other names which are created).

Since "Elul" is above the four *yuds* (the final letters of Elul), and consequently, it is above the name *Av* (because the four *yuds* are in the name *Av*), it must be that the *avodah* of Elul is above even the level of *yechidah* ("Eisan," the name *Av*).

The explanation for this: Seemingly, the level of *yechidah* is the most exalted—"Eisan," the name *Av* which is uncreated—so how can there be anything above it? This is based on what is known [30] that even the level of *yechidah* is only a *name* for the essence of the soul, as emphasized in the expression [28], "Five *names* were called *for it*: *nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*," meaning that even "yechidah" is one of the "five names called for it," *for the essence of the soul*, and the essence of the soul is above even the level of *yechidah*.

This is the innovation in the *avodah* of the month of Elul (which is above the four *yuds*, the name *Av*, the level of *yechidah*) compared to the *avodah* of the entire year—that throughout the entire year, the *avodah* can be within the five names (up to the level of *yechidah*) only, without knowing what is happening with the essence of the soul, as we find even with Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai, who wept and said, "I do not know on which path they are leading me" [31]. For, even when the *avodah* in the revealed powers is perfect, it is impossible to know what is happening with the essence of the soul [32]. In contrast, in the month of Elul, the *avodah* can be from the *essence of the soul* (which is above even the level of *yechidah*), and this is the concept of "I am to my beloved."

**E.** Based on this, it can be said that the same applies to the matter of marriage below—that the dedication of the groom and bride to build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos is from the essence of the soul, which is above even the level of *yechidah*.

#### 297

Seemingly, one could ask: How can the *avodah* be from the essence of the soul—after all, even Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai did not know ("I do not know") what was happening with the essence of the soul?!

The answer to this is that this matter is accomplished through the connection to the Rebbe, the Nasi of the generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe:

The Rebbe—of whom it is said [33], "I stand between Hashem and you"—is (not an intermediary that separates, but) an intermediary that connects [34].

—One of the Chassidim writes to me in a letter regarding the Rebbe, that he (the Rebbe) and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are one and the same.

And since through the connection to the Rebbe one connects with the *Atzmus* (the Essence), then he "knows" where the Essence is [35].

From this, it is understood that when one stands to build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos (and with an addition for Chassidim:) as they are illuminated by the light within the Torah, which is the teachings of Chassidus [36]—one must connect to the Rebbe with the entire essence, and through this, an *hemshech* of the *makif* is effected from a level that is completely above limitations. Consequently, it is drawn down below into material matters as well, to be blessed with everything necessary, and even more than one would wish for oneself ("*nochmer vi m'vinsht zich alein*").

## 298

The significance of the days from Chai Elul through the third day of Selichos was explained in the introduction to the Kuntres Chai Elul 5710[1](#_ftn1655), based on what I found in the writings of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. I also transcribed there the letters regarding the nature of the avodah for these days, from Chai Elul onwards.

Regarding the effect of the day of Chai Elul itself upon one’s avodah, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, related[2](#_ftn1656] in the name of the elder Chassidim that Chai Elul is the day that infused—and continues to infuse—vitality into Elul.

***

The month of Elul is the month of accounting for the year that has passed, and the month of preparation for the year to come.

It can be said that for this reason, the essential categories of a person’s avodah—through which one must achieve repentance and rectification for the past, and make good resolutions for the future—are alluded to in the very name of this month.

As our Sages state: The acronym for Elul (*Aleph-Lamed-Vav-Lamed*) is *Anah Liyado V'samti Lach* ("He caused it to come to hand, and I will appoint for you" [a place of refuge])[3](#_ftn1657], referring to the cities of refuge. In the context of a person’s avodah, this is the **line of Torah**, for the words of Torah provide refuge[4](#_ftn1658).

Elul is also an acronym for *Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li* ("I am to my Beloved, and my Beloved is to me")[5](#_ftn1659). This is the **line of avodah**, which is tefillah[6](#_ftn1660)—especially in these times, when we have only the "avodah of the heart," which is tefillah[7](#_ftn1661), which *tofel* (joins)[8](#_ftn1662) and connects Yisrael to their Father in Heaven.

## 299

Elul is an acronym for *Ish L're'eihu U'matanos La'evyonim* ("Each man to his fellow, and gifts to the poor")[9](#_ftn1663)—the **line of gemilus chasadim**.

And as a preface and foundation for all these lines:

Elul is an acronym for *(U'mal Hashem Elokecha) Es Levavcha V'es Levav (Zarecha)* ("And Hashem your G-d will circumcise your heart and the heart of your offspring")[10](#_ftn1664)—the **concept of teshuvah**.

***

There have been many paths to infuse vitality into a person’s avodah to their Creator. However, in these final generations, the "heels of Moshiach," when concealments and darkness have multiplied and cover the world twofold,

This is the path for the many and for the individual—the path paved by our holy Rebbes, the Nesi'im—to attain true life in the avodah of Hashem: through engagement with the inwardness of the Torah, the *neshamah d'oraysa* (soul of the Torah)[11](#_ftn1665), in general, and the teachings of Chassidus in particular.

For Chai Elul is the birthday of the founder of the general teachings of Chassidus—the Baal Shem Tov—and the birthday of the founder of the teachings of Chabad Chassidus—our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe.

These revelations are renewed and reawakened every single year on this day[12](#_ftn1666).

By studying their teachings and walking in the ways of Chassidus that they have instructed for all the children of Yisrael, one infuses a soul and vitality into all categories of avodah; one infuses *Chai* (life) into *Elul*: in teshuvah, in Torah, in avodah, and in gemilus chasadim.

Through all of this, one also brings about the Geulah, as is also alluded to in the acronym of Elul and as our Sages state:

Elul is an acronym for *L'Hashem Vayomru Lemar Ashirah* ("To Hashem, and they will say, saying: I will sing"), for then all the sparks will emerge from exile[13](#_ftn1667),

Through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

**M. Schneerson**

*13 Elul, 5711*

*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## B’s”d. Reshimos of Parshas Teitzei, 14 Elul, 5711

#### 300

– After Mincha –

Unedited

(The Rebbe turned to R. Zalman Duchman and related:)

The wedding of the Rebbe Rayatz took place on 13 Elul (5657), and the wedding of his father, the Rebbe Rashab, took place on 11 Elul (5635).

Immediately after his wedding, on the first day of the seven days of feasting, the Rebbe Rayatz was summoned to report for military service[1](#_ftn1668). Before leaving, he painted and blackened his face so that he would appear older and they would exempt him, and he returned to the farbrengen of the Sheva Brachos with his face blackened...

There is also a story regarding the exemption of the Rebbe Rashab from military service[2](#_ftn1669):

When he was summoned to the army, his father, the Rebbe Maharash, traveled to the Governor to demand that he be exempted from military service. When the Governor refused, the Rebbe Maharash informed him unequivocally that his son would not serve in the army, telling him: "I will succeed regardless"... adding that the choice was his to spare him the trip to Moscow (by rescinding the decree), but if he did not fulfill his demand and he was forced to travel to Moscow, he would pay a heavy price for it.

When the Governor did not accede to his request, and wishing to pull a "trick," he sent for him to be summoned to the army again—the Rebbe Maharash traveled to Moscow and succeeded in having him exempted from military service.

During that time, the Governor fell ill, "twisted like a pretzel," and after some time, he died in great agony.

## 18 Elul, 5711

#### 301

**A.** 18 Elul is the day the luminaries were suspended — as the Rebbe Rayatz [1](#_ftn1670) revealed that 18 Elul is the birthday of the two great luminaries: the **Baal Shem Tov** — founder of the general teachings of Chassidus, and the **Alter Rebbe** — founder of the Chabad Chassidic teachings.

— The first 18 Elul, the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov (in the year 5458), fell on Monday, Parshas Nitzavim-Vayelech, and the second 18 Elul, the birthday of the Alter Rebbe (in the year 5505), fell on Wednesday, the day the luminaries were suspended, corresponding to the order of "Arise, shine, for your light has come" [2](#_ftn1671) (the beginning of the Haftorah for Parshas Tavo) — as is the calendar arrangement this year.

**B.** The primary work of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe in founding the teachings of Chassidus was (not for themselves alone, but) for all Bnei Yisrael:

Among the essential matters in the path of Chassidus — which it established as a foundation (in addition to the matter of love of Hashem and love of Torah) — is the matter of *ahavas Yisrael* toward every single Jew, even the simplest of the simple.

As is known [3](#_ftn1672), before the revelation of the path of Chassidus, there was a separation and a partition dividing Torah-learned Jews from simple people and *amei ha'aretz*. The Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, and the Alter Rebbe, and those who followed them, invested their energies into this — to explain, to teach the path, and to enable even the simplest of the simple to reach the highest ascents ("*צו די העכסטע הויכן*"), ascents such that in previous times it was thought they belonged only to great scholars, and among them, only to the select few.

And as the Rebbe Rayatz [4](#_ftn1673) said, the intention of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, was that the teachings of Chassidus should belong (not only to a portion of Bnei Yisrael, a specific movement among Bnei Yisrael, but) to all Bnei Yisrael, and ultimately the matter will be fulfilled, that the teachings of Chassidus will be the inheritance of all Bnei Yisrael, so that they will all be Chassidim.

#### 302

**C.** This matter is also one of the reasons for the general difference in the conduct of the *gedolei Yisrael* before the revelation of the path of Chassidus and after [5](#_ftn1674):

Before the revelation of the path of Chassidus, the way of the *gedolei Yisrael* in leading Bnei Yisrael was that they would **sit in their place**, and Jews would come to them to ask about matters of Torah and to seek guidance in *avodas Hashem*.

— There were indeed *gedolei Yisrael* who also made a practice of traveling from their place, but their travel was **for their own benefit**: to undergo ("*פּראַווען*") *galus*, "*galus* atones" [6](#_ftn1675), or to know what was happening in the world of Torah scholars. In any event, their travel did not bring benefit to the correction of the status and situation of all Bnei Yisrael (including simple people) who were in the places through which they traveled. Furthermore, when they were on these journeys, they would make a practice of **concealing and hiding** their identity so that they would not be recognized, and in such a state, they could not act to correct the status and situation of the Bnei Yisrael in the places through which they traveled.

With the revelation of the path of Chassidus, a general innovation occurred in the conduct of the *gedolei Yisrael* — to bring the light of Torah to all places where Bnei Yisrael dwell:

The Baal Shem Tov would frequently walk and travel from place to place, from city to city, from village to village, and even from settlement to settlement.

And after him, the Alter Rebbe as well — in addition to the many journeys he made himself, he would also send his students as "*meshulachim*" [who were called "*shadarim*" or "*mashpi'im*"] to the other places he did not travel to himself, so that they would travel in his stead — "*shlucho shel adam k'moso*" [7](#_ftn1676) — to those places.

And on these journeys (they did not conceal and hide themselves, but on the contrary) they would reveal themselves in all their matters, such that they brought with them the light of Torah, "*ner mitzvah v'torah ohr*" [8](#_ftn1677), reaching to the "*ma'or*" [the luminary] within the Torah, from the "center" to all places where Bnei Yisrael dwell — without waiting for Jews to come to them to inquire of them.

**D.** Regarding the differences between the two aforementioned modes of conduct:

When the conduct is such that Jews must come and inquire — then

#### 303

the influence is only for those who feel that they are lacking, and therefore they come and demand that their lack be filled.

— This itself indicates a certain *darga* [level], that even though he is lacking, he nevertheless knows and recognizes at the very least that he is lacking, and he has the strength and *mesiras nefesh* to wander from his place and be an exile to a place of Torah or a place of *tefillah*, to find a place where his lack will be filled, or where they will show him the path through which he himself can fill his lack.

But all those who have not reached even such a level that they feel they are lacking something — are liable, *chas v'shalom*, to remain with the lack of many matters that will not belong to them.

And this is the innovation of the path of Chassidus — from the foundation of *ahavas Yisrael* — that they did not wait for Jews to come to them, but on the contrary, they wandered from their place, went and traveled and spread out ("*מיט דער גאַנצער התפשטות*") to all places where Bnei Yisrael dwell, and brought with them the "*ma'or*," and through it illuminated the "*ner Hashem nishmas adam*" [9](#_ftn1678) of **every single one** of Bnei Yisrael, even those who do not know that they are lacking anything. First, they awakened in them the knowledge and recognition of the existence of a matter that they are lacking and that they are in need of. Afterward, they explained to them and encouraged them not to despair, *chas v'shalom*, thinking that they do not belong to this, but to know that the matter is within their ability. And they did not suffice with this, but they set them on the straight path and the path of truth, and showed them the path in which they should walk in order to come and reach all the levels they can reach by virtue of the root of their soul.

And not only that, but in every place they arrived, they revealed and accomplished everything that could be accomplished in that place, also for the future — by establishing from among them Jews who were worthy and belonged to being (not only influenced, but) also **influencers**, "*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*" [10](#_ftn1679), and they revealed in them the "power of the influencer," such that they themselves became those who spread the light of Torah throughout the entire surroundings.

**E.** Another point in this — that the beginning of the Baal Shem Tov's activity to illuminate all Bnei Yisrael and the entire world was regarding young children:

It is known [11](#_ftn1680) that before his revelation, the Baal Shem Tov served as a "*bahelfer*" (assistant) to a teacher of children in the "*cheder*."

#### 304

A "*bahelfer*" does not learn with the children advanced studies, like Gemara with the commentary of Tosafos, or even Gemara alone, or even Chumash. The role of a "*bahelfer*" is to lead the children from their homes to the "*cheder*" and from the "*cheder*" to their homes, and to teach them the simplest things — however, these simple matters are the **essentials of faith**, and consequently they are the **essential vitality** of every single Jew — *Aleph-Beis*, "*Shema Yisrael*," "*Modeh Ani*," "*Amen yehei shmei rabba*," and "*Baruch hu uvaruch shemo*."

And in this matter, the Baal Shem Tov occupied himself before his revelation — and in this was his "test" [12](#_ftn1681) ("*דערמיט האָט מען אים אויסגעפּרואווט*") — as the beginning of his work to illuminate all Bnei Yisrael and the entire world!

And in the language of the verse [13](#_ftn1682), "From the mouths of babes and sucklings You have founded strength," and not only that, but this is the advice "to silence the enemy and the avenger" (as the verse continues), to nullify all the concealments and hidings, as the Rebbe Rayatz explains in his well-known *maamar* [14](#_ftn1683).

And based on this, the reason is also understood for the greatness of the effort that the Rebbe Rayatz invested, specifically regarding the children of the *cheder*, and not necessarily regarding those who already belong to the study of Gemara or Chumash, or even to the study of Hebrew, but also regarding those who belong only to the study of *Aleph-Beis*, and even regarding those who do not yet belong even to the study of *Aleph-Beis*. The Rebbe Rayatz demanded that everyone should endeavor to occupy themselves with them as a "*bahelfer*," and to explain to them matters of Yiddishkeit in the language of the country — for if it was appropriate for the Baal Shem Tov in his time and in his days to occupy himself with this, one can estimate the greatness of the value of this work and what can be accomplished through it!

**F.** And as we stand on the day of 18 Elul, the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov — we must know and remember that the Baal Shem Tov opened and paved and showed the path and gave the strength to each and every one of us, to be a "*bahelfer*" himself and to seek out simple people found in his surroundings, and to speak with them about simple matters, and to illuminate through this their *nefesh elokis*, the "*ner Hashem nishmas adam*."

And since this is so, a **holy obligation** is incumbent upon each and every one (and especially those who merited to receive and hear themselves, or to whom explicit instructions were given regarding this matter) to act upon all Bnei Yisrael found in his surroundings — to light their "*ner Hashem nishmas adam*"

#### 305

or to enlarge the small fire that burns quietly and is barely visible ("*דער פייער'ל וואָס ברענט שטיל, און קוים קוים אַז ס'זעט זיך אַרויס*"), until it becomes a great bonfire!

One must know that in every single Jew there is a "spring," a "well of living waters" [it is true that sometimes it is covered, and in this itself there are those whose spring is more covered or less covered, but nevertheless, the spring **is there**, and when one removes the concealment and the covering, then the spring **is revealed**], and since it is the nature of "living waters" that they do not remain in their place (for themselves), but go and spread to a distance, such that through them it is accomplished, "and you shall give drink to the congregation and their cattle" [15](#_ftn1684), it is found that it is in the power of every single Jew (who has a well of living waters in him) **to give drink to an entire congregation of Israel**, and even "to their cattle," which refers to the *nefesh habehamis* and all physical and material matters, so that their connection to Jews and Yiddishkeit will be evident ("*אידישע ממון, אידישע נכסים, און אַ אידישע קהילה*").

And as stated, this matter is in the power of everyone, only one must reveal it in himself, and also, not to make calculations if occupying oneself with this is according to his honor or not according to his honor, and not to be impressed by the fact that sometimes he will need to light the "*ner Hashem*" by teaching "*kamatz aleph ah*," by saying "*Shema Yisrael*," or even by translating "*Shema Yisrael*" into English... since this Jew does not yet understand the original language.

**G.** And may it be the will that starting from 18 Elul, in which the essential preparation for the coming year begins, everyone will go out with the strengths that the Rebbes give us, and with joy and vitality, for the work of the coming year — **to illuminate** (through the "*ner Hashem nishmas adam*" within him) in his four cubits, in the street, and in the entire surroundings.

Until it is accomplished that "for all Bnei Yisrael... there was light in their dwellings" [16](#_ftn1685), as it was before the first redemption, that even though in the entire land of Egypt there was a plague of darkness [17](#_ftn1686), "three days" and another "three days" [18](#_ftn1687), nevertheless, "for all Bnei Yisrael there was light in their dwellings" — so it is also before the final redemption, speedily in our days, that even though "darkness shall cover the earth" [19](#_ftn1688), that in the entire world a darkness of gloom prevails, "a darkness that can be felt" [20](#_ftn1689), "*אַ געוואַלדיקער חושך*," to the extent that "a person cannot stand

#### 306

and one who is standing cannot sit" [21](#_ftn1690), "*עס רירט זיך ניט פון אָרט*"... — Bnei Yisrael are not impressed by the darkness prevailing around, and everyone acts to illuminate in his four cubits and in his portion of the world.

And through this, they accomplish the fulfillment of the prophecy, "Arise, shine, for your light has come" — through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

***

**H.** As stated above (Section 2), the intention of the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in founding the teachings of Chassidus was **for all Bnei Yisrael**, and since this was their intention, they certainly accomplished it, as our Sages say [22](#_ftn1691), "A *tzaddik* decrees and the Holy One, Blessed be He, fulfills," that they opened and paved a path for the many — not just a narrow path, the way of the individual, or even a trail for the many, but **a paved and wide path for all Bnei Yisrael** — so that every single Jew, without regard to his status and situation (for "no one shall be cast out from Him" [23](#_ftn1692)), will be able to ascend the path and reach the "**ma'or**" within the Torah, the *pnimiyus* of the Torah.

There are those who think that the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, the teachings of Chassidus, belongs only to those who have already filled their bellies with *Shas* and *Poskim* [24](#_ftn1693), and even if they have not yet filled their bellies with *Shas* and *Poskim*, they feel in themselves that they have already been clarified and refined and have become on the level of a complete *tzaddik*, and consequently they are worthy to study the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, and as long as they have not reached such a level, they must occupy themselves with the study of the *nigleh* of the Torah alone.

But the truth is, that for everyone and on every level that one is found, there can and should also be the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, as stated, that the path to the *pnimiyus* of the Torah is a paved and wide path **for every single Jew**, that everyone can find in the teachings of Chassidus matters **that are appropriate for him**, for the senses of his soul, and when he begins to occupy himself with the study and fulfillment of the instructions of the teachings of Chassidus in the matters appropriate for him, he will reach in the course of time the study and fulfillment of all the matters that he can attain by virtue of the root of his soul ("for this is an instruction that this is sufficient for him, or since... he occupies himself with everything that is possible for him, the Holy One, Blessed be He, will complete for him, etc." [25](#_ftn1694)).
