And furthermore, and this is essential — that the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah gives **vitality** also to the study of the *nigleh* of the Torah, as is known that the *pnimiyus* of the Torah and the *nigleh* of the Torah are like a soul

#### 307

and a body [26](#_ftn1695): the *pnimiyus* of the Torah is the "*nishmasa d'oraisa*" [soul of the Torah], and the *nigleh* of the Torah is like a body, in the language of our Sages [27](#_ftn1696), "These are the bodies of the Torah," and just as the soul enlivens the body in such a way that the body itself becomes alive, likewise through the study of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, the *nishmasa d'oraisa*, the study of the *nigleh* of the Torah, the bodies of the Torah, also becomes a living thing (like the superiority of a living body over a non-living body).

**I.** And regarding this matter — that every single Jew in whatever status and situation he is (even if he is in a lowly situation) can ascend and walk in the path of Chassidus because it is a **paved and wide path for all** — one should bring an example from the "way of the cities of refuge":

"Cities of refuge" are intended for those who have committed a sin **of the most severe sins** — bloodshed (even literally), *rachmana litzlan*, and even **intentionally**, for "at first, whether accidental or intentional, they would flee to the cities of refuge" [28](#_ftn1697), so that in the meantime, until the judgment and trial are held, a "*hatzalah purta*" [a small rescue] is accomplished for him [29](#_ftn1698]. And not only that, but even when "the *Beis Din* sends and brings him from there" in order to judge him, there are several ways (many ways to the Place) that he will be saved from the liability of death — if they do not find witnesses, or if the witnesses fail in the interrogation and examination, or because they ceased to judge capital cases [30](#_ftn1699), and the like.

And here we see how much the Torah endeavors even for those who are in the lowest situation — that they should be able to flee to the cities of refuge:

In addition to the fact that "the word 'Refuge' was written at the crossroads so that the murderer would recognize (the path leading to the city of refuge) and turn there" [31](#_ftn1700), there is a special law regarding **the path** itself — that a general public road (sixteen cubits) is not enough, but "the path to the cities of refuge [must be] **thirty-two cubits**... for it is written [32](#_ftn1701), 'You shall prepare for yourself the way, the way [the path]' ('The way could have been written, and it is written the way, to add another way')" [33](#_ftn1702) — a path **twice as wide** as a general public road!

That is to say: even though seemingly **there is no necessity** for such a wide path — thirty-two cubits — in order to reach a city of refuge [unlike that which "the word 'Refuge' was written at the crossroads," which is a necessary thing to know the path leading to the city of refuge],

#### 308

and especially that those who need to use these paths to reach the cities of refuge — murderers — **were not many**, for we find in the Mishnah [34](#_ftn1703), "When murderers multiplied, [the law of the cities of refuge] was abolished, etc.," from which it is implied that generally there were not many murderers — nevertheless, the Torah said **that the path** to a city of refuge must be **extremely wide**, to the extent that even a general public road is not enough!

**J.** And from this we learn also regarding spiritual matters:

Even one who has sinned and blemished and gone off the path, accidentally or even intentionally, that through this he is spilling the blood of the human of holiness [35](#_ftn1704) — the Torah has prepared for him **an extremely paved and wide path** to walk to the "city of refuge," so that he can (first of all) be saved from the "avenger of blood," and then he can, with tranquility ("*רואיקערהייט*"), make an accounting of all the matters for which he needs correction and *teshuvah*, and find the path to return and correct them,

— as hinted in the law [36](#_ftn1705) that "a murderer who fled to his city of refuge and the people of the city wanted to honor him, he should say to them, 'I am a murderer'... for it is said [37](#_ftn1706), 'And this is the matter of the murderer,'" that is, he must recognize and admit that he is in an undesirable status and situation (as emphasized in the declaration "I am a murderer"), and as a result of this, he will endeavor to find correction and *teshuvah* for his not-good matters (unlike if he considers himself a complete *tzaddik*) —

And not only that, but the Torah assists him and gives him all the matters necessary to find and ascend the **path of life** — to the extent that "they exile his teacher with him, for it is said [37](#_ftn1706), '*And he shall live*,' do for him something *so that he will have life*" [38](#_ftn1707), that is, they return him to life ("*מ'מאַכט אים צוריק לעבעדיג*"), through his walking in the path of the Torah, including and especially the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, the "*nishmasa d'oraisa*," which gives vitality also to the *nigleh* of the Torah (as stated in Section 8).

**K.** And this matter is especially relevant to the month of Elul:

The month of Elul — the month of accounting and *teshuvah* for the entire year, as it is in the writings of the AriZal [39](#_ftn1708) in the interpretation of the verse [40](#_ftn1709), "And she shall bewail her father and her mother a month of days," which refers to the month of Elul — is like a "**city of refuge**" (as discussed above at length [41](#_ftn1710)).

#### 309

Someone might think that the "path" to the "city of refuge" of "Elul" is a narrow path, difficult to walk in, and with a slight deviation one falls off the path, and loses all the effort invested previously — to this they say to him: "The path to the cities of refuge [is] thirty-two cubits," that is to say, this is **an extremely paved and wide path** that is easy for everyone to walk in.

And as is also understood from the explanation in *Likkutei Torah* [42](#_ftn1711) regarding the matter of the month of Elul — "according to a parable of **a king** who, before he comes to the city, the people of the city go out to meet him and receive his face **in the field**, and then everyone who wants is permitted to go out to meet his face, etc.," and there is no need for special preparations, special garments, and the like, and they do not need to pass through the king's ministers, the entourage above or the entourage below, like all the restrictions in the regular order of entering to the king — these restrictions are nullified, and everyone can approach the king immediately. And all the more so in the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, about which it is said, "Call upon Him while He is near" [43](#_ftn1712), the closeness of the *Ma'or* to the *nitzotz* [spark] [44](#_ftn1713), and likewise in the days of preparation of the month of Elul.

And through the appropriate preparation in the month of Elul in the order of the work of the "city of refuge," the undesirable matters that were during the year are nullified, and when Rosh Hashanah comes, the day of judgment and trial, it will be in the manner of "and the congregation shall judge, etc., *and the congregation shall save*" [45](#_ftn1714), and one merits, within the totality of Israel, a good and sweet inscription and sealing for a good year.

***

**L.** The Rebbe Rayatz explains [46](#_ftn1715) that in addition to the fact that the month of Elul in its totality is the month of accounting and *teshuvah*, there is a special matter in the last twelve days of the month of Elul, which begin on 18 Elul, that these twelve days correspond to the twelve months of the year, a day for a month, a day for a month, that each day one must make a private accounting for one month of the twelve months of the year, starting from 18 Elul, which is the day of accounting for the past month of Tishrei.

When one makes a righteous accounting for the past of all the not-good thoughts, speech, and deeds, then one reaches the conclusion that it is impossible to demand and claim from the Holy One, Blessed be He, but only to request in the manner of **charity**: "To You, Hashem, is the charity" (since "to us is the shame of the face") [47](#_ftn1716).

And in order to merit that the Holy One, Blessed be He, will give us in the manner of charity, we must also give

#### 310

charity — as it is in *Tanchuma* [48](#_ftn1717) on the verse [49](#_ftn1718), "If you lend money," "He who lends to Hashem favors the poor [50](#_ftn1719), as it were, to Hashem he is lending, and He will pay him his reward [50](#_ftn1719]... The Holy One, Blessed be He, said, 'The soul of the poor man was fluttering to go out from hunger and you gave him sustenance and kept him alive, by your life, I will return to you soul for soul, tomorrow your son or your daughter will come, etc., and I will remember for them the mitzvah you did with the poor man and I will save them, etc.'"

And from this it is understood that in the month of Elul, and especially from 18 Elul, the time of accounting and *teshuvah* — one must endeavor and add and increase in the giving of charity, for this is the preparation to receive charity from the Holy One, Blessed be He, "To You, Hashem, is the charity."

**M.** And more specifically:

It was explained above (Section 11) that the month of Elul is like "cities of refuge," "to flee there" from the "avenger of blood," "until he stands before the congregation for judgment" [51](#_ftn1720), and in the meantime, one can and must utilize the time in such a way that when he "stands for judgment," all the arguments he can claim in his favor will be arranged for him, through which he will be able to be "and the congregation shall save," and likewise in the *nimshal*, that one must utilize the time remaining until the days of judgment and trial — from 18 Elul until Rosh Hashanah — for the work of *teshuvah*, which can also be "in one hour and in one moment" [52](#_ftn1721), as the Rebbe Rayatz explains [53](#_ftn1722) that "*sha'ata (chada)*" is also from the expression of turning, "*mit ayn ker*" [with one turn], and as is also understood from the legal ruling [54](#_ftn1723) that one who betroths a woman "on the condition that I am a *tzaddik* (complete [55](#_ftn1724)), even a complete *rasha* is betrothed, perhaps he contemplated *teshuvah* in his mind," that is, that through the contemplation of *teshuvah*, which is in one moment, he becomes a (complete) *tzaddik*.

— The Rosh [56](#_ftn1725) wrote that it is a "doubtful betrothal," and so it is ruled in the *Shulchan Aruch* [57](#_ftn1726): "She is betrothed *out of doubt*." But, that she is betrothed only out of doubt is because of the doubt "*perhaps* he contemplated *teshuvah*," and from this it is understood that when he contemplated *teshuvah* certainly, she is certainly betrothed.

And among the essential matters in which one must endeavor in the time remaining until the days of judgment and trial in order to accomplish "and the congregation shall save" — is the matter of **charity**, as stated,

#### 311

that through his action of keeping the soul of the poor man alive, the Holy One, Blessed be He, keeps his soul and the soul of his household alive, physically or spiritually, at the time they are in need of it, and therefore, without regard to all the calculations regarding his conduct in the past year, he can request from the Holy One, Blessed be He, in the manner of charity, "To You, Hashem, is the charity," since he also endeavored in the giving of charity to keep the soul of the poor man alive.

**N.** And this matter belongs to every single Jew — that without regard to his status and situation, it is in his power and ability to give charity to the poor:

The giving of charity, "you kept the soul of the poor man alive," is not only at the time one gives an abundance of silver and gold — for this matter is not in the power of everyone, but also in the giving of **one *prutah*** to the poor, and not only that, but "everyone who gives a *prutah* to the poor is blessed with six blessings" [58](#_ftn1727), that is, that for one *prutah* alone he is blessed **with six blessings**, six blessings that include all good! And furthermore (as the Gemara continues): "And he who appeases him with words is blessed with eleven blessings," that when he appeases him with words, speech alone — which is certainly in the power of everyone — he is blessed (not only with six blessings, but) with another five blessings, **eleven blessings**!

And just as physical charity is in the power of everyone, so it is regarding spiritual charity:

When one makes an accounting of his status and situation as he knows in his soul, and sees that he himself is "poor" — he might think that he has no power to help the other, at the same time that it is possible that the other is on a higher level than him.

But, the truth is, that "there is in each and every one aspects and levels that are not in his fellow, and all are in need of each other, and it is found that there is an advantage and superiority in each and every one that is higher than his fellow and his fellow is in need of him, and like the parable of the person who is a master of stature with head and feet, that even though the feet are the end of the level and below, and the head is the highest and superior to it, nevertheless, in one aspect there is an advantage and superiority to the feet that one must walk with them and they are also the ones that stand the body and the head, etc." [59](#_ftn1728).

And from this it is understood that everyone **can** occupy himself with the matter of charity: whether in giving a *prutah*, or in appeasing with words, whether in physical charity or in spiritual charity, but, in any event, it is a clear matter that each and every one can help his fellow in whatever matter it is, and consequently, everyone can prepare for the days of judgment and trial through the endeavor in the matter of charity.

#### 312

**O.** And on the other hand, even those who occupied themselves with the matter of charity during the entire year, **must** in the month of Elul **add** in charity with greater intensity and greater strength:

And by way of introduction — that in all *mitzvos* there are differences of levels in the manner of fulfilling the *mitzvah*, *hiddur mitzvah*, up to *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, but in the *mitzvah* of charity, the greatness of the necessity for its fulfillment in perfection is emphasized most — as is told in the Gemara [60](#_ftn1729) that the daughter of Nakdimon ben Gurion "was gathering barley from between the dung of the animals of the Arabs," because even though her father Nakdimon ben Gurion "did charity," nevertheless, "as it was required *for him* to do, *he did not do*, as people say, 'According to the camel is the burden'"!

That is to say [61](#_ftn1730), even though Nakdimon ben Gurion gave charity in a very great abundance, not in proportion to the amount that others gave (as is told in the Gemara [62](#_ftn1731) the greatness of the wonder in his giving of charity in a manner of exaggeration!), nevertheless, since in proportion to the greatness of his extreme wealth it was required of him to give more, and he did not give as they estimated he should give... the matter was avenged upon his own daughter ("*אין זיין אייגענע טאָכטער*") — even though this matter was not her fault... — that not only was her sustenance extremely limited, but even this limited sustenance she did not merit to receive in a way of honor, purity, and cleanliness... — that "she was gathering barley from between the dung of the animals of the Arabs"...

And it is found that even after the giving of charity during the entire year, it is impossible to demand from the Holy One, Blessed be He, even in the manner of charity, since "to us is the shame of the face" also in our work in the giving of charity itself, which was not "as it was required for him to do," "according to the camel is the burden"!

And therefore, everyone must — even those who occupied themselves with the matter of charity during the entire year — utilize the time remaining until the days of judgment and trial, and add in the matter of charity with greater intensity

## B"H, 3rd Day of Selichos, 5711

#### 329

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel,
Wherever you may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

At the end of the year, as we prepare for the beginning of the year that is approaching us and all the sons and daughters of Israel for good and for blessing, each and every one of us maps out a plan—at least in general terms—for our conduct and activities in the days to come, with a *kabbalah tovah* and a resolution to ascend ever higher.

The year 5712, which is fast approaching, is a *shmittah* year—a year of which it is written, "The land shall have a Sabbath of solemn rest, a Sabbath to Hashem... and the Sabbath of the land shall be for you to eat... and for your cattle, etc."

The verse does not depart from its literal meaning.

However, beyond this, our holy Torah has provided a great hint, and has prepared for us a detailed plan for the coming year:

"A Sabbath of solemn rest to the land"—a cessation from all the earthliness and materiality in our daily lives and activities.

"A Sabbath to Hashem"—and not for the sake of false ideologies and foreign perspectives that mislead and divert the Jewish person from his original and essential path, which is the path of Hashem. This is the path for which our first forefather, Avraham, sacrificed his life, and he commanded his children and his household after him to keep this path. They did so, and our people, the Jewish people, have lived according to this path for more than three thousand years.

"And the Sabbath of the land shall be for you to eat... and for your cattle"—the cessation of materiality

#### 330

and the attainment of spirituality are not intended only for the times of *tefillah* and Torah study. One should not say in his heart, "In my business, in my eating, and the like, the House of Israel is just like all the nations."

That is not our way.

There is *one* G-d and *one* Torah for the people of Israel, *one* nation on earth. Unity and wholeness must exist in our lives—*unified* lives, founded upon and permeated by one idea: that Israel, the Torah, and the *Kudsha Brich Hu* are all *one*.

The "Sabbath of the land," the "Sabbath to Hashem," must be present in *all* our affairs—"for you to eat" and "for your cattle" as well.

Only through such a way of life has our existence been sustained until now, and through the resolution to bring this conduct into practice in our daily lives for the future as well, we will merit to be inscribed and sealed for a good, sweet year, with good that is revealed and manifest.

One who blesses and is blessed with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**Menachem Mendel ben Chana Schneerson**

## 331

You should certainly make an effort to study the maamarim together with friends. For if Chazal spoke at such length regarding the virtue of studying not in isolation at any time, then how much more so during the days before Rosh Hashanah, on Rosh Hashanah, and during the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah—when there is a special virtue in the bond of friends.

This is as explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the verse, "You are standing today, all of you," a parsha that is always read before Rosh Hashanah. It is hinted at in the word "today," which refers to Rosh Hashanah, that all the sparks of the souls are standing and elevating to their source until "before Hashem." And it must be "all of you," meaning that everyone gathers together to become unified as one: "your heads, your tribes," etc., until "your water drawer."

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, concludes with this —that he heard from his holy father, the Rebbe, who had it as a tradition from Rebbe to Rebbe, that when the Alter Rebbe was in Mezritch, his teacher—the Maggid of Mezritch—revealed to him who he was... and that his avodah was to reveal and explain the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov regarding Ahavas Hashem and Ahavas Yisrael, and to reveal the path of Chassidus Chabad. And above all—his teacher, the Maggid of Mezritch, transmitted to him in the name of his own teacher, the Baal Shem Tov—the path of avodah is that one must also bring close simple people, for one must love a Jew because he is a Jew.

He adds further explanation that the Baal Shem Tov revealed the concept of the connection of Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael. The Maggid of Mezritch revealed the intellect and comprehension in the synthesis of these three loves, with the inner explanation of these three modes of love: "with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might." And our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, revealed the path of how every single person *can, must, and is obligated* to bring these three loves into action, stating that Ahavas Yisrael is the "upper gate," upon which it is written in illuminating letters, "This is the gate to enter."

## 332

And through this—that we are all standing together as one—"Hashem our G-d establishes us today," which is the day of Rosh Hashanah, "to be for Him a people, and He will be for us a G-d." He is destined to shine for us with an eternal light and will redeem us with the true and complete Geulah, speedily in our days, literally.

**Menachem Mendel son of Chana Schneerson**

*Tuesday of Selichos, 5711*
*Brooklyn, N.Y.*

## B’siyata D’Shmaya. Wednesday, 25 Elul, 5711

#### 333

**A.** Chazal have said[1](#_ftn1810) that when ten Jews gather together, the Shechinah rests among them. This gathering, which consists of many more than ten Jews and is convened for a worthy purpose, is certainly one in which the Shechinah rests; therefore, it must lead to positive results in actual practice.

May Hashem grant us the strength to say what needs to be said, and to hear, listen, and obey all that we need to hear and absorb on an occasion such as this.

Standing only a few days before Rosh Hashanah, this is the appropriate time for us to conduct a *cheshbon hanefesh*, to examine the summary of our actions throughout the past year, in order to rectify what requires rectification and to resolve that our future lives will be more elevated and "richer."

**B.** Time is a precious gift that the Ribono shel Olam has given us, and therefore we must always utilize it to the maximum extent. These words are especially true regarding the moments that still remain of the passing year, when a re-evaluation and reflection on the importance of time is required.

Everything created in the world exists for a purpose and a goal[2](#_ftn1811). Time, too, is a creation of the Ribono shel Olam[3](#_ftn1812). From this, it follows that every minute and every fraction of time contains a divine purpose and intent. It is understood, therefore, that even the smallest duration of time must be utilized to fulfill the purpose and goal that the Creator gave it. If we allow time to pass in a manner of waste, we are not only squandering a precious gift given to us by the Ribono shel Olam, but we are also failing to fulfill the purpose for which this time was given to us.

Time is like a vessel that must be filled to its brim and beyond. Every second of time given to us must also be filled with deeds

#### 334

of creation, not only for ourselves, but also for the benefit of others, which is a fundamental part of the general purpose of life. I wish to emphasize here, in particular, the sense of responsibility with which every man and woman of Israel must be imbued for the sake of the other, and for the environment in general. This is the duty to spread the light of Hashem around us.

This sense of responsibility must be especially strong among the youth, because the youth are those who have received a blessing in broad measure from Hashem with choice powers of energy, courage, and enthusiasm. In light of the above—that everything created by the Ribono shel Olam must be utilized in its fullness—there is an additional responsibility and duty placed especially upon the youth, and there is a limited time to fulfill this duty and responsibility.

**C.** We find that three important things are meeting here now: the "foundation" of time in general, the current time of Erev Rosh Hashanah in particular, and the "foundation" of the youth with the possibilities hidden within them and their special responsibility.

Therefore, I am confident that you will relate to all of this with seriousness, and resolve to fully utilize your tremendous powers in fulfilling your duties, both to improve yourselves and—at the same time—to influence your families, your friends, and the environment in general.

**D.** You, young men and young women, who are engaged in the study of matters of science and wisdom, and have thus been educated toward a serious, orderly, and logical approach to life, must adopt the same approach toward the Jewish duties and responsibilities that are unique to you. Their essence is the duty to spread the light and warmth of Yiddishkeit, and to introduce Jewish life into your surroundings.

The first condition to reach this goal is your steadfast observance of Torah and mitzvos. Then you can be absolutely certain of success, for every action that comes from intention and determination draws down special divine powers that ensure its success.

**E.** We are approaching Rosh Hashanah. The mitzvah of the day of this holy day is the blowing of the shofar[4](#_ftn1813). In general, the sound of the shofar has a dual meaning: it is a call to teshuvah, reminding us to repent for our shortcomings during the past year and to resolve to conduct ourselves in the path of Torah and mitzvos in the coming year; and together with this, the sound of the shofar is also a sound of victory, declaring that the Ribono shel Olam surely accepts our teshuvah and grants us a year of joy and happiness.

#### 335

May the new year be a year of victory over all obstacles, both within and without, so that each of us will be able to perform his or her part in turning darkness into light, and to reach a Jewish life with the proper blend of spirituality and a life of joy.

*L’shanah tovah tikasevu v’seichosemu.*

## With the help of Heaven. Shabbos Parshas Nitzavim, 28 Elul, 5711

#### 336

(Unedited transcript)

**"You are standing today, all of you, before Hashem, your G-d: your heads, your tribes, etc., from your woodchopper to your water drawer"**[1](#_ftn1814). This parsha is always read on the Shabbos before Rosh Hashanah[2](#_ftn1815), for this refers to "today" (You are standing today), which refers to the Day of Judgment of Rosh Hashanah[3](#_ftn1816)—"This day is the beginning of Your works"[4](#_ftn1817). And regarding this it is said, "You are standing today," which is similar to the teaching of our Sages[5](#_ftn1818) regarding the verse[6](#_ftn1819), "You are all alive today"—even on a day when the entire world is dying, you are alive. And in order for it to be "You are standing today," it must be (as the verse continues) "all of you," meaning that all of Israel must be in a state of inclusion and unity[7](#_ftn1820), where the distinctions of the particulars are not apparent, but rather one complete stature[8](#_ftn1821). Then, "You are standing today," meaning that even at a time when everyone else is dying, you are alive.

One must understand[9](#_ftn1822) what is written afterwards: "your heads, your tribes, etc., until your water drawer." Seemingly, since it has already been said "all of you," which includes all the particulars, why then does it specify the ten categories of Israel[10](#_ftn1823)? Especially according to what is explained[10](#_ftn1823), that the main point of "all of you" is that they should be one complete stature where the particulars and differences in levels are not felt. Based on this, it would seem that specifying the individual levels of Israel contradicts the concept of "all of you." One cannot say that by saying "your heads, your tribes, etc.," the intention is not to refer to the differences of the particulars as each category stands on its own, but rather to explain the word "all of you"—that the meaning of this is "your heads, your tribes," etc. For if so, it should have said "from your heads until your water drawer." Since it counts all ten categories in detail, it is understood that the intention is not only to explain the word "all of you," but also to refer to the differences of the particulars as each category stands on its own. From this it is understood that in the avodah of Rosh Hashanah, there are two matters: the unity of the collective in the manner of one complete stature, and the division of the particulars as each one stands on its own[10](#_ftn1823).

#### 337

b) **To understand** this, we must preface that it is known that the primary avodah of man is to draw the *oros* (lights) into the *keilim* (vessels), for the ultimate intent is to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower worlds[11](#_ftn1824), and the preparation for this is through the *hislabshus* (enclothement) of the *oros* in the *keilim*. The matter of this[12](#_ftn1825) is that the *oros*, which are in a state of *giluy* (revelation), are in a state of ascent to their source and in a state of manifest *dveikus* (cleaving) to their source[13](#_ftn1826), while the *keilim*, which come about through a *hefsek* (interruption), etc., are in a state of *he'elem* (concealment) and in a state of unmanifest *dveikus*[13](#_ftn1826). If so, they are opposites of one another; how is it possible for them to be joined together?

However, since the *or* (light) senses the virtue of the *kli* (vessel)[14](#_ftn1827), and through this the *or* also acts within the *kli* so that its virtue is felt, it is possible for the *oros* and *keilim* to be joined. For the *or* is in a state of *giluy*, and therefore in every matter to which the *or* is drawn, it senses (and also reveals within it) its virtue. This is the meaning of the *or* sensing the virtue of the *kli*, which is the matter of *he'elem*—that the virtue within it is[15](#_ftn1828) because its root is from the aspect of the "ability not to shine," which possesses more strength than the aspect of the "ability to shine"[16](#_ftn1829). However, the *kli* itself, being in a state of *he'elem* and unmanifest *dveikus*, its virtue is not felt within it. It is only the *or* specifically—since its nature is *giluy*—that senses the virtue of the *kli*[17](#_ftn1830), and it also reveals the virtue within the *kli*. Through this, it is possible for there to be a joining of *oros* and *keilim* from the side of the *or*. And also from the side of the *kli*: since the nature of the *kli* is *bitul*[18](#_ftn1831)—meaning that it is nullified to everything that is not a *kli*—and especially to the *or* that revealed its virtue within it (for from its own side it is an aspect of *he'elem*, and it was the *or* specifically that revealed its virtue within it, and therefore it is nullified most profoundly to the *or*)—therefore, it is possible for the joining of *oros* and *keilim* to exist also from the side of the *kli*.

**And the root** of the matter of the joining of *oros* and *keilim* is from their root in the names *Havayah* and *Elokim*, for *Havayah* is the root of the *oros*, and *Elokim* is the root of the *keilim*[19](#_ftn1832). Therefore, from the aspect of the *yichud* (unification) of *Havayah* and *Elokim*, the joining of

#### 338

*oros* and *keilim* is drawn down. The matter is[20](#_ftn1833) as it is written[21](#_ftn1834), "For a sun and shield is *Havayah Elokim*." Just as the function of the shield is in two matters: first, that it conceals the light of the sun, and second, that through the fact that it conceals the essence of the light, it reveals the light below—so too is it with the names *Havayah* and *Elokim*. The name *Elokim* conceals the light of the name *Havayah*, and through this it causes the light of *Havayah* to be revealed within the *keilim*. This matter is not in the way of a struggle where they overcome one another, for if so, there would sometimes be an overcoming of the name *Havayah*, at which time there would be an aspect of total *giluy* without limitation, and sometimes an overcoming of the name *Elokim*, at which time there would be an aspect of total *he'elem*. Since the name *Elokim* conceals the name *Havayah* and yet the light of *Havayah* shines through it, it must be that this is not in the way of one overcoming the other, but in a manner where they are suited to one another, and because of this they both act as one, and through this it is possible for the joining of *oros* and *keilim* to exist.

The explanation for this is that the name *Havayah*, whose nature is the matter of *giluy*, the ultimate purpose of *giluy* is that the light of the *Ohr Ein Sof* should shine in every place, even to the lowest depths. This matter can only be achieved through enclothement in the name *Elokim*, the aspect of *keilim* specifically. Thus, the matter of *giluy* is completed specifically through *he'elem*. Likewise, the name *Elokim* does not have the purpose of concealing the *giluy* of the name *Havayah*, but on the contrary, that through the *he'elem*, the *giluy* of the name *Havayah* should reach the lowest depths. Thus, the matter of *he'elem* is to complete the matter of *giluy*. It turns out that in truth, the names *Havayah* and *Elokim* are included within one another, to the point that *Havayah* and *Elokim* are truly one[22](#_ftn1835).

**And likewise** it is in the root of the matter regarding the aspect of the first *Tzimtzum* and the revelation of the *Kav* (line) after the *Tzimtzum*. For the intent of the *Tzimtzum* is for the sake of *giluy*. That is, even though the *Tzimtzum* is different from other *tzimtzumim*—all of which are in the way of a reduction, whereas the first *Tzimtzum* is in the way of a total removal[23](#_ftn1836)—the intent of the first *Tzimtzum* is also for the sake of *giluy*. And likewise regarding the matter of *giluy*, which is the light of the *Kav*: the matter of *Tzimtzum* is felt within it, for before the *Tzimtzum* the light was in the aspect of *Ein Sof*, and after the *Tzimtzum* the *giluy* is in the aspect of a thin *Kav*[24](#_ftn1837), which was brought about by the *Tzimtzum*. Nevertheless, its nature is *giluy*, for the illumination of the *Kav* is not drawn from the *Tzimtzum* itself, but from the aspect of the great circle that was before the *Tzimtzum*[25](#_ftn1838). Thus, in the *Tzimtzum* there is

#### 339

the intent of *giluy*, and in the *Kav* the matter of *Tzimtzum* is felt. From this, it is also drawn into the names *Havayah* and *Elokim*, that they are not in the way of one overcoming the other or in the way of a war, Heaven forbid, but in the way of a joining. And from this it is also drawn into the *oros* and *keilim* that there should be a joining of *oros* and *keilim*.

**And from this** it is also drawn into the avodah of man[26](#_ftn1839) that there should be a joining of the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis*. For the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis* are truly opposites of one another, for the *nefesh elokis* is in the aspect of ascent, like fire that rises upward, as it is written[27](#_ftn1840), "For Hashem your G-d is a consuming fire," and the *nefesh habahamis* is from the spirit of the beast that descends downward[28](#_ftn1841). Nevertheless, the ultimate intent is to transform the *nefesh habahamis* itself into *Elokus*, and the *nefesh elokis* will perform its avodah through the *nefesh habahamis* itself[29](#_ftn1842). This matter is accomplished by the *nefesh elokis* sensing the virtue of the *nefesh habahamis*, that it contains a most high spark, only that it fell downward, etc. Furthermore, the *nefesh habahamis* possesses the matter of *bitul* like a beast, which is nullified to the *nefesh elokis*. Therefore, it is possible for the joining of the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis* to exist.

d) **The aforementioned matter** that the *nefesh elokis* transforms the *nefesh habahamis* into holiness is the matter of the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim*. That is, the ten powers of the *nefesh elokis* clothe and fill the powers of the *nefesh habahamis*, which become filled[30](#_ftn1843) with the powers of the *nefesh elokis*. However, it is known that the ultimate intent is[31](#_ftn1845) to arrive at the aspect of simple *ratzon* (will) that is above *ta'am v'da'as* (reason and intellect), meaning above the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim* [and the intention is not that the aspect of simple *ratzon* should not be in the *keilim*, but that even the simple *ratzon* which is above the aspect of *keilim* should be drawn into the *keilim*—*oros* in *keilim*—but that the *oros* in *keilim* should act as they must from the side of the simple *ratzon* that is above *ta'am v'da'as* and above the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim*]. The revelation of this aspect is something that comes from above; it is not within the power of man from his own side, but rather what is given to him from above. That is, after he performs his avodah to transform the *nefesh habahamis* into holiness, so that the powers of the *nefesh habahamis* are filled with the powers of the *nefesh elokis*—which is the avodah that everyone can reach through their own power—then the aforementioned aspect of simple *ratzon* is drawn to him from above. And regarding this it is said[32](#_ftn1846), "I give you your priesthood as a gift of service."

#### 340

e) **The explanation** of the matter: Our Sages said[33](#_ftn1847), "The way of flesh and blood: an empty vessel holds, a full vessel does not hold; the way of the Holy One, blessed be He: a full vessel holds, an empty vessel does not hold." It is explained in many places[34](#_ftn1848) that both ways exist in the avodah of Hashem, but the way of flesh and blood is the avodah that one can reach through one's own power, and the way of the Holy One, blessed be He, is the avodah that is drawn from above. Regarding this they said, "The way of flesh and blood: an empty vessel holds, a full vessel does not hold." For the *nefesh habahamis* "preceded its burden"[35](#_ftn1849), meaning it entered man first and became rooted in him, and it became even stronger as time went on, as he used it much for eating, drinking, and other matters of this world[36](#_ftn1850). Because of this, man is a "full vessel," meaning he is full of desires, claiming and saying, "I want this thing, and I need this thing, and I cannot survive without this thing," etc. Regarding this they say, "A full vessel does not hold," meaning that when he is a full vessel, not only regarding forbidden things that distract him, but even regarding permitted matters, and even things that are permitted but are not done for the sake of Heaven—because he is a full vessel, he does not hold. Therefore, he must be in the aspect of an "empty vessel," meaning that he should empty himself of his physical matters and not desire even permitted things. And even the things that are necessary for him (and not just things he thinks are necessary, but things he truly needs) according to Torah, he should desire only the spirituality within them. This is the meaning of "empty vessel"—it does not mean that he is totally empty of physical things, that he does not eat or drink, etc., but rather that he does not desire the physicality of the things, only their spirituality. Then he is called an "empty vessel," since he has emptied himself of the physicality of things.

**This will be understood** from the interpretation of the Sages' teaching, "The way of flesh and blood: an empty vessel holds, a full vessel does not hold," as it relates to physical influence, which is the way of flesh and blood in its literal sense. When a person is a full vessel—meaning he is filled with desires, etc.—then he does not hold even the blessing of physical influence, because since the purpose of man's creation is for spiritual avodah, he does not hold physicality, as that is not his purpose. But when he is an empty vessel—meaning he has emptied himself of all physical matters—then he holds even physical influence. For although the purpose of his creation is for spiritual avodah and physicality is not his purpose, nevertheless, since he has become an empty vessel—that he does not desire physical things, only the spirituality within them, and only from that side does he perform physical things—then his physicality is spirituality (and spirituality is his purpose, for which he was created), and therefore he holds the physical influence. Furthermore, he holds physical influence without limit; although his place is limited, he holds an abundance of influence, for since his physicality is spirituality, and spirituality does not occupy space (as is explained in the *drushim* of Parshas Nitzavim[37](#_ftn1851), the analogy there regarding the enclothement of several powers—will, intellect, and thought—in one brain), therefore he can hold physical influence without limit. From this, one also understands the matter of "an empty vessel holds" according to the interpretation that the way of flesh and blood also exists in the avodah of Hashem (avodah through man's own power), that "empty vessel" does not mean he does not eat or drink, but that even when he eats and drinks and does all his needs, he does not desire the physicality of the things; he does not desire permitted things, and even the necessary things he does only for the sake of the spiritual benefit within them. Therefore he is called an empty vessel, for since his physicality is not physicality, he is empty of physical things. And when he is an empty vessel, then "an empty vessel holds," meaning he holds spiritual influence, which means he has the ability to perform his avodah to transform his *nefesh habahamis* into holiness, so that all the powers of the *nefesh habahamis* become filled with the powers of the *nefesh elokis*.

**And after this**, the avodah is performed in the way of the Holy One, blessed be He, that "a full vessel holds." That is, after he has reached in his avodah as far as his hand can reach, so that he has become a full vessel—that all the powers of the *nefesh habahamis* have become filled with the powers of the *nefesh elokis*—then he holds also what is not within the power of man by himself, but what is given to him from above. This is the aspect of simple *ratzon* that is above *ta'am v'da'as* and above the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim*. This matter is in such a way that even the light that is above the enclothement in *keilim* is drawn into the *keilim*, and furthermore, it is drawn also into physicality, at which point the physicality is in a different manner, in the aspect of "without limit." This is similar to what we find regarding the *manna*, "bread from heaven"[38](#_ftn1852), that although the *manna* was measured by the measure of an *omer*[39](#_ftn1853), nevertheless it was without limit, for "the one who gathered much and the one who gathered little received the *omer* equally"[40](#_ftn1854). So too is it regarding the influence that is above the aspect of the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim*; even as it comes into *keilim* and into physicality, it is in the aspect of "without limit."

f) **Just as** in the individual avodah of everyone, there is the avodah in the manner of the joining of *oros* and *keilim*, and there is also the avodah that is above *ta'am v'da'as*,

#### 342

likewise, in the complete stature of the collective of Israel, there are two aspects of avodah. The avodah in the aspect of the enclothement of *oros* in *keilim*, which is with limitation, and therefore it contains levels and individual aspects, which are the ten categories among the Children of Israel: "your heads, your tribes, etc., until your water drawer." And there is also the avodah that is above *ta'am v'da'as*, which is in the aspect of "without limit," and therefore the division of particulars does not apply to it, but it is in the aspect of the collective.

**This is** "You are standing today, all of you, etc."[41](#_ftn1855). This parsha is always read before Rosh Hashanah, at which time there must be a general drawing down from its root and source, etc.[42](#_ftn1856), and therefore there must also be the avodah in the aspect of the collective. As it is said[43](#_ftn1857), "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one"—for the drawing down of the blessing is specifically when we are "all of us as one," in the aspect of the collective. Therefore, there must be at that time the matter of "You are standing today, all of you," without differences of levels. However, since the intent is that there should be a drawing down of *oros* into *keilim* specifically, therefore the verse continues, "your heads, your tribes, etc.," which is the manner of avodah that must be throughout the entire year (after the general avodah of Rosh Hashanah), in the manner of enclothement in *keilim* specifically. And since the intent is that even in the aspect of *keilim*, the aspect of the light that is above *keilim* should be drawn down—meaning that the aspect of the collective that is above the particulars should be drawn into the particulars specifically—therefore it is said, "all of you, etc., your heads, etc.," meaning the drawing down of the collective into the particular. Its matter in avodah is as is known[44](#_ftn1858), that the *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) of Rosh Hashanah is not the same as the *kabbalas ol* of the entire year. For on Rosh Hashanah, the *mitzvah* of the day is *kabbalas ol*, and this is the matter of a general *kabbalas ol* that is above *ta'am v'da'as*, which is the avodah in the aspect of the collective. This is also what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, said in many *maamarim*[45](#_ftn1859), that on Rosh Hashanah one must value time greatly, so that not even a moment should go to waste, and one must increase in the letters of Torah, *tefillah*, and the recitation of *Tehillim*. The reason for this is because in the avodah of reciting the letters, everyone is equal (unlike in matters of intellectual comprehension, where there are differences of levels), and this is the avodah that is in the aspect of the collective that is above the division of particulars. This aspect is drawn down in the individual avodah of the entire year. Through this, we will merit a good writing and sealing for a good and sweet year, in revealed and manifest goodness.

## With the help of Hashem. Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Nitzavim, 28 Elul, 5711

#### 343

(Unedited)

**1.** It is stated in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of Parshas Nitzavim that "this parsha is always read before Rosh Hashanah,"[1] and it is hinted at in the word *Hayom* ("You are standing today" [Nitzavim] [2]) which refers to Rosh Hashanah,[3] for "this [4] day is the beginning of Your works, a remembrance of the first day." Sometimes we also read Parshas Vayelech before Rosh Hashanah, when Nitzavim and Vayelech are read together; however, Parshas Nitzavim is always read on the Shabbos before Rosh Hashanah.

**2.** Maamar on the verse "You are standing today, etc."

***

**3.** The Rebbe Rayatz related[5] in the name of the Alter Rebbe:

The Baal Shem Tov was asked why we do not bless the month of Tishrei as we bless all the other months of the year. The Baal Shem Tov replied that "the seventh month, which is the first month of the months of the year, *Hashem Himself blesses it* on Shabbos Mevarchim, which is the last Shabbos of the month of Elul, and through this power, Yisrael blesses the months eleven times a year."

It can be said that this matter (that Hashem blesses the first month, and through this power Yisrael blesses the other months) is similar to what is written,[6] "He declares His words to Yaakov, His statutes and His judgments to Yisrael"—"What He does, He tells Yisrael to do,"[7] meaning that Hashem’s action is the empowerment that enables Yisrael to act as well.[8]

**4.** And we must understand:

It is a known principle that the Torah "is not in heaven,"[9] but was given specifically down here on earth,

#### 344

meaning that the ruling determined by the Beis Din below is in effect even above, to the point that Hashem says, "My children have defeated Me, My children have defeated Me."[10]

This is emphasized most strongly in the sanctification of the months and the intercalation of the years—which was entrusted entirely to the Beis Din below, to the extent that "when the ministering angels gather before Hashem to ask when Rosh Hashanah is... Hashem says to them, 'Why do you ask Me? Let us, I and you, go to the Beis Din below.'"[11] Furthermore, it is entrusted to whichever Beis Din it may be, as Chazal expound[12] on the verse,[13] "The appointed times of Hashem which you shall proclaim,"—"You (the word is written without a *vav*, implying 'you' even in error, even if mistaken, even if coerced)." And even more than that, as the Gemara states,[14] "You, even if willful," meaning that the sanctification of the months is determined even by a willful Beis Din!

The explanation for this is that the entirety of the Torah was given down here specifically to effect the *tikkun* of the world. In particular, the matter of intercalating years and sanctifying months, because it is connected with the *diminishment of the moon* [both the intercalation of years, to equalize the deficit of the lunar year relative to the solar year, and the intercalation of months—a short or full month—because "you calculate days for the month, but you do not calculate hours,"[15] and also because "sometimes it comes long and sometimes it comes short"[16]] which caused the opening for the *sin of the Tree of Knowledge* [as explained in Chassidus[17] that the shattering of the vessels is the root of the moon's diminishment, and the moon's diminishment is the root of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge]. Therefore, it was entrusted specifically to the Beis Din below, so that through them the *tikkun* (for the moon's diminishment, and consequently also) for the sin of the Tree of Knowledge would be effected.

Based on this, we must understand the reason why "the seventh month, which is the first month of the months of the year, Hashem Himself blesses it"—for seemingly, since the entire matter of sanctifying the month was entrusted specifically to the *Beis Din below*, what is the reason that specifically the *first* month, in which the general influence for all the months is effected, is blessed by *Hashem* Himself, and not by *Bnei Yisrael*, to whom the entire matter of sanctifying the month was entrusted?

**5.** The core of the explanation is this: As an empowerment for the entirety of man's *avodah* in the manner of *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below), there must be an influence from above in the manner of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above) from the highest possible source.

#### 345

By way of introduction:

It is known[18] that there are two (general) categories of *is'arusa d'le'eila*: (a) *is'arusa d'le'eila* that precedes *is'arusa d'lesata* and activates it, such as the "Heavenly Voice" (*bas kol*) that proclaims teshuvah,[19] which is the arousal that comes from above to awaken man to teshuvah; (b) *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is drawn down through man's *avodah* in *is'arusa d'lesata*.

Now, although the second category of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (which comes through *is'arusa d'lesata*) has an advantage over the first (which precedes *is'arusa d'lesata*)—in that the first, being without any preparation at all, can be fleeting and passing,[20] whereas the second, being after man's preparation, has permanence[21]—nevertheless, the first *is'arusa d'le'eila* is a level incomparably higher than the second. For the second, which comes through *is'arusa d'lesata*, is *proportionate* to the *is'arusa d'lesata*, drawn from a lower level that *is reached* by *is'arusa d'lesata*. This is not the case for the first *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which is drawn of its own accord (without *is'arusa d'lesata*) from a level so high that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach there at all.

**6.** And furthermore:

"There is yet a third category of *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which is also *is'arusa d'le'eila*... that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all... yet it does not settle and reveal itself unless there is perfection in the deeds of the lower beings, such that they have already been influenced by the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is proportionate to *is'arusa d'lesata*. Then, the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is far above the level of *is'arusa d'lesata* also settles and reveals itself."[22]

[Similar to what was explained earlier in the maamar[23] regarding the *avodah* of the level of simple *ratzon* (will) that is above intellect and emotion, which is Hashem's attribute, which man does not have the power to attain, but is in the nature of a gift from above—that after one has become a full vessel, having reached in his *avodah* to the place his hand can reach, then he is given from above to hold onto Hashem's attribute, so that he also possesses the *avodah* of the level of simple *ratzon* that is above intellect and emotion].

Seemingly, this third *is'arusa d'le'eila* is the *most exalted*, possessing both advantages (of the first and second categories) together—it has permanence

#### 346

(unlike the first, which is fleeting) because it is after man's preparation, and it is from a level that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach (unlike the second, which is proportionate to *is'arusa d'lesata*) because it is after the perfection of man's *avodah*.

However, despite the fact that the third *is'arusa d'le'eila* is also from a level that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all (like the first), the very fact that it does not settle and reveal itself until after perfection in the deeds of the lower beings proves that man's *avodah* has *some value and connection* to this *is'arusa d'le'eila*.[24]

Therefore, the true perfection of *is'arusa d'le'eila* that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all is the *first* *is'arusa d'le'eila*,[25] which comes before and without any need for *avodah* and preparation on man's part at all, being from the most exalted level, to which man's *avodah* has *no value or connection whatsoever*.

**7.** And through this first *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which is from the *most exalted level*—the power is drawn for the entire matter of *is'arusa d'lesata* that activates and draws down *is'arusa d'le'eila*:

It is known[26] that "the general matter of why *is'arusa d'lesata* causes *is'arusa d'le'eila* is not a necessity at all from its own side... just as in the nature of people, where love and closeness from one to another also causes love and closeness from the other to him... as a necessary matter coming from value and connection. But the created being relative to the Creator—there is no comparison at all."

—This is not only regarding *is'arusa d'le'eila* from a place that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach, but even regarding *is'arusa d'le'eila* that *is'arusa d'lesata* does reach, it is a matter of no comparison at all—

"If so, that *is'arusa d'lesata* causes *is'arusa d'le'eila* is not a necessary matter, G-d forbid, but only because *so it arose in His will, may He be blessed*, that *is'arusa d'lesata* should cause *is'arusa d'le'eila*."

And this matter—that "it arose in His will, may He be blessed, that *is'arusa d'lesata* should cause *is'arusa d'le'eila*"—is the first *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which is drawn from the most exalted level *that has no limitations at all*,

[above the third *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which, although it is also from a place that *is'arusa d'lesata*

#### 347

does not reach, has the *limitation* that it does not settle and reveal itself unless there is perfection in the deeds of the lower beings],

and due to the *absence of limitation* in this level—the entire matter of *is'arusa d'lesata* causing *is'arusa d'le'eila* is established, so that *is'arusa d'lesata* has the power to awaken and draw down *is'arusa d'le'eila*: first the *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is proportionate to *is'arusa d'lesata*, from a place that *is'arusa d'lesata* reaches, and afterwards also the *is'arusa d'le'eila* from a place that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach, but which is drawn down after the perfection of the deeds of the lower beings.

An additional advantage of the first *is'arusa d'le'eila* is that due to its greatness, it has the power to act so that every Jew, in whatever standing and situation he may be, without any preparation on his part, can come to an awakening for the *avodah* of Hashem, just as with the heavenly proclamations through which there can be an awakening of teshuvah even among *resha'im* (wicked), as Chazal say,[27] "The wicked are full of regrets"—which is the exact opposite extreme of the third *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which does not settle and reveal itself unless there is perfection in the deeds of the lower beings.

Thus, the action of the first *is'arusa d'le'eila* (due to its greatness) is twofold: (a) that it enables *is'arusa d'lesata* to exist, (b) that *is'arusa d'lesata* will effect the drawing down of *is'arusa d'le'eila*.

**8.** Based on this, we can also explain the content of Hashem's blessing for the month of Tishrei—similar to the first *is'arusa d'le'eila*, which is the empowerment for the entire matter of *is'arusa d'lesata* causing *is'arusa d'le'eila*:

It is known[28] that on Rosh Hashanah there must be a new influence from the root and the first source [as mentioned earlier in the maamar[29] that the influence of Rosh Hashanah is in the category of a *klal* (generalization), and this *klal* is not a *klal* for particulars, but a *klal* in essence], not only from a level after *Tzimtzum*, but before *Tzimtzum*, and not only from the level of revealed *ratzon*, but from the level of the absolute *ratzon* in His essence, etc.—the most exalted level, which *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all, and its influence is only in the manner of *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is drawn down of its own accord.

And this is what we say on Rosh Hashanah, "This day is the beginning of Your works, a remembrance of the first day"—that Rosh Hashanah is like the first day of the beginning of Your works, when the influence was not through the *avodah* of the created beings in *is'arusa d'lesata* (as it is now, where it depends on *is'arusa d'lesata*), but in the manner of *is'arusa d'le'eila*, because "He desires kindness,"[30] and similarly every Rosh Hashanah, on which the first *is'arusa d'le'eila* is drawn down from a level that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all.[31]

And this *is'arusa d'le'eila* is the empowerment for the entire *avodah* of *is'arusa d'lesata* in the coming year:

After the honest accounting of the month of Elul regarding the past year—all his thoughts, words, and deeds that were not as they should be—one might come to the conclusion that he does not have the power to awaken himself to the *avodah* of Hashem, to the point that through his *avodah* he would awaken *is'arusa d'le'eila*. The answer to this is that there exists an *is'arusa d'le'eila* that is drawn from the most exalted level that *is'arusa d'lesata* does not reach at all, and therefore it has the power to act so that, regardless of his previous standing and situation, man will awaken to the *avodah* of Hashem, and his *avodah* in *is'arusa d'lesata* will effect the drawing down of *is'arusa d'le'eila*.

However, since Rosh Hashanah is only a "*remembrance* of the first day," a "remembrance" alone, and not the "first day" literally, because it is after the order has already been established that it depends on *is'arusa d'lesata*, therefore, also regarding the drawing down of *is'arusa d'le'eila* that comes because "He desires kindness" (as on the "first day"), there must be some matter of preparation—and this is the *avodah* of the month of Elul.

***

**9.** [The Rebbe Shlita instructed to play the "Rosh Hashanah *tnuah*" (melody), and instructed to repeat it several times, and the Rebbe Shlita himself played with terrible weeping. And afterwards he said:]

We are now standing at the entrance to the "Days of Awe," in which the attribute of *yirah* (fear/awe) is revealed from above,[33] and consequently, the *avodah* is also along the line of *yirah*.

Within *yirah* itself there are several levels, and generally: *yirah tata'ah* (lower fear) and *yirah ila'ah* (higher fear). And within *yirah tata'ah* itself there are several levels, among them: fear of punishment and fear of majesty (as the Rebbe Rayatz brings in the maamar published for Chai Elul[34]).

#### 349

Seemingly, when one is at the beginning of the *avodah* along the line of *yirah* (during the Days of Awe), one should begin from the first level of *yirah tata'ah*—fear of punishment.

But the truth is that since on Rosh Hashanah there is also the *avodah* of teshuvah, through which a *leap* is made that is not according to order and progression, above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, to the point that in one hour and in one moment one can change from a complete *rasha* to a complete *tzaddik*, [35] there can also be a beginning of *avodah* at *exalted levels*.

From this it is understood that the *avodah* can and must be *specifically with joy*—because the movement of the leap (which is through teshuvah) is connected with joy, which breaks through barriers.[36]

**10.** And more specifically:

It is written,[37] "And rejoice with trembling," meaning that even the *avodah* of the "Days of Awe" along the line of *yirah*, "trembling," must be from within joy—"*Rejoice* with trembling."[38]

And we must add the precision of the verse's language, "rejoice with trembling"—and not "tremble with rejoicing"—that the *beginning* is with the matter of *joy* ("rejoice"), but the joy must be covered with trembling.

And what is stated in the writings of the Arizal[39] that "anyone who does not weep on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, his soul is not complete"—this does not mean weeping of bitterness over his not-good situation, but weeping of *joy*, which, because of the greatness and intensity of the revelations of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur that his brain-vessel cannot contain, results in weeping with tears, similar to what is said[40] about Rabbi Akiva, whose eyes flowed with tears when he heard the secrets of the Torah from his teacher Rabbi Eliezer.[41]

[Based on this, the precision of the language "anyone who does not weep... his soul is not *complete*" is understood, for this weeping is connected with the *completeness of the soul*—since it does not refer to weeping of bitterness over his not-good situation, which is not related to the completeness of the soul, and on the contrary, etc., but rather it refers to weeping that comes from the feeling of the greatness and intensity of the revelations of Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, which these revelations are felt specifically because of the *completeness of the soul*, but because they are extremely exalted revelations, even with the completeness of the soul, he does not have the power to contain them].

#### 350

**11.** And in explaining the reason why even during the Days of Awe the beginning of the *avodah* must be specifically from within joy ("rejoice"):

If the beginning were "with trembling"—it is possible that the awakening to the *avodah* itself would not come. For when he makes an honest accounting in the month of Elul of all his not-good thoughts, words, and deeds that occurred during the past year and sees that his conduct was not as it should be, and he continues to make an honest accounting of the *avodah* of the month of Elul itself, that even in the special month that Hashem gave to fix the entire year, his conduct was not as it should be—then he will come to a state of extreme submission and humility,

—like the parable of "the poor man crushed by suffering... who needs no awakening to weep,"[42] "when he remembers... his great distress... he will weep in the bitterness of his soul immediately, etc."[43]—

to the point that he will not be able to dare to ask Hashem to be King and to accept him as a servant! Not only will he not be able to demand and argue that He should accept him as a servant, but he will not even be able to ask for it as an act of charity. He will not have the chutzpah and the daring to ask Hashem—even as an act of charity—to accept him as a servant!...

(The Rebbe Shlita wept much, and afterwards continued:) And even when Hashem already forgives him, and is ready to give him his request regardless of whether he is worthy of it or not, he still must "stretch out his hand,"[44] and consequently, he must have a "vessel" through which he can receive—and since so, the question is asked: with what will he be able to receive ("*mit vos vet er nemen, mit vos*")?!...

**12.** And therefore, the beginning must be specifically from within *joy* ("rejoice")—which breaks through barriers:

Through joy, a breaking of barriers is effected within him—that without considering his standing and situation, he will fulfill Hashem's command in the Torah:[45] "Say before Me on Rosh Hashanah 'Kingship' (Malchiyos), etc., so that you will make Me King over you!"

Hashem says to Bnei Yisrael: Jews, proclaim Kingship ("*Iden, shrait Malchiyos*")—which is an empowerment for all Bnei Yisrael and for every Jew, that regardless of their standing and situation, they can say Malchiyos, to ask Hashem to be King

#### 351

over them, and furthermore, to *praise* ("say" like "you have declared," a term of praise[46]) Hashem regarding the matter of Kingship—"so that you will make Me King over you."

And when a Jew does not consider his standing and situation and says Malchiyos, then they deal with him from above in such a way—that they do not consider his standing and situation, whether he is worthy or not, whether he is a vessel and has with what to receive or not, and they give him everything—even the vessels, as it is written,[47] "And He will sustain you," meaning that Hashem gives even the vessels[48]—not because of the greatness of his *avodah*, but because of the matter of "*He chooses* for us our inheritance, the pride of Yaakov whom He *loves* forever."[49]

[The Rebbe Shlita instructed to play a joyous *nigun*].

***********

## With the help of Heaven. Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5712

#### 352

Unedited

[Following Shacharis and the order of Hataras Nedarim, the Rebbe said:]

Since we are entering the year of Shemitah, one must also execute a Pruzbul, as the Alter Rebbe writes in Shulchan Aruch that "every G-d-fearing person should be stringent with himself to execute a Pruzbul." He adds that "the time for the Pruzbul is, ideally, at the end of the sixth year before the Rosh Hashanah of the Shemitah year"—that is, on Erev Rosh Hashanah of the Shemitah year.

(The Rebbe concluded, turning to the Beis Din who were officiating:) I do not know if anyone owes me any debt, but if so—"I hereby hand over to you all debts that I have, so that I may collect them whenever I wish".

(And afterwards he said:) Certainly, everyone should act in this manner.

(And he concluded:) May everyone have a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

*

While distributing the *panim*, the Rebbe said:

May Hashem help us fulfill our supreme mission here below, within the ten *tefachim*, with expansion, peace of mind, and physical well-being.

And may Hashem help us merit the complete Redemption very soon, and may the Rebbe lead us to Eretz Yisrael with Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

## B"H. The text of the telegram that the Rebbe shlita was pleased to send to Anash sheyichyu throughout the world in anticipation of Rosh Hashanah, 5712

#### 353

Please convey my blessing to Anash: May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year.

**Menachem Schneerson**
